

 # Chapter 631: Gu Can is Still That Gu Can

This year, Yunlou City (Yunlou Cheng) in Shujian Lake (Shujian Hu) hosted the Water-Land Grand Gathering and the Zhou Tian Grand Sacrifice, spending countless amounts of money. They invited many divine beings from both Buddhist and Daoist sects, and not the kind that merely sought fame.

This was largely due to the unique status of the two organizers—Jiejiang Zhenjun Liu Zhimiao, who transitioned from a prisoner of Gongliu Island to a revered figure of the Zhenjing Sect, and General Guan Yiran, stationed at Shujian Lake. Otherwise, the costs would have at least doubled. Convincing these mountain cultivators to descend required considerable offerings. Of course, it was a fortunate event as well, allowing the participating divine beings to accumulate merits while also getting acquainted with Liu Zhimiao and Guan Yiran, which motivated the Daoist gods and high-ranking monks to take these rituals seriously.

Among them, three figures remained inconspicuous in the background. However, the military officials accompanying General Guan held a certain admiration for their accounting skills.

Those three were named Gu Can, Zeng Ye, and Ma Duyi.

The two grand events successfully concluded, and everyone praised the merits of Liu Zhimiao and General Guan. 

That night, after drinking a victory toast with the officials under General Guan, a tall and slender youth dressed in a green robe walked alone back to his residence, a quiet alley in the city of Chishui (Chishui Cheng). He rented a small house there, and waiting at the door was a tall young man, anxiously looking out. This tall youth was Zeng Ye, a fortunate one rescued from the fire pit by the old cultivator Zhang Ye of Qingxia Island, who subsequently worked at the sect's gate. During that time, he assisted an accountant and traveled across various countries, improving his cultivation through unconventional methods.

Ma Duyi was also awake. Being a ghost herself, she trained better at night. Currently, she had lit a lamp on the table and was calculating expenses for the two grand events, which had cost a fortune. Fortunately, an old hunchbacked man named Zhu Lian had sent two large sums of money, one delivered personally by Zhu Lian himself, who was amiable and talkative, and the second entrusted to a young man named Dong Shuijing, who brought it to them in Yunlou City.

Ma Duyi was dressed in the fox fur of the Xu family from Qingfeng City, her beauty captivating.

Gu Can stood outside, patting his clothes to dissipate some of the alcohol smell. He lightly knocked on the door, entered, poured himself a cup of tea, and sat opposite Ma Duyi, while Zeng Ye took a seat on the stool between them.

Ma Duyi did not lift her head, “The officials from the General’s mansion are far less greedy than those county officials we dealt with back in the day. Aside from some minor expenses, there’s hardly any corruption.”

Gu Can replied nonchalantly, “Not greedy? First, they lack the guts to act carelessly under General Guan’s watch. Second, they have a bright future ahead and wouldn’t want to jeopardize their careers over money. It’s not wise to sacrifice their prospects for a little silver. Those who can’t see that clearly won’t last long as General Guan’s aides. However, there are indeed some civil officials who, while not after wealth, will act accordingly in the future.”

Ma Duyi stretched lazily, and Gu Can had already handed her a cup of tea.

Over time, having spent day in and day out together, even Ma Duyi no longer felt the slightest awkwardness. As for Zeng Ye, he had long taken the cup of tea Gu Can handed over.

Gu Can smiled, “Everyone’s worked hard.”

Ma Duyi finished her tea in one gulp, rubbing her wrist with enthusiasm, “Finally, we have some leisure time to explore! I plan to visit all the surrounding countries near Shujian Lake! Shihai Kingdom, Meiyou Kingdom, I want to go to all of them!”

Gu Can reminded her, “I’ll give you the Taiping Wushi talisman later. When visiting these vassal states of the Great Li, try to stick close to the main cities where the Great Li garrisons are stationed. If trouble arises, you can seek help. But during normal times, it’s best not to reveal the talisman to avoid attracting hostility from those who’ve lost their kingdoms.”

Ma Duyi rolled her eyes, “You’re being too fussy! Do I need you to teach me these basic things? I’ve been on the road with Mr. Chen long before you!”

Gu Can shrugged, smiling, “Then I’ll head off to rest. Socializing in taverns is exhausting.”

Exiting the small room, Gu Can went to the study on the side of the main house. On the desk lay the ghostly artifact “Underworld” Yama Hall, acquired from the accountant back in the day, along with a replica of the Liuli Pavilion sold by the venerable Yuhai of Qingxia Island to the accountant. Compared to the Underworld, this Liuli Pavilion only had twelve rooms, with eleven filled with resentful spirits, all former cultivators at the fifth realm, now turned into vengeful ghosts, filled with deep attachments. Years had passed, and around half of the rooms were still occupied.

Gu Can sat in a chair, gazing at the Underworld Yama Hall, lost in thought. His mind was as small as a mustard seed, yet as vast as Qingxia Island compared to all of Shujian Lake. Gu Can’s spirit was immersed in it, willing to assist the souls and resentful spirits seeking to leave through the Water-Land Ritual and the Zhou Tian Grand Sacrifice—over two hundred of them. Most were spirits who had achieved their wishes and no longer clung to this life, hoping for rebirth to live differently.

Yet some spirits chose to remain in the Underworld, day after day, year after year, cursing and berating him, the main perpetrator. Many of them also included that accountant in their vile curses.

Despite all this, Gu Can still adhered to his agreement with them, not only refraining from destroying any spirit but also needing to periodically offer them celestial coins to retain some spiritual light, preventing them from becoming vengeful ghosts.

Withdrawing from the Underworld, Gu Can shifted his focus to the Liuli Pavilion, walking through each dark room where nothing was visible. Only when a ferocious spirit stood at the door could Gu Can make eye contact with them.

At that moment, a ghostly figure in snow-white clothing stood stiffly at the doorway. Despite being only a foot apart, she showed no intent to attack.

Before Gu Can took over the Liuli Pavilion, these spirits had made a pact with the accountant, agreeing that if he entered the Liuli Pavilion to seek revenge, he could do so without consequence, but the opportunity was limited to one time.

Back then, none of the eleven spirits chose to attack, but now, two had each made their own requests and decided to leave the mortal realm entirely. One requested that Gu Can promise to care for his family for at least a hundred years, ensuring they would be wealthy and free of calamity. Gu Can agreed. The other requested that Gu Can gift her a direct disciple and a magical artifact, ensuring that the disciple reached the fifth realm and that Gu Can would not interfere with their cultivation, nor harbor any malicious intent. Gu Can also agreed, saying that the artifact must be promised but that he could secretly assist her disciple on their path.

Three others chose to serve Gu Can as ghost generals, essentially becoming lowly deities in Gu Can’s future mountain sect, with their future financial paths and promotions based on their contributions. One of them was the old ghost who had left the Liuli Pavilion early to help Ma Duyi scout for opportunities, and he no longer visited the Liuli Pavilion for cultivation, instead managing the finances for the three of them.

Gu Can withdrew from the Liuli Pavilion, closing his eyes to rest, in a state akin to sleep.

Meanwhile, in the small room, Ma Duyi and Zeng Ye remained seated at the same table.

Ma Duyi was still daydreaming about future travels and considering her current possessions and little savings.

Zeng Ye hesitated, not wanting to leave. 

Ma Duyi asked, “What’s the matter?”

Zeng Ye replied, “What do you plan to do next?”

Ma Duyi frowned, “Isn’t it nice here? This Shujian Lake isn’t what it used to be, a place where life and death were beyond control. Now it has changed, look at how many wild cultivators have become disciples of the Zhenjing Sect. Of course, they’re all high-ranking, mostly from major island families. You, Zeng Ye, a nobody, can’t compare. But if you’re willing to ask Gu Can to help you clear a path, maybe in a few days you could become a ghost cultivator under the Zhenjing Sect. Even if you don’t want to join the Zhenjing Sect, you could just focus on your cultivation. After all, we have a good relationship with the General’s mansion. So Zeng Ye, you’re quite secure in Shujian Lake.”

Zeng Ye lowered his head, “I’m really afraid of Gu Can.”

Ma Duyi laughed, scolding him, “Look at your lack of ambition!”

After Zeng Ye left, Ma Duyi fell into contemplation.

Gu Can was increasingly resembling that accountant, but Ma Duyi was well aware that it was merely a resemblance.

Therefore, in truth, Ma Duyi also feared Gu Can.

At the General’s mansion within the Fan family in Chishui City, General Guan Yiran was still in his study working on official matters when the knock on the door sounded. He closed a confidential document and said, “Come in.”

A military cultivator named Yu Shanfang boldly crossed the threshold, took a chair, slumped back, and burped, “That drink was refreshing! That little brat named Gu, though young, really knows how to drink. He can hold his liquor! Damn it, I ended up in a drink-off with him and two brothers, and we agreed he’d be the one crawling under the table, but before we knew it, the three of us started fighting among ourselves. With nearly twenty people at two tables, only that brat and I managed to stand and leave. That kid even carried a few back to his place.”

Guan Yiran asked, “What do you think of that youth?”

Yu Shanfang replied, “I’ve heard so many rumors about Qingxia Island and that kid, but after a year of interaction, it’s not what I expected!”

Guan Yiran nodded, not saying much more.

Yu Shanfang couldn’t be bothered to think too deeply. His rugged soldier life didn’t allow for many complexities, and with Guan Yiran, a comrade who had been through life and death together for many years, he had little to fear.

Guan Yiran asked, “Yu Shanfang, I plan to get closer to that young man Dong Shuijing from Longquan County. I’m preparing to help him connect with my family to expand some small businesses.”

Yu Shanfang, feeling frustrated, said, “Why tell me this? I can’t be the accountant, nor can I be a guard dog. Let me make it clear, don’t ask me to be Dong Shuijing’s attendant. I’m a proper military cultivator of the Great Li. That clunky talisman armor belongs to my wife. If you dare to make me take it off for some petty fortune, I’ll kick you to death out of spite!”

Guan Yiran maintained a calm expression, “The financial routes below, the grain transport has always been a source of wealth. In the mountains, it’s akin to the celestial ferry service. All secular dynasties with grain transport have officials with considerable authority and reputation. Our Great Li court is about to establish a new office to oversee a ferry route and many docks, and the head will be just one rank below the Minister of Revenue. The court has already begun to fight for positions, and my Guan family has secured three. I can take the lowest position, which is rightfully mine, and no one in the family can object.”

At this point, Guan Yiran asked, “Yu Shanfang, I don’t want you to retire from the battlefield. That would frustrate you to death. I know you too well. I just want to use this opportunity to send you to that new office, so you can be in the open while Dong Shuijing operates in the shadows, helping each other out. You rise in rank and he makes money. Don’t worry; it’s all clean. Just consider it a favor for me.”

Yu Shanfang grumbled, “I’m not interested in any official position, so forget it. Give that opportunity to someone else.”

Guan Yiran asked, “Do you really want to die on the battlefield?”

Yu Shanfang grinned, “There are no death-defying battles now!”

Guan Yiran hesitated a moment, then said cautiously, “The upcoming battlefield is just as dangerous; it’s just not on horseback anymore. I’ll only tell you one thing, which isn’t classified. It’s something I’ve figured out: all military cultivators stationed outside of Great Li are at risk, including me. We could drop dead at any moment for no reason. Especially those near vassal states facing annihilation, the closer you are to the old capital or the fallen celestial peaks, the higher the likelihood of death for military cultivators. I can firmly say that treacherous assassinations will be frequent. Very, very frequent.”

Yu Shanfang replied, “Well, I guess that settles it. Not taking on an official role is the right choice. With your mediocre skills, without me around, wouldn’t you worry about getting stabbed in the back even when going to the toilet?”

Guan Yiran, annoyed, grabbed a bronze paperweight and threw it at him.

Yu Shanfang caught it with a smile, “Thank you for the generous gift, General!”

He leaped up, dashing to the door.

Guan Yiran sat there, irritated, “It’s just a worthless piece worth a couple of taels of silver, and you have the nerve to take it?”

Yu Shanfang stopped, turning back with a disdainful expression, throwing back the bronze paperweight, “You, a Guan family scion from Yizhou, display this shabby object on your table? I almost feel embarrassed for the old master Guan!”

Unexpectedly, Guan Yiran quickly extended his hands to catch it, gently exhaled, and carefully placed it back on the table, grinning, “This is a gift from the Emperor of the Zhu Ying Dynasty’s imperial study, personally given to me by General Su. It’s actually quite valuable.”

As Yu Shanfang opened the door, he turned his back to the future head of the Guan family, raised his arm high, and gave a middle finger before slamming the door behind him.

Guan Yiran shook his head with a smile. When his gaze fell back on the table, his smile faded.

He continued to peruse a lengthy secret report from the Green Wave Pavilion of the Great Li, which was quite rare in the Great Li court. Under the implementation of National Master Cui Zhan, all documents aimed for brevity.

The reason Guan Yiran was able to read this secret report wasn’t because he bore the Guan surname but because he happened to be the military general stationed in Shujian Lake, needing to provide his personal feedback.

This report came from a minor official in the Liu family of Qingluan Kingdom and had significant implications. Just glancing at a few lines made Guan Yiran feel a chill.

It detailed the future strategies concerning Shujian Lake.

Among them was mention of Gu Can, as well as Guan Yiran himself.

An old man quietly descended into the courtyard of the rented house.

Gu Can stored away the Underworld Yama Hall and the replica of the Liuli Pavilion into a bamboo box by his feet. He picked up a bamboo fan crafted from Shenxiao bamboo, tucked it into his waist, and smiled as he opened the main door.

The uninvited guest was none other than his legitimate master.

Rumored to have turned misfortune into fortune while in the water prison, Liu Zhimiao of Qingxia Island now had hopes of breaking through his bottleneck to the Nascent Soul stage.

After Gu Can opened the door, he performed a bow, “Disciple Gu Can pays respects to Master.”

Liu Zhimiao smiled and nodded, “There’s no need for such formality between us.”

The two sat in the main hall, beneath a plaque left by the previous occupants that read, “Eternal Renown.”

The couplets hanging on both sides were also quite old and hadn't been replaced, radiating an antique charm. “Upon opening the door, the mountains and rivers are clear to the eye. When closing the window, moral texts refine the heart.”

Liu Zhimiao surveyed the room, “The place is a bit small, but it’s peaceful.”

Gu Can asked, “Would Master like some wine? There’s no celestial brew here, but I have plenty of a friend’s sweet rice wine. However, you may not be accustomed to such common drinks.”

Liu Zhimiao waved his hand, smiling, “Let’s skip the wine.”

Gu Can refrained from saying more, maintaining a smile as he sat up straight.

Liu Zhimiao asked with a grin, “Master previously went out with a sect reverend and has formed some ties with General Su Gaoshan. Are you considering joining the military to seek a position as a martial officer?”

Gu Can shook his head with a smile, “Disciple wouldn’t waste Master’s offerings.”

Liu Zhimiao didn’t press further but suddenly sighed, “Gu Can, you aren’t even fourteen yet, right?”

Gu Can nodded.

Liu Zhimiao fell into silence for a moment, “If Master successfully breaks through to the upper fifth realm, as a reverend, I can make three requests of the Zhenjing Sect, which was promised by the Sect Leader Jiang long ago. I plan to ask the Zhenjing Sect to grant you the vassal islands including Qingxia Island and Suling Island.”

Gu Can maintained a calm demeanor, not rushing to respond.

Liu Zhimiao continued, “Master considers not only you, my favored disciple, but also has my own selfish motives. I don’t want the incense of the Qingxia lineage to be extinguished. With you at Qingxia Island, the ancestral hall won’t be considered closed. Even if in the end, few remain at Qingxia Island, it doesn’t matter. This way, I, the island master of Qingxia, can wholeheartedly serve Jiang Shangzhen and the Zhenjing Sect.”

Gu Can asked, “What does Master need from disciple? Please speak freely. I won’t say any flowery words like I’ll die without hesitation. What I can do, I will, and will try to do it even better.”

Liu Zhimiao looked pleased, stroking his beard while smiling. After a moment’s thought, he said slowly, “Help the ancestral hall of Qingxia Island branch out. It’s that simple. But let me make it clear beforehand—aside from that true Nascent Soul reverend Li Fuju, I’m not familiar with any other reverends, large or small. I even have potential enemies. Jiang Shangzhen has never truly confided in me. So taking over the ancestral hall of Qingxia Island and several vassal islands isn’t entirely a good thing. You need to weigh the pros and cons carefully. After all, sudden wealth can be deadly. You are the only disciple I regard highly; that’s why I speak frankly with you.”

Gu Can replied, “Then I’ll think it over thoroughly and can give Master a clear answer within three days at the latest.”

Liu Zhimiao nodded, “That’s best. Be cautious; fear of death leads to hesitation, while risking your life for big gains is the foundation of our mountain cultivators.”

Gu Can nodded, “Master’s teachings, I will remember.”

At this point, Gu Can chuckled, “In the past, I thought I understood everything, but really, I understood nothing. I was foolish and ignorant, making a fool of Master.”

Liu Zhimiao laughed, “Those who proudly proclaim they understand everything are usually the least informed. In truth, your actions back then may have seemed reckless, but they weren’t as disgraceful as you thought. As long as you survived, all the hardships you endured are the true foundation of a mountain cultivator. The wisdom of swallowing bitterness is the real understanding.”

Gu Can responded with a hum.

Liu Zhimiao took out an ancient book made of what appeared to be gold and jade, its surface shimmering with light, the title written in four golden ancient characters: “Jiejiang True Scripture.”

Liu Zhimiao extended his fingers, gently pushing the book toward the composed youth in the green robe, speaking in a deep voice, “In the past, the techniques Master taught you were merely the foundational methods of Qingxia Island’s ancestral hall, considered side doors. Only this celestial secret manual is truly the essence of Master’s great path. To be honest, I was once afraid and unwilling to pass this method to you, fearing you would team up with that little mudfish to kill me.”

After presenting the ancient manual he had cherished for hundreds of years, Liu Zhimiao didn’t glance at it again. “Times have changed. If I break through to the upper fifth realm, everything will be easier to discuss. If, unfortunately, I die, there will be no more Liu Zhimiao in this world, and you needn’t worry about settling scores with me.”

Gu Can didn’t reach for the nearly priceless celestial tome but stood up and bowed to Liu Zhimiao once more.

Liu Zhimiao remained seated at the main table, returning the bow from his disciple.

The intricate dynamics of their master-disciple relationship had been filled with schemes over the years.

Tonight, this exchange of a book and bow was quite pure, just the most straightforward transmission of the way in the world of cultivation.

After tonight, the existing complexities of old debts and calculations between master and disciple would likely continue to persist.

Gu Can tucked the celestial manual into his sleeve.

Liu Zhimiao chuckled, “Your senior sister Tian and the other brothers are all increasingly foolish.”

Gu Can smiled, “They brought this misfortune upon themselves; they can’t blame others.”

Liu Zhimiao pondered for a moment, “Go get two jars of wine; let’s chat a bit longer. We can drink and enjoy ourselves, no need to be polite.”

The main door remained open, and moonlight streamed into the room.

Gu Can went to the kitchen, making two trips to bring back two jars of hometown wine gifted by Dong Shuijing, two white bowls, and a few plates of side dishes.

Liu Zhimiao poured a bowl of wine, picked up a crispy dried fish from Shujian Lake, chewed thoughtfully, and took a sip of wine.

This was the flavor of humanity.

Although there was great hope for his breakthrough, and Jiang Shangzhen would spare no effort to assist him, ensuring the Zhenjing Sect would gain another Jade Purity stage reverend, nothing was guaranteed.

This meal under the moonlight might very well be Liu Zhimiao’s last supper in this life.

Liu Zhimiao chuckled, “Back then, the ten heroes of Shujian Lake you stirred up were known by many, but it was really just you nine. I’d wager that even now, few could guess that the last one was that accountant at the gate of Qingxia Island. What a pity; it should have been a grand tale in the making.”

Liu Zhimiao propped one foot on a stool, squinting as he sipped his wine, and started counting with his hand, “The scourge of Qingxia Island, Gu Can; the Lord of Suling Island, Tian Hujun; the fourth senior brother, Qin Jue; the sixth senior brother, Chao Zhe; the young lord of Chishui City, Fan Yan; Lu Caisang of Huangli Island; Yuan Yuan of Guming Island; the exiled prince Han Jingling; and the son of the general, Huang He.”

Liu Zhimiao remarked, “Your senior sister Tian has visited Gongliu Island twice, but I haven’t seen her. The first time she lingered by the border for a day and night, only to return disappointed. The second time, she became increasingly fearful of death and wanted to storm Gongliu Island, risking half her life for a chance at a full one. But alas, as her cold-hearted master, I still didn’t bother to see her. That half-life she risked was wasted. What do you plan to do with her? Will you beat her or kill her?”

Gu Can smiled and said, “Master’s kind intentions are to lead Senior Sister Tian to a dead end, hoping that I, Gu Can, and future Qingxia Island might gain a talented and sensible person.”

Liu Zhimiao replied, “In dealing with Tian Hujun, your previous methods were not bad, but it’s like…”

At this point, Liu Zhimiao pointed at the dishes on the table, “Just drinking without side dishes can make the taste much poorer. It’s easy to say, but hard to do; you can learn from me and my old brother Zhang Ye. This is one of the few good intentions I have. In reality, it’s proven that instead of seeking simplicity with a one-size-fits-all approach, applying benevolence and coercion, tempting with benefits, is essential. The incense of any mountain sect cannot last long.”

Gu Can nodded, “Different people need different incentives, of course, whether it be fame, wealth, magical artifacts, or opportunities for cultivation. Fishing for people’s hearts is a great art.”

Liu Zhimiao laughed heartily, “No wonder I heard that you’ve taken a liking to fishing by the lake, even if the catch isn’t big; you go every time.”

Liu Zhimiao’s joy was not over Gu Can’s seemingly trivial pursuits but because Gu Can had finally learned the art of moderation, understanding the timing of heartfelt exchanges instead of believing that shedding the luxurious dragon-skin robe for a coarse blue robe was enough for everyone to trust that Gu Can had turned over a new leaf and become a kind-hearted youth. If that were the case, it would only indicate that Gu Can had grown since those days, but not by much. He still habitually took others for fools, and where would that lead him?

Fan Yan from Chishui City, acting like a fool, had simply pinpointed Gu Can’s soft spot, and back then, had been able to toy with Gu Can as easily as walking a dog.

Since Liu Zhimiao could offer that “Jiejiang True Scripture,” he could easily take it back at any time.

Thus, Liu Zhimiao would have to put Gu Can to the test regarding his character.

That Tian Hujun, who was destined to be inconsequential, would merely become a side dish on the table tonight.

But the Jiejiang True Monarch wasn’t in a hurry.

This was just the beginning of their drinking.

Liu Zhimiao casually remarked, “Fan Yan has long been the true decision-maker behind the scenes in this Chishui City; you’ve noticed, right?”

Gu Can smiled wryly, “Master, I’m not blind.”

Liu Zhimiao chuckled, “Then have you noticed that Fan Yan already has connections in the court? It’s neither General Guan Yiran, the direct descendant of the old Minister of the Li Department, nor General Su Gaoshan, who was the first to breach the capital of the Zhu Ying Dynasty.”

Gu Can considered, “I’ll just endure him a bit longer.”

He hoped that by then, Fan Yan and his parents would still be alive, preferably in a prosperous and thriving family.

Liu Zhimiao continued, “Yuan Yuan was born with good fortune, as his parents were both Golden Elixirs, and the support of Guming Island. To be precise, it’s Yuan Yuan’s mother’s backing, a Nascent Soul sword cultivator from the Zhu Ying Dynasty. Yet he was chased for thousands of miles by an enigmatic young man in white and Ruan Xiu of Longquan Sword Sect, ultimately being killed near the border. Logically, Guming Island should have perished, but now they’ve secured a reverend from the Zhenjing Sect and even obtained the Taiping Wushi talisman from the Great Li’s court.”

Gu Can didn’t hold much animosity towards this chubby little Yuan Yuan. How clever could a braggart be, flaunting his cunning? 

Guming Island’s opportunism was nothing remarkable; anyone could do it.

As long as this fellow didn’t provoke him again, letting him be a guest of Qingxia Island would pose no problems. 

As for Yuan Yuan’s sneering remarks behind his back, how much weight could those words carry?

Gu Can had heard worse insults throughout his life.

Now, Gu Can wouldn’t be driven to kill out of spite.

At least not for the moment.

And this “moment” might stretch out to be extraordinarily long.

But Gu Can could wait; he had that patience.

For he had learned one truth: when you can only break rules without the power to establish them, you must first adhere to the rules. During this period, not dying after suffering hardships is an invisible gain. Because Gu Can can learn more, every bump and bruise, every wall he hits and closed door he faces, is a lesson about the rules of the world.

Liu Zhimiao said, “Han Jingling, the new emperor of Shihai Kingdom, is truly remarkably fortunate.”

Han Jingling ignored the plight of the commoners under the vassal kings and fled to Shujian Lake. Miraculously, he became a widely praised sage king, donned the dragon robe, and sat on the dragon throne—he probably laughed in his sleep for two years. Meanwhile, the once-promising prince, Han Jingxin, perished in the wilderness beyond the capital, so this new emperor’s position is quite stable. Huang He, who helped elevate Han Jingling to the throne, also isn’t doing too badly. As a young Vice Minister of Rites, he was conferred the title of the new Five Peaks of Shihai Kingdom, accompanying the new emperor everywhere. The Minister of Rites doesn’t even dare to complain, and when he arrives at the office, he even proactively serves tea. Huang He’s father is said to be the one who effectively crowned the emperor, although he isn’t wearing the dragon robe, he certainly can wield a sword in court.

Gu Can smiled, “Good fortune can also be a talent.”

This arrogant kid, Huang He, likely wouldn’t need Gu Can’s intervention; sooner or later, Han Jingling would deal with him in a far more severe manner.

Still, Gu Can hoped to get a hold of Huang He.

Because this was the only one who dared to step onto Qingxia Island and demand entry into that room after Gu Can had fallen into obscurity.

Gu Can was waiting for an opportunity.

And this opportunity had to be reasonable and within the rules.

After Liu Zhimiao finished naming everyone, Gu Can’s general attitude towards each individual was evident to the Jiejiang True Monarch.

He still held grudges.

Yet compared to his earlier recklessness, Gu Can had become clearer-headed. Not only could he endure without a word, but he also seemed to accept his current situation of being under someone else’s roof, bowing to others in all things, with no complaints, rather relishing the experience.

Excellent.

This could lead to living longer and better.

Among the immense hardships and difficulties, those who can endure the most intolerable sufferings will eventually see sweetness. 

This is another form of cultivation.

Liu Zhimiao never worried about Gu Can’s visible path of cultivation being fraught with obstacles.

This kid was a born wild cultivator, and perhaps one that could rival the seasoned Liu from Gongliu Island!

Liu Zhimiao poured himself another bowl of wine, asking, “How will you deal with those resentful spirits and ghosts? If it’s something you can’t speak of, you don’t have to.”

Gu Can had just lifted his wine bowl when he set it down, pausing before shaking his head, “There’s nothing I can’t say. If they die and become ghosts, with their only obsession being revenge, it’s simple. I’ll give them the chance to seek vengeance. You should already know, Master, that Sect Leader Jiang has carved out several islands with continuous mountains and rivers near Yunlou City, intending to hand them over to me, Gu Can. I’ll build a ghost cultivation sect there, where all the resentful spirits can cultivate. Need funds for cultivation? I, Gu Can, will provide! Need secret manuals? I’ll help find suitable ones. Whenever they feel ready for revenge, they just need to let me know. Besides that, for various requests and wishes, I will do as much as I can. I know many of these spirits are waiting for the right price; it’s all fine, as long as they’re willing to speak up.”

Liu Zhimiao suddenly laughed, “If back then, Chen Pingan could have killed you with a punch or a sword, wouldn’t it have been an easier choice for both of you?”

Gu Can lowered his head, lifting his bowl of wine, his wrist hovering, thinking for a moment before expressionlessly saying, “Chen Pingan isn’t that kind of person, and I wouldn’t want to die so early.”

When he lifted his head to drink, the youthful expression had returned to normal.

Liu Zhimiao chuckled dismissively.

In reality, Liu Zhimiao felt turmoil within.

He had no knowledge of the island's fate!

Liu Zhimiao sighed; thus the final test of Gu Can's character had some variables.

However, after weighing his thoughts, Liu Zhimiao still asked, “Where do you think Qingxia Island’s path lies? No rush; drink up and think it over.”

Gu Can set down his wine bowl, wiped his mouth, bent down, and plucked a small dried fish from the banquet table to chew slowly, then began to slowly articulate, “First, I can reach the upper fifth realm. Second, I’ll find a backing from the Great Li, at least a powerful family head from a prominent lineage. Third, through this backing, I’ll meet the Great Li emperor and become a pawn he can use to keep the Zhenjing Sect in check in Shujian Lake.”

Liu Zhimiao’s eyes sparkled, “How about a fourth?”

Gu Can smiled, “Let’s take it slow.”

Liu Zhimiao pressed on, “If you proceed with this plan, won’t it be ungrateful to me, your master, who serves as a reverend in the Zhenjing Sect, and to Jiang Shangzhen, who has given you the islands?”

Gu Can’s demeanor remained calm as he turned to look outside, “The long night stretches on; I can drink several bowls of wine and enjoy many dishes. Today, discussing this matter might seem like an act of ingratitude, but by the time I do this in the future, it may very well be a timely aid. Moreover, in the midst of this speech and action, there are countless dealings to be made. It’s possible that one day I, Gu Can, might just die.”

Liu Zhimiao, who rarely drank much at once but raised his cup frequently, now had only one final bowl of wine left. He downed it in one gulp.

At this juncture, it was no longer a mere exchange of sentiments.

Tonight’s gathering was indeed worth the trip.

Unbeknownst to Gu Can, seeing that Liu Zhimiao had finished his wine and there was no wine jug left, he stood up, took his own jug of wine, and poured another bowl for the elder.

Liu Zhimiao didn’t stop him.

After sitting down, Gu Can lifted what was also his last bowl of wine, saying to the elder, “Let’s discuss matters without sentiment; I, Gu Can, want to thank you, Master, for leading me out of Mud Bottle Lane back then, allowing me the opportunity to do so many things and live to this night to speak so much.”

Liu Zhimiao raised his wine bowl, clinking it with Gu Can’s, and they both drank their wine dry.

Liu Zhimiao stood up, and Gu Can followed suit.

They walked together to the door of the main house, standing shoulder to shoulder. Liu Zhimiao said with a smile, “If youths don’t enjoy themselves and don’t seek pleasures while young, they waste their golden time.”

Gu Can shook his head, “Youth is fleeting; how much time can we have?”

Liu Zhimiao raised an eyebrow, surprised. Turning his head, he smiled, “Have you read quite a bit?”

Gu Can nodded, “I’ve read the reports from the mountains and miscellaneous books from the lower world; I’m willing to read anything. After all, I’ve only attended a few days of school; it’s a bit of a regret. From Mud Bottle Lane to Shujian Lake, I haven’t moved much, so I want to learn more about the world through reports and books.”

Liu Zhimiao glanced at the bamboo fan at Gu Can’s waist, smiling, “That’s a good item.”

Gu Can took the folding fan down, offering it to the elder, his eyes clear, “If Master likes it, take it.”

The moment this item was revealed, it signified that Gu Can had made a decision regarding a certain sacrifice.

Liu Zhimiao waved his hand, “Keep it for yourself. Who gave it to you?”

Gu Can replied, “A friend’s friend.”

A friend’s friend, not his own.

Even if that person was Liu Xianyang.

But Gu Can had never considered Liu Xianyang as a friend.

From childhood, Liu Xianyang was merely that person’s friend. Even Gu Can had to admit that Liu Xianyang was one of the few good-hearted people in his hometown.

But Gu Can would never regard Liu Xianyang as a friend.

He disliked Liu Xianyang’s carefree nature, especially when he made jokes about his mother, which led Gu Can to chase after Liu Xianyang a few times, crying and fighting.

Usually, in the end, Liu Xianyang would laugh and apologize.

Then, the tear-streaked little snot would walk back to Mud Bottle Lane with another person.

As they walked, that little snot would often laugh and shed his worries.

So he, Gu Can, only ever had one friend.

In the past, now, and for his entire life, it would always be so.

But he, Gu Can, would never become someone like that.

Gu Can is Gu Can.

There is only one Gu Can in this world.

Yet he is willing to change his words and actions.

And he learns quickly and adapts well.

Because that person said something when they parted ways.

A tree that stands out in the forest will be felled by the wind, which are two different principles.

Liu Zhimiao finally asked, “Gu Can, do you know what family foundation means?”

Gu Can smiled, “Please enlighten me, Master.”

Liu Zhimiao said, “It’s not the vast wealth of a wealthy merchant, nor the vast fields of a rich family, nor is it the many officials and generals in the bureaucracy, nor is it the clouds of immortals in the mountains.”

Liu Zhimiao only said half of it and still didn’t provide an answer.

Gu Can pondered it over, nodding, “Understood. It’s a family that, after making a grave mistake, can restore itself, not one that vanishes without a trace.”

Liu Zhimiao expressed regret, “I, Liu Zhimiao, was unable to do so. After this calamity, I ended up disappointing Zhang Ye. Even if I miraculously become a Jade Purity cultivator, I am merely a hound for the sect’s ledger.”

Gu Can smiled, “Qingxia Island still has me, Gu Can.”

Liu Zhimiao shook his head, “It’s that Shujian Lake still has you, Gu Can!”

Mountain cultivators, grievances are clearly defined.

Even between master and disciple, it is the same.

Liu Zhimiao vanished, returning to the ancestral hall of the Zhenjing Sect on Gongliu Island, where he began his seclusion.

Gu Can did not sleep all night.

He merely strolled slowly in the small courtyard.

Although Liu Zhimiao had concealed the words and actions within the house, the elder didn’t deliberately hide when he stepped out.

Thus, both Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi naturally learned of the Jiejiang True Monarch’s arrival and departure.

Ma Duyi opened the window, looking around before making eye contact with Gu Can, silently asking if there was trouble.

Gu Can smiled and waved his hand, signaling her not to worry.

As for Zeng Ye, being timid and naive, he remained hidden in the house, feeling anxious to himself.

However, cultivation is a strange matter. Zeng Ye had great foundational skills but Ma Duyi’s aptitude for cultivation was better, while Zeng Ye had better opportunities, and Ma Duyi’s character was evidently more pleasant.

In the end, Zeng Ye was more likely to reach greater heights.

Fortunately, Ma Duyi, who had died once, didn’t care much about these things.

So sometimes, Gu Can envied Zeng Ye’s naïveté and also envied Ma Duyi’s worry-free nature.

Zeng Ye tossed and turned, eventually falling into a deep sleep.

Gu Can sighed; if this Zeng Ye had practiced in the Shujian Lake of the past, even with his current level of cultivation, he would still have walked into a tiger’s den, leaving no bones behind.

Through the various banquets at the General’s mansion, Gu Can had noticed a clue.

The rules of Shujian Lake had been established, and that young general Guan Yiran, destined to come from a wealthy family, had likely received an accounting book in advance because Gu Can felt a sense of familiarity.

Thus, in today’s Shujian Lake, the traces of that accountant from Qingxia Island were everywhere.

Gu Can held the folding fan, gently tapping his shoulder, muttering to himself, “There’s still much to learn.”

This fan crafted from Shenxiao bamboo had inscriptions on both sides.

“Clear Breeze, Bright Moon. Five Thunder Eruptions.”

This should have been personally written by Liu Xianyang, a show of his scholarly pursuits to display to Gu Can.

However, Gu Can had always felt that if Liu Xianyang had gone to the same school as that person, he would have only been left behind, eating dust.

But fate had allowed that person to roam the world, while Liu Xianyang pursued his studies.

Thus, Gu Can had never quite liked this world.

As for that celestial manual hidden in his sleeve, Gu Can had not opened it that night.

Do I, Gu Can, need to rush my cultivation?

At dawn, Gu Can opened the door, sitting on the steps outside. The door gods and spring couplets had been purchased last year.

Once a snot-nosed kid had vowed to hang the spring couplets he wrote on a certain house in Mud Bottle Lane.

At that time, the person must have been very happy, rubbing the snot-nose’s head, saying this year, he’d pay for the spring couplets for both families.

Wasn’t that nonsense?

Ever since that kid became an apprentice at the dragon kiln, the family at the end of Mud Bottle Lane had received spring couplets purchased by him every time.

The poorer people often spent more money on others.

What a strange phenomenon.

How could such people exist in the world?

Gu Can sat at the bottom of the steps, resting his elbow on the step above, quietly waiting for the door of the small family across the way to open.

Because there was a brat over there, who always had two sticky little dragons on his face.

That was why Gu Can chose to rent a house here.

Across the way was a poor family, both parents working to make a living, with a kid who had just started school not long ago. He had an older sister who wasn’t particularly pretty, and her name wasn’t pleasant either. The delicate and shy girl easily blushed and would lower her head and walk quickly whenever she saw him.

Gu Can certainly wouldn’t like such a common girl.

A boisterous child preparing to go to school swaggered out, sniffling upon seeing Gu Can, stepping back two paces, standing on the threshold, “Hey, Gu, what are you looking at? My sister is such a beauty; how could a poor boy like you have eyes for her? I advise you to give up on that thought; you’re not worthy of my sister! I don’t want to call you brother-in-law.”

Gu Can straightened up, gently tapping his knee with the bamboo fan.

The kid couldn’t help but glance at the fan a few more times, jumping down from the threshold to sit beside Gu Can, extending his hand, “Let me play with it.”

Gu Can teased, “Shouldn’t you go study your classics?”

The kid rolled his eyes, “Those classics won’t run away. I’ll go later and tell the teacher my stomach hurts.”

Gu Can squinted, “You better smear some mud on your butt before heading to class, otherwise the teacher won’t believe you.”

The kid pondered for a moment, then suddenly erupted into a curse, “Gu, are you stupid? The teacher won’t beat me; if I dirty my pants and go home, my mom will probably kill me!”

After cursing, the kid asked, “Hey, Gu, can you teach me some fancy words? So I can show off to my two friends.”

Gu Can casually recited, “The old man at the east village guards against the tiger, as the tiger enters his room, he bites its head. The child of the west family doesn’t recognize the tiger, wields a stick to drive it away like it’s a cow.”

The kid fumed, “So many words? I need something shorter, more impactful!”

Gu Can said, “A boy sharpens his knife at night; whoever dares defy me will die standing or kneeling.”

The kid frowned, “That’s too murderous; I’m afraid of getting beaten. But I could say it to those who can’t outrun me.”

Gu Can burst into laughter, slapping the kid’s head, “You’re so clever, just like I was as a child.”

Gu Can stopped laughing, “Forget that nonsense; just forget it after hearing it. I’ll teach you a phrase that has more bravado.”

The kid eagerly nodded, “Hurry up!”

Gu Can said seriously, “Every night, the bed is chilly.”

The kid, blushing with anger, slapped the boy’s shoulder, “You’re the one who wets the bed!”

Gu Can suddenly asked, “By the way, the teacher doesn’t hit you? Don’t you often go home crying, saying that old bastard loves to hit you with the board?”

The kid shrugged, laughing, “You don’t know? We changed to a new teacher at school. The old one was so annoying; he never beat the good students, only targeted us who didn’t study well, beating us like we stole something from his house. I was thinking of growing a bit bigger, not a child anymore, and once I had some strength, I’d secretly beat him up. But now, this new one is great; he never beats anyone and doesn’t even care about us. Life is so comfortable now!”

Gu Can chuckled, “So you like the new teacher better now?”

The kid froze, “Hey, Gu, did you hit your head on the door this morning? Why are you asking such dumb questions? If you were to go to school, wouldn’t you like the new teacher? Now we can mess around as long as we don’t disturb the obedient students. The new teacher never cares about us; he doesn’t even beat or scold us!”

Gu Can leaned back, smiling, “A teacher who only cares for good students can be called a good teacher? What do teachers in this world need to do?”

The kid sighed dramatically, “Gu, your brain is really fried. Actually, I used to want you and my sister to be together, but now I’ve given up. If I don’t study hard, what if one day my brother-in-law isn’t up to par?”

Gu Can smiled, “How do you know you won’t excel in your studies? I think you’re quite clever.”

The kid drooped his head, “Not only the new teacher but the old teacher also said I’m hopeless, just a waste. The old teacher beat me every time he scolded me. He hit me the hardest; I hate him!”

Gu Can ruffled the kid’s hair, “When you grow up, if you see those two teachers on the street, you can ignore the new one. After all, he’s just a hired hand, not really a teacher. But if you run into that old teacher, make sure to call him ‘Sir.’”

The kid suddenly looked up, indignantly retorting, “Why should I!? I won’t!”

Gu Can looked up at the sky, “Just because that teacher still has hope for you.”

The kid was left puzzled, feeling misty after a lengthy pause. He tentatively asked, “Have you been beaten hard by a particularly bad-tempered teacher too?”

Gu Can nodded, softly saying, “But he had a good temper.”

The kid gasped, “How pitiful! You’re not much better off than I am! Hey, I’m better off; the old teacher is no longer around, and the new one doesn’t hit people.”

The kid stood up, wiped his face, secretly rubbed against Gu Can’s shoulder, and fled.

Gu Can turned to look, seeing only the kid’s snot.

Gu Can quietly shook his clothes, dispersing the traces.

He stood up, returned to the house, and closed the door behind him, tucking the folding fan back into his waist.

Many people would die, and inevitably, there would only be more in the future. But the precondition was that Gu Can must first survive, to later use so-called good deeds to accumulate power, complemented by clever methods of managing people’s hearts, and then kill according to the rules. Although it wasn’t particularly satisfying, what else could he say? He did good deeds and killed bad people, and he killed in such a way that even Chen Pingan couldn’t find any fault!

Gu Can leaned against the door.

Yet he felt a bit sorrowful.

Because that snot-nosed kid from Mud Bottle Lane was, in fact, truly dead.

In Chen Pingan’s heart, in Gu Can’s heart, he had died.

But what saddened Gu Can even more was another possibility.

That he had never changed.

But that Chen Pingan was no longer that grass-soled youth from Mud Bottle Lane; he had changed too much.

Regardless of how it turned out, no matter who had changed.

Gu Can.

Can.

That person, so full of hope, the beautiful jade that once shone, was forever lost.

The room sounded with a door opening.

Gu Can instantly removed the folding fan, snapping it open to cover his face.

Moments later, Gu Can closed the fan, his smile radiant, greeting, “Zeng Ye.”

Zeng Ye smiled and scratched his head, responding with a soft “Mm.”

In truth, his forehead and palms were all sweaty.

Gu Can walked into the main room, diving into his studies. 

(End of Chapter)


 ### Chapter 632: The Kites in the Sky Have Their Differences (Part 1)

On Gongliu Island, even at the end of autumn, the willows still swayed gracefully.

This island was the main peak of the True Realm Sect, the very site where the Ancestor Hall was constructed. Throughout this year, the entire area around Shujian Lake, including Gongliu Island, had been bustling with construction. Dust filled the air, blocking out the sun. The affluent True Realm Sect had employed numerous mechanists from the Mohist school and geomancers from the Yin-Yang school to survey the terrain, assess the water routes, and oversee the work of various craftsmen from mountain clans. As the sect leader Jiang Shangzhen put it, "Don’t you dare save on expenses for the immortals! Every tile, every window decoration, and every flowerbed must be the finest on Baoping Continent."

Among those especially skilled in crafting immortal residences were several hundred cultivators, the vast majority hailing from Tongye Continent. Just the cost of transporting them across continents via the intercontinental ferries, coupled with the True Realm Sect's comprehensive takeover of the project, meant that many old sects on the islands of Shujian Lake could go bankrupt overnight due to the amount of celestial money spent.

Thus, all the mountain cultivators on Baoping Continent became aware of a second piece of news: the True Realm Sect was wealthy to an outrageous degree.

The first piece of news, of course, was that the True Realm Sect had three and a half offerings at the upper fifth realm. One was a female sword immortal named Li Cai from the North Julu Continent, who had once hoped to assume the position of sect leader. The second was the elder Liu Lao Cheng from the Yuguizong, and the half offering was the True Monarch of the Jiang River from Qingxia Island.

Now that Liu Zhimo had begun his seclusion to break through, the islands surrounding Gongliu Island had recently been sealed off.

Two individuals strolled slowly along the willow-lined banks: Sect Leader Jiang Shangzhen and Chief Offering Liu Lao Cheng.

Jiang Shangzhen plucked a willow branch and wove it into a ring, placing it on his own head. He smiled and said, "In the past, I was like this. Right, Brother Liu?"

Liu Lao Cheng remained silent.

Jiang Shangzhen was a peculiar kind of hero; his methods were ruthless, adept at concealing daggers beneath his smile. Yet, he placed great importance on rules. This feeling wasn’t conveyed through Jiang Shangzhen’s words, but rather by the fact that this location, chosen by Yuguizong for its sect, was meant to communicate this principle to the sect cultivators. Of course, many of the rules Jiang Shangzhen established were quite unyielding.

As a result, General Guan Yiran of the Great Li Iron Cavalry had negotiated with the True Realm Sect multiple times, while Yuan Ying Offering Li Fuju often had to argue with the general’s office. Both parties would become red-faced, banging the table and glaring at each other. Luckily, they had argued without resorting to violence.

It wasn’t that Li Fuju had a particularly good temper; rather, Jiang Shangzhen had warned this woman, who seemed to represent the True Realm Sect, that her life was of little value—just as the sect’s face was also of little value. In this world, what truly held value was only money.

Jiang Shangzhen’s earlier remark, "In the past, I was like this," meant something rather simple. The fact that he was willing to openly discuss this matter with Liu Lao Cheng indicated that he was aware of Liu’s past entanglements with love and hatred. Jiang Shangzhen reassured Liu that he would not engage in any underhanded actions against him.

Liu Lao Cheng, feeling reassured, did not hold back.

As for Liu Zhimo successfully breaking through, the True Realm Sect's upper fifth realm offerings had dwindled to three.

Because that high-ranking member of the Yuguizong, who had publicly claimed to be in seclusion, or more accurately, the elder from the Tongye Sect, was now dead beyond resurrection.

At the time, they had set up a formation to jointly kill him, but only two had actually made a move.

Liu Lao Cheng and Liu Zhimo had merely acted as anchors, or one could say, they had just watched the performance.

To kill a chicken to scare the monkeys.

Right here on Gongliu Island.

Li Cai and Jiang Shangzhen, one drew a sword from its sheath, the other summoned a willow leaf. That old acquaintance who had brought a heavy treasure from the Tongye Sect to join the Yuguizong, upon seeing Li Cai, didn’t even entertain the thought of perishing with Jiang Shangzhen, the madman. Unfortunately, he failed to escape and thus died.

The fight lacked any dramatic flair; even many cultivators on Gongliu Island merely sensed a momentary change in the atmosphere, and then the world fell silent, the clouds light, and the moon bright.

Jiang Shangzhen suddenly said, "In the future, when encountering the Daoists of the Divine Decree Sect, let our True Realm Sect disciples show some respect. They should act with their tails tucked between their legs. Regardless of right or wrong, as long as there’s a confrontation, if someone dies, the True Realm Sect will treat it as though nothing happened. If someone accidentally kills the opponent, the True Realm Sect will behead this so-called hero and send the head to the Divine Decree Sect as an apology."

Liu Lao Cheng nodded, "Understood."

Jiang Shangzhen smiled, "Are you not quite understanding?"

Liu Lao Cheng shook his head.

It wasn’t difficult to understand.

The taller the tree, the more the wind blows; becoming a target for all.

The True Realm Sect had no connections on Baoping Continent. Although it appeared to be prosperous, it was, in reality, surrounded by enemies, such as the Great Li Song family’s iron cavalry.

However, understanding aside, Jiang Shangzhen, this young sect leader, was willing to bow down to this extent, which Liu Lao Cheng found somewhat admirable.

This master of a vast celestial ground was indeed more unruly than the wild cultivators of the mountains.

Jiang Shangzhen sighed, "My current situation is actually similar to yours and Liu Zhimo’s; we need to grow stronger and accumulate power while making our opponents feel they can control us. What remains unclear is which individual the Great Li Song family will eventually send to hinder our True Realm Sect. The only drawback of Baoping Continent is this: the Song family is the ruler of a continent, a secular dynasty, and they have hopes of completely controlling both the mountains and the world below. If it were Tongye Continent, with the sky high and the emperor small, the cultivators in the mountains would truly be at ease."

Liu Lao Cheng chuckled, "The old Shujian Lake was actually like that too; the kings and nobles of surrounding nations were all on edge."

Jiang Shangzhen shook his head, "Not the same. A place like Shujian Lake, which lacks rules, resembles the barbarous lands of ancient times. With myriad demons running rampant, the gods in the heavens feed on human incense, and the demon races on the ground feed on people, thus the separation of virtue and saintly beings. It’s not just foolish people who are ignorant of their blessings; in fact, almost all of us fall into this category."

Jiang Shangzhen walked slowly, "Today, when our common folk talk about deities, flower spirits, wood charms, strange creatures, and ghostly beings, what are they? They are far removed in the high heavens and in the shadows, in scarcely visited mountains, lakes, and marshes. Even if there are those who live among us, they are still bound by unimaginably complex rules. Thus, we hear the saying that where demons cause trouble, the Heavenly Masters draw their swords. In the urban alleys, there are peach charms, door gods, and ancestral temples filled with incense, where one can pray for blessings and exorcise disasters, and there are opportunities to visit the mountains and seek immortals."

Jiang Shangzhen stopped, looked around, removed the willow ring, and casually tossed it into the lake. "So, if one day we, whether commoners or cultivators, must reverse our positions with them, what kind of situation will that be? Are you afraid? As for me, Jiang Shangzhen, I am afraid."

Liu Lao Cheng replied, "I won’t think about these things."

Jiang Shangzhen nodded, "That’s fine. Because some will think about it. So, you and Liu Zhimo can focus on your own cultivation. Because even if the world turns upside down in the future, you’ll still be able to find refuge and survive. With sufficient cultivation, there will always be an escape route and a way to live. And no matter how bad the world becomes, it seems there will always be someone to cushion the fall for you and Liu Zhimo; you two are born to live a life of comfort. Hmm, just like me, I can make money standing, and I can also make money lying down."

Liu Lao Cheng frowned.

Jiang Shangzhen chuckled, "But what if all the cultivators on the mountain tops think like you, Liu Lao Cheng?"

Liu Lao Cheng shook his head, "They won’t."

Jiang Shangzhen scratched his head, sighing, "So that’s the most interesting part; all the good we take for granted, there’s no need to think too much about it. Those bad things, we grit our teeth and can think about them for a long time."

Liu Lao Cheng was somewhat puzzled, not knowing what this sect leader aimed to convey with these words.

Jiang Shangzhen had already shifted the topic, appearing relaxed, without the unusual tension from before, his steps light. "In martial tales, a hero's friends always do good deeds, and even if they die, they die for a good reason. In tales of gods and spirits, human hearts fluctuate, and ghosts run rampant; there’s always retribution for both good and evil. Liu Lao Cheng, do you read these miscellaneous books?"

Liu Lao Cheng shook his head, "Never."

Jiang Shangzhen laughed, "Then you should read more."

Liu Lao Cheng knew that the sect leader was joking and naturally did not take it seriously.

This sect leader was bored every day; outside of cultivation, he would cast illusions and wander among the four great cities by Shujian Lake. Each time he returned, he would buy some toys for the child of the sword immortal Li Cai, teasing the child and teaching him to walk. Jiang Shangzhen could spend a long time on this, and sometimes even Liu Lao Cheng would feel frustrated, wondering whether it was Jiang Shangzhen’s inscrutable nature that had allowed him to reach his current position or whether it was the change of heart and temperament after ascending that had led him to become the sect leader of the True Realm Sect today.

Jiang Shangzhen approached a ferry dock. "Before Liu Zhimo entered seclusion, he asked me for the old territories, including Qingxia Island and Su Lin Island. He plans to give them to his disciple Gu Can. Little did he know, that territory near Yunlou City was specifically allocated for Gu Can by me. Yet, that young lad dared to accept it after hearing this, truly a case of 'the timid starves, the bold survives.'"

Liu Lao Cheng remarked, "This kid staying at Shujian Lake might be a hidden danger for the True Realm Sect."

Jiang Shangzhen turned his head, a playful smile on his face.

Liu Lao Cheng candidly added, "Naturally, it’s not just about the enmity between me, him, and Qingxia Island. I, Liu Lao Cheng, and the True Realm Sect would not want to see Gu Can quietly rise to power; nurturing a tiger brings disaster, and that is a great taboo."

Not just that.

Jiang Shangzhen laughed, "What do you think Gu Can's greatest support is?"

Liu Lao Cheng replied, "Of course, it’s the Chen Ping’an who is no longer in Shujian Lake, along with the rules he taught him. Guan Yiran, who has a good relationship with Chen Ping’an, or others I may not know, will definitely keep an eye on Gu Can’s every move. This means that Guan Yiran will also be watching me, Liu Zhimo, and the True Realm Sect. Gu Can should have already thought of this."

Regarding the so-called nurturing a tiger that brings disaster, Jiang Shangzhen remained noncommittal.

Although Liu Zhimo's realm was lower than Liu Lao Cheng's, he had often dealt with the Great Li court and had once aspired to be a legitimate ruler of Shujian Lake, so he saw some things more clearly than Liu Lao Cheng. Ultimately, it involved Liu Zhimo's interests, so his thoughts were more elaborate; while Liu Lao Cheng, as a wild cultivator, pursued the Great Dao, his thoughts were naturally purer and less cluttered.

In fact, before Liu Zhimo entered seclusion, he found Gu Can in a humble dwelling in Poolwater City.

Jiang Shangzhen could guess the reason behind it.

To impart knowledge and teachings.

Asking for the territory of Qingxia Island from the True Realm Sect was a means of long-term protection for Gu Can.

Because Liu Zhimo had also guessed Jiang Shangzhen’s long-term plans.

Rather than letting the Great Li Song family support an unknown force against the True Realm Sect, it was better for the True Realm Sect to send suitable candidates right to their doorstep.

For both parties, this was the most sensible choice without "internal strife."

Jiang Shangzhen had strutted into Longquan County twice; those with keen eyes would not fail to notice. This was something Jiang Shangzhen intentionally wanted others to ponder.

The down-and-out Chen Ping’an from Laopo Mountain.

Jiang Shangzhen of the True Realm Sect.

The bridge between them was Qingxia Island and Gu Can.

Thus, the True Realm Sect's true challenges never lay with Gu Can, Shujian Lake, or even the Divine Decree Sect.

But rather, in facing two major forces: one was the Great Li Iron Cavalry swallowing a continent, and then blocking another even greater force.

Only then would it be a critical moment for the True Realm Sect to transition from choice to decision.

However, none of this was known to Liu Lao Cheng or even Liu Zhimo; they were completely in the dark. The vast True Realm Sect stood before the two wild cultivators, and would they ponder deeply about matters seemingly unrelated to them?

Wild cultivators, aside from having some cultivation weight and a slightly larger fist, what else did they understand?

Having endured enough disdain and oppression from celestial lineage cultivators, yet in the end, they foolishly thought that cultivation was everything.

They wouldn't take the time to consider why the Yuguizong had a sect leader about to ascend, or why Jiang Shangzhen could possess the current estate he had. The order of precedence must not be mistaken. The strictly regulated three teachings and hundred schools had all originated from humble beginnings, struggling for survival on the earth. Who hadn’t been a puppet in the hands of deities?

Jiang Shangzhen did not look down on the wild cultivators of the world; in fact, he had spent many years as a wild cultivator during his travels in North Julu Continent, and had done quite well.

Jiang Shangzhen gazed at the rippling waters of Shujian Lake and softly said, "The teachers’ yardsticks are not too many, but too few. They strike too lightly; disciples often have poor memories and forget the beatings. Yet, no one considers whether the teachers have their own worries about daily sustenance, or whether one day, they might simply say they’re disappointed. All those who like to calmly discuss reason, once disappointed, fall into true despair."

Liu Lao Cheng still felt little impact from this.

Jiang Shangzhen suddenly turned and asked, "A sect leader of the upper fifth realm lays bare his heart to you, and you don’t have to listen carefully. What about an immortal?"

Liu Lao Cheng shivered.

Jiang Shangzhen grinned, "Ignorance is no crime, after all, as the sage said, 'To punish without teaching is cruelty.'"

Jiang Shangzhen rubbed his chin, "I originally shouldn’t have revealed the truth to you so early. The mountain treasure I hid on my maid Yaya is the real matter of life and death for you and Liu Zhimo. But I’ve changed my mind. Because I suddenly realized one thing: when reasoning with you wild cultivators, a fist is sufficient. Spending more thought is simply wasting my money."

Not time wasted in making money, but time wasted in spending money.

Liu Lao Cheng's expression remained unchanged, and he did not say another word.

The once familiar deadlock, the long-lost aura of danger.

Jiang Shangzhen sighed, "I always thought that everyone, whether good or bad, whether on the mountain or below, would become smarter once they reached a higher level. But after all these years, I’m quite disappointed. Liu Lao Cheng, if you don’t tighten your grip and truly immerse yourself in your heart, changing some fundamental thoughts and ideas, let alone catching up to me, even Liu Zhimo could leave you behind. Of course, there’s also that Gu Can; it’s only a matter of time. By then, you, the chief offering, would be a huge joke. The future will find Gu Can, who has always been like an ant, could never be killed, and Liu Zhimo would already stand on equal footing with you, while I, Jiang Shangzhen, would need to look up at him."

Jiang Shangzhen raised his hand, shook his sleeve, and casually spun, producing a green water bead condensed from the essence of water transport, then gently pinched it apart with his fingers. "Do you think that the accountant who came to the island to see you back then was looking up at you? No, what he respected and feared was the rules you had amassed at that time. But one day, perhaps not too far in the future, a few decades? A century? You, Liu Lao Cheng, could be standing atop Gongliu Island, yet that person standing at the ferry dock would make you feel shorter."

Liu Lao Cheng said, "I’ve learned a lot."

Jiang Shangzhen laughed, "Indeed, talking with an immortal is much more pleasant to hear. So you need to read more, and I need to cultivate harder."

Liu Lao Cheng let out a sigh.

Jiang Shangzhen inexplicably said, "Perhaps one day, I might return to Tongye Continent to take charge of Yuguizong. Then you would become the next sect leader of the True Realm Sect. As for Liu Zhimo, you could control him at the bottleneck of the upper fifth realm, preventing him from daring to break through to the immortal realm. If you feel good at that time and think he no longer poses a threat, you could generously allow him to ascend, letting him create a branch of the True Realm Sect on Baoping Continent."

Jiang Shangzhen kept his hands tucked in his sleeves. "This isn’t just painting a pie in the sky for you, Liu Lao Cheng; I’m not that lowly."

Liu Lao Cheng seemed to have gained some insight.

Now, the True Realm Sect had dedicated individuals collecting all the news from the mountains and rivers of Tongye Continent. Among them were rumors that the Yuguizong, which held the top position among immortals on Tongye Continent, might already have its sect leader in seclusion.

Pursuing the elusive realm of ascension.

As for the old sect leader Xun Yuan, Liu Lao Cheng was not unfamiliar, having traveled far on Baoping Continent together.

In fact, Liu Lao Cheng was originally appointed as an offering of the True Realm Sect by Xun Yuan.

However, on Jiang Shangzhen's side, this connection held no value whatsoever.

Liu Lao Cheng took a deep breath, feeling the vastness of the world, suddenly filled with ambition. He nodded solemnly, "Then from now on, I, Liu Lao Cheng, will sincerely fight for my True Realm Sect, risking my life!"

Jiang Shangzhen turned his head and gently patted Liu Lao Cheng’s shoulder, "We’re all family here. I may have said some harsh words earlier, so Brother Liu, don’t take offense."

Liu Lao Cheng hesitated for a moment.

Jiang Shangzhen said, "As family, you can certainly speak a few harsh words. Don’t mind it; I am a person who worries about nothing, only that I have too much money."

Liu Lao Cheng replied with a stern face, "Sect Leader Jiang, why are you so insufferable?"

Jiang Shangzhen rubbed his cheek, pondering for a moment, then suddenly realized, "Perhaps it’s because you’re not a woman."

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 633: The Kites in the Sky Have Their Differences (Part Two)

In the country of Qingluan, there was a strikingly handsome young man dressed in white, accompanied by an old man and a child, as they roamed through the picturesque landscapes of the half of the nation.

Previously, this young man had seized an opportunity in the hometown of Liu Laocheng, the only Fifth Stage wild cultivator from Baoping Continent. At the Bee Tail Ferry, he had acquired a deposed national seal from a man whose family had fallen on hard times. However, this seal belonged to the Kingdom of Wenjing, which had not been destroyed under the hooves of the Great Li's iron cavalry, but rather succumbed to the annals of history long before that.

The last prince of Wenjing seemed to have abandoned any thoughts of restoration. After all these years, he still had not descended the mountain, remaining in seclusion to cultivate. As a result, even if remnants of Wenjing's luck still lingered, it was effectively the end of the line for the kingdom. After all, any cultivator at the Fifth Stage could never become an emperor—this was an unbreakable law of the mortal realm.

Besides the low-priced national seal he had acquired, the young man also visited an old apricot tree known by several titles: "Emperor Wood," "Prime Minister Tree," and "General Apricot." He stood there, captivated, squatting at the tree's hollow and muttering to himself for quite some time.

Later on their journey, having obtained the national seal, the young man used the excuse of "collecting for completeness" to visit a certain mountaintop. There, he engaged in a game of chance with an elderly cultivator who walked the path of the dragon. After winning a wager, he raised the stakes again and again, narrowly emerging victorious each time, until finally, he had wagered everything and won the last two seals from a foreigner named Cui. This foreign man, driven by his gambling passion, foolishly declared he would bet his sixteen treasures against the last two seals, and, astonishingly, he won.

Thus, through sheer luck, the young man in white inexplicably acquired the remaining sixteen treasures of the Kingdom of Wenjing. With a swagger, he descended the mountain, stuffing those priceless national seals into a cotton bag, which a frail child was tasked with carrying. As they made their way down, the bag clinked and clanked.

The elderly servant, the Liuli Immortal, felt an uneasy chill as they traveled down. He worried that the protective mountain array would activate at any moment, leading to a chaotic ambush. Of course, who would be attacking whom was hard to say. The old cultivator was concerned that the treasures might misfire, and if Cui Daoshi failed to care for them, he could end up being mistakenly killed. The old cultivator understood well that the only person Cui Daoshi cared for was that muddle-headed child with cloudy eyes.

Fortunately, luck was on their side, and no one attacked them on the way down.

The trio walked quite a distance. They witnessed the so-called iron cavalry of the Kingdom of Yunxiao perform in the capital, enjoyed the Mid-Autumn Festival lantern fair in the capital of the Kingdom of Qingshan, and the old cultivator felt a twinge of regret for missing the emperor's eccentric preference for "plump beauties." Otherwise, it would have been a good opportunity to broaden his horizons. Nevertheless, Cui Daoshi purchased a popular book titled "Qian Ben Cao" (The Book of Money), which wasn't a rare edition but rather a common find in bookstores. He often perused it while walking along the mountain paths, claiming it had a bit of substance.

After crossing the border into Qingluan, Cui Daoshi began to move slower, frequently taking out a national seal and rubbing it against the face of the child he affectionately called "Little Gao."

The Liuli Immortal served as a portly servant, carrying an assortment of goods. Yet, he felt he was luckier than that frequently-mounted "Little Gao," so he often reminded himself to cherish his fortune.

As for Cui Daoshi's whimsical behaviors, the old cultivator had grown quite accustomed to them. For instance, during an encounter with a group of wild cultivators, one of whom was named Lu Yangzhen, they traveled together for a while. The Liuli Immortal couldn't understand what qualifications these mere wild cultivators had to engage in friendly conversation with Cui Daoshi. Eventually, they were granted an opportunity by Cui, who intentionally left behind a chance for them—a rain shelter cave. Accidentally triggering a mechanism inside, one of the array masters was incredibly fortunate, receiving a large stack of talismans known as Huangxi (Yellow Seals). If converted into divine currency, it would amount to a significant fortune, while Lu Yangzhen and his companions also enjoyed considerable gains. Those three must have felt as if they had stepped in dog poop only to discover gold hidden beneath.

As the Liuli Immortal observed the three wild cultivators rejoicing, he hesitantly suggested sharing some divine currency with Cui Daoshi, who unexpectedly accepted it with a look of "pleasant surprise" and "overwhelming gratitude." The Liuli Immortal was left feeling sour.

But what could he do? He decided to not think about it. The Liuli Immortal, a practitioner of the demonic path, had a clear understanding of certain matters.

As for the cosmetics shop in the Kingdom of Yunxiao, where many female cultivators gathered, the young man in white stood at the entrance with his hands on his hips, loudly hawking his divine spring palace illustrations. Naturally, no deals were struck, and he was soon chased down the mountain by a horde of furious female cultivators.

Such events were hardly worth mentioning.

The Liuli Immortal felt that he had made great strides in cultivating his heart along this journey!

Aside from these antics, Cui Daoshi occasionally grew serious, which left the old cultivator in awe. At the Golden Osmanthus Temple, Cui Daoshi sat down with the temple master to discuss the Dao. As their conversation deepened, the old master fell into a state of forgetfulness.

This master, named Zhang Guo, was at the Dragon Gate stage, and it seemed he was on the verge of advancing to the Golden Core stage.

The Liuli Immortal watched with envy.

At the White Water Temple, where water bubbled up from below, Cui Daoshi sat atop a well that had been inexplicably sealed, engaging in discourse with a young monk who preached more outside the temple than inside it.

Both were dressed in white.

One was a Confucian scholar, and the other a monk.

Initially, they debated the saying, "Any deviation from the classics is heresy." The Liuli Immortal found the discussion completely uninteresting.

The child, "Little Gao," squatted by the bamboo gate, listening to the various arguments within, occasionally babbling as he still could not speak properly.

Eventually, the young man in white, sitting cross-legged atop the well blocked by a blue stone, continued to chuckle and share a few Zen sayings: "To sever the tongues of all under heaven, shall we not sit and silence the world's voices? Should we not kick over the lotus seat and smash the Buddha's head?"

With that, he slapped down, shattering the blue stone that sealed the well.

The young man in white hovered above the well, laughing as he asked, "Does the old monk also have a cat's nature, afraid to call out in front of people?"

The white-clad monk lowered his head, clasping his hands together, and softly intoned a prayer.

Cui Daoshi chuckled again, "The Buddhist scriptures are heavy; only those who can carry them can let them go. There are two doors in the West; if you cannot see through them, you cannot open them."

The young monk raised his head, sharing a knowing smile, and slowly said, "A game as brilliant as you, the world is rare; a fool like me, there is none."

At that moment, the Liuli Immortal observed Cui Daoshi, who seemed to have said all he wanted, then jumped down from the well, laughing as he left. He playfully tapped the child's head, and the three departed from the White Water Temple.

As the young man in white swayed his large sleeves, he exclaimed, "If this stubborn stone refuses to nod, buried in the weeds and thorns and never encountering the unexpected, would it not be a great pity?!"

The Liuli Immortal, having not understood a word, feigned comprehension and nodded, "Master, you are indeed knowledgeable; I never thought you also possessed such profound Daoist wisdom and deep Buddhist understanding. You could certainly participate in debates among the Three Teachings!"

The young man in white laughed and scolded, "You speak nonsense!"

The Liuli Immortal felt a bit awkward but still nodded, "The Master is right."

Cui Daoshi turned, "You have quite a good mind; why not stay here and become a monk?"

The Liuli Immortal feigned despair, "I would rather not! I truly lack the aptitude to practice Buddhist teachings! Not even the slightest!"

Afterward, Cui Dongshan, accompanied by the old man and the child, visited the capital of Qingluan.

They met with the master of a small Daoist temple called the White Cloud Temple, which was a secluded place the size of a tofu block, adjacent to shabby alleys where chickens crowed and dogs barked amidst the laughter of children and vendors shouting their wares.

Cui Dongshan stayed there for several days, donating a considerable amount of incense money. Of course, he also borrowed and perused many books, as the temple master had a vast collection. This unremarkable middle-aged Daoist had accumulated nearly a million words of reading notes, which Cui Dongshan read even more. The temple master was generous and did not hoard his knowledge, glad to have someone peruse his works, especially since this foreign youth was a generous patron, ensuring that their White Cloud Temple would not face financial ruin.

On the morning of Cui Dongshan's departure, a young temple boy who had finally enjoyed a few days of heavenly life was genuinely reluctant to see him go, crying and sniffling. Even the temple master felt a twinge of sadness, questioning his own inadequacies as a master.

Cui Dongshan had not gone far when the young temple boy continued to grieve while sweeping the temple, distracted.

Then, seven or eight ox-drawn carts arrived outside the White Cloud Temple, claiming to deliver books.

The carts were filled with various texts from a hundred schools of thought, which were carried into the small temple box by box. The sight left the thin-faced middle-aged temple master utterly dumbfounded.

However, when the last cart unloaded a plaque, the temple master joyfully called over the ecstatic young temple boy to carefully carry it to the study.

The plaque bore two characters, "Zhai Xin" (Auspicious Heart).

After leaving the capital of Qingluan, the Liuli Immortal served as the driver for a horse cart, with Cui Dongshan sitting beside him and the child napping inside the cart.

The old cultivator softly asked, "Master, why do you hold the master of the White Cloud Temple, who is not a cultivator, in such high regard?"

Cui Dongshan waved his arms, one left and one right, one up and one down, as he said, "He is someone like my previous two teachers. In a time of peace, their greatness does not shine; but in tumultuous times, they become..."

The old cultivator waited for further elaboration, but there was only silence.
