Just as he was about to give up on the answer, Cui Dongshan smiled, "The best teachers."

Cui Dongshan paused, then spoke slowly, "Ordinary teachers can help good students improve their studies; slightly better teachers help both good and poor students and are willing to guide people to correct their mistakes and do good. As for the very best teachers, they are those who wish to extend the greatest patience and kindness to great evils that arise from ignorance. Such people, regardless of where they are, their schools and the sound of books are always there. Some may find it noisy, but it doesn't matter; as long as someone can listen, that is sufficient."

Cui Dongshan suddenly stood up, raising his arm high as if holding a wine cup. At that moment, the young man in white stood tall, his spirit soaring, "In this world, there are many rich and indulgent things that everyone desires, and there is nothing wrong with that; it should be so. When thirsty, one can drink water, so help yourself—how delightful and fortunate is that?!"

The Liuli Immortal carefully drove the cart.

Alas.

Cui Daoshi spoke in such a way that left people puzzled.

Suddenly, the old cultivator received a kick from behind, and someone cursed, "Damn it, can’t you say a word of flattery or give a little applause?!"

The old cultivator was startled and hurriedly began drafting a response.

But such words of flattery were not easily conjured, and after such a scare, the Liuli Immortal could not come up with even one suitable compliment.

Fortunately, the person behind had already said, "Forget it; anyway, you won’t have the fortune to visit the Falling Dust Mountain in this lifetime."

The Liuli Immortal then felt a bit lighter.

Around the cart, paper birds folded from colored paper fluttered like real creatures, circling and spiraling around.

These were not the ordinary Yellow Seals that Fifth Stage cultivators purchased with great sums. Instead, they were made from a rare and precious material known as "Clear White Talismans," believed to be special talisman paper used by Daoist sects, extremely rare and expensive.

The old cultivator had some expertise in talismans. 

Therefore, he recognized that the most mysterious talisman paper was a type of blue talisman that contained the true essence of the sages, without a specific name.

Yet, these precious talismans were carelessly used to fold paper birds.

Cui Daoshi—was this appropriate?

It would be nice if you could give me a few as family heirlooms.

The old cultivator sighed deeply within.

Throughout this tumultuous journey, he had not truly gained any benefits; he could only hope that one day in the future, Cui Daoshi would acknowledge that he at least had some share in the labor despite not having any merit.

However, thinking of being a beast of burden lightened his mood a little.

The child in the cart was the true beast of burden.

Cui Dongshan suddenly said, "Let's take a detour; we're not going to the Liu family's Lion Garden. We're going to see a pitiful person."

Then the old cultivator followed the route provided by Cui Dongshan, steadily driving south.

Along the way in the Kingdom of Qingluan, there were many rumors about the Liu family's Lion Garden.

The head of the Liu family, a leader among scholars, had fallen from grace, his reputation tarnished. Once regarded as a national literary treasure, he had become a laughingstock, with his poetry and prose deemed worthless. There were even more scandals pouring down on him, and there was no escape—one of the four private gardens in Qingluan had turned into a den of filth. Various small bookstores in the city were filled with poorly printed scandalous pamphlets, circulating among officials and commoners alike.

Thus, when Liu Qingshan returned from his travels and held a wedding banquet at the Lion Garden, marrying an unknown woman from outside, the old Minister Liu did not see a single familiar face among his friends.

As for the eldest son, Liu Qingfeng, who had "sacrificed family for righteousness," he had long been removed from the Liu family tree. Now, he held a low-ranking position overseeing the transportation of goods, and while he was technically promoted from county magistrate, no one believed he could rise to a prominent position in the esteemed Qingluan Kingdom. It was likely that one day he would lose even his official title, and no one would care to discuss him—he was just another dull joke.

Moreover, the Kingdom of Qingluan was flourishing, its national fortune invigorated.

In the temples, on the mountains, within the martial world, and among scholars, talent was emerging like bamboo shoots after the rain—a magnificent display.

For instance, a six-year-old child had quickly gained fame as a prodigy within a year. During this year's Mid-Autumn Festival, the young prodigy was summoned to the capital by the emperor and empress. The doting empress, upon seeing the child, affectionately held him on her lap, while the emperor personally tested the child's poetry, asking him to compose a poem on the spot. The child, cradled in the empress's embrace, pondered briefly before effortlessly reciting a verse. The emperor was delighted and awarded the child the title of "Da Zhou Zheng" (Official Candidate), which, while not a formal government position, signified an official status. This meant that the child was likely to be the youngest civil official in the history of both the Kingdom of Qingluan and the entire Baoping Continent!

At this moment, as winter approached, atop a bumpy cart along the bank of an incompletely dredged river, the young man in white sat cross-legged, while the child held a kite made from a Qingluan specialty known as a "Muyu" (Wood Kite).

As long as the string remained unbroken, all kites in the world were destined to fly high, yet could not venture far.

Cui Dongshan leaned back, gazing blankly at the kites in the sky.

How is my master doing now?

The reopening of the river transport was an extremely complicated matter, involving many aspects of the Kingdom of Qingluan. Thus, the court did not rush, and progress appeared slow.

The officials overseeing this matter were not of high rank—three in total. Two were low-ranking officials summoned to the capital from the Ministry of Revenue and the Ministry of Works, and the third was a governor from a certain state along the river route. Since the court had not publicized this matter widely, there was little attention to it among the populace. The two court officials seemed more interested in theoretical matters, while the local governor was pragmatic. In reality, the opposite was true; the governor, who had initially thought this would just be a formality, found that the two officials from the capital were already well-prepared, with detailed procedures that bordered on tedious. Even he, an experienced local administrator, felt he had little to contribute, only needing to follow the established process.

In addition to the two officials from the Ministry of Revenue and the Ministry of Works, there was another one—a fifth-rank assistant named Liu Qingfeng.

Governor Hong, who had a disdainful attitude toward this Liu Qingfeng, was quite contemptuous. It was already looked down upon in the martial world to sell friends for profit, and to sell one's father for gain in the officialdom was even more despicable. Governor Hong found it exhausting to discuss matters with such a person, feeling that he would need to change his official robes each day to rid himself of the unpleasantness. Just drinking a cup of tea felt uncomfortable.

For the past six months, Governor Hong had treated Liu Qingfeng with disdain. The two court officials seemed to understand Hong's feelings and deliberately ignored him. As for Liu Qingfeng, he likely pretended to be respectful due to his small official hat and his guilty conscience, seldom speaking unless prompted by the two court officials.

One day, near a section of the river, there was lively entertainment with bamboo horse jumping.

A scholar, who had traversed the old river route twice, sat on a low earthen wall with a teenager named Liu Suo, watching the lively scene of drums and gongs. The bamboo horses, woven from bamboo strips and wrapped in colorful cloth, were tied at the waist of the performers. According to local customs, specific colors were designated for different participants—red for the groom, yellow for the young men, green for the girls, white for the scholars, and black for the warriors, each with its own meaning.

The scholar had completely lost the appearance of an official; his skin was tanned and shiny, wearing rough hemp clothing, save for a sturdy but worn pair of deer-hide boots that were not typical for common villagers.

Not every village hosted bamboo horse performances; it depended on which village had the funds. The more money spent, the better the performance would be.

This village clearly had invested quite a bit, making their bamboo horse performance particularly spectacular.

Nearby the wall, there were many young men from other villages who had come to enjoy the show, pointing at the girls from the wealthy village and making crude remarks about which maiden would surely develop a fuller figure in the future. The atmosphere was filled with laughter and banter, with discussions over which girl was the most beautiful in the area, as everyone had their own opinions.

The scholar watched the girls they pointed out without hiding his gaze, making the young servant beside him feel somewhat helpless. "Master, why are you behaving so indiscreetly?"

The scholar smiled, "The essence of a woman lies in her complexion; it's the white ones that are hardest to find. Actually, size doesn't matter."

The servant replied helplessly, "If you say so, Master."

The scholar chuckled, "You're still young; you'll understand in the future. A woman's face is not the most important; a good figure is what truly matters."

The servant rolled his eyes, "Master, what does that have to do with me? I haven't read many books yet, and I still have to take the examinations to become an official like you."

The scholar nodded, "You're a seed of knowledge; you will surely become an official one day."

The servant's spirits lifted instantly. 

Whatever Master said was authoritative!

In the distance, cheers and applause erupted from the bamboo horse performance.

Yet around them, there were also many onlookers who were scrutinizing the performers with skepticism, and more than a few scoffed, their applause sparse.

The servant softly asked, "Master, since you are so knowledgeable about the origins of the bamboo horse performances, can you tell me if they really aren't performing well? I think they’re quite good."

Liu Qingfeng replied softly, "Of course, they are good. But since we aren't paying, why should we say so? In this world, good things always come at a cost."

The servant was puzzled, "What does that mean?"

Liu Qingfeng smiled faintly, saying no more, and patted the boy's head, "Don't overthink these things; you are in the prime of your studies."

The servant nodded, then recalled something and curiously asked, "Why has Master only been looking into the historical records of the Ministry of Revenue's taxation lately?"

The boy didn't yet understand that these were not records accessible to a mere official like his master, but documents secretly delivered to his desk.

Liu Qingfeng spoke quietly, "When reviewing history, it’s always written by later emperors about the affairs of previous dynasties, which inevitably distorts the truth. However, the matter of money—its inflow and outflow—remains untainted. So, when we read history, we must examine the biographies of those who had control over finances throughout the ages, as well as the processes by which they minted and distributed various coins. By centering on an individual and expanding from there, it will be easier to see the successes and failures of national policies."

The servant scratched his head.

Liu Qingfeng gazed at the distant commotion, smiling, "You need not hurry; whenever you wish to read, I have plenty here."

Seeing his master in a talkative mood today made the servant happy since the grueling inspections along the river had drained him, and at that time, his master had not been very chatty, merely taking notes while observing the indistinct mountains and waters.

Taking advantage of his master's willingness to converse, the servant asked, "Master, why is it that whenever you arrive at a place, you always take a moment to speak with the local scholars and teachers?"

Liu Qingfeng replied, "Where do the seeds of knowledge come from? After one’s parents, it is the teachers. How could this not be a matter of great importance for us scholars? Is it possible for learned individuals to just fall from the sky?"

The servant nodded, "That makes sense, Master."

Liu Qingfeng smiled slightly, "This is something you should start pondering now."

The servant replied eagerly, "Certainly!"

Suddenly, a group of young men came rushing over, pushing their way toward the prime viewing spot where Liu Qingfeng and the servant sat. One of them jumped onto the wall, shouting, "Get lost!"

The young servant's face flushed with anger.

However, Liu Qingfeng had already stood up without saying a word and silently jumped down from the low wall. The boy had no choice but to follow suit, moving to another vantage point to watch the bamboo horse performance, but from that distance, it was harder to see.

This left the boy feeling quite upset.

His master was great in every way, but his overly accommodating nature was a flaw.

"Not arguing with those who spread rumors means in the end, you become one of them."

Liu Qingfeng chuckled, "Do not contend with false gentlemen over fame; do not compete with true villains for profit; do not argue with stubborn individuals over reason; do not vie with commoners for bravery; do not compete with resentful scholars for talent. Do not offer kindness to foolish people."

This was about not contending.

Yet there was also an art to contention.

However, Liu Qingfeng felt it would be better to discuss this with the boy later.

The young scholar, not focusing on his studies and merely contemplating grand principles, would not find it beneficial.

He just needed to avoid making major mistakes.

The young Liu Suo mustered his courage, rebelling for the first time against his all-knowing master, "If we don't contend for anything, then won't we end up with nothing? That seems like a huge loss! How can living mean stepping back at every turn? I think that's not good!"

Liu Qingfeng smiled, "Think it over again."

Liu Suo shook his head, "I just can’t understand."

Liu Qingfeng withdrew his gaze and turned to the boy, teasing, "With such foolishness, how can you be my servant?"

Liu Suo laughed sheepishly.

Liu Qingfeng suddenly said, "Let's go."

Liu Suo followed his master as they departed.

Liu Qingfeng walked slowly, contemplating matters of both minor and major significance.

Young Liu Suo originally had more questions, but upon seeing his master's demeanor, he understood he should not disturb him.

Li Baozhen's actions were for Liu Qingfeng merely a matter of observation.

Li Baozhen's ambition could be said to be considerable, though not small.

As one of the key figures among the spies of the Southern Green Wave Pavilion of the Great Li, he was attempting a careful strategy from the ground up, manipulating the chess pieces of scholars, martial heroes, and officials from the moment he entered the Kingdom of Qingluan. All were now effectively his pawns, and most were still young and ignorant, like the prodigious child awarded the title "Da Zhou Zheng."

At first glance, this might seem improper and reek of conspiracy, appearing ominous and threatening. However, it was not entirely so.

Li Baozhen was building a structure, with his first objective not to become the hidden emperor of the Kingdom of Qingluan, but to one day control the fates of even the immortals on the mountains through the secular dynasty. The reasoning was simple: even the seeds of cultivation had been sent to the mountains by Li Baozhen and the Great Li court. Year after year, as those seeds matured into founding ancestors or pillars of various sects, it would become quite easy to discuss the rules of the mortal world.

During this time, the great general of the Kingdom of Qingluan, Wei Liang, observed coldly from the sidelines, occasionally establishing rules that even Li Baozhen himself had to abide by.

Liu Qingfeng saw through Li Baozhen’s plans—from his intentions to his methods, he understood them clearly. To speak bluntly, either they were ideas Liu Qingfeng had discarded, or he had purposely left them for Li Baozhen.

For example, since the beginning of this year, several notable literary figures in the Kingdom of Qingluan had fallen from grace.

How to proceed? It was still the three tactics Liu Qingfeng had taught Li Baozhen back in the day: first, to praise them, declaring their poems and writings to be as commendable as those of the sages, lifting their personal integrity to the level of moral saints.

Then, someone would voice an opinion of moderation, quietly building momentum to lead public opinion in the literary sphere, causing neutral parties to grow increasingly weary of these so-called moral saints, whom they themselves found absurd.

Finally, it became simpler: "Aren't you flawless moral saints?" Then, using casually spoken words, they would fabricate accusations of personal faults against these figures. At this point, it would be the turn of the martial world and the marketplace to act. Traveling storytellers and booksellers would take turns stepping up, not to mention Li Baozhen’s carefully cultivated group of “imperial” writers, who would start expressing their indignation and taking up the righteous cause. In the end, one by one, they would be ruined, and the public, who had unknowingly stoked the flames, would hardly care for the truth. There might be a few who did, but they would be few and far between; most were just there for the spectacle. Just like Liu Qingfeng today, watching the lively bamboo horse performance from a distance.

Why expect those who already sought entertainment from a spectacle to think deeply?

Liu Qingfeng would not.

Moreover, there has never been a lively event that did not come to an end.

After the clamor, only silence remained.

This had always been the case.

Liu Qingfeng smiled to himself, "I’ve made a good start."

Furthermore, Li Baozhen was clever and easily drew inferences from one example to another.

Liu Qingfeng suddenly halted and said to the boy beside him, "Liu Suo, remember this: if one day someone tries to persuade you to harm me, whether as a long-term hidden pawn or in a rushed assassination, you must nod in agreement. Not only that, you must give it your all without hesitation or mercy."

The young servant's face turned pale.

His mind went blank.

He couldn’t understand why his master would say such frightening things.

Liu Qingfeng maintained his usual demeanor, speaking softly, "Because you will definitely fail. Keeping you by my side is, in fact, a way to harm you, so I must save you once. I don't want you to die in vain because of some so-called principles. During this time, how much you learn from me, how many connections you accumulate, and where you ultimately end up are all up to your own abilities. As for why I would keep you around knowing this, it is because I want to see if you can become a second Li Baozhen, only smarter—smart enough to genuinely benefit the world."

The young servant's face was drenched in tears, frightened by the unfamiliar nature of his master.

Liu Qingfeng gently asked, "Do you remember?"

The boy wiped his tears and nodded.

Liu Qingfeng smiled, "Very good. Now, from this moment on, you should try to forget all of this. Otherwise, you won't be able to deceive Li Baozhen."

Moments later, Liu Qingfeng was surprisingly astonished.

A young man in white was approaching him, but the personal guard sent from the Great Li had not shown himself at all.

That young man held a kite in his hand, his smile bright, "Liu Qingfeng, I'm here to dig my own foundation with a little shovel. You’ve been mingling with that old bastard, and it leads nowhere. Come follow me, Cui Dongshan. Besides, what is mine is mine, and his is still mine—no need to be polite. In the entire southern part of Baoping, I am the biggest; that old bastard has no authority over me!"

Liu Qingfeng laughed, "That seems a bit difficult."

Given the young man's hidden identity, Liu Qingfeng could access all the intelligence of the Green Wave Pavilion, allowing him to guess some things. Even if it was just a superficial identity, it was still sufficient for the young man to boldly spout such rebellious words.

Cui Dongshan tossed the kite he held to Liu Qingfeng, who caught it and looked down to find there was no string attached, prompting laughter.

Liu Qingfeng raised his head, shaking his head, "You should know that my aspirations do not lie here. The pursuit of self-preservation and material freedom has never been the goal of scholars like us."

Cui Dongshan strode forward, tilting his head and extending his hand, "Then give it back to me."

Liu Qingfeng smiled, "Of course, if someone gives it to me for free, that’s even better. I’ll keep it without returning it."

Cui Dongshan grinned, "Liu Qingfeng, if you keep satisfying my tastes like this, I might just have to help my master take disciples!"

Liu Qingfeng inquired with a smile, "I wonder who your master is?"

Cui Dongshan stood still, his feet unmoving, shoulders bobbing playfully as he mischievously grinned, "You've already met him."

Liu Qingfeng pondered for a moment, "I can’t guess."

Cui Dongshan burst into laughter, "To show my sincerity, I won’t keep you in suspense. My master is the very person who caused your cart to fall into the water back then."

Liu Qingfeng froze for a moment before tentatively asking, "Chen Pingan?"

Cui Dongshan was momentarily stunned, then in an instant, he jumped in front of Liu Qingfeng, lightly slapping the latter on the head with a loud smack, nearly causing Liu Qingfeng to stumble, as he angrily scolded, "You little brat dare to call out my master's name directly?!" 

---

*End of Chapter*

 ### Chapter 634: The Land of One Continent Awakens to Sword

Two Daoists, one old and one young, were bound by local customs to travel on foot. The elder Daoist was no exception as he walked alongside his disciple by the banks of the Great River. The young Daoist, Zhang Shanfeng, was wide-eyed with wonder.

The Chen family of Yingyin truly deserved their reputation as the singular embodiment of "scholarly elegance." They were indeed the pinnacle of scholarly families in the realm. It wasn’t that they couldn’t hire a carriage to reach the Chen family shrine; rather, they were financially constrained. Even if Zhang Shanfeng consented, his pockets didn’t allow for it.

Fortunately, Zhang Shanfeng was used to traversing the rivers and mountains, and though he felt guilty for making his master endure hardship, it was clear that his master’s cultivation might not be high, but he had long since attained the practice of fasting, making the hundreds of miles not too difficult to travel. Still, a disciple should show filial piety, right? Each time he turned back, he found his master walking along, dozing like a chick pecking at rice, which made Zhang Shanfeng admire him. His master could sleep even while walking.

As they passed a blue stone cliff by the riverbank, Zhang Shanfeng spotted a young scholar in a Confucian robe, sitting with his back turned to them, lost in thought.

The Fire Dragon True Man opened his eyes and smiled, saying, “Ah, another who loves to sleep. Surely he will amount to something great.”

Zhang Shanfeng replied with a hint of grievance, “Master, when I first ascended the mountain, I was young and loved to sleep. Why didn’t you say the same about me? Why does my senior brother always use a chicken feather as a command to get me up for practice? Senior Brother Xiangzhi always claims he has the same talent as I do, saying it would be a great pity if I were to slack off in my cultivation. So even if you didn’t care, he couldn’t just let me waste my chance at cultivation on the mountain. In the end, I found out that Senior Brother Xiangzhi was actually only at the cave dwelling level. Whenever he spoke, he always carried such an air of authority, making me think he was a true Golden Core Earth Immortal. So, when he passed away, I cried terribly—not just because I couldn’t bear to part with Senior Brother Xiangzhi, but because I was somewhat disappointed in myself, feeling I was both foolish and lazy, destined to never reach the cave dwelling level in this life.”

The Fire Dragon True Man chuckled, “How could the teachings of a master turn into chicken feathers? Besides, what makes the cave dwelling level so low?”

Outside of Padi Peak, under the Fire Dragon True Man were the four main branches: Taixia, Taoshan, Baiyun, and Zhixuan. Even though the Fire Dragon True Man never set strict rules for the mountain, allowing any disciple to roam freely, the great cultivators of Taixia, including Lady Li Yu, forbade disciples from disturbing the True Man's sleep at Padi Peak. The disciples of Padi Peak were notorious for being reclusive and, indeed, their cultivation levels were not high.

Thus, disciples from the other branches, regardless of their seniority, primarily remembered their elders at Padi Peak as merely high-ranked with low skill levels.

During this time, Zhang Shanfeng had been the most deceived among the disciples of Padi Peak. Perhaps in the eyes of the great cultivators like Lady Li Yu, this little junior brother was as oblivious as one could be under the lamp, but seeing how well his master got along with him, they didn’t dare to intervene.

What’s more, back when Zhang Shanfeng boldly declared he would descend the mountain to slay demons and remove evil, his master, the Fire Dragon True Man, had played a trick on him, suggesting that since he was going down for experience, he might as well go far because there were no demons plaguing Padi Peak.

As a result, when Zhang Shanfeng left, he not only distanced himself from Padi Peak but eventually traveled far away to Baoping Continent. At that time, while Lady Li Yu was in seclusion, the founding ancestors of Taoshan, Baiyun, and Zhixuan grew somewhat anxious, fearing that their junior brother might stray too far from their mountain, leading to unforeseen accidents. Especially for the ancestor of Zhixuan Peak, whose combat strength could match that of an Earth Immortal, they hoped the master would permit him to leave Beijulu Continent to secretly protect Zhang Shanfeng. However, the Fire Dragon True Man did not agree, stating, "Cultivators should focus on their own practice; having someone guard them leads to nothing."

The founding ancestors felt somewhat uneasy but had always obeyed the master's words as law and did not dare to defy him. However, the ancestor of Baiyun, along with the other two masters, privately discussed the matter and believed that their master was not attentive enough toward the junior brother. Thus, they felt it was their responsibility to protect the path. The old Daoist then concocted a plausible excuse and went down the mountain to quietly escort Zhang Shanfeng for a while.

Hence, the dangers Zhang Shanfeng faced while slaying demons and the frustrations that followed were well known to the ancestor of Baiyun, and it implied that the other two ancestors understood as well. Especially when the ancestor of Zhixuan learned that Zhang Shanfeng had boarded the ferry to Daijiao Mountain with a heavy heart, the ancestor of Taoshan calculated and was shocked. He couldn’t help but decide that even if the master forbade him from following, he would let the Zhixuan Peak junior brother carry a sword down the mountain to protect his little junior brother. But unexpectedly, the Fire Dragon True Man suddenly appeared and stopped them. When the Zhixuan ancestor tried to argue, he was pushed back into his secluded cave by the master's hand. When the Fire Dragon True Man turned and smiled at the direct disciple of the Taoshan branch, the latter immediately said there was no need to trouble the master and returned to the mountain to enter seclusion.

Later on, the Baiyun ancestor received a message from the ancestor of Padi Peak via flying sword and promptly returned to Padi Peak, inevitably receiving a scolding.

However, when he left Padi Peak, he wore a joyous expression, while the two junior brothers of Taoshan and Zhixuan learned that their master had scolded their senior brother and then rewarded him with a date to eat.

In the end, everything was within the master’s calculations; it was merely a matter of who had the courage to care more for the little junior brother and dared to take the risk of being held accountable by the master, resolutely descending the mountain to escort him. Both were high-level individuals and quickly understood everything, leading the Zhixuan ancestor to chase after the Baiyun branch's senior brother, wanting to spar. Unfortunately, their senior brother escaped quickly, leaving no chance for his junior brother to vent his frustration.

Upon reaching the blue stone cliff by the river, they were already nearing the Chen family. A distance of several dozen miles wasn’t too long for cultivators. Even without riding the wind, they were only a few steps away in spirit.

Zhang Shanfeng spoke up, “Master, although we were invited this time, we still need to observe the proper etiquette when visiting. Let's not emulate that time at the Middle Land’s Shenze, where we just stomped our feet to greet the host without waiting for them to come out to meet us.”

The Fire Dragon True Man nodded with a smile, “Alright.”

Zhang Shanfeng asked with concern, “Will the books we bought from the bookstore truly not offend the scholars?”

The Fire Dragon True Man shook his head, “Giving books to scholars is the greatest courtesy in the world.”

Zhang Shanfeng felt somewhat reassured.

In truth, the young Daoist still had no idea who they were about to meet.

Zhang Shanfeng recalled something, “Master, as cultivators, we embrace the mountains and waters, cleansing our hearts with spiritual energy and distancing ourselves from the mundane. We do not visit kings or bow to emperors. But how do Confucian disciples cultivate? Is it truly solely through studying? If studying alone could lead to enlightenment, wouldn’t that mean everyone in the world could cultivate? If someone were to secretly transport the vast teachings of the world to other realms, especially to that wild land, wouldn’t it lead to disaster, with an influx of demon cultivators? What would happen then?”

The Fire Dragon True Man chuckled, “That is indeed an excellent question. However, it is not something an old Daoist like me should answer, or else it would truly be lacking in decorum, right?”

Zhang Shanfeng suddenly felt a refreshing breeze and turned to see an old scholar in a green robe approaching, smiling and nodding, “Before answering your question, I’d like to know what books you’ve brought for me?”

The Fire Dragon True Man patted his disciple’s shoulder, “Shanfeng, do you see? Someone is asking you for a gift.”

Zhang Shanfeng quickly bowed and addressed the old man as “Mr. Chen,” then unwrapped his bundle and took out three books.

The old man received them and glanced at them with some reluctance. After thanking the young Daoist, he tucked them into his sleeve.

Chen Chunan was regarded by the world as the foremost disciple of the Sub-Sage lineage.

Ironically, this outsider, the Great Celestial Master from Longhu Mountain, had gifted him three books that were supposed to be banned and destroyed by the Confucian School.

After accepting the books, Chen Chunan said, “Confucian disciples actually follow a cultivation path quite similar to that of Daoists, just with the added nurturing of the righteous qi within the heart. You embrace the mountains and waters, distancing yourselves from the world to create a pure realm free from the dust of both self and others. As for us scholars, we merely ‘read behind closed doors as if in a deep mountain.’ Regarding the places of cultivation and methods, they are akin to study rooms and the writings of sages, along with the principles contained within the texts. However, there are certainly thresholds; not everyone can cultivate simply by reading. For instance, the foundational breath control methods must be taught by virtuous gentlemen to the Confucian students. As for the innate roots of cultivation, that is another threshold. Therefore, many eloquent literati and seasoned scholars still cannot extend their lives simply by reading.”

Zhang Shanfeng found this explanation quite profound but still bowed and said, “Thank you, sir, for the clarification.”

Chen Chunan smiled, “There’s no need for excessive decorum. Scholars study, and cultivators cultivate; we are all kindred spirits. The essence of etiquette lies in its simplicity, not in its complexity.”

In truth, Chen Chunan was well aware of Zhang Shanfeng’s last question but deliberately chose not to reveal the answer.

Contrary to what the young Daoist thought, Confucianism never prohibited the existence of sentient beings in the world from studying and cultivating.

This was a rule set forth by the Sage of Rites.

Zhang Shanfeng turned to look at his master.

The Fire Dragon True Man chuckled, “What’s wrong? Just because you happened to encounter an imagined transcendent figure, you’re now finding fault with your own master for lacking a celestial demeanor?”

Zhang Shanfeng blinked, somewhat taken aback. This was something his master had said himself; he hadn’t thought that way.

The Fire Dragon True Man pointed to the not-so-far-off blue stone cliff, “Is that the kid who practices swordplay in his dreams?”

Chen Chunan nodded, “It’s a pity I’ll have to return it to Baoping Continent later. I’m somewhat reluctant. Over the years, I’ve often chatted with him here, and it seems I won’t have the chance anymore.”

The Fire Dragon True Man said to Zhang Shanfeng, “That person is the best friend of Chen Ping’an. Aren’t you going to say hello?”

Zhang Shanfeng was momentarily stunned, then bid farewell to his master and the old gentleman before rushing over.

The Fire Dragon True Man and Chen Chunan didn’t head toward the Chen family shrine but instead strolled leisurely along the riverside. The old master said, “At least you’re here on Nanposao Continent. What about the other southeastern Tongye Continent and southwestern Fuyiao Continent?”

Chen Chunan remained silent for a long time.

It was a somewhat strange question.

If the demon race from the wild land truly broke through the Sword Qi Great Wall, flooding like a tide and submerging the greatest mountain seal in the world, the Upside Down Mountain…

Then could Chen Chunan defend the Nanposao Continent, which was closest to Upside Down Mountain? It was uncertain. What relation did he have with Tongye and Fuyiao Continent?

Chen Chunan smiled, “The old scholar once advised me, which amounted to two choices: either don’t die or die early, so as not to die at an inopportune moment.”

The Fire Dragon True Man lamented, “The former Sage views the hearts of men, and there are none like it in the world.”

Although the Fire Dragon True Man was much older than that old scholar, he still sincerely regarded him as a senior.

Chen Chunan nodded.

He didn’t refute.

Even though he was the backbone of the Sub-Sage lineage, his own understanding was fundamentally at odds with that advocated by the old scholar.

In the world of Haoran, the contention of the sages regarding the direction of the Dao ultimately hinges on who’s great path better protects the common people and benefits society.

The contention of gentlemen is about clear distinctions of right and wrong, striving to establish a definite truth.

The contention of wise men merely concerns the temporary merits and flaws of their own knowledge, disputing on paper.

The intricate rules of Confucianism serve as the greatest protector of the realm of Haoran.

Yet the confinement of each Confucian Sage is the most binding action in the world.

That individual in the southern end of Baoping Continent, who was personally punished heavily by the Sub-Sage and regarded by the myriad cultivators as one of the seventy-two sacrificed sages who lost their chance to enjoy cold pig head meat, had also, in the matter of knowledge, led the Confucian disciples of different sects and academies across the continents to great benefits, thus enabling the wise to rise to the ranks of gentlemen. Despite his deep-seated animosity towards the old scholar, who was not a disciple of his, the old scholar still acknowledged the excellence of that individual’s knowledge, seeing the potential merits of it for the current world.

Time passes endlessly, indifferent to night and day, as it has since ancient times.

Two long-separated elders discussed the greatest matters in the world.

Meanwhile, two young men on the blue stone cliff found a common language, talking about trivial matters.

The young scholar dozing at the cliff was Liu Xianyang, who had been brought to Posa Continent from Baoping Continent by Chen Ping’an.

Upon learning that the young Daoist named Zhang Shanfeng was a close friend of Chen Ping’an, Liu Xianyang became quite happy and began to inquire about the sights and experiences from their travels.

Liu Xianyang knew some insider information about Baoping Continent, the Great Li Iron Cavalry, and the Li Zhu Cave Heaven, but not much, as he could only glean bits and pieces from the Mountain Water Gazette. He had no one to rely on while studying away from home, needing to be frugal. In the Yingyin Chen family, all books, no matter how rare or expensive, could be freely browsed by students, but the Mountain Water Gazette required payment. Fortunately, Liu Xianyang had made friends with a few disciples of the Chen family and scholars from the academy, allowing him to learn about affairs from other continents through them.

Compared to the tall, bright young man from the small town of years past, Liu Xianyang had become increasingly composed and introspective, diligent in his studies and rigorous in his academic pursuits, quietly cultivating without any laxity, increasingly aligning with the scholarly family tradition of the Chen family and the landscapes around him.

Conversely, the boy from Mud Bottle Alley, Liu Xianyang's best friend, was in pursuit of his own freedom of mind, having achieved what he sought.

Zhang Shanfeng poured out his admiration for Chen Ping’an.

For the young Daoist of Padi Peak, even if he found out he had missed the Great Celestial Master from Longhu Mountain, he might feel some regret, but he wouldn’t be too heartbroken. More so, he’d just think his master was foolish. Did he, Zhang Shanfeng, really dare to reach for the Great Celestial Master’s title? He wouldn’t even dare to think about it.

Even upon learning of that inexplicable loss, Zhang Shanfeng wouldn’t be too disturbed.

This might just be one of Zhang Shanfeng’s most unrecognized virtues.

Even more so than his belief that his master’s Daoist skills were mediocre at best.

However, when Zhang Shanfeng spoke of his parting with Chen Ping’an, he genuinely felt a pang of sadness.

Zhang Shanfeng took the ancient sword he had been carrying on his back and handed it to Liu Xianyang, a newfound friend, with a bright smile, “This is the sword that Chen Ping’an bought at Qingfu Workshop, called ‘Zhenwu.’ The previous armor charm that could transform into a rain of sweet dew was also on credit; I owe Chen Ping’an quite a bit. But now my master has helped me obtain two vials of water elixirs from the Shenze side. In the future, whenever I get the chance, I can give them to Chen Ping’an as repayment of my debt.”

Liu Xianyang slowly unsheathed the sword, noticing its fine cracks and rust. 

He flicked the blade with his fingers, producing a soft, resonant sound, nodding, “It’s very heavy.”

Zhang Shanfeng was puzzled, “This sword isn’t that heavy, is it?”

Liu Xianyang squinted, observing the subtle ripples along the blade, sensing the underlying mysteries within it. This had nothing to do with Liu Xianyang’s cultivation level; in fact, he had experienced numerous absurd battlefields in his dreams, witnessing countless fine swords—many were easily unsheathed, while others he couldn’t lift even if they were broken. However, Liu Xianyang had grown accustomed to remembering the names of those swords, their scabbard designs, and the patterns of sword energy they emitted, carefully feeling the differences in sword intent of each.

The more mysterious aspect was that he, who could disregard the passage of time in dreams, often found himself facing the swords of ancient masters, leaving him breathless and forcing him to withdraw from the dream in a cold sweat. In worse cases, he would vomit blood and suffer dizziness for days afterward.

Thus, when it came to swords, Liu Xianyang had already become quite an expert.

Not to mention his level of cultivation, just his broad horizons alone might surpass many sword immortals from Beijulu.

Liu Xianyang gently returned the sword to its sheath.

This sword, he had never seen in his dreams.

Yet the feeling seemed familiar, as if he had clearly sensed it on the greatest battlefield ruins, making him feel as if the world was a bit heavier.

As for whether this sword was indeed that one, it was hard to say; perhaps it was a finely crafted imitation, carrying a hint of “sword intent.”

Zhang Shanfeng re-secured the Zhenwu ancient sword on his back and turned to find the tall young man seemingly lost in thought.

Zhang Shanfeng was somewhat puzzled as to why Liu Xianyang, upon hearing that his best friend from his hometown had achieved so much, still appeared more melancholic than joyful. 

Liu Xianyang, with his fists pressed against his knees, gazed into the distance and murmured, “You’ve known Chen Ping’an longer than I have, so you might not know that his greatest hope in this life is simply to be safe and sound. He’s the most timid person, scared of illness and disaster. Yet, in the early days, he was the least afraid of ghosts in the world. Isn’t that strange? Back then, it seemed he felt that as long as he was living earnestly, if he were to die, he would have no regrets, thinking that perhaps he would reunite with people in another place.”

Liu Xianyang continued softly, “So the Chen Ping’an you know has become so cautious because he must have found an absolute reason for not wanting to die. Would you think there’s anything wrong with such a change? I think it’s good, but I understand it will be burdensome for him. When we met, aside from me, no one knew how much he had done for the mother and child from Mud Bottle Alley who had shown him kindness, how much effort he put in, and how much grievance he bore.”

Liu Xianyang smiled, “I’ve only seen him cry twice in my life. The last time was when I was close to dying. The first time was long ago when we were both apprentices at the dragon kiln, and I heard some gossip from Xinghua Alley, accusing the woman from Mud Bottle Alley of having an unclear relationship with him. I got out of bed in the middle of the night and didn’t see him, so I went outside and found him sitting on a stool by the door, tears streaming down his face.”

“I squatted beside him and learned what had happened. My heart became heavy. I had always been carefree about the trivial matters of the marketplace, initially treating it as a joke, so I laughed and asked him if there was any truth to the rumors. He was already so heartbroken that he ignored me. So I knew at that moment he was truly hurt. I refrained from making light of the situation. I couldn’t comfort him, so I could only stay with him. In the end, he came to terms with it, telling me that the favor from Gu Can’s family would take a lifetime to repay. In the future, he would have to be even more diligent in helping them, not letting others gossip and speak ill, nor could he only care for his own feelings, ignoring everything, because in the end, the ones who would suffer the most would be Gu Can and his mother.”

Liu Xianyang leaned back, resting his head on his hands, “Actually, I wanted to tell him back then, could it be possible that Gu Can’s mother didn’t care about those idle words, and it was just him, Chen Ping’an, overthinking? But in the end, I never said those words because I couldn’t bear to. I was afraid that if I spoke, he would become enlightened, and our bond would change. These were my selfish thoughts because I knew that if he treated Gu Can poorly today, he would naturally treat me less well tomorrow. But now that I’ve traveled across a continent to here, after so many years, I regret not letting Chen Ping’an be who he truly is. Why should he live his life for others? Why should he?”

As dusk fell over the riverside stone cliff, a gentle breeze caressed them.

Tonight, the same bright moon would hang in the sky.

Zhang Shanfeng fell silent for a long time before softly asking, “When will you return home to take a look?”

Liu Xianyang lay there, closing his eyes, “I’ll strive to return as soon as possible, maybe within ten years at the shortest.”

Zhang Shanfeng sighed, “It should be sooner. The books say that wealth and honor do not return to one’s hometown, like wearing brocade at night. For us cultivators, it’s quite difficult. On the mountain, we lose track of the seasons. It seems like just a blink, and when we return home, what will be left? Who can we boast to? Even if the family still exists, with descendants, what more can we say?”

Liu Xianyang replied, “I don’t have much attachment to my hometown. I’m not going back to prove anything to anyone. So when I return to Baoping Continent, the first place I want to go isn’t that small town, nor the first person I want to see, not even Chen Ping’an.”

Zhang Shanfeng turned to look, “Is there a knot in your heart?”

Liu Xianyang kept his eyes closed, smiling, “The only way to untie a dead knot is through death.”

Suddenly, Liu Xianyang sat up, “When I reach Baoping Continent, I’ll choose a Mid-Autumn Reunion Night to ask the Sword at Zhengyang Mountain in my dreams!”

Zhang Shanfeng softly asked, “Aren’t you waiting for Chen Ping’an?”

Liu Xianyang crossed his arms and laughed, “Don’t forget, it’s always been me, Liu Xianyang, taking care of Chen Ping’an!”

Yet Liu Xianyang didn’t forget.

In truth, from the first day they met, it was Chen Ping’an who had saved Liu Xianyang from that Mud Bottle Alley.

Zhang Shanfeng didn’t think Liu Xianyang was speaking grandly.

After all, Chen Ping’an had often mentioned that there was someone named Liu Xianyang who had taken care of him a lot and taught him many things.

However, the two best friends hadn’t spoken a word about their encounters and partings in their youth.

Suddenly, Liu Xianyang turned his gaze northeast.

Something stirred in his heart.

Liu Xianyang suddenly said, “I need to sleep for a while.”

Zhang Shanfeng felt somewhat helpless; he was quite like his master.

In the distance, an old scholar in a Confucian robe and an old Daoist in a Daoist robe both sighed at the same time.

Especially the Fire Dragon True Man, who felt a deep sense of sorrow.

For the friend who had visited Padi Peak before embarking on the long journey to Upside Down Mountain had been the first sword immortal from Beijulu Continent to die in battle south of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Now that Beijulu had received the news, this was the commotion that ensued.

This was an ancient tradition passed down through generations in Beijulu.

To hold a sword memorial.

The sword energy soared to the heavens.

The world would know.

On a small hill in the Fuhua Kingdom, Chen Ping’an quietly stayed for three days, both practicing his fist techniques and cultivating.

Regarding the breathing methods of cultivators, Chen Ping’an had never been so focused and dedicated. Sitting cross-legged, he was able to forget himself entirely.

When the time came, the array set by Liu Jinglong that could withstand three attacks from the Nascent Soul dissipated on its own.

This commotion finally caused Chen Ping’an to open his eyes.

Previously, Chen Ping’an had already taken off his black Daoist robe and changed into a plain green robe. He slung a bamboo box over his back and took out a simple green bamboo walking staff, heading down the mountain.

Once more, he resembled a scholarly traveler.

The serene cultivation of a fifth realm cultivator, besides refining the spiritual energy of heaven and earth into their own small world, also strengthened their bones, unlike ordinary people. Upon reaching the cave dwelling realm, their bones became strong and solid, appearing like jade. When the power reached them, it manifested.

Upon reaching the Golden Core realm, further along, as bones and meridians melded, they exhibited the “golden branches and jade leaves” phenomenon, with clouds and mist swirling around their energy chambers, lingering for long periods. Especially upon reaching the Nascent Soul realm, they would open small worlds within their bodies at critical acupoints, refining the condensed essence of heaven and earth into a small Nascent Soul that resonated with their own great path. This was the foundation of the outer body of the Yang God of fifth realm cultivators, though it was similar to that of the Golden Core, each having its own hierarchy.

This was the innate nature and potential of a Qi practitioner.

The so-called innate nature of a cultivator refers to the size of their small world, which can carry spiritual energy.

As for potential, it determines whether a Qi practitioner can reach the Earth Immortal level and the quality of their Golden Core and Nascent Soul after embarking on the cultivation path. The speed of a Qi practitioner’s cultivation may vary drastically.

As for temperament, it pertains to cultivating the heart, being the most ethereal and elusive, yet often failing at critical moments, leading to unforeseen incidents. For example, the determined Liu Laocheng from Gongliu Island could have perished early due to a momentary lapse caused by a heart demon born from love. Lu Fang from Ouhua blessed land, too, was troubled by love, and for a century, Jiang Shangzhen, who had taken the name Zhou Fei, still couldn’t fully open his heart.

In contrast, Jiang Shangzhen, who seemed to have been marred by more romantic entanglements, was not troubled by such heart demons at all.

This was all due to the differences in temperament.

As for opportunities, they were difficult to seek, appearing to rely solely on fate.

Previously, He Xiaoliang from the Divine Revelation Sect, Huang Ting from Tongye Continent, and of course Li Huai, who was well acquainted with Chen Ping’an, all belonged to that kind of fortunate individuals.

Now, Chen Ping’an had successfully refined two of his life’s objects, the Water Character Seal from the Water House and the Five-Color Earth from Great Li, creating a splendid landscape of mountains and waters.

In terms of cultivation, progress accelerated significantly.

The extraction and refining of spiritual energy became quicker and more stable.

Thus, it could be said that as long as Chen Ping’an sought a serene and beautiful place rich in spiritual energy, even if he remained still on that small hill, just sitting there, day and night would be spent in cultivation, actually enhancing his cultivation and realm.

Therefore, it’s not hard to understand why the more talented cultivators are, the less likely they are to linger on the mountain, unless they encounter a bottleneck, they will descend the mountain for a while, engaging in quiet reflection and heart cultivation, avoiding wayward paths and walls without realizing it. Many insurmountable obstacles are incredibly profound; perhaps moving just a step may lead to a new world, or perhaps it requires traversing thousands of miles, accumulating profound insights in order to make a breakthrough, turning what was once an obstacle into a path.

For ordinary cultivators, the third realm is a moderately sized hurdle, referred to on the mountain as the “Retaining People’s Realm.”

However, this notion is utterly fallacious in properly inherited sects of immortal families.

This is why wild cultivators envy the disciples of the sects so much.

They might have to bleed and suffer before finding a path through the third realm's difficulties, whereas for the disciples of the great immortal families, it’s as simple as lifting a hand to observe hand lines; all paths are laid bare.

And Chen Ping’an's third realm is that of the wild cultivators.

Because regarding cultivation, it seems no one ever provided any specific guidance.

Initially, the Bridge of Longevity was broken and shattered, discussing this matter would be meaningless.

Later was the practice of swordplay and fist techniques, with a focused heart.

Previously, at the Luying Kingdom’s Dragon Head Ferry, the immortal guest known as the Kingfisher had detailed the key to the cultivation of the lower five realms. However, since both parties belonged to different sects and lineages, Qi Jinglong was bound by mountain rules and restrictions, making it impossible to explore Chen Ping’an’s various energy chambers, thus he couldn’t give precise guidance.

Nonetheless, Qi Jinglong’s advice remained invaluable.

Because it was destined to be correct.

It required Qi Jinglong to stand at an elevated position on the mountain to articulate it clearly.

Chen Ping’an naturally remembered this well.

He had just taken a sip from the jar of wine left by Liu Jinglong, savoring it slowly, intending to save at least half a jar.

Refining on the first and fifteenth days was still quite taxing.

Currently, his bodily injuries had not yet healed, so Chen Ping’an walked increasingly slowly and cautiously.

However, when he neared the border of Lujiu County, he became aware of something.

He simply continued to feign ignorance.

Dealing with such matters of being tailed, Chen Ping’an wouldn’t claim to be exceptionally skilled at it, but among his peers, he likely wouldn’t be too far from the mark.

Earlier, when Li Fuhua, a Nascent Soul cultivator from Shujian Lake, had secretly followed him, Chen Ping’an had sensed something was awry early on. Later, he had engaged in mutual calculations with Gao Cheng from Beijulu’s Jingguan City, leading to that second wave of assassins from Gela Mountain.

Moreover, the current stealthy assassin couldn’t be considered very powerful, and was merely self-assured in their concealment, but they displayed incredible patience, refraining from making a move despite several seemingly opportune moments.

Chen Ping’an allowed this assassin to “guard the path” for him.

Lujiu County was the hometown of the down-and-out scholar Lu Dun, whom Chen Ping’an had once encountered on the mountain.

However, Chen Ping’an had no intention of visiting his family because even if he had that thought, he might not find anyone.

One of the nearby scholars, surnamed Zhou instead of Lu, possibly out of a precautionary mindset, didn’t reveal his true surname to Chen Ping’an.

But Chen Ping’an believed this was the right approach.

True sincerity in meeting others is never just about exposing one’s heart through words.

Casual acquaintanceship can easily lead to self-deception.

If one cannot even be responsible for oneself, how can they be responsible for the world and others, and then genuinely offer goodwill?

However, while the principle stands, the world has its complexities, and being genuine everywhere is ultimately not too good.

Chen Ping’an detoured around the small town, unwilling to entangle himself further with the assassin.

Thus, on a secluded path, he suddenly vanished, appearing next to the assassin who was lying in the reeds. Chen Ping’an stood atop a reed, his figure swaying with the wind, quietly looking down to find a young boy dressed in black robes with a snow-white mask—definitely an assassin from Gela Mountain. Yet this was the most intriguing part; this young assassin from Gela Mountain had been trailing Chen Ping’an all this way, enduring considerable hardship. Either Qi Jinglong hadn’t found the right person, or reason had failed to communicate, leading to the involvement of high-level cultivators from Gela Mountain in the assassination attempt on him. Alternatively, it could mean that Qi Jinglong had thoroughly clarified the reasoning behind it, leading Gela Mountain to choose to abide by a larger rule: even if different employers were involved, if they attempted to assassinate the same person three times, they would no longer attack even if someone else came along offering mountains of gold and silver.

If that were the case, why hadn’t Qi Jinglong shown his face?

Chen Ping’an pondered and spoke, “Aren’t you in a hurry to find your employer?”

The Gela Mountain assassin moved stiffly, turning to look at the young man in green standing amidst the reeds.

It wasn’t that he didn’t want to flee, but his intuition told him that escaping would mean death, while staying put offered a slim chance of survival.

He sat up, took off the mask, and said, “I made a pact with that Liu fellow: as soon as you discover my whereabouts, even if my assassination attempt fails, I’ll follow him in cultivation and call him master, so please don’t kill me.”

Chen Ping’an asked, “And where’s he?”

The boy shook his head, “He told me to inform you that he needs to make a trip to the Great Zhuang Capital first and will return to find us later.”

At this point, the boy slammed his fist into the ground, feeling frustrated, “This is my first time descending the mountain to assassinate someone!”

Chen Ping’an gracefully landed, stepping out of the reeds, using his walking staff to clear the path.

The boy hesitated for a moment, then gritted his teeth, discarding the mask and following behind the young man.

Chen Ping’an slowed his pace, and the boy glanced at him, stiffly keeping up, walking side by side.

Regarding this assassination target, there had been some rumors within Gela Mountain. As someone who was heavily cultivated and had grown up alongside the mountain lord, he had the chance to learn some insider information.

In general, despite looking amiable and scholarly, the mountain lord had once told the boy that the person standing next to him was someone who could get into trouble easily and excel at resolving issues.

Chen Ping’an asked, “Are you a sword cultivator?”

The boy nodded, “My master says I’m a valuable innate sword seed, so I must cherish my life and not rush to take on tasks. Otherwise, with all the resources he’s invested in me, he’d suffer a loss. So I’ve always wanted to take on work early to help my master and Gela Mountain earn money. I never expected to encounter someone like Liu. He claims I can simply stand still and let my master make his moves. Every time he attacks, I have to listen to him explain something, and my master ended up making two moves, then followed two of his words.”

Upon reaching this point, the boy looked utterly despondent.

In his memory, his master had never returned empty-handed after a sword strike.

Regardless of the opponent’s cultivation level, they had always ended up with their heads rolling.

The boy let out a long sigh, releasing the pent-up frustration that had been building inside him. “Our Gela Mountain always keeps its word. In the end, my master had no choice but to send me to assassinate you. From now on, I’ll have no connection with Gela Mountain, and I’ll have to go with that Liu fellow to some ridiculous Taohui Sword Sect.”

Chen Ping’an smiled as he extended his hand, opening his palm.

The boy frowned, “What are you doing?”

Chen Ping’an said, “You should thank me for allowing you to go to the Taohui Sword Sect for cultivation.”

“You must be joking!” The boy rolled his eyes, “Who wants to be a disciple of a pedigree immortal? I’m just lacking in ability. Those countless opportunities I’ve had don’t feel like opportunities. If it weren’t for that, I would have stabbed you to death long ago and felt utterly relieved!”

Chen Ping’an withdrew his hand, laughing, “Such a heavy killing intent should be directed towards Qi Jinglong instead.”

The boy turned his head and spat, “Even if that Liu fellow is better than our mountain lord, so what? Do I have to switch my allegiance? Besides, he looks like a bookworm; if I follow him, every day I’ll have to call out ‘master’ to this slowpoke. I’m afraid I won’t even become a sword immortal in this lifetime.”

Chen Ping’an said, “Have you thought about the possibility that your master actually hopes you can follow Qi Jinglong?”

The boy was silent for a moment, “I can guess. My master treats me well; I’ve always known that. So I plan to call that Liu fellow ‘master’ on the surface, but in my heart, I’ll only recognize my master as my one true master.”

The boy turned his head, worrying that the fellow might spread rumors about him when he reached Liu Jinglong’s side, which would cause him trouble in the future.

But for some reason, as he walked alongside this person, he felt the urge to speak more of his heart.

Perhaps the change was too immense, and he couldn’t hold it in anymore; it wasn’t hard for the boy to feel like he might suffocate.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “It’s good that you can think this way now, and it’s also correct. Changing your thoughts in the future doesn’t mean your current feelings were wrong.”

The boy furrowed his brow, “Who do you think you are to say such profound things? What? You think I can’t kill you, so you’re acting all high and mighty? You think you can just point fingers at me?!”

This temper of his...

Was truly not good.

Chen Ping’an remained unbothered, “Anyone can speak reason. I’m stronger than you and still willing to talk reason. Is that a bad thing? Do you want me to punch you to death, or beat you half to death, forcing you to kneel and beg me to impart reason? Would that be better?”

The boy felt a headache coming on, raising his hand, “Stop it! My mountain lord has been annoyed by that Liu fellow for half a day, and now I’ve been kicked out without even being allowed to say a word.”

Chen Ping’an smiled and twisted his wrist, producing two flasks of sweet rice wine, “Drink or not?”

The boy’s eyes lit up as he snatched one of the flasks, opened it, and took a hearty swig. Afterward, he grimaced, “So this is what wine tastes like? Not interesting at all.”

Chen Ping’an didn’t even glance back, just continued walking slowly, “Now that you’ve had a drink, you might as well finish it. It’s fine if you take your time. If you dare to toss it aside right now, I’ll teach you some lessons that you won’t want to hear.”

The boy wore a sarcastic expression, “See? In the end, you’re still resorting to force. Don’t think I’m saying this lightly; you’re not even as good as that Liu fellow!”

Chen Ping’an laughed, “While Qi Jinglong hasn’t returned yet, you should enjoy your wine. If all goes as planned, you might not get to drink for a long time in the future.”

The boy’s brows knitted together, “You know Liu warned me in advance not to drink if you offer it to me?”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “I’m not a clairvoyant.”

The boy raised his arm and glanced at the wine flask in his hand. After hesitating a moment, he didn’t dare to toss it aside. He took another sip of the rice wine; in truth, it wasn’t bad, and he didn’t feel any burning sensation in his throat.

It seemed he was someone who could naturally drink.

No wonder he was an innate sword seed!

He suddenly asked tentatively, “How about you speak to Liu and tell him you’re willing to accept me as your disciple?”

Chen Ping’an didn’t respond.

The boy began to persuade this young man in green, saying he would definitely remember his kindness and would repay him in the future. When he returned to Gela Mountain, he would burn incense at the shrine, acknowledge his ancestors, and would not charge for helping him assassinate his enemies…

Chen Ping’an asked, “By the way, what’s your name?”

The boy wasn’t typically one to answer questions readily, but this matter of names was a source of personal pride, even more so than being an innate sword seed. He scoffed, “My master named me Bai Shou! Don’t worry, within a hundred years, there will be a sword immortal named Bai Shou in Beijulu!”

Chen Ping’an exclaimed, “Then you should be careful of your future title. Bai-Tou Sword Immortal or something, that doesn’t sound pleasant.”

The boy thought about it, and Chen Ping’an’s words made sense!

He nodded, “Thanks for the heads up!”

Chen Ping’an raised his wine flask, and the young sword cultivator named Bai Shou paused for a moment before realizing, raising his own flask to clink it against Chen Ping’an’s, then both took a drink.

Bai Shou wiped his mouth, feeling quite good; he believed he had a bit of heroic spirit and sword immortal demeanor now.

Chen Ping’an murmured with a smile, “You should listen to your master in other matters, but when it comes to drinking, a sword immortal should partake; it would be a pity otherwise.”

Bai Shou nodded vigorously, “Although you were quite annoying at first, I find you much more agreeable now. What’s your name?! You should know, I Bai Shou won’t remember many names in my lifetime. Do you see that Liu guy? Have I ever called him by his full name?”

Chen Ping’an replied, “My name is Chen Haoren.” 

Bai Shou angrily retorted, “You better know your place!”

Chen Ping’an turned to ask, “Are you going to hit me?”

Bai Shou rolled his eyes, “You think I’m an idiot?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Exactly. Go ahead and hit me.”

Bai Shou felt deeply humiliated, downing another gulp of wine.

This was practically the second humiliation since he had come down the mountain.

Chen Ping’an turned his head.

Dusty and weary, Qi Jinglong should have arrived long ago, having followed them for quite a while.

Qi Jinglong sighed helplessly, “Are you really addicted to persuading others to drink?”

Chen Ping’an laughed, “Every swordsman will likely remember those who encouraged them to drink.”

Qi Jinglong asked, “Who was it that encouraged you?”

Chen Ping’an said, “Originally, it was a swordsman, later an old gentleman.”

Despite Bai Shou’s constant mention of that Liu fellow, upon Qi Jinglong’s arrival, he immediately fell silent, as if standing next to Chen Ping’an while holding the unfinished wine flask. Even if he wouldn’t drink anymore, it felt wrong.

The land dragon of Beijulu, Liu Jinglong, had indeed remained stationary, allowing Bai Shou’s master, the mountain lord, to deliver two sword strikes!

What appeared to be a casually drawn talisman array, a place unseen by the flying swords of the small world, after two strikes from his master, had left him with no will to deliver a third.

Qi Jinglong said, “Before I set out, let’s find a secluded mountaintop. You will witness a rarely seen spectacle. Afterward, you will understand more about us Beijulu.”

Chen Ping’an nodded, naturally in agreement.

That night, the three of them reached the peak of a high mountain.

At the Great Zhuang Capital, by the banks of the Yuxi River.

Ji Yue stood on one side of the riverbank.

A green-robed old scholar stood on the opposite bank, smiling, “Just go ahead and hold the sword memorial.”

Ji Yue nodded, “I still trust your character, Gu You.”

That night in Beijulu.

From a great sword immortal who had journeyed to Upside Down Mountain in his early years, the sword cultivators of the mountain gate were the first to raise their flying swords, shooting into the heavens.

Like a bright white rainbow of sword energy arising from the earth.

Then came the first sword immortal of Beijulu, Bai Shang, whose dazzling sword light soared into the sky.

Moreover, all the sword cultivators of the Taohui Sword Sect, led by their sect leader, rode their flying swords, illuminating the night sky with their sword lights, casting brilliance over the entire sect’s territory, making the heavens shine bright as day.

Zhixuan Peak also had an ancestor who raised the peach wood sword, often used for slaying demons and removing evil.

Even as the battle of life and death with a tenth realm martial artist was about to commence, Ji Yue still first took to the skies with his sword, memorializing a fellow cultivator who had died far away.

At the Floating Duck Sword Lake, led by the sword immortal Li Cai, all sect sword cultivators drew their swords.

From the ancestor hall of the Mima Sect, aside from a few sword cultivators already raising their swords, the sect leader Zhu Quan pressed the hilt of his sword, allowing Pang Lanxi beside him to also ride her long sword into the sky to pay tribute.

On the Bone Marsh, the spirit of the hero Pu Rang also unsheathed his sword, with Gao Cheng breaking the heavens’ taboos with a punch, solely to allow Pu Rang’s sword to rise higher!

Even all the sword immortals, sects, and sword cultivators, who opposed the sword immortal who had died, without exception, raised their swords to memorialize.

Thus, one by one, beams of varying sword energies rose from the territory of Beijulu.

Under the night sky of Haoran, there were naturally many lights in the human realm.

But never had Beijulu seen so many sword immortals and sword cultivators raising their swords together, illuminating the entire continent like lights simultaneously.

On a nameless high peak within the Fuhua Kingdom, Qi Jinglong also began to raise his sword.

This time, he gave it his all. His life’s sword, named “Regulations,” shot up into the sky, its sword energy like a rainbow, creating a magnificent spectacle.

Qi Jinglong stood with his hands behind him, gazing at the delicate lines rising from the earth.

All were sword cultivators of the continent memorializing that fellow cultivator, while also honoring a shared great path among sword cultivators.

He suddenly turned his head to look at Chen Ping’an beside him, smiling, “Have you truly thought it through? If someone with ulterior motives sees it, revealing your hidden methods might bring you trouble in your future travels.”

Yet Qi Jinglong was already aware of the answer.

At some point, Chen Ping’an had already grasped a long sword.

The sword's name was Sword Immortal.

Chen Ping’an tilted his head slightly and softly said, “Thinking of so many things others would rather not think about is precisely for the sake of not having to ponder some matters.”

In that moment, the green-clad figure swayed atop the mountain, his sleeves fluttering loudly.

The boy named Bai Shou, who had already been dazzled by Qi Jinglong’s sword light, instinctively strained to open his eyes, not wanting to miss that scene.

When that person gently called out, “Let’s go,” a golden sword light appeared in the heavens, soaring sword energy shooting up to the sky.

Moreover, two streaks of white and green sword light flew out from that person’s acupoints, rushing into the sky.

When Qi Jinglong retracted his life’s sword, Chen Ping’an raised his sword sheath, the Sword Immortal descending from the heavens, the sound of metal ringing as it returned to its sheath.

Then, the traveler from Beijulu, this green-clad swordsman, gently slung it over his shoulder.

At that moment, the young sword cultivator named Bai Shou felt that receiving a jar of wine from that green-clad man was quite something to take pride in.

They parted ways.

Qi Jinglong rode the wind back north, while Bai Shou could also ride the wind to journey far.

Bai Shou turned to see that person standing in place, performing a gesture of raising his flask in salute. Bai Shou nodded vigorously, and both sides didn’t exchange words.

Unexpectedly, Qi Jinglong spoke, “As for drinking, don’t even think about it.”

Bai Shou, infuriated, retorted, “Liu, if you keep this up, I might just slip away and seek out your friend to make him my master!”

Qi Jinglong laughed, “You’re welcome to try; he’ll surely send you away.”

Bai Shou questioned, “Why would that be?”

Qi Jinglong smiled, “Because he’s stingy with wine money.”

Bai Shou scoffed, “You’re lying! How could he be that stingy?”

Qi Jinglong nodded, “He’s stingier than you could imagine.”

Bai Shou sighed, “I must have been blind, thinking I’d make him my master.”

Bai Shou suddenly asked, “So is it because you’re worried about delaying my sword practice or is it because you’re stingy with money that you don’t allow me to drink?”

Qi Jinglong said, “It’s both.”

Bai Shou angrily exclaimed, “You’re even worse than him!”

Qi Jinglong turned his head, smiling, “When did I ever say I was better than him?”

Bai Shou felt a surge of frustration, having held it in for so long, he finally couldn’t help but shout, “You and your friend are both like this! Damn it, have I fallen into a den of thieves?”

Qi Jinglong laughed, “That’s not quite the case.”

Bai Shou sighed again.

Times were truly tough.

On the other side of the mountain, the re-equipped Chen Ping’an began to descend slowly, thinking that Qi Jinglong and his newly accepted disciple were probably discussing his good traits, like being generous and magnanimous. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 635: On the Path of Cultivation**

As Chen Pingan descended from the mountain peak, he hesitated for a moment before donning the black robe known as the "Hundred-Eyed Glutton," which he had "picked up" from Yang Ningxing of the Chongxuan Bureau in the Dayuan Dynasty. The robe's golden embellishments were still too conspicuous. Previously, he had switched to a plain blue shirt out of caution, worried that traveling along this peculiar river that led to the ocean at both ends would attract unnecessary attention. However, after witnessing Qi Jinglong's sword offering at the mountain's summit, Chen Pingan reconsidered. Now that he had entered the realm of Liu Jin (the realm of staying), wearing a robe of decent quality would help him absorb the spiritual energy of heaven and earth more quickly, beneficial for his cultivation.

Lu Jiu County was one of the top counties in the Kingdom of Fuqu, known for its rich cultural atmosphere. Chen Pingan had bought several miscellaneous books at a bookstore in the county city, including a collection that had gathered dust for years—a compendium of agricultural edicts issued in early spring by the Kingdom of Fuqu. Some of the texts were eloquent, while others were simple in style. As he meticulously flipped through the collection, Chen Pingan discovered that those similar scenes he had observed in the Three Continent lands each spring were, in fact, part of a set routine: land prayers for good harvests, official tours, and encouragement for the people to engage in farming.

The beauty of reading and traveling lay in the serendipity of flipping through a book, as if the sages had helped future generations of readers string together a thread, linking the affairs and emotions of the world into a dazzling array of beads.

After taking a rough tour of the scenic spots in Lu Jiu County, Chen Pingan spent the night at a well-known inn in the city. Upon entering the county, he deliberately suppressed the robe's ability to absorb spiritual energy to avoid attracting attention from the City God's Pavilion or the Civil and Military Temples.

In fact, for every Qi practitioner, especially those who had reached the Middle Five Realms, traveling through the mountains and rivers of the mortal world was akin to a dragon swimming through the river, not an insignificant affair. Generally, once they descended from the mountains to continue their training and absorb the spiritual energy of various landscapes, it was a matter of adhering to the rules. As long as one did not show obvious signs of over-extraction—like fishing in a dried-up pond—the local deities would usually turn a blind eye.

Under the night sky, Chen Pingan lit a lamp on the table in his inn room and flipped through the compendium of agricultural edicts again. After closing the book, he began to enter a meditative state.

Not relying on the Hundred-Eyed Glutton robe to absorb the thin spiritual energy of the county city did not mean he was not cultivating. Absorbing spiritual energy was never the entirety of cultivation. Throughout his journey, within the small universe of his body, it resembled the crucial acupoints of the Water Palace and the Mountain Shrine. The accumulation and refinement of spiritual energy were fundamental to cultivation. The interconnectedness of his two life-bound items required him to cultivate a phenomenon akin to the interplay of mountain roots and water currents. In simple terms, Chen Pingan needed to refine the spiritual energy and solidify the foundations of his Water Palace and Mountain Shrine. However, the spiritual energy he had gathered was far from reaching a point of overflowing saturation. Thus, the urgent task was to find an unclaimed treasure land of feng shui. Unfortunately, this was not easy, so retreating to a place like the Dragon Head Ferry in the Green Oriole Nation to seclude himself for a few days was a viable alternative.

In fact, he could use the naturally rich spiritual energy of the Immortal Money to directly refine it into spiritual energy for his Qi Palace. However, at this moment, Chen Pingan had not even fully refined the existing spiritual energy, making such an act counterproductive. The lower the cultivation realm, the slower the absorption of spiritual energy, while the spiritual energy of Immortal Money was exceedingly pure and dissipated too quickly. This was akin to many precious talismans losing their effectiveness once "opened," resulting in a valuable talisman becoming worthless paper. Even if the Immortal Money could be crushed and refined for temporary storage by the robe, it would inadvertently conflict with the illusion spell applied to it, making him even more conspicuous.

Every cultivator was essentially the lord of their own small universe, relying on their skills to become their own sage. The key was the extent of control over their domain and the size of their territory. The path of cultivation was akin to a cavalry force expanding its territory on the battlefield.

Ultimately, the height of a realm and the efficacy of one's Dao were determined by how many residences one could establish. In the mortal world, there were countless types of buildings, each with its own hierarchy, and caves were no different. The best quality naturally belonged to blessed lands and paradises.

After steadying his breath and focusing his mind, Chen Pingan first arrived at the entrance of the Water Palace. With a thought, he could effortlessly pass through walls, as if the rules of heaven and earth did not bind him; he was the rule, and the rule was him.

However, he paused outside the door for a moment before two young attendants in green quickly opened the door, bowing respectfully to him with beaming faces. 

Inside the Water Palace, which now featured a suspended water character seal and a mural depicting water currents, the little green-robed boys, who finally had work to do, were evidently in high spirits and very busy.
