They were no longer idly sitting around, waiting for Chen Pingan to stroll through their small universe. In the past, they would line up neatly on the ground, looking up at him with mournful eyes, silently watching.

They were diligent little ones, never slacking off, but having someone like Chen Pingan, who was not particularly focused on cultivation, was akin to being a skilled cook without any rice—how could they not feel disheartened?

Now, the scene had completely transformed. The Water Palace was bustling with activity; the little ones ran around cheerfully, working diligently, finding joy in their tasks.

From a small pond resembling a narrow well, Chen Pingan scooped up water. Since the harvest from Cangjun Lake, he had reaped considerable rewards. In addition to several streams of exceptionally pure and rich water currents, he had also received a bottle of Water Pill from the Lake Lord. The green-robed boys split into two groups: one used their innate divine abilities to send strands of dark green water currents into the slowly rotating water character seal, while the other group, armed with tiny brushes that seemed to have appeared from nowhere, dipped them into the pond and then dashed toward the mural, carefully painting and adding color to the mural that depicted water currents in a meticulous style. 

They had already painted tiny water deities and slightly larger shrines on the vast mural, which Chen Pingan recognized as the water deities and shrines he had personally visited, including the Water Goddess of the submerged river in Tongyezhou, which should now be referred to as the Bi You Palace.

However, those water deities had yet to be animated, and the shrines lacked the lively scenes of incense wafting. For now, they remained as lifeless as the mural itself, lacking the vitality of the surging rivers depicted.

Standing beside the small pond, Chen Pingan looked down and saw a water dragon, carried in by the green-robed boys from Cangjun Lake, swimming lazily. It had not been directly refined by the little green figures, while another anomaly appeared: the Water Pill gifted by the Lake Lord had seemingly transformed into a small bead resembling a green "Li Pearl," which, no matter how the little dragon swam, remained suspended at its mouth, like a dragon holding a pearl, drifting through the rivers and clouds.

Chen Pingan planned to visit the Mountain Shrine next. Some of the green-robed boys smiled at him, raising their tiny fists, likely encouraging him to keep up his efforts.

With a touch of helplessness, Chen Pingan thought about the water currents. The more refined they appeared like jade, the more they represented the fundamental path of the water deities. Surely, it was not so simple to find; it was something as difficult to obtain as Immortal Money. Just imagine if someone were willing to offer one hundred Gu Yu coins to buy a foundational stone from a mountain shrine—Chen Pingan might acknowledge it as a profitable trade, but would he genuinely be willing to sell? It was merely a transaction on paper; the path of Dao cultivation should never be so calculative.

After leaving the Water Palace, Chen Pingan began to travel "visiting mountains." Standing at the foot of a mountain that resembled a blessed land, he looked up at the summit, where five-colored clouds swirled. The mountain appeared shrouded in fog and presented a grayish-black hue, still giving off an ethereal, uncertain feeling, while the majesty of the mountains paled in comparison to the previous Water Palace.

Fortunately, at the mountain's base, there were some shimmering white stones. However, compared to the towering mountain peak, this little patch of glistening white was pitifully small. Yet, it was already the result of Chen Pingan's arduous cultivation journey since leaving the Dragon Head Ferry in the Green Oriole Nation.

The foremost sword immortal of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Qingdu, with his keen insight, had predicted that if Chen Pingan's innate porcelain was not shattered, he had the potential of an Earth Immortal.

In the mundane sense, both Golden Core and Nascent Soul cultivators were considered Earth Immortals. But perhaps, in the eyes of that great sword immortal, there was no difference between the two.

Thus, Chen Pingan neither overestimated himself nor underestimated his worth. He understood that even with the same Water Palace and Mountain Shrine, if it were in the hands of a true genius like Qi Jinglong, the phenomenon would be much grander.

However, cultivators in the world were ultimately rare geniuses among the common multitude. If Chen Pingan lacked even this degree of composure, he would have already lost his spirit in the martial path at the Sword Qi Great Wall. As for cultivating, he would be repeatedly struck down until his mental state shattered, not much better than a broken bridge to immortality. The foundation of a Qi practitioner, like Chen Pingan's Earth Immortal potential, was akin to a naturally gifted "iron rice bowl." Yet, it still required one to talk about potential, which came in countless forms. Finding the cultivation method that suited oneself best was the true blessing.

Competing with others, whether in strength or reason, would always reveal shortcomings and lead to lifelong dissatisfaction. But competing with oneself would yield long-term benefits, accumulating every bit of progress as one's own foundation.

Every mistake made, as long as one could recognize and correct it, would seem like a stream that flows gently, even if the mental journey remains hard to erase. The riverbed remains, and there is no need to fear floods; this is the essence of cultivating the heart, ensuring that even in the face of great adversity, as long as one lives, their resolve will not collapse. By observing oneself through the lens of one's mindset, even if the mirror has cracks, one does not have to genuinely believe they have become unrecognizable.

Chen Pingan had once feared becoming one of the people atop the mountain, just as he feared becoming like Gu Can, the person he once despised most. For instance, the man who nearly killed Liu Xianyang in Mud Bottle Alley, the drunkard who had once kicked Gu Can in the stomach, and later, Fu Nanhua, the Mountain Moving Ape, and then Liu Zhimo and Jiang Shangzhen.

Chen Pingan even feared that the teachings of the old master of the Dao Viewing Temple, which he had repeatedly used to weigh worldly affairs and emotions, would one day quietly overshadow the orderly teachings of the venerable Confucian sage, without him even realizing it.

Yet, in truth, as he remained grounded, moving step by step, the truths of the world, regardless of which school of thought, were never fearsome. What was truly frightening was being unable to discern clearly while mistakenly believing one already "knew."

To truly open one's eyes is to see the light.

This phrase had come to Chen Pingan after he had closed his eyes in deep sleep atop the mountain and then opened them again, not only recalling the phrase but also seriously inscribing it on a bamboo slip.

On the bamboo slip, Chen Pingan recorded numerous poetic phrases, but the words he had truly comprehended were few and far between, carefully etched with gravity.

He left the five-colored "Mountain Shrine" and made his way to a pass.

The sword energy surged like a rainbow, like iron cavalry striking the gates, a tide of momentum that could never breach the impervious fortifications. This was the final barrier of the Sword Qi Eighteen Stops.

Chen Pingan stood at the mountain peak, facing the iron cavalry and the pass, sitting cross-legged in silence for a long while, propping his chin in thought.

Afterward, he went to two "Sword Mounds," locations for refining on the first and fifteenth days of each month.

The two flying swords, which appeared small and delicate in the eyes of mortals, towered like mountains within Chen Pingan's Qi Palace, suspended upside down on two vast, smooth mountain platforms. The sword tips rested against the stone platform that manifested as the Dragon-Slaying Platform, sparks flying everywhere, creating a magnificent scene of fire raining down upon the entire Qi Palace. Even though Chen Pingan had already experienced this scene before, each time he beheld it, his spirit would still sway.

One could imagine that if the two flying swords were to leave the confines of the small universe of his Qi Palace and return to the vast world, if they bore such an aura, how would those opposing him feel?

Chen Pingan's mind left the sword polishing area, retracting his thoughts and exiting the small universe.

In fact, there was another place that resembled a hermitage by a heart lake; however, seeing it or not seeing it made no difference.

Because it was all part of himself.

Even without the need for divine awareness, Chen Pingan was fully aware.

After opening his eyes, Chen Pingan gently exhaled a breath of turbid air, then continued to close his eyes, slowly refining the spiritual energy of the Water Palace and the Mountain Shrine through breath control.

Before long, dawn broke, and Chen Pingan stopped refining the spiritual energy. After practicing stances for an hour, he settled his bill and left the inn.

There were no immortal inns in Lu Jiu County, nor were there any significant immortal sects in the Kingdom of Fuqu. While it wasn't a vassal state of the Dayuan Dynasty, the emperors and ministers of the Kingdom of Fuqu throughout the ages had admired the cultural lineage of the Dayuan Dynasty, nearly to the point of obsession. Without discussing national strength, this aspect alone was somewhat reminiscent of the early literary scene of the Great Li Dynasty, where almost all scholars would eagerly focus on the moral essays and poetic works of the Lu Dynasty and the Great Sui. Even if one's own family produced great scholars, without the recognition of these two literary powerhouses, their works would still be seen as crude and inferior. 

There was once a young and wild scholar from the Lu Dynasty who claimed that even if he wrote poetry using his toes, it would still be better than anything produced by the barbarians of the Great Li Dynasty with sincerity.

Later, it was said that this wild scholar, who for years had been drinking and failing to gain recognition in the capital of the Lu Dynasty, encountered the hooves and blades of the iron cavalry under Song Changjing of the Great Li Dynasty. No one knew the exact details, but in the end, this man transformed into one of the bureaucratic officials stationed in the Great Li, later going to the Hanlin Academy in the capital, where he was responsible for compiling the history of the Lu Dynasty, personally writing the "Records of Loyal Ministers" and "Records of Sycophants," placing himself in the final chapter of the latter, and then it was said he hanged himself.

Some say it was the National Master Cui Zhan who detested this man and secretly poisoned him after he completed the two records, disguising it as a hanging. Others say that this wild scholar, who had never managed to secure an official position in the Lu Dynasty, became a historian for the Great Li and would place a good jug of wine on the table for every "Records of Loyal Ministers" he wrote, only writing at night, drinking as he penned, often shouting in the middle of the night. Whenever he wrote a "Records of Sycophants," he would do so during the day, claiming he wanted to expose these treacherous ministers to the light of day, then he would cough up blood, spitting it into an empty cup, which would eventually accumulate into a vat of regretful wine. Thus, it was neither a hanging nor a poisoning—it was a life spent in sorrow.

The neighboring country of the Kingdom of Fuqu had an immortal ferry with a dedicated route leading straight to the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven. The ferry route passed by most of the scenic mountains and waters along the Great Ditch, making multiple stops for passengers to enjoy the landscapes and explore hidden gems. This was essentially a sightseeing route, with the exchange of immortal goods being secondary. Had it not been for the connections to the Chongxuan Bureau and Yang Ningxing, visiting the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven would have been a must for Chen Pingan, as it was a famous place for making a fortune.

The Dragon Palace Cave Heaven was jointly held by three parties, including the Yang family of the Chongxuan Bureau from the Dayuan Dynasty and the sword immortal Li Cai of the Floating Duck Sword Lake.

Logically, the Floating Duck Sword Lake was an important charm for Chen Pingan's journey to the Dragon Palace Cave Heaven, which would surely help him avoid many unforeseen events. 

However, relationships, like spiritual offerings, should be conserved whenever possible. Following the customs of his hometown, it was better to save some for New Year's Eve and the first day of the new year.

Many casual friendships required a certain level of reciprocity, provided one could pay back at any time. 

Chen Pingan did not feel that he could currently return any favors to the likes of the Pei Ma Sect's Zhu Quan or the Floating Duck Sword Lake's Li Cai.

As for Qi Jinglong, he was an exception. 

Why bother being polite with him? 

That would be looking down on the vision of this land dragon in making friends.

Chen Pingan left Lu Jiu County City without incident, carrying the sword immortal on his back and holding a green bamboo staff, traversing mountains and rivers at a leisurely pace toward the neighboring country.

In the end, he had no opportunity to meet that self-proclaimed scholar, Lu Dun.

Life often unfolded this way—one meets, then parts ways, never to see each other again.

Without those encounters that leave one feeling like even if the world changes, stories linger in the heart.

Chen Pingan walked the path of cultivation.

So does everyone else. 

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 636: A Faraway Land**

The Kingdom of Shui Xiao was a renowned realm of lakes and rivers. Most of its cities, including the capital, were built upon islands of various sizes, making water transport bustling and boats plentiful. One notable stream leading into the lake was called Peach Blossom Water. Its waters were exceptionally gentle, flanked by peach trees on both banks. Tourists flocked here, many being distinguished scholars and elites from neighboring countries, drawn by its fame.

Chen Pingan followed this stream, choosing not to head directly to a lakeside county but instead veering off onto a small path that led to a celestial haven known as Peach Blossom Ferry. Those who practiced the Dao only needed to break through a simple illusionary barrier to access the ferry. Once inside this secret realm, their vision would open up to reveal a serene landscape: a green hill surrounded by a tranquil lake whose waters shimmered with a deep emerald hue. Above the ferry, white clouds hung perpetually in the sky, resembling a celestial figure adorned with a white crown. The ferryboats traversed the sea of clouds, making their true forms often invisible to ordinary mortals.

Peach Blossom Ferry belonged to the foremost celestial estate of the Shui Xiao Kingdom, the Colorful Sparrow Estate. The estate was entirely composed of female cultivators who spent years refining the waters of Peach Blossom and various celestial herbs and flowers. With a secret technique passed down from ancient times, they wove a special kind of Daoist robe known as a mountain gate ceremonial robe. The Colorful Sparrow Estate spared no effort or resources, producing only six of these robes each year. It was said that celestial masters from major mountain peaks in the central part of Baoping Continent had already booked their orders for a hundred years later, mostly for the direct disciples of the ancestral hall near the bottleneck of the lower five realms, as one of the congratulatory gifts for their eventual advancement to the middle five realms.

Chen Pingan was already well-acquainted with the ferry process. He entered the ornate building at the ferry terminal that bore the plaque "Spring at the Streamhead" to inquire about the ferry service. After paying, he received a peachwood token intricately engraved with a beautiful design, confirming his passage to the Dragon Palace cave heaven at midnight tonight. The ferry would make several stops along the way, allowing guests to disembark and explore various celestial attractions, a common practice seen in Baoping Continent's underground Dragon Roads and the osmanthus island of the Fan family in Old Dragon City. Passengers enjoyed the scenic views and often bought local celestial specialties, making it a mutually beneficial arrangement, with the ferry earning offerings from the various celestial locations.

The Colorful Sparrow Estate had set up a special workshop at the ferry terminal where visitors could watch the intricate weaving process of the Daoist robes. There was no need to pay any celestial fees; anyone could come and observe.

Naturally, Chen Pingan wouldn’t miss this opportunity. After entering, he walked slowly through the corridors, observing the young female cultivators who were diligently working in each room. As he moved further back, the robes nearing completion became increasingly radiant with precious light.

Chen Pingan actually contemplated purchasing one, but as a newcomer and a novice in the realm of Daoist robes, he worried about haggling for a price only to end up being taken advantage of. In many mountain trades, the celestial masters with lineage certainly had more bargaining power than those wild cultivators, and it was because these transactions were not one-off deals; sellers would consider the background of the buyer, while wild cultivators, often living on the edge, could lose their heads at any moment. Celestial masters preferred to maximize their profits rather than exchange favors with someone who might be in a precarious position.

Chen Pingan believed that the Colorful Sparrow Estate would keep one or two of the finest quality robes on hand, along with a reserve of treasured ceremonial robes for emergencies. However, they certainly wouldn’t entertain requests from ordinary cultivators.

Feeling a bit regretful that Qi Jinglong wasn’t around, Chen Pingan thought that if that guy were here, he could help negotiate a fair price with the female cultivators of the Colorful Sparrow Estate. After all, if a prominent fairy from the estate admired the earthly dragon from the North Ju Lu Continent, she would certainly sell him the robes at face value, and Chen Pingan wouldn’t be able to refuse that, right?

As he left the workshop, Chen Pingan was filled with a sense of longing. Regardless of the robe’s quality, even a low-ranking one from a sect was still valuable, especially for someone from a celestial lineage. 

The high prices of military-grade armors stem from this very sentiment.

Cultivation is for longevity, and time flows endlessly, indifferent to seasons. Yet, one fears the uncertainties. Celestial robes, like military-grade armors such as the Divine Exposure, Golden Crow's Thread, and the Three Treasures of Incense, are all meant to guard against those uncertainties. When cultivators descend the mountains to explore, the presence of a robe or armor makes all the difference.

Just after Chen Pingan exited the workshop, a woman with an impressive demeanor approached him slowly.

Since she was from the Colorful Sparrow Estate, Chen Pingan stopped and greeted her.

After she returned the gesture, she smiled and said, “I am Wu Qian, a lawmaster from the Ancestral Hall of the Colorful Sparrow Estate.” 

Chen Pingan felt puzzled as to why this prominent cultivator, who had not been in the workshop before, sought him out. He introduced himself, “My surname is Chen, and my given name is Haoren.” 

Without a trace of shame.

However, the name Wu Qian had a lovely meaning, not inferior to Chen Haoren's.

Having seen many passing cultivators, Wu Qian was unperturbed by his name and hesitated briefly before getting straight to the point. “May I ask if you know Liu Jinglong of the Taihui Sword Sect?”

Chen Pingan smiled, “Who in the North Ju Lu Continent doesn’t know Liu Jinglong?”

In the North Ju Lu Continent, people still preferred to refer to him by the name recorded in the Taihui Sword Sect’s Ancestral Hall, Liu Jinglong, rather than Qi Jinglong, his name before ascending the mountain.

Without delving into the details, Chen Pingan remained silent about any secret matters, and Wu Qian chuckled softly.

This answer lacked sincerity, but it was hard to find fault with it.

Wu Qian smiled and said, “Our estate lord is currently in seclusion, but the lord had the fortune to travel with Liu Jinglong for a while back in the day, which greatly benefited her cultivation. She has always held Liu Jinglong in high esteem. However, it has been years since Liu Jinglong has passed by our mountain, which our estate lord finds regrettable.”

In truth, Wu Qian’s words were a mix of truth and falsehood. The current young lord of the Colorful Sparrow Estate, by lineage, was her disciple, but her talent was significantly superior to that of her master. In the cultivation world, those with the greatest abilities were respected first. The young lord admired Liu Jinglong not only for his skill but also harbored feelings for him. Thus, this time, it wasn’t merely seclusion but rather a hurried pursuit, following a thread of clues from the previous sword sacrifice to the country of Fu Qu, hoping for a chance encounter. However, such matters were to be kept discreet, and Wu Qian couldn’t speak openly.

Chen Pingan understood immediately.

The estate lord's seclusion was a top priority for any celestial estate.

However, the tranquil atmosphere of the Colorful Sparrow Estate and Peach Blossom Ferry seemed inconsistent with this. Moreover, a lawmaster from the Ancestral Hall might not be the most powerful in a sect, but they often had considerable experience in cultivation. If it were genuinely a case of the estate lord being in seclusion, Wu Qian wouldn’t casually disclose information to an outsider. Considering the courteous words exchanged between the estate lord and Liu Jinglong, Chen Pingan figured it was likely they were trying to intercept Liu Jinglong’s return to the north.

Chen Pingan decided to drop any pretense. Since the other party had been sincere, he returned the favor, saying, “I do know Liu Jinglong quite well.” 

He reverted to their previous way of addressing each other.

Wu Qian’s heart trembled slightly, yet her expression remained calm.

Although she had her suspicions, upon hearing Chen Pingan admit to knowing Liu Jinglong, this Golden Core Earth Immortal felt an invisible pressure.

The reasoning was simple. Previously, in the relatively tranquil borders of the neighboring country Fu Qu, when Liu Jinglong summoned his sword, that unmistakable aura of "rules" was seen through by their estate lord, confirming his identity.

It was evident that next to Liu Jinglong’s destined flying sword, another sword immortal had also accompanied him in the sword summon, and it was a dual-sword attack!

It was the great sword immortal who had perished at the Sword Qi Great Wall alongside Liu Jinglong.

Wu Qian was no fool.

If this seemingly inscrutable black-robed swordsman arrived at Peach Blossom Ferry and even revealed his Earth Immortal sword cultivation, loudly proclaiming to be a close friend of that earthly dragon, Wu Qian would not believe a word of it.

But a stranger who could summon swords alongside Liu Jinglong at the mountain peak—regardless of whether he cried and shouted he didn’t know Liu Jinglong, Wu Qian would never believe it.

On the mountains of North Ju Lu Continent, regardless of whether they were from the lineage celestial masters or the wild cultivators, none feared that earthly dragon, because no one believed Liu Jinglong would indiscriminately kill innocents or bully others with his power.

However, at the same time, regardless of whether one was a top-tier cultivator in the upper five realms, one would still feel a tinge of fear when facing Liu Jinglong’s sword.

Even the most methodical swordsman, Liu Jinglong, who enjoyed discussing principles and reasoning, would choose to draw his sword in person. Who wouldn’t wonder if they were in the wrong, if they had lost their moral compass? Would they become a pariah, losing the protections they once thought were their due? In the world of cultivation, reputation was of utmost importance, even for demonic cultivators.

This was the true power of Liu Jinglong.

Thus, among the young ten of this generation in North Ju Lu Continent, the first and second, although vastly different in temperament, both regarded Liu Jinglong with awe. The others, including Xu Xuan, the only disciple of the North's greatest sword immortal Bai Chang, once publicly declared that the seven who followed Liu Jinglong were all worthless. This caused quite a stir, leading to the tale of the fourth-ranked wild cultivator, Huang Xi, attempting to assassinate Xu Xuan. However, the details and outcome were shrouded in secrecy, and Xu Xuan continued to avoid diligent cultivation, instead preferring to play the role of a weak scholar with two female sword attendants, while Huang Xi faded into obscurity for years.

Chen Pingan asked, “Senior Wu, does the Colorful Sparrow Estate have any spare robes for sale?”

Wu Qian smiled, “Of course we do, but the price isn’t cheap. The robes showcased in this workshop are only the lowest-tier robes, suitable for cultivators in cave dwelling realms, priced at fifteen Grain Rain coins. We also have two types of higher-tier robes, reserved for the Viewing Sea and Dragon Gate realms, as well as for Golden Core and Nascent Soul great cultivators.”

Wu Qian’s intention in coming forward was to gauge the status of Liu Jinglong’s friend, hoping to form a connection that could benefit the Colorful Sparrow Estate significantly.

In the mountain realm, everyone valued longevity, so they paid special attention to the subtleties of relationships.

A single incense offering made today could potentially lead to a great fortune in the coming year.

Of course, some seemingly trivial actions could also lead to disastrous consequences in the future.

Such was life in North Ju Lu Continent.

Thus, when approached with a request for robes, Wu Qian felt a bit more at ease.

Dealing with cultivators was the forte of the Colorful Sparrow Estate.

If their estate lord had no prior connections with Liu Jinglong, what could Liu Jinglong possibly discuss with her? Would they engage in philosophical debates or swordsmanship exchanges?

This was why Wu Qian was willing to come down the mountain; otherwise, if this outsider entered the ferry without the connection of Liu Jinglong, even if he wore a rare robe that the Colorful Sparrow Estate’s cultivators could recognize, Wu Qian would still choose to ignore him.

Chen Pingan asked, “May I inquire about the prices for both types?”

Wu Qian didn’t answer directly but smiled and invited, “Chen Xianshi, would you mind walking and talking? We have a tea house at Peach Blossom Ferry that brews tea using Peach Blossom Water. The tea leaves are unique to the back mountains of the Colorful Sparrow Estate, with only twelve ancient tea trees in total. During the pre-spring and rainy season, a rare bird called the Colorful Sparrow is tasked with picking the leaves. The tea is then refined by cultivators using a secret method. It was once praised by a great literary figure in a poem as ‘Little Xuanbi.’ The boiling tea reveals the wonders of tides and shifts of stars, and this tea house is not open to the public; we can go there to discuss in detail.”

Chen Pingan, of course, complied with local customs, willingly following.

If this Little Xuanbi tea could be purchased alongside the robes, that would be even better.

After all, Chen Pingan was still a wandering merchant, and rarity dictated value. As long as something was not exclusive to him, the price could be flexible.

He welcomed this promising business opportunity, reminiscent of when he had bought a complete set of goddess murals in the mural city, where he had bargained for a long time, almost becoming a shop assistant just to secure a better deal.

Upon arriving at the quiet tea house by the lakeside, Wu Qian and Chen Pingan entered a pavilion where a female cultivator was preparing tea. After an introduction from Wu Qian, Chen Pingan learned that she was the tea house’s proprietor.

Wu Qian mentioned that the Colorful Sparrow Estate had two top-tier ceremonial robes in their collection and sixteen mid-range robes, with striking price differences—fifteen Grain Rain coins for the top-tier ones, and just five for the mid-tier.

After considering, Chen Pingan acknowledged that he wanted to buy a robe, but not immediately.

It wasn’t that he couldn’t afford a top-tier robe from the Colorful Sparrow Estate; he was still making money during this journey. Not to mention, properties like the Chaotian Street in Chunlu Garden and the Jade Crystal Cliff he acquired from Liu Zhiqing were all valuable sources of celestial currency. Furthermore, Chen Pingan had some valuable items on him.

However, since he would be traveling extensively in the future, he didn’t see the robe as a necessity at this moment, so there was no rush.

Chen Pingan also decided not to be overly reserved and directly asked Wu Qian if the Colorful Sparrow Estate could hold two robes for him. He would give a definite answer within the next few years, regardless of whether he ended up buying them.

Wu Qian was genuinely worried about encountering a wealthy patron who might buy up all the robes in the Colorful Sparrow Estate’s collection, leading to a loss on their part. After all, the robes had always sold well.

Even if she had built a rapport with this young guest surnamed Chen, the Colorful Sparrow Estate would still feel the pinch.

But since he had made such a request, Wu Qian felt more relaxed, as reserving two robes was a small favor, and regardless of whether the transaction happened, he would owe the Colorful Sparrow Estate a debt of gratitude.

Thus, Wu Qian, who typically preferred to keep her conversations brief, found herself speaking more.

This surprised the tea house’s proprietor, who regarded the amiable young man with newfound respect.

After all, Wu Qian was a lawmaster from the mountain peak and typically did not personally involve herself in the estate’s business affairs.

Chen Pingan was remarkably patient; as long as Wu Qian spoke, he wouldn’t lower his head to drink tea. He only lifted his cup to sip once Wu Qian concluded her remarks, thanking the tea house’s proprietor each time she served tea.

Words and expressions could be feigned.

But one’s gaze and aura were hard to disguise.

The tea house proprietor grew increasingly convinced that this person had origins among the elite celestial families, like the highly regarded Yang Ning from the Yunxiao Palace.

During this time, Wu Qian naturally extolled the exquisite craftsmanship of the Colorful Sparrow Estate’s ceremonial robes.

In North Ju Lu Continent, the best-crafted treasures belonged to the spiritual armor crafted by the Sanlang Temple. The imitation flying swords from various sword immortals at Hate Sword Mountain, the tri-colored kasayas from the Buddhist Temple’s red, purple, and jade garments, and the crane cloak feather garments produced by the Chongxuan Bureau of the Dayuan Dynasty were all renowned. Additionally, there were four mountains, each possessing unique treasures, including the robes from Laojun Alley, which had an unparalleled sales record, although nearly all were monopolized by the Qionglin Sect, keeping the prices consistently high. Nonetheless, the luminous robes produced every sixty years from Laojun Alley remained the first choice for all upper five realm cultivators outside the sword immortals of North Ju Lu Continent.

Furthermore, Laojun Alley also provided the “Imperial Armor” for monarchs of secular dynasties, symbolizing the pinnacle of wealth and beauty.

Although ridiculed by mountain cultivators as “flowery garments” that looked good but were useless, they were still immensely revered by earthly rulers.

Next, there were the ceremonial robes of the Colorful Sparrow Estate.

Chen Pingan was well aware.

The Colorful Sparrow Estate fell short of Laojun Alley mainly due to a superior secret technique to craft robes similar to the upper five realm luminous robes, a rare opportunity. The latter two factors could be negotiated, perhaps by collaborating with the Qionglin Sect, the largest business entity in North Ju Lu Continent, allowing the Colorful Sparrow Estate to retain critical techniques while Qionglin assisted with resources. However, this approach could easily lead the Colorful Sparrow Estate to become a subordinate sect over time. 

Besides, the Qionglin Sect's reputation in North Ju Lu Continent wasn’t exactly stellar.

Numerous “couplets” had been composed by mountain cultivators regarding the wealth-generating Qionglin Sect, particularly the old master who had amassed his wealth through celestial money.

Aside from the most popular couplet, “Two Sleeves of Clear Wind—Qionglin Sect, Flowery Pillow of the Upper Five Realms,” there were many others that were even more cutting.

“Affordable and Great Value—Qionglin Sect, Unmatched in the Upper Five Realms.” 
“Honest and Transparent—Qionglin Sect, Crushing the Sword Immortal in the Upper Five Realms.” 
“Never Cheating—Qionglin Sect, Real Talent in the Upper Five Realms.”

Sipping tea in the lakeside pavilion, with the gentle breeze, both parties conversed merrily.

Chen Pingan intended to rest here while waiting for the ferry to the Dragon Palace cave heaven. He spoke with Wu Qian, who graciously agreed, even instructing the tea house proprietor to attend to him well.

After Wu Qian departed, Chen Pingan expressed his apologies for any inconvenience caused, causing the tea house’s female cultivator to feel flattered, and she offered a polite comment about the “sword immortal drinking tea, enhancing the ambiance.”

As night fell, Chen Pingan sat alone in the pavilion, closing his eyes to rest.

The clear night was devoid of dust, and the moonlight shone like silver.

In the stillness of the night, with the moon illuminating a foreign land, one could easily feel the longing buried deep within.

I miss someone, who is far away.

Ning girl is one, and Liu Xianyang is too. As for that little snot-nosed child from Mud Bottle Alley, it’s probably even more so.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 637: An Accidental Encounter

At the hour of the pig, the practitioners of Dao were once again praised for their dedication. 

Especially for the Daoist Qi practitioners, this hour was deemed crucial for cultivation—a perfect moment for quiet contemplation and focus, offering an unparalleled natural tranquility. 

Chen Pingan, needing to catch the ferry departing at the hour of the rat, reluctantly relinquished his peaceful mindset. He withdrew his focused thoughts from his personal little world and ceased to watch the scene of sword qi striking the gate from his perch on the mountain. He rose, preparing to set off.

To his surprise, the owner of the tea house approached him, carrying a beautiful green porcelain tea canister and standing at a distance from the water pavilion. 

Chen Pingan quickly walked over. After the lady cultivator from the Caijue Mansion had completed her greeting ritual, she presented the lovely glazed canister with a smile. “Master Chen, this is this shop's harvest of the year—small Xuanbi tea. A small gift, nothing too grand.”

Chen Pingan accepted the green porcelain canister and asked, “Does the tea house still have any small Xuanbi left? I’d like to buy some.” 

The lady cultivator shook her head apologetically. “There are only a few old tea trees on the back mountain of Caijue Mansion, and many have been reserved. Our tea house's share is already quite limited, and there’s not much left now.” 

Chen Pingan laughed. “Then I’m just getting a can of tea for free.” 

The lady cultivator nodded, smiling without a word. 

Chen Pingan inquired, “Is there a report on the landscapes of Taohuadu after autumn that I can purchase? I’ve missed quite a bit while traveling from Longtou Ferry in Green Oriole Country.” 

The lady cultivator replied, “We have some at the tea house. Master Chen doesn’t need to pay; it holds no meaning for us to keep them.” 

Chen Pingan lifted the tea canister, saying helplessly, “It doesn’t feel right to drink tea for free with Senior Wu, take a can of small Xuanbi for free, and then request a few reports on the landscapes for free as well.” 

The lady cultivator chuckled. “Three times is just right.” 

Chen Pingan sighed in resignation. “That makes sense.” 

These little favors were indeed genuine gestures of goodwill. 

He recalled how Sun Jiashu from Old Dragon City had first entertained him, the lady owner of Qingfu Workshop who had deliberately concealed her identity, and now this lady cultivator from the tea house—all of them were quite adept at these customs. 

He noted them down in his mind.

On the journey of life, there were too many sights to behold. One mustn’t forget along the way, and sometimes it’s perfectly fine to do so.

The lady cultivator asked Chen Pingan to wait a moment while she went to fetch three copies of the immortal’s landscape reports as gifts for her esteemed guest. 

After leaving the tea house, Chen Pingan began to peruse the reports while walking.

Wu Qun’s warm hospitality was straightforward enough. 

Given the proximity to Fuhua Country and following his and Qi Jinglong's sacrificial sword rituals, the commotion was considerable. 

Though the landscape reports of Beiju Luzhou appeared to be unconstrained, there was an unwritten rule: once a sword immortal perished at the Sword Qi Great Wall, news would swiftly return to Beiju Luzhou, and any sacrificial sword rituals would not be recorded in the landscape reports. 

Qi Jinglong had clearly stated his reasons; it wasn’t something to be taken lightly. 

The customs of the world all have their reasons. 

At the water pavilion, the grandmaster Wu Qun sat in his original position, though the opposite seat was now empty. He had no desire to drink tea anymore and simply sat quietly, admiring the moonlit lake with its shimmering waves. 

The lady cultivator stood on the steps outside the pavilion. 

Wu Qun asked, “Has there been any news from the Great Seal Capital? Has no mountain head managed to get insider information to write in the landscape reports?” 

The lady cultivator shook her head. “It seems the Emperor of the Lu family in the Great Seal Capital issued a decree forbidding any leak of information. At that time, there were very few who observed the battle from the city walls or by the Jade Seal River. With that sage from the academy personally overseeing the area, no one dared to let an earth immortal eavesdrop on the situation. Even the divine beings observing the mountains and rivers with their powers were hesitant to do so.” 

Wu Qun chuckled. “That sage certainly has a temper. However, after he acted twice, the central mountains and valleys of Beiju Luzhou indeed stabilized quite a bit.” 

The lady cultivator curiously asked, “Grandmaster Wu, why not directly gift that Master Chen a fine robe?” 

Wu Qun gestured for this junior disciple to take a seat. Once she sat down, he smiled and replied, “To cater to one’s preferences. For those who value rules and etiquette, we shall adhere to them. For the greedy and lustful, we need different calculations.” 

The lady cultivator cautiously said, “It’s just a can of small Xuanbi. Master Chen was truly delighted to accept it.” 

Wu Qun glanced at this intelligent junior disciple who assisted in welcoming esteemed guests to the Caijue Mansion tea house. 

Being the owner of the tea house that entertains celestial guests, she naturally possessed a keen mind. 

But sitting in such a position implied that her path in cultivation was already dim, akin to the difficult situation faced by most ferry managers in this world. 

Wu Qun preferred not to elaborate further. 

Cultivators see things more through introspection. 

Discussing matters that touch the essence of cultivation with this junior disciple would hit close to home. 

After all, she treated others with careful consideration and never acted impulsively, which was enough for him. 

Wu Qun sighed. 

He wondered if his mansion's master had met that land-bound dragon. 

There were many stories worth telling about this Liu Jinglong of the Taihui Sword Sect, who was not just some innate sword embryo. 

Yet many of the rumors and events surrounding him were too distant from a third-rate celestial force like the Caijue Mansion. However, the mansion's master had traveled with Liu Jinglong in the past, and she never concealed her admiration for him. She openly asked others about matters of love, even consulting Wu Qun for advice, which filled the lady cultivator with curiosity and yearning for Liu Jinglong. 

In general, women admired the charisma of sword immortals, while men were infatuated with celestial maidens. 

Thus, Wu Qun was genuinely curious about how those celestial couples on the mountains managed to stay united through thick and thin. Were they truly able to stand by each other in times of great peril? 

Wu Qun did not know and hoped he would never have to learn, wishing only to focus on his cultivation. Sadly, he was well aware of his own limitations—he was merely waiting for death. 

Thinking of this, Wu Qun instructed the tea house owner to fetch two jugs of wine. 

The lady cultivator hesitated at first. 

Wu Qun laughed, “What’s wrong with drinking wine at the tea house? Besides, I’m the grandmaster of the Caijue Mansion—who dares to stop me?” 

Only then did the lady cultivator rise, her steps lighter as she went to fetch the wine. 

Even the grandmaster Wu Qun acted this way; how could a cultivator like her, who had little hope in her path, not secretly indulge in wine to drown her sorrows while guarding this modest tea house year after year?

A colorful rainbow beam descended from the sky, gracefully landing on the lake and entering the water pavilion. She was strikingly beautiful, sitting across from Wu Qun, and muttered, “Drinking is good; let me join.” 

Wu Qun smiled, “Things not going well? Is that Liu person still the lumbering blockhead the mansion master speaks of?” 

The lady sitting opposite him was none other than the young mansion master of Caijue Mansion, Sun Qing, a renowned lady cultivator, and technically Wu Qun’s junior. 

Sun Qing shook her head. “Liu Jinglong has changed a lot. During our last meeting, he spoke frankly and directly—though I understand his reasoning, I still feel a bit displeased.” 

Wu Qun asked in confusion, “What did he say?” 

The young mansion master waved her hand dismissively. “Let’s not talk about it; it’s somewhat embarrassing.” 

Wu Qun was left speechless. 

She had already confronted him; what was there to be shy about? 

But Wu Qun was genuinely puzzled. Although his mansion master wasn’t an extraordinary genius, she was still a nearly century-old Golden Core-level cultivator and one of the ten celestial maidens of Beiju Luzhou. It wouldn’t raise any eyebrows if an upper fifth realm sword immortal actively sought to become her celestial partner. 

However, in terms of practical calculations, it was fair to say that his mansion master was no match for the Water Journey Mountain’s maiden, Lu Sui, who not only rose to the top ten alongside Liu Jinglong but was also more beautiful than Sun Qing. 

Wu Qun softly asked, “Have you completely given up on Liu Jinglong?” 

Sun Qing laughed heartily. “How could that be? I like him even more!” 

Wu Qun put a hand to his forehead, speechless. 

How could the most reasonable Liu Jinglong be so unreasonable? 

The three of them began to drink. 

The lady cultivator remained somewhat reserved, but when three female cultivators of varying statuses intentionally dropped their cultivation powers, they would become drunk, their cheeks blooming like peach blossoms. 

In the end, they were just women. 

When women spoke of risqué topics, there were no more restrictions. 

It had a unique charm that was particularly captivating. 

———

One large and one small, riding the wind northward towards the Taihui Sword Sect, Qi Jinglong was moving slowly to care for his newly recruited disciple, Bai Shou, whose cultivation was not very high. 

Then they unexpectedly encountered the young mansion master Sun Qing halfway. 

Qi Jinglong now had considerable confidence, casually conversing with the celestial maiden. 

The extremely beautiful Sun Qing remained unchanged throughout their interaction. 

However, after she took her leave, the young Bai Shou shook his head, clicking his tongue. “That Liu guy, such a beautiful celestial sister actually likes you—he must be blind. If I remember correctly, the mansion master Sun is one of the ten celestial maidens of Beiju Luzhou. Liu, my friend, it’s not that I’m criticizing you; even if you don’t want a celestial partner, I believe Sun Qing would agree to you. How could you pass up such a good opportunity?” 

Qi Jinglong, feeling somewhat relieved, continued on his journey northward with the young boy. He laughed, “Trying to reason with you, especially about love, is like playing a lute to a cow.” 

Bai Shou angrily retorted, “Are you just full of hot air? Why not take me back to cut deer mountain?” 

Qi Jinglong replied slowly, “Rather than have one more sword cultivator who kills for money in Beiju Luzhou, I’d prefer to see a truly accomplished young sword immortal.” 

Qi Jinglong continued, “Don’t worry, once you join the Taihui Sword Sect and register at the Ancestor Hall, you won’t have to identify yourself as a disciple of the Taihui Sword Sect. You don’t even have to acknowledge me as your master. Within the rules, you just need to wield your sword; neither I nor the sect will bind your spirit. However, you must clearly understand the rules of our sect. I don’t want to hear you say you don’t understand the rules when I have to punish you in the future.” 

Bai Shou sulked. 

He had no interest in the rules of the Taihui Sword Sect or Liu Jinglong; he thought they were dull, rigid, and utterly boring. 

What’s so great about being a disciple of a scholarly immortal or a sword immortal? 

It couldn’t compare to the freedom of being an assassin from Deer Cutting Mountain. 

In the martial world, one ought to embody heroism and swift revenge; the assassins of Deer Cutting Mountain need not care about such things. As long as they got paid, they could kill without a care, and that was true freedom. 

Qi Jinglong remained silent for a moment, then softly said, “Whether you want to listen or not, I need to tell you—so long as you abide by the rules, no matter who you draw your sword against in the future, whether you lose or get beaten up, just let me know when you return. I will reason with them until they understand.” 

Bai Shou crossed his arms, “Don’t kid me! A talent like me, having trained in the sword, would lose to anyone? Fine, I can’t take on a sword immortal for now, but for my peers, if they hop in front of me, I could easily slice them to pieces with a single strike.” 

“When you truly start training, you won’t have much energy left for boasting,” Qi Jinglong laughed. “As for not needing my help to reason, it would be best if you could draw your sword; that alone is already a form of reasoning.” 

Though Bai Shou looked unconvinced, he couldn’t help but catch a glimpse of Liu Jinglong's profile from the corner of his eye. 

The youth’s heart still felt a bit different. 

Like a tattered child in the harsh winter of his youth, basking under an elusive, warm sun. 

But this feeling was fleeting. 

Suddenly, Bai Shou exclaimed, “If I memorize the rules of the Ancestor Hall of the Taihui Sword Sect, will you allow me to drink?” 

Qi Jinglong shook his head. “No money.” 

Bai Shou angrily retorted, “No money in your pocket? Don’t you know how to chalk up a tab with that Chen guy?” 

Qi Jinglong thought for a moment, “I’m afraid of being pressured to drink, so it’s not worth it.” 

The previous money for buying wine had been borrowed from another sect, Tai Xia. 

Qi Jinglong never took extra cash or belongings when he left the sect for practice. 

Eating the essence of sunlight and moonlight, and absorbing the spirit of the heavens and earth, was all a cultivator needed for sustenance. 

As the most powerful sword cultivator in the world, he had no need for robes or any precious weapons. 

While borrowing money from her, he thankfully refrained from saying a word that could lead to further complications. 

Qi Jinglong initially intended to say he would repay it when passing by Tai Xia Mountain next time. 

But in a flash, he realized that such words would certainly lead her to misunderstand his intentions, thinking he wanted to get close to her, Gu Mo. So it was better not to say anything and just keep it in mind. 

After reflecting on this, Qi Jinglong felt that perhaps he had learned something by association, opening one door would open many others. 

Bai Shou asked, “Liu, does your Taihui Sword Sect have any particularly pretty girls? You know, those beautiful girls around my age!” 

Qi Jinglong asked in confusion, “What’s the matter?” 

Bai Shou sighed. “When they meet me, they’re truly unfortunate, destined to be infatuated with a man who won’t like them.” 

Qi Jinglong laughed. “Who taught you that?” 

Bai Shou replied firmly, “That guy who calls himself Chen the Good Man!” 

Qi Jinglong shook his head, then hesitated, realizing that guy would go to any lengths to convince others to drink, undoubtedly pouring a lot of his character into the wine jug. So he asked, “Did he really tell you that?” 

Bai Shou began to embellish the story. 

Qi Jinglong chuckled; it seemed not to be the case. 

Bai Shou was puzzled about how Liu Jinglong knew it wasn’t that guy who taught him. 

Qi Jinglong looked into the distance, “Later, come with me to meet two gentlemen; remember to say less and listen more.” 

Bai Shou slapped his forehead. 

Now hearing the word “gentlemen,” he felt a headache coming. 

In a golden sea of clouds, two cultivators stood side by side. 

One was a tall, middle-aged man in a scholar's robe, with a jade token hanging from his waist. 

The other was an elderly cultivator, bent over and carrying a long sword on his back. 

The former was the sage of the academy, currently the most famous figure in Beiju Luzhou, named Zhou Mi, who hailed from the Ritual Learning Academy of the Central Divine Continent. It was said that the academy's grand ritual wine would gift this disciple the title “Mighty Anger.” 

Indeed, after leaving the academy, this person had beaten down two unrestrained great cultivators without any chance of retaliation, loudly demanding, “Have you communicated?” What could those two great cultivators do but say they had? As a result, they received another beating, followed by a disdainful, “You call that communication?” 

However, Qi Jinglong certainly knew that this sage’s knowledge was truly exceptional, not only proficient in his craft but also well-versed in Buddhist and Daoist teachings. He had been praised by someone as “rigorously scholarly, impenetrable; gentle, respectful, and a pillar of talent.” In fact, if the sixteen-character evaluation had only twelve characters, no one would question it. Unfortunately, due to the four words “gentle, respectful,” this scholar from the Ritual Learning Academy faced considerable controversy. Just imagine, a student about to head to a different continent to become the academy sage would be given the title “Mighty Anger”—how could it possibly be related to “gentle, respectful”? 

Yet Zhou Mi took great pride in those four words. He never acknowledged the other twelve. 

The elderly cultivator, carrying a sword, was named Dong Zhu, a fallen Jade Purity Realm sword cultivator. He was a great cultivator who, despite reaching the immortal realm years ago, had never founded a sect. Instead, he continued to view himself as a wild cultivator of the mountains and valleys. For over a hundred years, he had been seriously injured and needed to recuperate on his own mountain; otherwise, every outing would be a torment. That was why he hadn’t traveled to the Hanging Mountain. 

There were rumors that sword immortal Dong Zhu was actually the preacher of the young wild cultivator Huang Xi, but neither side ever confirmed or denied it, leaving the public to speculate wildly. Since Huang Xi wasn’t a sword cultivator, most mountain heads deemed the matter absurd. 

During Qi Jinglong's battle with Huang Xi, he had similar thoughts. 

However, after truly engaging, Qi Jinglong found it hard to judge. 

Huang Xi was indeed a sword cultivator and possessed two of his life’s flying swords. 

The reason Huang Xi chose to reveal his identity as a sword cultivator rather than escape was undoubtedly due to his opponent, Liu Jinglong. 

In fact, over the years, Qi Jinglong had never mentioned it to anyone. 

As Qi Jinglong and Bai Shou descended before the two seniors, he bowed and saluted. 

Dong Zhu looked disapprovingly at this promising young sword cultivator, questioning why he was learning from a scholar. 

He found it quite unpleasant. 

Had it not been for Zhou Mi discovering Qi Jinglong’s whereabouts and insisting on a conversation, he wouldn’t have bothered to waste a single word with this land-bound dragon. 

If they were to truly interact, it would be after Qi Jinglong broke through to the Jade Purity Realm, and Dong Zhu would go to the Taihui Sword Sect to seek a sparring match! 

Bai Shou was most annoyed by these formalities and rituals. He simply hid behind Qi Jinglong, playing the part of a wooden figure. If they didn’t know him, he certainly didn’t know them; what was the point of exchanging pleasantries? 

Qi Jinglong didn’t force the boy. 

Everything could wait until they reached the Taihui Sword Sect. 

Sage Zhou Mi appeared to be an ordinary scholar at first glance, with an elegant appearance. He straightforwardly said, “Currently, neither of the two sword immortals of the Taihui Sword Sect are stationed at the mountain. You are about to break through; should the three of us ask about swords, would you like me to help stabilize the situation? So no one uses this custom to suppress you and the Taihui Sword Sect.” 

Qi Jinglong bowed again and, upon rising, smiled, “No need for Master Zhou to stabilize the situation. Whether it’s three swords or three swords, even if there are seniors with ulterior motives, I cannot stop them, nor will I blame the heavens or others.” 

Zhou Mi turned to smile at Dong Zhu. 

Dong Zhu grinned, “Alright, count me in. Add in Li Cai from Floating Duck Pond; the last one is the most dangerous.” 

Dong Zhu addressed the young man in green, “Don’t thank me; when I ask about swords, I won’t cut corners. Just don’t come crying to me later; I won’t be responsible for any typos.” 

Qi Jinglong nodded, saying, “Respectfully, I shall not express my gratitude.” 

Zhou Mi smiled knowingly. 

Dong Zhu rubbed his chin, “What makes you so cheeky?” 

Qi Jinglong smiled. “Let me break through first, then we’ll see.” 

The boy eavesdropping behind Qi Jinglong quietly thought, “Cut him, cut him, don’t hesitate. Once I’ve dealt with that Liu guy, I can run away.” 

Zhou Mi laughed, “How did you end up with such a disciple?” 

Qi Jinglong replied, “He has a good heart; the difficult ones need to be taught well.” 

Zhou Mi hummed in agreement. “That’s a fair point.” 

Bai Shou sighed. 

Dong Zhu also felt bored. 

In fact, the duo of old and young gathered together might have plenty to talk about. 

Zhou Mi said, “Qi Jinglong, I came to see you this time to discuss the matter of stabilizing the situation for your breakthrough. Since it’s unnecessary, I can save some effort.” 

Qi Jinglong hesitated for a moment, then asked, “Master Zhou, may I inquire about the outcome of a certain matter?” 

Zhou Mi smiled, “You care about this? What, do you have some connection with those two?” 

Qi Jinglong recalled the guy who had received three punches from Gu You and chuckled. “A bit.” 

Zhou Mi said, “Let’s walk and talk. I can share some insights on scholarly matters and irritate Dong Zhu a bit; that will make this trip worthwhile.” 

Dong Zhu had no other option. 

Zhou Mi’s foul temper was precisely to Dong Zhu’s taste; he asked for it. 

Dong Zhu didn’t want to discuss scholarly principles with these two well-read fellows. 

He glanced sideways at the boy. 

The boy shot back a glance. 

Dong Zhu glared, “Hey, haven’t you heard of the name of Sword Immortal Dong?” 

The boy shot back, “What if I have? I have parents and ancestors of my own; I’m not related to you.” 

Dong Zhu clicked his tongue. “You little brat, you’ve got some guts.” 

Bai Shou raised an eyebrow. “When I reach the upper fifth realm, you can come and test your sword against me. By then, you’ll know who has the guts.” 

Dong Zhu gave Bai Shou’s head a playful smack, sending him sprawling on the ground, laughing, “Do you realize what you just said? It’s like a little kid still in their diaper trying to act like a seasoned pro in the flower fields! Who taught you that? Your master Liu Jinglong?” 

Bai Shou stood up, not retaliating against the old man. He wasn’t foolish enough to act recklessly. A man must know when to be flexible. 

Bai Shou coldly huffed, “Liu isn’t my master. I only have one master in this lifetime, but I have a drinking buddy I haven’t truly acknowledged yet, called Chen the Good Man! If you have the guts, go find him—bullying me is nothing that a senior should do; he could make you run home crying with a single strike!” 

Qi Jinglong turned his head, frowning, “Bai Shou!” 

The boy immediately feigned illness. “Fine, for now, Chen the Good Man is still not as good as the old senior.” 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 638: Parting Whispers

On the ferry, Chen Ping'an had already put away the various reports from the mountain and river district. He hadn’t turned to the page with the outcome he wanted to know; the latest report from the capital city made no mention of the recent events there.

The battle between the Boundary End Warrior Gu You and the Sword Immortal Ji Yue from the Monkey Crying Mountain remained shrouded in uncertainty for both fighters.

Previously, Qi Jinglong had mentioned this matter, asserting that Gu You had always acted with caution throughout his life. He would never engage in a reckless duel for the sake of pride, nor would he venture to the Jade Seal River merely to meet his death in a duel with Ji Yue.

Standing at the bow of the ferry, Chen Ping'an flipped through several reports, and while he didn’t find the information he sought, he did uncover some noteworthy details. For instance, in ten days’ time, there would be a major battle on the Zhi Li Mountain. The two parties involved had significant backgrounds: one was the renowned wild cultivator Huang Xi, and the other was the female warrior Xiu Niang. Both were among the top ten young figures in the Northern Julu Continent, ranked closely—Huang Xi at fourth and Xiu Niang at fifth. The reasons behind this deadly confrontation varied between reports; some suggested Huang Xi had returned to his old ways, clashing with the oddly-named female warrior in the martial world, while others claimed they had quarreled over a precious artifact in a shattered cave paradise and, unable to settle their dispute, agreed to duel on Zhi Li Mountain.

This battle was highly anticipated and would surely draw the attention of many practitioners from the Upper Five Realms. One could easily imagine that the mountain near Zhi Li, which had been bought by the Qionglin Sect and had numerous immortal residences built upon it, would be crowded at that time.

On the cross-continent ferry belonging to the Pima Sect, Chen Ping'an had purchased a spirit artifact—a porcelain brush wash adorned with a powder-blue glaze that gleamed beautifully. However, he later learned he could simply charge it to his account at Piyun Mountain.

Surprisingly, the mountain and river reports also contained several pieces of news regarding the Baoping Continent, and they were quite extensive. This indicated a significant shift in perception toward the previously overlooked Baoping Continent, especially after the cavalry of the Great Li Song clan began their march from the northernmost region, heading toward the southern end at Old Dragon City. It was evident that the practitioners from other continents had begun to recognize the smallest continent in the vast world of Haoran.

The true master of the Great Li cavalry was the Boundary End Warrior Song Changjing.

After challenging the Celestial Monarch Xie Shi, he made his way to the Snowstorm Temple Sword Immortal Wei Jin at the Sword Qi Great Wall. Both individuals had made monumental contributions.

Then there was the Zhenwu Mountain's Ma Kuxuan, who had, in just six months, killed two formidable Golden Core sword cultivators from the Zhu Ying Dynasty, earning him the title of the top young practitioner of the Baoping Continent in the Northern Julu reports. He had single-handedly decimated the Tide Iron Riders, leaving the family that had made an enemy of him humiliated. A young female cultivator had miraculously survived and had become Ma Kuxuan's personal maid. In the eyes of the lead writer of one report, someone like Ma Kuxuan, who was so favored by fate, should not have been born on the Baoping Continent; instead, he ought to be rooted in the Northern Julu Continent, establishing his own sect like the female sect leader He Xiaoliang of the Qingliang Sect. It was a pity that he was destined to flourish like a dragon in a shallow pond, flapping its tail in vain.

The writer also announced that he would soon compile a list of the ten young practitioners of the Baoping Continent and then compare it with the new ten from his own Northern Julu.

The articles in the Northern Julu reports tended to emanate a sense of superiority over the Baoping practitioners. However, this was a stark contrast to the earlier days when they wouldn’t even bother to glance at it.

In addition, there was news about the Great Li’s North Peak Master Wei Bo breaking through his limits. There were auspicious omens and continuous good signs within his domain, indicating he was on the verge of becoming a Mountain God of the Upper Five Realms. This clearly showed that the fortunes of the Great Li Song clan were flourishing and should not be underestimated. The reports began to advise Northern Julu merchants to bet on the Great Li dynasty early; otherwise, if they arrived late, they might miss out on the profits. There were also subtle mentions of the Pima Sect, praising the sect leader Zhu Quan, as it was rumored that the Bone Beach’s wooden garment mountain had already established connections with the Great Li’s North Peak.

Moreover, there was a detailed discussion in the reports about the subordinate sect of the Yuguan Sect from Tongye Continent, which had chosen Shujian Lake as its location.

As Chen Ping'an read those texts, he could almost feel the writer's gritting teeth.

There was no choice.

The first sect leader of the Zhenjing Sect, Jiang Shangzhen, was someone whose cultivation level was not particularly high yet caused headaches for the Northern Julu practitioners.

This fellow had single-handedly harmed three of the ten fairy maidens from the Northern Julu in their early years. It was also rumored that two other stunning female cultivators had crossed paths with Jiang Shangzhen back then. However, whether or not there were heart-wrenching romantic entanglements remained unclear.

Thus, towards the end of the report, there was a vehement attack on the Great Li cavalry and the new emperor of the Song clan, calling them foolish for allowing the Zhenjing Sect to successfully choose a site and establish themselves in the central region of the Baoping Continent. If the Great Li Song clan had secretly colluded with Jiang Shangzhen, they would be in even deeper trouble, as there were better options than partnering with a treacherous person like him. This clearly indicated that the so-called Great Li Embroidered Tiger, who betrayed his own master and exterminated his ancestors, was not that remarkable either. Even if he had snatched an entire continent through sheer luck, he could not secure his empire and would merely be a fleeting phenomenon.

The report, which had initially been meticulously worded, with logical arguments and beautiful prose, fell apart when it came to the Zhenjing Sect and Jiang Shangzhen, degenerating into vulgar expletives, akin to a literate market woman.

Chen Ping'an was genuinely curious about the origins of these mountain and river reports.

Back when he was at Shujian Lake, he had only learned a few superficial details.

Even earlier, while in the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, there was a building shrouded in mist known as the Admiration Tower, which specialized in gathering and collecting murky tidings from the martial world.

Returning to the cabin of the ferry, Chen Ping'an retrieved a booklet written by the ferry, detailing various scenic spots along the route.

After departing from Peach Blossom Ferry, the first scenic spot was a sect located near the borders of the Water Cloud Kingdom, named Yungshang City. Its founding patriarch, through serendipity, traveled to the Luminous Cloud Continent and acquired a half-refined sea of clouds from a broken cave paradise. Initially, it only occupied an area of ten miles radius, but later, it established itself in the relatively water-rich border of the Water Cloud Kingdom. Through the continuous refinement and empowerment by successive patriarchs, it absorbed the essence of mist and fortified the sea of clouds with cloud runes. Now, the sea of clouds had expanded to over thirty miles in radius.

The ferry would remain at Yungshang City for six hours, hovering at the city’s edge.

Before dawn, the ferry slowly came to a halt.

Chen Ping'an halted his practice of the Three Stances Unity Fist, returning from a state of half-sleep and half-wakefulness. When he stepped out of the cabin, he slung a pack over his back.

Outside Yungshang City, there was a market bustling with wild cultivators, where they traded goods from the mountains, all set up by fellow cultivators.

Chen Ping'an took out some not-so-valuable spirit artifacts from his pack, which were leftovers he hadn’t sold back at the old Huai Street. While their quality wasn’t impressive, they were relatively rare and had an appealing appearance, suitable for selling to those who believed that an item worth a fortune was worth having, even if they had to pay a premium for it. This time, however, he was primarily selling a few talismans unrelated to the "True Record of Dan," most of which came from the secret manuals of the formation master among the first batch of assassins from the Deer Cutting Mountain. Among them were three types: the Thunder Department Talisman, the Great River Flowing Talisman, and the Earth Binding Talisman, all effective in battles.

Before leaving, Qi Jinglong had also taught Chen Ping'an two unconventional barrier-breaking talismans, named the "Bai Ze Road Guidance Talisman" and the "Sword Qi Bridge Talisman." Both were learned from ancient texts and did not involve any sect secrets. Although their quality wasn't high, outsiders wouldn't be able to learn them easily, as the techniques for drawing talismans were intricate and cumbersome, differing greatly from the core teachings of several current talisman schools. It was only because Qi Jinglong had explained the techniques thoroughly that Chen Ping'an was able to learn these two talismans.

Therefore, Chen Ping'an often felt it was a pity that Qi Jinglong didn’t teach at a school.

Warriors drawing talismans adhered to a pure essence of true qi, but their talismans were not long-lasting; they could only open mountains but not seal them. The advantage was that it didn’t consume the spiritual energy of the practitioner, and drawing talismans itself was a rather uncommon form of cultivation, capable of refining one’s true qi. However, Chen Ping'an found that after reaching the third level of Qi Refining, drawing talismans became much smoother, though the physical benefits had become quite minimal. He was reluctant to use up too much talisman paper, as a talisman that couldn’t retain spiritual energy equated to losing divine money every moment.

Moreover, once a real battle began, his limited knowledge of talismans wouldn’t suffice; it wouldn’t even be a mere embellishment but rather a hindrance to seizing the opportunity.

However, for cultivators, drawing talismans initially sealed the mountain, allowing the spiritual energy to dissipate slowly. Yet the greater the talisman’s power, the more easily its core would wear down. It was said that the ancestral masters who vanquished demons at the Longhu Mountain Tianshi Mansion had a forbidden area. To maintain one talisman, each generation of Grandmasters would need to empower it once every sixty years. Historically, there had been a massive upheaval at the Tianshi Mansion when the last Grandmaster ascended, and the new Grandmaster was undecided during the crucial period of the talisman’s empowerment. Because the new Grandmaster had not yet emerged, the Tianshi Seal could not be passed to another, resulting in the creation of a new talisman, leading to a slight flaw in an ancient talisman that had existed for many years. This allowed a tremendous demon that had been suppressed for countless years to escape, which led to the new Grandmaster’s first task being a disastrous visit to Baidi City, where he quarreled with the city’s Lord.

Chen Ping'an's talismans were all drawn after the Water Palace Mountain had formed a mountain-water relationship. Otherwise, it would be a scam. Although the business of the Packing Room relied on the discernment of both parties, similar to the antique trade in the mundane world, there were always bargains to be found. However, Chen Ping'an was still keen to speak about the righteousness of the martial world.

Speaking of righteousness required spending money.

These talismans required Chen Ping'an to expend a considerable amount of Water Palace spiritual energy. Yet there were gains and losses; what he lost was a portion of the Water Palace's reserves, while what he gained was the potential to gradually open up a small realm of the Water Palace, forming a hidden vein in rivers and lakes. As a result, those young green-robed children had no objections to his drawing of talismans and supported him wholeheartedly.

On the path of cultivation, how one viewed gains and losses was a question of the Dao.

As for balancing those gains and losses, it required Chen Ping'an to continually draw talismans over time, constantly exploring and honing his skills. Fortunately, those little green-robed children from the Water Palace also provided reminders.

Dressed in a black robe and holding a green bamboo staff, Chen Ping'an stepped out of the cabin and gazed around.

In the mundane royal dynasty, there were homes nestled in the depths of the white clouds. Among the mountains, there were immortal sects, indeed, cities above the clouds.

Beyond the city, there was a small bustling market town illuminated by lights.

Yungshang City was a place of cultivation, heavily guarded, and rarely allowed outsiders in. It seemed that the local environment nurtured its own people. Similar to the Caique Palace within the jurisdiction of the Water Cloud Kingdom, Yungshang City also produced a robe known as the Cloud-Soaring Robe, though its quantity and quality were vastly inferior to that of the Caique Palace, with little fame and mediocre business. Most customers were lower-level practitioners from nearby mountains, especially those wild cultivators who weighed their coin purses carefully before purchasing a single piece.

Perhaps it was due to the sect’s limited financial resources that the Packing Room market had emerged.

It wasn’t just the shops without legs; even those with stalls needed to pay a fee to Yungshang City.

The ferry came to a stop, fifty zhang away from the sea of clouds, unable to approach any closer.

Otherwise, if the bow accidentally collided with the sea of clouds, or if they got too close and the vessel brushed against the sea, it could lead to catastrophic damage to Yungshang City’s foundational structure.

Therefore, those disembarking rode upon clouds and rode magical beasts, as they pleased.

For pure martial artists below the Golden Body stage, crossing this fifty zhang distance wasn't an easy feat.

Chen Ping'an took a deep breath, stepped back a few paces, then leaped high, landing on the ferry’s railing, using its leverage to soar into the air. After gracefully touching down, he swayed a few times before standing firm.

On this ferry belonging to a subordinate sect of the Dragon Palace, a woman with a delicate face and her friend extended their hands, smiling as they said, “Hand it over.”

The two were wagering whether this young sword wielder boarding from the Caique Palace was a mountain sword cultivator or a martial rogue from the rivers and lakes. The ferry woman guessed he was a pure martial artist traveling with a sword, while the old practitioner observing the sea speculated he was a concealed young sword cultivator.

The old practitioner shook his head and said, “What if this person is just deliberately putting on a show?”

This was just stubbornness; it was clear he intended to renege on the payment.

The woman scoffed, “Our continent's young sword cultivators, which of them isn’t a cultivator of the Cave Dwelling realm, with the aura of an Earth Immortal and the demeanor of someone from the Upper Five Realms? Can you find one like that?”

The old practitioner replied earnestly, “The world is vast; it’s not unusual for someone to be modest, concealing their brilliance, and act with caution.”

The woman in charge angrily said, “Enough with your nonsense! Pay up! Just a tiny Summer Solstice coin!”

The old practitioner sighed, pulling out a divine money coin and slapping it heavily into the woman’s palm before soaring off toward Yungshang City. He had decided to disembark here to buy a better-quality Cloud-Soaring Robe for his direct disciple. After all, the women at the Caique Palace were exceedingly shrewd in their dealings, offering good products at outrageously high prices. The old practitioner had to settle for less and had previously made a deposit with the workshop in Yungshang City to create a robe tailored to his specifications, complete with cloud runes and possibly some celestial materials to enhance its effects. Afterward, he would need to work hard at the foot of the mountain, earning a meager living from various sources. It took him decades of diligent savings to finally gather enough divine money just as his proud disciple was about to enter the Cave Dwelling realm. 

Especially considering he had a small mountain to manage, like a head of the family, where every grain and every expense was a worry.

The woman was just about to express her delight when she suddenly noticed that the divine money coin in her palm felt wrong—the weight and spiritual energy didn’t match that of a Summer Solstice coin. Looking down, she jumped up in anger.

It turned out to be just a Snowflake coin.

However, the old practitioner had already used his full strength and quickly flew past the market, heading straight for Yungshang City.

After she finished cursing, her mood lightened a bit, and she smiled again. Being able to pluck a feather from the notoriously stingy old man was still quite an achievement, even if it was just a single Snowflake coin.

She was a Golden Core practitioner, not just a ferry. The Golden Core management was already sufficient.

What’s more, the Golden Core practitioners from the Dragon Palace’s cave heaven could very well be treated as Nascent Soul practitioners based purely on their status.

Aside from her own sect, she had connections with the Yuyuan Dynasty’s Yungxia Palace and the Floating Pulp Sword Lake.

For mountain practitioners, being able to earn money still meant a significant trading relationship, which was more reliable than the relationships between rulers and subjects or between spouses down the mountain.

And that old practitioner who had known her early on had a bleak future, already showing signs of aging in the Sea Observation realm.

It was worth noting that this person had once been far from the stingy stereotype, being quite suave and charismatic in their youth.

However, over a hundred years of time had seemingly worn everything away.

He was no longer the youthful and handsome figure he once was, nor did he possess the same spirit, becoming an old practitioner who spent years socializing in the mansions of the powerful down the mountain and seeking treasures in the rivers and lakes.

Yet she still liked him.

Whether she liked the man from back then or the old man now was something she herself couldn’t quite define.

Chen Ping'an entered the market, finding a spot on a bustling street full of passersby. He opened his pack to set up his stall, revealing a large piece of blue cotton cloth he had prepared.

Surrounding him were fellow cultivators; some were loudly hawking their wares, while others were waiting for customers, some yawning in indifference.

Soon, two young men and women dressed in white robes approached to collect fees—one Snowflake coin per day.

Chen Ping'an asked if it would be half price if he stayed for four or five hours.

The young male cultivator smiled and shook his head, saying it started at one Snowflake coin.

Chen Ping'an didn't say much more and handed over a Snowflake coin. The same pricing applied at the Bone Beach, where dark tea was sold.

He asked a few more questions about renting or purchasing a shop in Yungshang City and received friendly responses from the young male cultivator, who explained the various price differences based on shop grades.

In the end, this foreign Packing Room merchant, who had come down from the ferry to try his luck, merely thanked them and didn’t pursue the shop matters further. The young male cultivator remained unfazed, even wishing this young wild cultivator a prosperous opening.

Chen Ping'an squatted down, starting to arrange his goods. Among them were a hardbound yellow book of divine images, a stock of "big demons" from the Bone Beach's summer retreat, and a few items from the underwater Dragon Palace of the Cangjun Lake—around twenty items in total, all of which were far from being quality treasures. However, more importantly, there were those talismans, five types neatly arranged like an army on the opened blue cloth.

Chen Ping'an looked up to see the pair of young men and women from Yungshang City walking side by side down the street, gradually fading into the distance.

The young man seemed to be in charge of the market, greeting shopkeepers and many Packing Rooms he knew.

The young woman said little, mostly watching the man beside her.
