Her eyes spoke of silent conversations.

Chen Ping'an, with his hands in his sleeves, quietly observed this scene.

The scenery was absolutely beautiful.

The street was filled with tourists, all practitioners. Compared to the mundane folk visiting temple fairs and stalls, they were much quieter, with better patience. Most had already visited numerous Packing Rooms before but would rarely ask about prices, moving slowly. Occasionally, they would stop to examine an item that caught their eye, and after some consideration, they would quietly walk away, or some might attempt to haggle, often starting with a sharp cut in price. The more amiable stall owners would calmly recount the history of the spirit artifact, explaining its significance, while the less friendly ones simply ignored them, shrugging off the presence of those they deemed blind and poor.

Chen Ping'an soon encountered his first customer—an old man holding a child’s hand. He squatted down, glancing at the various items on the blue cloth, finally settling his gaze on a row of talismans made of yellow paper.

The old man stared intently at the five talismans.

The talisman paper was quite ordinary, but the quality of the talismans and their drawing techniques varied.

Different talismans had different values.

The old man quickly came up with an estimate in his mind and felt he had to negotiate.

To his surprise, he had only brought his grandchild out for a casual evening stroll, yet here he was with unexpected gains.

The old man pointed at a lightning talisman, smiling as he asked, “Shopkeeper, how much for this lightning talisman if I buy just one?”

Chen Ping'an smiled and replied, “One lightning talisman is eleven Snowflake coins, but if you buy all ten, it’s one hundred Snowflake coins. However, I don’t negotiate prices at this stall.”

The old man nodded and smiled, saying, “These are good talismans, but the paper quality is somewhat lacking, unable to fully harness the power of the lightning talisman. That’s quite a discount, and the price is a bit high.”

Chen Ping'an smiled without saying a word.

This person was at least half an expert.

Thus, he didn’t need to say any more.

The old man then inquired about the prices of the earth and water talismans, which were roughly similar, with each talisman differing by only a Snowflake coin or two.

The lightning talisman was the most expensive, as lightning techniques were renowned as the foundation of all techniques in the world, and the Longhu Mountain Tianshi Mansion’s very foundation was rooted in the “authentic lightning techniques.”

However, according to Qi Jinglong, this Thunder Department Talisman could only fetch a decent price if drawn on yellow paper from the Huang Seal. Otherwise, drawn on ordinary merchant's yellow paper, its power would be too average, and even ordinary Golden Core cultivators might not take it seriously.

In response, Chen Ping'an quipped, “You, Qi Jinglong, think these talismans are exceptional; do I still need to hawk them as a Packing Room merchant?”

The old man’s gaze shifted as he asked, “If I’m not mistaken, these two are barrier-breaking talismans?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, saying, “These were taught by a master, a secret not to be shared, unique in the world. I struggled for years before finally learning how to draw these talismans, but I can only assure a success rate of about fifty to sixty percent. If I sell them cheaply, I would be disrespecting that esteemed senior.”

The old man looked up at the young stall owner dressed in black robes and bearing a long sword, hesitating for a moment before asking, “Can you tell me the names of these two talismans?”

Chen Ping'an was relieved.

This was someone who truly knew their goods.

He countered, “The names of talismans often align with their true meanings and can reveal secrets of the heavens. May I ask, sir, when martial artists clash in the rivers and lakes, do they announce the names of their martial arts moves?”

The old man laughed, “Of course not.”

Chen Ping'an continued, “If you buy the talismans, even if it’s just one of each, I’m willing to reveal the names of these two secrets.”

The old man suppressed a laugh and shook his head, “Not only is it common for shops selling talismans to share some insights, but even your little Packing Room traveling the world would find it normal to sell good talismans while revealing a bit of their true essence.”

“Good things don’t worry about selling.”

After saying that, Chen Ping'an smiled and added, “However, given your discerning eye, I’ll make a deal: if you buy just one talisman, I’ll share the names of both.”

The child beside the old man widened his eyes. 

Goodness, this fellow was quite thick-skinned.

The old man actually nodded, “Alright, I’ll take that talisman.”

He pointed at the Sword Qi Bridge Talisman.

Chen Ping'an asked with a smile, “Aren’t you going to ask the price first?”

The old man replied, “In business, a good start is essential. I see that you’ve just opened your stall, and I am your first customer, so even for good luck, you should give me a discount.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “The original price was fifteen Snowflake coins. For this good fortune, I’ll sell it to you for ten.”

The Sword Qi Bridge Talisman, if its true essence could be converted into divine money, would certainly be worth much more than the Thunder Department Talisman, the Great River Flowing Talisman, and the Earth Binding Talisman.

However, in the realm of mountain techniques and treasures, offensive talismans were always priced higher than defensive ones, and barrier-breaking talismans were generally considered entry-level, making it difficult to raise prices. It relied on thin margins for mass sales.

Usually, wild practitioners from the mountains needed offensive talismans more, while scholars of talismans were more willing to pay for barrier-breaking talismans since the latter had a larger customer base and higher consumption.

The old man reached into his sleeve for a coin pouch and pulled out ten Snowflake coins, handing them over.

Once Chen Ping'an accepted the coins and was about to casually pick up a talisman, he was taken aback when the old man smiled and grabbed one for himself, tucking it into his sleeve.

What a sharp eye.

It was the most spiritually resonant one among the talismans he drew, being the last talisman he had completed.

Chen Ping'an caught a glimpse of the street behind and, using his increasingly adept heart lake ripples, subtly informed the old man, “The talisman you bought is called the Sword Qi Bridge Talisman. It contains sword intent and is quite rare. Not only does it break through geographical barriers, but it also exudes an intangible deterrent. As for the other barrier-breaking talismans, they are… ‘Road Guidance Talismans’.”

When he mentioned the second talisman, he intentionally omitted the words “Bai Ze,” as Qi Jinglong had always referred to it that way, emphasizing respect. He had written the two characters himself.

This was a trivial matter.

For mountain practitioners, it was common knowledge that Bai Ze had long been suppressed by the Confucian sages in one of the nine great towers of the Haoran realm. Even shouting “Bai Ze” a thousand times a day or cursing it wouldn’t be considered a taboo, unlike directly calling the names of great Confucian saints.

However, the fact that Chen Ping'an could become friends with Qi Jinglong spoke volumes about their shared understanding of such “trivial matters,” which were rooted in mutual respect and shared customs.

Chen Ping'an used his hand to write the five characters for the Bai Ze Road Guidance Talismans in the air.

After the old man saw it, he nodded, “The shopkeeper is honorable for not deceiving me. Therefore, I plan to buy another Road Guidance Talisman.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “The original price was fifteen Snowflake coins, but since this is a transaction with you, I’ll still charge ten.”

The old man didn’t hesitate and handed over ten Snowflake coins.

The child tugged at his grandfather's sleeve, whispering, “Ten Snowflake coins for a barrier-breaking talisman is still expensive.”

The old man smiled, “Although earning money is difficult, Snowflake coins are common. Good talismans are hard to come by. These two barrier-breaking talismans are worth collecting, making it a fortunate transaction.”

Chen Ping'an sincerely complimented, “Your insight is commendable.”

He then smoothly transitioned the conversation, “So, old sir, why not take all ten of these lightning talismans? It would be fortunate for them to meet someone of your caliber; they wouldn’t be wasted.”

Despite the child’s good upbringing, he couldn’t help but roll his eyes.

The old man pondered for a moment and said with a smile, “In that case, along with the barrier-breaking talismans, I’ll take five of each of the other types. The two barrier-breaking talismans are good, and I’m indeed tempted. So, at fifteen Snowflake coins each for those, I won’t haggle. That’s one hundred and fifty Snowflake coins. As for the remaining lightning, water, and earth talismans, which aren’t the best, I’m only willing to pay a total of one hundred and twenty for those.”

Chen Ping'an frowned, “If we average that out, that’s only eight Snowflake coins for each talisman?”

The old man replied, “Shopkeeper, considering I’m buying twenty-seven talismans in one go, that’s no small purchase. Everyone on this street can see it; I’m helping draw in customers for your stall. Isn’t that a fair statement?”

Chen Ping'an stood his ground, “No, I suspect that most of the customers on the street have already deduced that you and I are in cahoots, so there’s no real customer-drawing involved. It might even create a bad impression that could hamper my business. Honestly speaking, I’m just being sincere here.”

The child was wide-eyed, witnessing this exchange.

The old man laughed heartily, “Alright, I’ll add ten more Snowflake coins for the remaining three talismans.”

Chen Ping'an sighed, “With such great insight, you should have the stylish demeanor of a good merchant to match your standing!”

The old man straightened his face and shook his head, “If you keep bullying an honest person like me, I might just walk away without buying a single talisman.”

Chen Ping'an laughed, “Alright, alright, to celebrate a smooth opening, you’re honorable, and this little Packing Room, I can’t afford to act tough. For the sake of good fortune, I won’t charge you the extra ten Snowflake coins; for twenty-five talismans, I’ll only take two hundred and seventy Snowflake coins!”

The child didn’t think the young stall owner was generous at all. He raised his little hands, moved his fingers, and quickly calculated the price in his mind, wary that the stall owner might be trying to cheat them.

Fortunately, the price checked out.

The child put his hands away, still feeling it was too expensive, but since his grandfather liked it, he didn’t help haggle.

Otherwise, he would have been scared to negotiate himself.

The old man dug out three Summer Solstice coins along with the additional thirty Snowflake coins, bargaining with the young stall owner for a beautifully crafted hardbound divine image book and a small tea cake from the Xuanbi.

The old man then selected five of each type from the five rows of talismans.

Chen Ping'an allowed the old man to take his pick.

However, the old man’s choices surprised Chen Ping'an. With a ripple of heart lake, he softly asked, “Given your discerning eye, why not select those talismans of better quality instead of opting for the less impressive ones?”

The old man seemed quite puzzled and laughed, “Shopkeeper, your business sense is quite extraordinary.”

Chen Ping'an chose not to elaborate further.

This was where the conversation ended, and no more needed to be said.

The world is full of wonders, yet people remain the hardest to comprehend.

Once the old man left, others began to arrive.

Chen Ping'an's stall quickly became bustling.

Customers came and went, but no one was truly willing to spend money just yet.

The old man with the child drifted off into the crowd.

Chen Ping'an, with his hands tucked into his sleeves, squatted in place, rubbing the Snowflake coin he collected in his palm, which bore the engravings of “Always Envy the Jade Carver of the Mortal Realm” and “Su Zi’s Poems Resemble Paintings” on both sides.

Snowflake coins had their own unique charms, with various engravings throughout the continent. However, a coin with seven ancient characters like this one was exceptionally rare.

Besides earning an unexpected three Summer Solstice coins, Chen Ping'an was also delighted to add a newly minted Snowflake coin to his collection.

Moreover, three Summer Solstice coins had a premium value when converted to Snowflake coins, making it a small profit.

Initially, Chen Ping'an had estimated the value of all the talismans he was selling at half their actual worth.

This journey to Yungshang City had proved fruitful for his Packing Room.

Typically, any shop at a ferry in the celestial realm could sell talismans made of yellow paper for one Snowflake coin each, so his pricing was already considered high.

He hadn’t expected to earn three Summer Solstice coins unexpectedly, as they simply flew into his pocket.

Everything is difficult at the beginning.

With a generous old man serving as a good omen, he then sold two more lightning talismans.

The water and earth talismans, as well as the barrier-breaking ones, had yet to find a buyer; many customers were put off just by hearing the prices.

One rugged-looking man bought an item from the Cangjun Lake Dragon Palace, which was heavily scented and seemed aimed at impressing a woman or for offering to certain female cultivators. Upon hearing the price of five Snowflake coins, he cursed under his breath but ultimately paid up.

He pointed at the imposing Thunder Department Talisman and asked for its price.

Chen Ping'an smiled and replied, “Two ‘damns’ and two extra Snowflake coins.”

The man scoffed, “Are you slaughtering pigs or what?!”

Even someone with Chen Ping'an's audacity found himself momentarily speechless.

Nearby onlookers burst into laughter.

The man realized he had misspoken and cursed himself instead; it seemed illogical to argue. He scratched his head, caught between desire and a tight purse. He genuinely needed to buy a lightning talisman to deal with a major demon occupying a mountain. If it worked out well, he would reap substantial rewards; if it failed, he would suffer greatly. Twelve Snowflake coins were indeed a significant burden. In the end, he couldn’t bring himself to pay and left in frustration.

Chen Ping'an didn’t try to stop him.

After the man walked a distance, he couldn’t help but glance back, seeing the young stall owner smile at him. The man felt even more disheartened and strode off, trying not to dwell on it.

Chen Ping'an continued his business.

This was a relief as the prices for the talismans and all other items were fixed.

Having earned three Summer Solstice coins, his Packing Room felt much lighter.

He planned to continue as a Packing Room in the same spot, but upon entering his cabin, he immediately focused on drawing talismans.

There was no time for idleness in cultivation!

However, after drawing over ten talismans, the Water Palace stirred.

Chen Ping'an had to set his brush down.

The ferry was about to officially set sail, and there was something in Yungshang City that couldn’t be missed.

As long as the ferry docked at the sea of clouds, Yungshang City would be bustling, likely allowing them to earn some scattered divine money.

Chen Ping'an stepped out of the cabin, watching as several Yungshang City practitioners boarded three ordinary spirit boats. Over the special sea of clouds, they cast large nets to catch a type of fish that enjoyed pecking at clouds.

Of course, the flying fish could also be sold for money.

Chen Ping'an leaned against the railing, admiring the picturesque scene.

It resembled a fisherman casting nets, yet this was a sea of clouds.

Afterward, they left the boundaries of the Water Cloud Kingdom, coming to the narrow water region of the Beiting Kingdom, passing by a mountain dedicated to wishes where no temple or monastery existed.

In the mortal realm, when there are prayers, there are also offerings.

Many who originally burned incense might be thousands of miles away from home. Many devout elderly, having aged or fallen ill, unable to travel far, would entrust their younger family members to make a not-too-distant journey to the Wish Fulfillment Mountain to burn incense in reverence to the gods.

In the Northern Julu, there were several such Wish Fulfillment Mountains.

In contrast, the Baoping and Tongye Continents had no such examples.

Chen Ping'an, not being foolish, didn’t go to the Wish Fulfillment Mountain to burn incense. He neither made wishes nor offered thanks; he simply paid his respects to the mountain.

Behind the Wish Fulfillment Mountain, there was a waterfall flowing in reverse.

Chen Ping'an watched for a long time, but couldn’t fathom its meaning.

In the deep pool, there was also a spring that gushed forth whenever sword wielders and knife users drew their weapons by the water, as if responding to their actions, shooting upward.

Of course, those who yelled at the top of their lungs could also cause the spring to erupt.

But it lacked the essence and wonder of a sword or knife being drawn, which created a miraculous scene akin to a “line of heaven” appearing out of nowhere.

While observing the reverse waterfall, Chen Ping'an also took note of the sprays of water that were shouted out.

Behind him, the sword immortal’s aura rippled slightly.

Chen Ping'an said in his heart, “Can we not be so childish? You should at least display the dignity of a divine weapon, right?”

Only then did the sword immortal quiet down.

Perhaps it was because the semi-divine weapon had been referred to as a divine weapon?

Chen Ping'an felt a bit worried; could the feng shui of the Falling Mountain truly be affected by him?

That reasoning made no sense.

How could he be compared to Pei Qian or Zhu Lian? And even closer, wasn’t Du Yu from the Ghost Craft Palace an expert in this field?

After paying his respects, viewing the reverse waterfall and the spring, Chen Ping'an returned to the ferry.

He hesitated about one thing.

Whether to disembark halfway and actively seek treasures for the first time in his life.

Earlier on the ferry, some practitioners had whispered about a newly discovered cave dwelling in the Beiting Kingdom. Yet those practitioners felt there was no need to go, as there were many powerful figures from Yungshang City, Caique Palace, and several kingdoms in Beiting, along with many well-informed wild cultivators, who would have set out early. In their discussions, they highlighted how the wild, desperate mountain cultivators were the ones to fear the most; they would risk their lives for wealth, and any conflict could lead to fatal outcomes—not worth the risk.

Moreover, such openly publicized opportunities weren’t truly opportunities.

Chen Ping'an considered that the ferry route to the Dragon Palace was fixed, roughly once a month, and it would pass through Peach Blossom Ferry, Yungshang City, and the River God Ferry in Beiting. Thus, if he disembarked, he would likely delay his journey by a month.

Ultimately, at the River God Ferry, Chen Ping'an decided to disembark.

This journey, he thought, would be akin to the scholar from Lujiao County who went by the name of Lu Dun, seeking immortals and exploring the mysterious world.

A simple visit without the slightest competitive spirit, surprisingly, made Chen Ping'an a bit nervous, as he was used to not seeking outside help.

As for the exact route to the unnamed mountain, it wasn’t too difficult to find out.

There were practitioners to guide him.

He affixed a talisman from the Ghost Craft Palace’s secret travel scripts onto himself, and considering his injuries had nearly healed, though he wasn’t back to peak condition, he felt he could handle three punches from the old elder without dying.

Chen Ping'an concealed his figure, moving silently through the mountains and waters, as if he were Zhu Lian or Pei Qian, who would definitely praise him for his stealth.

That night, under the cover of darkness, Chen Ping'an rested on a high branch.

Suddenly, he opened his eyes, receiving a message from Liu Jinglong through a flying sword.

The contents of the message were still quite brief.

Just two sentences.

Gu You and Ji Yue are both dead.

Gu You drew an ancient Sword Sealing Talisman at his heart, sealing Ji Yue’s life sword for a moment, exchanging his life for another.

After feeding a divine money coin to the sword box, the message-carrying flying sword vanished in an instant.

Chen Ping'an cradled the back of his head and gazed into the distance where the flying sword had departed.

Once Qi Jinglong returned to the north, the journey would be longer, and it would be easy for the message-carrying flying sword to go forever.

So this was the last flying sword message before Qi Jinglong went into seclusion for a breakthrough.

Sitting on the tree branch, Chen Ping'an had somewhat anticipated these events, so he wasn't too heartbroken, but he did feel a sense of loss, leaving him staring blankly and abstaining from drinking. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 # Chapter 639: A Hidden Paradise

The trio traveled through the night, the gentle sound of a mountain stream flowing nearby, creating an ethereal and melodious atmosphere.

A tall, slender old Daoist, his eyes shining with wisdom, donned a flowing Daoist robe made of silk. The robe was relatively old-fashioned, adorned with intricate embroidery depicting the twelve months of the year. He carried a peach wood sword on his back and had a string of copper bells tied around his waist. Under the moonlight, the old man exuded an air of otherworldly grace.

Beside him walked a handsome young gentleman, dressed in white and carrying a short dagger with a golden sheath. The third member of their group was a scruffy man, burdened with a travel pack, who seemed to be the young master’s attendant.

Suddenly, the three paused. In the distance, by the stream, they could vaguely see someone sitting on a rocky ledge, seemingly engrossed in something under the moonlight.

The scruffy man glanced at the copper bells at the old Daoist’s waist but remained silent. The three of them felt a slight relief.

The bells were a rare spiritual artifact known as the Pagoda Bell, originally hung under the eaves of an ancient temple in the Great Source Dynasty. Later, the emperor of the Great Source Dynasty expanded the scale of the Chao Xuan Bureau, demolishing several grand halls of the ancient temple. During this period, the Pagoda Bell was lost to the people, changing hands several times before finally disappearing from public view. It was only by chance that the current owner found it on a white skeleton in a cave deep in the mountains, along with the remains of a giant python, earning a substantial profit of two hundred snowflake coins, while the Pagoda Bell remained with him.

It wasn’t about the lack of buyers for a high price; rather, it was a reluctance to part with something truly valuable, which always has a price but no market. The bell had been meticulously recorded by Yu Yuan, the owner of the Heartfelt Studio, in his book *Silent Collection*. However, in the catalog, the Pagoda Bell was listed rather low on the list. But any bell recorded in that catalog never lacked buyers.

With this bell in hand, cultivators could traverse mountains and rivers without needing various essential talismans such as barrier-breaking talismans, spirit-warding talismans, or heart-purifying talismans. While these talismans were noticeably useful for one or two trips into the mountains or waters, the costs could add up significantly over time, becoming a hefty expense. Moreover, with the bell in hand, it could be sold at any time; any ferry or immortal shop would be willing to pay a fortune, ideally selling directly to the Heartfelt Studio, to the discerning Yu Yuan.

The Buddhist bell symbolizes three meanings: awakening, joy, and preaching. This was, of course, a vague interpretation; for cultivators, the most crucial effect of the Pagoda Bell was its connection to "awakening." Whenever a demon or ghost approached, the bell would sound by itself. The more malevolent and powerful the creature, the more urgent and thunderous the bell's chime. Even the spirits and demons below the Dragon Gate realm could not withstand the warning of this bell. Additionally, it could be used to break barriers, allowing cultivators to see through and remain unconfused by the various illusions and misdirections one might encounter.

The young gentleman communicated with his companions through thought: "All three of us are skilled in close combat, but we lack someone with offensive skills and treasures. Why don’t we take a chance?"

The tall, old Daoist agreed, realizing it was a feasible idea. His seemingly ornate robe and the peach wood sword on his back were merely facades. In truth, he was a wild cultivator who had spent over a decade in a small local Daoist temple. His greatest regret in life was not having learned any authentic Daoist techniques during his time there, but rather, failing to purchase a Daoist lineage status through the temple's connection with the court. By seniority, he should have been able to buy a status, but unexpectedly, his master secretly sold the quota to a wealthy scion of a noble family. After promising to let him wait three more years, the master passed away, leaving the position to another affluent junior. Enraged, he left the temple, taking with him the temple's treasured manual, a secret book that no one had been able to decipher.

The scruffy man felt uneasy, knowing that the fellow could be anyone, and randomly adding a mysterious person to their group could easily lead to trouble.

The young gentleman laughed, "Let’s take it step by step. If it works out, that’s great; if not, we don’t lose anything. Plus, if we later split the spoils, three against one might yield us some extra wealth. Wouldn't you agree?"

The tall, old Daoist stroked his beard and smiled. The scruffy man finally nodded in agreement.

The young gentleman grinned. "Let me test the waters first. Brother Sun and Brother Huang, please wait here."

As the young man stepped forward, he advanced a few steps. The figure in black robes sitting with their back to the three still showed no signs of movement.

When the young man slightly increased his pace and advanced another ten steps, the figure in black suddenly turned around, standing up to fix a piercing gaze on the seemingly affluent young man.

The young man halted, smiling as he introduced himself, "I am Qin Juyuan, a citizen of Jiayou Country. The two friends behind me include Brother Sun, who has trained at the Thunder God’s residence on Infant Mountain, under one of the masters, the revered Jingming Zhenren! Unfortunately, Brother Sun is still a registered disciple and hasn’t yet entered the master’s hall for the lineage status. Brother Sun has traveled far, slaying demons and eliminating evils, accumulating considerable merit. After a joint demon-hunting venture, we became close friends, and upon hearing of an ancient cave appearing in the mountains of Beiting Country, we wished to explore it together for any fortuitous opportunities."

The figure in black was an elderly man, hands hidden in his sleeves, with faint ripples emanating from them. He was evidently wary of the unexpected visitors in the mountains.

The black-robed elder squinted and asked, "The Thunder God’s residence on Infant Mountain? How coincidental—I just heard of it. It is said that the unique lightning talismans from Infant Mountain can summon thunder and rain, possessing immense power. Furthermore, I happen to have a secret talisman from the Thunder God’s residence."

The elder retrieved a talisman, intricately woven with lightning patterns, holding it high and sneering, "I wonder if this Brother Sun recognizes whether it’s the Day-Slayer Ghost-Restraining Talisman or the Pestilence-Repelling Temple Talisman?"

The young gentleman stood with his hands clasped behind him, one palm open and the other clenched into a fist, signaling his companions to gauge the situation.

As he pressed down on the hilt of his dagger, it indicated the possibility of a preemptive strike. However, that was the worst-case scenario. If the opponent's talisman was of exceptional quality, they might end up just passing each other by, maintaining a peaceful distance.

But in reality, both sides had already forged enmity.

The sect masters on the mountain naturally had no need for such caution. This young swordsman, though a scion of a fallen family, was not truly from Jiayou Country; his real name was Di Yuanfeng. He had learned swordsmanship from a family of frontier soldiers, and the dagger he carried was a treasured heirloom. While he had not been in the Jianghu for long, he had already experienced the schemes of wild cultivators twice. Once with the rough-looking "Brother Huang," and the second time, he had allied with "Brother Sun."

The tall, old Daoist stepped forward a few steps and casually glanced at the talisman in the black-robed cultivator's hand, smiling, "There’s no need for such probing, my friend. The talisman you hold is undoubtedly a lightning talisman, but it is certainly not from our Thunder God’s residence; our talismans from Infant Mountain are unique, born from an ancient well where heaven and earth converge, nurturing a pool of thunder and lightning energy. The talismans crafted from this essence have a distinct reddish hue, unlike any other talisman. Furthermore, the five ancestral talismans of the Thunder God’s residence contain a secret that you clearly haven’t grasped yet. It is truly regrettable. If there’s an opportunity in the future, you may return to Infant Mountain with me, and you’ll understand its mysteries."

The black-robed elder nodded, stowing the talisman back into his sleeve, and offered a respectful bow. "I have met Brother Sun."

The young gentleman let out a sigh of relief.

Damn, these wild cultivators are as slippery as they come. They really are hard to deal with.

The tall, old Daoist was, of course, not a Daoist from the Thunder God’s residence, which was a powerful sect guarded by two Nascent Soul ancestors, one of the top-tier places in the land. It was unlikely for the surname Sun to have such good fortune to become a disciple of one of the five great masters of Infant Mountain. Although Jingming Zhenren was the last Golden Core Earth Immortal of the Thunder God’s residence, he was still revered in the eyes of the wild cultivators below.

Fortunately, since the surname Sun dared to masquerade as a wandering cultivator, he did have some understanding of the Thunder God’s residence’s talismans.

But if the other party produced a secret talisman from the ancestral hall, the surname Sun would certainly be left dumbfounded, as he only had hearsay from others. The five talismans had great significance, but what exactly they entailed was something Brother Sun had no right to know. Fortunately, even if the other party delved into the details, Brother Sun would not need to respond, for if he truly were a lineage master, how could he casually divulge the secrets of his own ancestral hall?

Thus, Brother Sun's responses were reasonable, demonstrating empathy. Even the young gentleman began to shed most of his doubts.

At that moment, the black-robed elder suddenly spoke without warning, "The divine general’s iron chains settle the mountains."

The tall, old Daoist laughed heartily, "The Five Thunder Commandments emerge from the Scarlet Palace!"

The elder visibly relaxed and bowed again, "I was rude; I apologize to Brother Sun for my previous behavior."

The black-robed elder clearly showed little interest in the young man and the scruffy man.

Di Yuanfeng felt a wave of resentment; indeed, the title of a lineage master from the Thunder God’s residence was effective everywhere. During their travels, on several occasions, he and the others had enjoyed the hospitality of lesser sects and small kingdoms simply by being associated with him.

The elder seemed to want to step down from the rocky ledge to treat the three with courtesy. Halfway down, he suddenly asked, "Brother Sun, why do you not wear the Daoist robe of the Thunder God’s residence while traveling down the mountain?"

Di Yuanfeng's temper flared. Was this ever going to end?!

He was on the verge of reaching for the dagger again.

This cautious old man certainly had a lot of variables in their alliance; at the very least, it wouldn’t be easy to just take down the three of them.

The tall, old Daoist stroked his beard and smiled, shaking his head, "Wearing the robes of the mountain would only draw unnecessary attention. Do you mean to say that the journey of cultivation should take place at a banquet?"

The black-robed elder smiled slightly and finally descended from the rocky ledge, sighing, "Brother Sun is indeed a high-minded person from Infant Mountain. This refreshing detachment from worldly riches is truly admirable. I trust that upon returning to the Thunder God’s ancestral mountain, you will surely advance further and become a direct disciple of Jingming Zhenren and the ancestral hall."

At that moment, the old fox, once seen only as a wild cultivator in the eyes of the trio, now bore a hint of reverence. Yet, his gaze remained fixed solely on Brother Sun, smiling, "I am Chen, from the impoverished Wuling Country, my Daoist cultivation is quite shallow, and my sect is not worth mentioning, merely a source of regret. I have only learned a bit of talisman writing, a trivial skill that hardly deserves any admiration. I certainly wouldn’t dare to showcase it before a master like Brother Sun. My earlier probing was merely a foolish act, and I am deeply embarrassed. I hope Brother Sun can forgive me."

Brother Sun smiled, "When traveling, caution is always wise. There’s no need for you to feel guilty, Brother Chen."

Brother Sun took the lead towards the black-robed elder, with Di Yuanfeng and the scruffy man naturally following behind.

In fact, among the three, Di Yuanfeng was originally considered the leader, so when it came to sharing the spoils, he could take 40%, while the other two would each take 30%.

The black-robed elder stepped aside to let Brother Sun "ascend the mountain." As soon as he did, Di Yuanfeng inserted himself, following closely behind Brother Sun, showing no deference to Di Yuanfeng and the scruffy man.

Di Yuanfeng and the scruffy man exchanged a quick smile. This behavior was very much in line with that of a wild cultivator.

After being cautious, they adapted to the situation seamlessly. This must be a fellow cultivator.

Good fortune.

The four of them sat together on the rocky ledge.

Brother Sun asked with a smile, "Are you also here for the cave in the mountains?"

The black-robed elder, who carried a blue cloth bag, had apparently deemed Brother Sun to be a master from Infant Mountain. After three rounds of probing, he no longer harbored doubts and revealed a hint of helplessness, speaking frankly, "Of course. However, I haven’t obtained the local government’s geomantic map, and I’ve been wandering here for quite some time. Otherwise, I would already be over a hundred miles deep in the mountains. With better luck, I could have found the cave’s entrance, which has already been opened."

Brother Sun glanced at Di Yuanfeng, who wore bamboo-staff sandals. The latter smiled slightly, retrieving a neatly folded county map, a copy of the terrain.

Geomantic maps have always been taboo in the courts of various countries, never to be leaked. The fact that Di Yuanfeng and the other two were able to copy it was undoubtedly due to Brother Sun's status. However, the local magistrate was no fool and had forced Brother Sun to display some of his Daoist arts and a dozen talismans that could be posted in the government office.

The tall, old Daoist was not skilled at drawing talismans; he had only seen a few entry-level talismans from Infant Mountain and had drawn them with about 70-80% accuracy. The secret manual he had stolen from the temple contained no talisman records. However, the talismans he drew did possess a hint of spiritual energy, enough to ward off the not-so-strong evil spirits in the marketplace.

These talismans would not actually be posted on the government’s main door but sold by the magistrate to those local nobles who were wealthy and feared for their lives.

The black-robed elder thanked him and took the map, studying it closely. "As expected of Brother Sun; you can accurately copy such a thing."

The tall, old Daoist stroked his beard and smiled, saying nothing.

The scruffy man, introducing himself as Huang Shi, fell silent again.

The black-robed elder hesitated to speak. Di Yuanfeng realized that this person had finally taken the bait.

Unfortunately, neither he nor Brother Sun had spoken a word. The other party needed to show some sincerity and investment first.

This "tension" black-robed elder was none other than Chen Pingan, hidden behind a facade.

With a weary face, carrying a long sword and slung with a bag, he looked dispirited, his eyes murky.

The supposed registered disciple of the Thunder God’s residence was something Chen Pingan had never believed from the start. Otherwise, he wouldn’t have been probing the other party’s identity with such shallow tactics.

After all, Infant Mountain was an important mountain gate on the western side of the Great Source Dynasty, and he had learned about it before coming to North Julu Continent, later inquiring in detail with Qi Jinglong about the Thunder God’s residence’s talismans.

Although Qi Jinglong was from the Taihui Sword Sect, his talismanic arts were widely known throughout the continent. 

Chen Pingan even learned that the key to the five talismans of the Thunder God’s residence was to use five ancestral seals, each representing a different title: "Great General of the Jade Court," "Five Directions Inspectors," and "Direct Hall Grand Advisor." Additionally, Qi Jinglong had personally drawn talismans to demonstrate the five thunder techniques, whose power, while not comparable to that of a true Earth Immortal from the Thunder God’s residence, still held significant worth. Chen Pingan believed that aside from the five masters holding the seals, no one from Infant Mountain could match Qi Jinglong’s understanding of talismans.

People can be infuriating.

Moreover, anger was of no use.

The reason he deliberately pretended to believe the other party's identity was because Chen Pingan hoped to use the three of them to create an extra layer of concealment for himself, rather than going to explore the cave alone.

As for how to deal with wild cultivators, Chen Pingan had some experience from his interactions with Liu Lao Cheng and Liu Zhi Mao.

Although each continent had its own customs and manners, wild cultivators were still just wild cultivators.

White wine for red faces, gold for black hearts. 

Traveling thousands of miles for wealth, leading with profit.

After weighing the pros and cons, Chen Pingan cautiously asked, "Does Brother Sun need an extra hand?"

After some consideration, Brother Sun pretended to nod in agreement. He knew that "Qin Juyuan" would obstruct him.

As expected, without needing to communicate through thought, Di Yuanfeng asked, "Brother Chen, if it were you, would you casually add an unknown companion to the team?"

Chen Pingan gritted his teeth and hesitated, pulling out a stack of yellow paper talismans from his sleeve, categorizing them, and laying them out one by one. In addition to the Heavenly Department’s Thunder Command talisman, there were also two River Crossing Talismans and two Soil Gathering Talismans, along with several barrier-breaking talismans. They were all made with gold and silver powder, in stark contrast to the fifty talismans sold at the Cloud City’s shop, aside from the material being the most ordinary yellow paper, the rest—be it brushwork, quality, or power—were worlds apart, and the prices were incomparable.

The art of talisman-making followed many rules. Just the ink used to "dip" the brush varied from ordinary red sand, gold powder, silver powder, and even the expensive immortal-grade dan shan. Among them, immortal-grade dan shan was a bottomless pit.

Thus, for cultivators who practiced talismans, drawing talismans was akin to burning money. The more authentic the sect's talismans, the more they consumed celestial money. Fortunately, as soon as talisman cultivators entered the door, they could immediately earn money to support their sect. However, talisman sect cultivators were heavily reliant on talent; one could gauge their future prospects based on the weight of their brush during their youth. Of course, it wasn’t absolute; there were late bloomers who suddenly became enlightened, but they were often the wild cultivators abandoned early on by the lineage masters.

The talismans Chen Pingan had taken out were all made with yellow paper and gold thread, which, compared to secular red sand and silver powder talismans, were naturally of higher quality.

Brother Sun glanced at the talismans and then at the black-robed elder, who was merely smiling in silence.

Chen Pingan then awkwardly smiled, pulling out the first talisman he had drawn with precious dan shan from Chun Lu Mountain and gently placing it on the ground.

Di Yuanfeng asked with a smile, “Brother Chen, where did you buy these precious talismans? They look quite impressive; I’d like to purchase some for myself.”

The black-robed elder responded with a sense of pride, "Although I’m not a lineage master, and I have no teaching from a talisman master, I do have some talent in the art of talismans..."

Just as he was about to continue, the elder suddenly reined in his proud demeanor, looking somewhat dejected. "Of course, compared to Brother Sun, my skills are merely child’s play."

Brother Sun felt the timing was right and, with an indifferent expression, said, "Brother Chen, you shouldn’t belittle yourself. To be honest, although I have practiced in Infant Mountain for many years, you should know that among the true disciples of the five masters of the Thunder God’s residence, they can generally be divided into two types: those who focus on practicing the Five Thunder True Methods and those who specialize in talismans, hoping to receive a secret transmission of a direct talisman from the ancestral hall. I belong to the former. So if Brother Chen is indeed a master of talismans, we would actually be willing to invite you to visit the mountain with us."

The scruffy man, claiming to be Huang Shi, spoke up, "I wonder how powerful the talismans that Brother Chen painstakingly crafted are?"

Chen Pingan hesitated but then picked up a River Crossing Talismans, forming a hand sign as if reciting incantations. After a moment, he tossed it into the stream, calling out swiftly, weaving his hands in intricate gestures.

The talisman dissolved upon entering the water, but its spiritual light radiated outward, illuminating the stream as shimmering strands crisscrossed.

The three men watched as the black-robed elder spoke a command and, with his fingers together, gently said, "Rise." Then, with a flick of his hands, a stream dragon shot out of the stream, circling the rocky ledge before returning to the water at the elder’s direction. The elder clearly aimed to showcase his talisman skills, and he still had some strength left; the quality of his talismans was notably high, as there was still more to come since the shimmering strands in the stream remained.

The black-robed elder lifted his sleeves, and columns of water shot skyward, swirling around the four men rapidly. In an instant, mist enveloped them, the coolness seeping into their bones.

Di Yuanfeng communicated with Huang Shi through thought, who then used his martial prowess to respond, "There’s some skill there, but the offensive power is weak. These tricks look impressive but can be shattered with just a few punches. However, if this person can control all the talismans, they’d be a significant asset since we lack a cultivator capable of ranged attacks. Moreover, a talisman cultivator is most suitable for breaking barriers."

The black-robed elder retracted his talismanic power, and the stream returned to calm, with no more spiritual light condensing. The elder took a deep breath, and his face slightly flushed.

Brother Sun thought to the two men, "Even if he’s at the cave realm, he’s likely still hiding something from us. I can still affirm that this person is definitely not a deity from the Dragon Gate realm. So, we should regard him as a cave realm cultivator or a sea-watching realm cultivator who is neither too skilled nor too weak—just right for us without posing any danger. Apart from the talisman that he revealed earlier, he must have a few genuine good talismans hidden, so we should stay vigilant."

Huang Shi suddenly focused his thoughts and said to the two, "This person’s black robe might very well be a magical robe."

Di Yuanfeng laughed, "No hurry, let’s take our time and observe. We can draw our conclusions later."

Brother Sun said to Chen Pingan, "If this trip to the mountain goes smoothly, you can return to Infant Mountain with me, and I will try to introduce you a bit."

The black-robed elder was taken aback for a moment, then his eyes shone with excitement; his lips moved as if he couldn’t find words to express his emotions. 

For a wild cultivator, being able to join a sect like Infant Mountain, where a Nascent Soul cultivator presided, was akin to being reborn.

Di Yuanfeng took all this in, then smiled, "I wonder, Brother Chen, if you could elaborate on the effects of these talismans?"

Chen Pingan pointed to the talismans on the ground and explained their functions one by one. He said little about the barrier-breaking talisman, merely stating it was a unique bridge-crossing talisman he had learned. After all, there wasn’t much to elaborate on the ordinary barrier-breaking talismans, and he was too lazy to elaborate on the water talismans he had previously demonstrated. However, he detailed the offensive power of the lightning talismans and the soil talismans, naturally raising some suspicion of self-promotion in the ears of the three.

After discussing the two critical talismans, he displayed sincerity and intimidation. This was the manner of a wild cultivator, and the same principle applied to Di Yuanfeng’s earlier demonstration of the copied terrain map.

This was the foundation that a lineage master from the Thunder God’s residence should have.

After the four exchanged pleasantries, they began to set off.

Di Yuanfeng noticed the black-robed elder had moved closer to the tall, old Daoist. 

As they walked a little further behind, Di Yuanfeng lightly shook his head, while Huang Shi maintained a neutral expression but glanced at the black robe a few more times.

Chen Pingan quietly asked, "Brother Sun, we know about the ancient cave in North Beiting. Do you think the two immortal sects of Cloud City and Caique Prefecture might join forces to occupy it and drive away all outsiders, later splitting the spoils?"

Brother Sun smirked inwardly; after all, he was just a wild cultivator visiting from afar, not daring to get too close to the local government, which meant he missed many old stories.

According to the drunken words of the magistrate of the North Beiting County, he had heard from the court officials in the capital that the Earth Immortal Shen Zhenze of Cloud City and the beautiful master of Caique Prefecture had some old grievances. The two sects had long ceased their dealings, and this seemingly worthless rumor turned out to be the most valuable—perhaps even more so than the terrain map.

If Cloud City and Caique Prefecture, two local forces, joined forces to occupy the cave, there could be no opportunity for them wild cultivators to even scavenge. It would be a blessing just to leave unharmed, let alone discussing treasures and precious resources. If these two sects became enemies, it would present a tremendous opportunity. It was not uncommon for lineage masters to fight over treasures, with bloodshed becoming common, showing little regard for the consequences, as they would face the fallout without worry, being supported by their sects.

The tall, old Daoist smiled, "Regarding this matter, my friends can rest assured. If we do meet those two sect masters, I will make my identity clear; I believe Cloud City and Caique Prefecture would show some respect to me."

However, the old Daoist quickly reminded, "But if that happens, it would hinder my ability to seek opportunities genuinely. So even if I encounter those two sect masters, barring any major misunderstandings, I won’t reveal my identity."

The old Daoist naturally didn’t want to easily disclose any insider information to the black-robed elder.

However, the black-robed elder had clearly already accepted this, praising, "Brother Sun acts with such wisdom; your composure is commendable. As for me, a rootless wild cultivator, used to eating from the hands of various factions, I originally thought I had some experience, but compared to Brother Sun, I am far from it. I feel quite ashamed."

The tall, old Daoist stroked his beard and smiled. The other party clearly was not a truly sincere person, but he had spoken some honest words.

The North Beiting Country they were currently traversing was a minor nation, while the Fuhe Country was even weaker, with little to offer. The only notable feature was a fortunate female cultivator who had long left home, perhaps providing some care for her family. Moreover, given her current distinguished background and status, even if she had heard of the opportunities here, she would most likely not come to join the fray. A cave realm cultivator could break through the first barrier of this so-called immortal residence, and what treasures lay within were unlikely to be of good quality.

Many grand and earth-shattering caves or magical treasures had appeared. 

Even if Di Yuanfeng and his group received news, without a genuine lineage master status, they would not go to their death; the pride of a young noble was hardly trifling.

Years ago, the North Julu Continent had a widely circulated *Cautionary Collection*, which became immensely popular throughout the continent. However, it was later inexplicably banned and destroyed within a year. The Qionglin Sect, which had made a fortune off it, spearheaded the ban, ordering all shops at various immortal ferry crossings not to sell this book. 

It was speculated that this was a joint proposal by several great sword immortals, praised as "hands that do not touch money, shoulders that bear righteousness," with the Qionglin Sect leading the charge. From then on, the book was no longer printed. 

Di Yuanfeng had always thought fondly of this book.

He had only heard that it was written by a foreign cultivator named Jiang, whose writing was exquisite and filled with wisdom. 

For instance, Di Yuanfeng had heard Brother Sun mention a piece of advice from the book, which warned wild cultivators traveling that if they dared to seize opportunities in dangerous places, they should be particularly wary of those with disciples of immortal beings by their side. The younger they were, the more caution was needed, because once a conflict arose, the young man would undoubtedly unleash all his strength, using treasures to kill a cave realm wild cultivator with the force of killing a Golden Core Earth Immortal, not caring about the consumption of spiritual essence. As for the wild cultivators opposing them, they would naturally meet a swift demise, like flowers blooming.

At the same time, the *Cautionary Collection* also offered countermeasures; if one truly found themselves on the verge of death, they should never stubbornly make threats but should kneel and bow, not to plead with the man, but to seek mercy from the immortal woman beside him, ensuring the bowing was loud and the cries to the goddess were fervent. They might still have a glimmer of hope.

Even if Di Yuanfeng had only heard snippets of the *Cautionary Collection*, he believed this Jiang senior was truly insightful and possessed profound knowledge.

As he traveled along the mountain path with the three, Chen Pingan looked up at the sky, suddenly feeling a bit self-deprecating.

Compared to searching for opportunities alone, he seemed to prefer interacting with others. Even if it meant dealing with those who had ulterior motives, he had grown accustomed to it.

However, he had always felt a sense of awe and fear towards this vast world. From the first time he stepped out of the Lihua Cave Heaven, he had this mindset, and it remained unchanged even now.

Otherwise, with his current cultivation level and abilities, he wouldn’t feel the need to team up with others to explore the mountain, which would ease his mind a little.

This was not a good state of mind.

But it could only be improved gradually.

In fact, years ago, Lu Tai had seen through this and advised him earnestly.

He understood that some truths were easy to grasp but difficult to act upon. Among the countless people in the world, how many were like Chen Pingan?

Currently, besides following the Great Source, he was also preparing to walk the waters for Chen Lingjun, but his own cultivation could not be delayed. Achieving the Golden Body realm had long been an urgent matter for him.

In addition, he planned to save up some money to buy one or two imitation flying swords from Hate Sword Mountain.

At the Bone Shore, he had learned a lot from Yang Ningxing, who had transformed his evil thoughts into the embodiment of a scholar. He had even showcased a replica flying sword from Hate Sword Mountain, which had impressive momentum and was quite intimidating.

Even Chen Pingan, who was no stranger to flying swords, had been deceived back then.

As long as he successfully refined them on the first and fifteenth of the month, even if they were not his innate flying swords, they could be refined into a cultivator's innate items, equivalent to having two additional offensive magical treasures.

If he managed to acquire two more imitation flying swords from Hate Sword Mountain, during a battle, his enemies would face unexpected challenges, making it even harder to defend against.

The first flying sword would be from Hate Sword Mountain; the second would come out on the first day, and the third would appear on the fifteenth. 

Surely the opponents’ psychological state would be quite turbulent.

The Jianghu is treacherous, and the mountains are windy; such deceptions are most beneficial.

The winding path beneath them wound on for more than a hundred miles toward the cave.

At that moment, Huang Shi slowed his pace, followed by Di Yuanfeng, who pressed his hand against the hilt of his dagger.

Brother Sun also sensed something was off and fixed his gaze ahead, where a dilapidated mountain pavilion stood, overgrown with weeds, appearing quite out of place, with signs of trees being cut down.

Chen Pingan had sensed the anomaly at the pavilion first.

Only a lineage master would dare to light a fire in such an open manner at night, and they must have considerable influence.

A burly man stepped out from the pavilion, and Chen Pingan immediately recognized his identity.

It was Gao Ling, a military general from the Fuhe Country.

Previously, while fishing with the filling-sea immortal, the armored Gao Ling had boarded the ship with a fierce demeanor but had been pushed back onto the ship by Chen Pingan's palm.

Aside from Gao Ling, who wasn’t donning his Ganylu armor, there was also an unfamiliar martial artist, who seemed quite imposing.

Perhaps he was another Golden Body realm cultivator. 

Though it was uncertain whether he was a local master from North Beiting or a martial artist from the Fuhe Country, the latter was less likely, as the Fuhe Country was small and its customs seemed to value literature over martial arts, so their martial prowess was limited.

As for the woman who had once protected Gao Ling on board, she was undoubtedly a female cultivator. Later, during a chat at the tea house of the Caique Prefecture's Peach Blossom Ferry, Chen Pingan learned from the innkeeper that there was a young woman of noble descent in Fuhe Country, named Bai Bi, who had been taken in as a direct disciple by a sect from North Julu Continent at a young age. Estimating the time she had left home and considering her appearance and rough realm, the girl who had returned on the ship must have been the disciple under the leader of the Water Dragon Sect, Bai Bi.

Then Chen Pingan asked a rather awkward question, "Brother Sun, should we just walk past the pavilion?"

Brother Sun remained expressionless, calm and composed, saying nothing, giving off an air of an immortal.

However, Di Yuanfeng felt a headache coming on.

Turning back, Di Yuanfeng frowned slightly, while the scruffy man, Huang Shi, maintained his usual demeanor.

Chen Pingan understood.

It seemed that this venerable elder from the Thunder God’s residence, Brother Sun, still hadn’t figured out who among the three of them was the true recluse.

The scruffy Huang Shi’s breathing and footsteps indicated he was merely a pure martial artist of the fifth realm.

But this was something that Chen Pingan excelled at—identifying individuals who were intentionally holding back.

It was unfortunate that experience could sometimes reveal traces, and indeed, he seemed to be a Golden Body realm cultivator. 

If only this master were more approachable.

As for himself, Chen Pingan felt that as a third realm Qi cultivator, being approachable was not out of line.

Gao Ling and the other martial artist stepped out of the pavilion, standing firm without retreating back indoors.

So, Chen Pingan wisely suggested, "Brother Sun, I believe that the other party is not easy to deal with; they seem ill-intentioned. Perhaps we should take a detour?"

Brother Sun, relieved, nodded, "As cultivators, we should avoid unnecessary conflicts."

Thus, the four prepared to leave the winding path. 

However, unexpectedly, a dashing young man in splendid garments emerged from the pavilion, with a crystal-clear jade flute at his waist. In winter, he held a folded fan and lightly tapped his palm, smiling at the four travelers, "Meeting is destiny; why rush along? How about we chat in the pavilion instead?"

Upon seeing the young man with the flute, Chen Pingan couldn’t help but recall He Lu, whom he had dealt with at Cangjun Lake, the crown prince of Huangyue City, who had been kept hidden by the city lord Ye Han.

He Lu had once been renowned as one of the finest couples alongside Yan Qing from the Baodong Immortal Realm, celebrated across a dozen kingdoms.

Di Yuanfeng lowered his voice and said, "He looks like the most famous young lord of North Beiting."

The only son of the heroic lord of North Beiting, Zhan Qing, was known to be a flirtatious and romantic figure, whose reputation was mixed; he would be condemned for seducing noble ladies from the North Beiting but praised if he entangled himself with influential women from other kingdoms like the Water Cloud Kingdom or the Fuhe Country.

As for this young lord, there seemed to be no rumors of him practicing martial arts or cultivation.

At this moment, regardless of how Brother Sun and Di Yuanfeng scrutinized him, they couldn’t discern his true nature. From the looks of it, he appeared light-footed, his words lacking conviction, likely just a frivolous young master enjoying the comforts of his noble household.

Chen Pingan, too, was unable to gauge the depths of this North Beiting young lord.

This required a cautious approach.

The young lord’s expression darkened, "What’s this? The four mountain immortals, relying on your identities and cultivation, think you’re above us? Do you think I must kneel and bow before you to earn your respect?"

Chen Pingan felt a twinge of emotion; if it weren’t for his substantial backing, he would not have survived until now.

However, this showed that the Cloud City and Caique Prefecture were indeed generous immortal sects.

Otherwise, if the lineage masters from those two sects had been domineering over the years, how could these local noble scions live so freely? They would have been beaten and learned their lesson long ago, having to bow their heads in submission.

At the very least, they shouldn’t act so arrogantly in front of unfamiliar cultivators in a narrow encounter, practically asking for trouble.

After exchanging thoughts with Brother Sun and Di Yuanfeng, they decided to take a detour to avoid the confrontation.

If they were to be pursued, it would only mean they would have to go all out, fighting for their lives. Did they really think wild cultivators were just timid believers?

Just then, a graceful young female cultivator emerged from the long-abandoned pavilion, followed closely by a hunchbacked elder with little to no breath.

The woman glanced at the four travelers standing awkwardly and smiled at the young lord, "Let it go; they are just a luck-seeking band of wild cultivators. Let them pass."

Zhan Qing nodded and returned to the pavilion with the woman, while Gao Ling and the attendants also stepped aside.

The four travelers could finally resume their journey. As they passed the pavilion, Brother Sun felt a chill run down his spine.

Everyone kept their gaze fixed ahead, not daring to look back at the scene within the pavilion.

Di Yuanfeng felt a weight on his heart; this treasure-seeking mission had suddenly become a significant variable.

When the four had moved far enough, within the pavilion, Zhan Qing revealed another side of himself, grasping a dry branch to poke at the campfire, casually saying, "Those wild cultivators are no trouble. The real issue comes from the two disciples of Shen Zhenze from Cloud City. Even if Shen Zhenze himself doesn’t follow, at least one of his Dragon Gate realm attendants will likely be dispatched. Especially the temper of the ancestor from Caique Prefecture, Wu Qian, has always been poor. In other words, we need to be cautious about offending these two neighbors, rather than the opportunities within the cave."

The young woman smiled, "Cautious? I can help you make a trip to Caique Prefecture and Cloud City."

Zhan Qing raised his head, exasperated. "Sister Bai, it’s not that simple. Down here, we seek long-lasting stability; there’s no sense in being on guard against thieves."

Then Zhan Qing smiled, "But once you become a Nascent Soul, it’ll be a different story, and I can rest easy."

It turned out that this young lord had known Bai Bi since childhood, the female cultivator who was treated with great respect by the emperor of the Fuhe Country.

Since then, they had maintained a correspondence.

Bai Bi, aware of the situation, was not particularly interested in the opportunities in the cave, even if it was within the boundaries of the Fuhe Country. She had come to see Zhan Qing, effectively acting as the protector of this North Beiting lord. Zhan Qing was also a cultivator, and his master was quite reputable; however, his master was an eccentric wild Nascent Soul cultivator. Zhan Qing’s journey to become this man’s disciple had been fraught with trials, and he had endured considerable hardship, which Zhan Qing himself understood well enough not to mention to outsiders.

This was also why Bai Bi maintained a long-term connection with this noble young lord from a small country.

Otherwise, if she had merely found a cute child in the past, her feelings would have long since faded during her cultivation journey.

Later, with Zhan Qing’s help, Bai Bi managed to secure a nominal position as a protector at the Water Dragon Sect.

Both parties had gained something from the arrangement.

However, upon seeing Zhan Qing again, Bai Bi had a peculiar joy.

She never expected that the adorable child she once held in her arms had grown into such a handsome figure. After Zhan Qing's persistent pursuit, she agreed to a private arrangement that if they both reached the Golden Core realm, she would formally become his Dao companion. While Zhan Qing was still merely at the cave realm, he was already considered an exceptional cultivator.

As for the ordinary women Zhan Qing had kept in his gilded cage, they meant little to Bai Bi. 

A decade would pass, and their beauty would fade; in thirty years, they would be old and gray.

Moreover, Zhan Qing’s heart was resolute, treating so-called beauties of the mortal realm more as playthings, similar to collecting art and treasures, without much distinction.

However, once Zhan Qing reached the Dragon Gate realm, the prospect of becoming Dao companions would change the dynamics entirely. If Zhan Qing continued to dally and mingle with the mundane world, he would have to be cautious that he could end up turning into an enemy instead.

Fortunately, Zhan Qing was not foolish.

Bai Bi held back the truth from him—she had already attained the Golden Core realm, belonging to the ranks of true cultivators of the mountain.

Thus, even without relying on her identity as a disciple of the Water Dragon Sect, she had reasons to instill some degree of fear in the two immortal sects of Cloud City and Caique Prefecture.

Bai Bi took out a small porcelain bottle from her sleeve, poured out its contents, and extended her palm. A small fish, azure and green as if carved from jade, crawled onto her fingertip, tilting its head slightly to face Zhan Qing.

Zhan Qing’s keen intuition made him shiver immediately.

Bai Bi lightly flicked the fish’s head with her finger, and only then did it obediently lay down. She smiled, "This is a rare Niuhou fish from the deep pond of our Water Dragon Sect, appearing once every hundred years. Its voice can roar like thunder; when facing you, its cry can rival the force of a blow from an Earth Immortal. I just received this as a reward from the sect. When we part ways, I’ll send it to you."

Zhan Qing's expression remained unchanged. He turned to look at the captivating woman illuminated by the firelight and softly said, "I hope that in this life, the Niuhou fish will always remain in Sister Bai’s hands."

The implication behind the young lord's words was that they would only meet again without parting.

Bai Bi’s face flushed with embarrassment, and she scolded playfully, "Flattery! You’re all talk and no action; you’re quite skilled at charming words!"

Zhan Qing wore an innocent expression.

Among the group of four, aside from the stoic Huang Shi, the other three sensed the underlying tension between the young couple.

Chen Pingan was the first to break the silence, not wanting to make Brother Sun feel awkward. 

He asked a common question, "Brother Sun, is this bell the Listening Demon Bell?"

The tall, old Daoist nodded, "I found it by chance; its quality isn’t exceptional. It can sound whenever a cave realm demon approaches."

Chen Pingan marveled, "That must be worth quite a bit of celestial money. It wouldn’t go for less than a hundred celestial coins!"

Brother Sun chuckled, "That sounds about right."

Di Yuanfeng, still feeling unsettled, thought about the North Beiting young lord’s appearance. He felt self-conscious about his own looks. The audacity of this young lord to bring a female companion along while they were on this precarious treasure-seeking venture was infuriating! Moreover, the young woman was clearly a cultivator with lineage!

It was no surprise that a few wild cultivators would have two powerful martial artists as their attendants.

As for Huang Shi, he maintained his usual expression, carrying the heavy bag and walking at the back of the group.

After passing the pavilion, the four of them walked at a brisk pace.

The winding mountain path stretched for over a hundred miles, and even seasoned country woodcutters found it challenging. Yet for the four of them, it felt like walking on flat ground.

This was the advantage of cultivation.

No matter how rough the roads of the mortal realm were, cultivators could traverse them without a care.

While the world was full of dangers and perils, cultivators seemed to effortlessly smooth things over.

As for the worries along the path of cultivation, it felt as though they were merely standing and talking, not needing to complain of back pain.

After over a hundred miles of hiking, they encountered no one.

With some basic geomantic skills, Brother Sun could easily discern the terrain, leading the three to a secluded cliff area. A dark, deep cave lay at the foot of the cliff, devoid of any stele or inscription, with vines hanging from either side. This plant could stabilize the terrain among worldly flora. The tall, old Daoist plucked a vibrant green leaf from the vine, crushed it between his fingers to smell it, nodded in satisfaction, but said nothing further. 

Then, the old Daoist began to pace, occasionally stamping his feet before finally crouching down to grab a handful of earth, weighing it in his hand. He then turned to ask, "Since you can draw soil talismans, you must be quite familiar with the nature of the earth. Do you have any unique insights? This might be helpful for us to enter the residence."

Chen Pingan appeared troubled.

Di Yuanfeng narrowed his eyes.

Huang Shi also turned to look at the black-robed elder, who was now showing signs of hesitation.

With a sigh, Chen Pingan took a few steps forward, varying the weight of his footsteps, seemingly trying to identify the soil, and spoke as he walked, "I suppose I should humbly share my knowledge, but with Brother Sun here, I worry it may be a joke. However, since Brother Sun has instructed me, I’ll dare to share some of what I've learned."

Chen Pingan crouched down to pick up a bit of soil, tossing it lightly before holding it in his palm and rubbing it gently. After releasing it, he moved to several other spots, repeating the process, and finally said, "Indeed, this soil has been enriched with spiritual energy, likely soaked for at least three hundred years. Due to its moist and heavy nature, it is far denser than ordinary soil. In worldly residences, or even in graves, if this soil is added, it can assist in gathering wind and water."

After finishing his explanation, the three men saw the black-robed elder apologize, saying to wait a moment, before hurriedly removing his bag from his shoulder. Turning his back to the group, he began to rummage through his belongings, taking out a small porcelain jar and hastily digging soil to fill it. However, he only managed to collect a little from several spots, and in the end, the jar couldn’t be filled.

Seeing this scene almost caused the tall, old Daoist to lose control and join in the digging.

But realizing that he was now a master from the Thunder God’s residence, Brother Sun refrained from following suit.

Chen Pingan adjusted his pack and clapped his hands, grinning, "Just earning a little pocket change; I hope I don’t make a fool of myself."

At this moment, Di Yuanfeng could finally confirm that if this old fellow were truly a lineage master, he could easily swallow that bamboo staff hiding a soft sword, including both bamboo and sword.

Then, the three of them noticed that the elder had fallen into a daze.

Brother Sun had no choice but to remind him, "Friend, shouldn’t you take out a barrier-breaking talisman before entering this residence?"

Although this first barrier was merely a common mountain water illusion, similar to being lost in a maze, it had already been broken by the previous unfortunate souls who arrived earlier. Yet, the following mechanism was life-threatening. Out of caution, it was still necessary to use a barrier-breaking talisman to clear the way, and anyway, the talisman wouldn’t cost the three of them anything.

Chen Pingan affected a look of sudden understanding, pulling out a common yellow paper talisman made of gold powder.

However, he quickly turned to glance back down the path, troubled, "That young lord is not far behind us."

Di Yuanfeng laughed, "If we can’t take the lead now, will we just hand over the treasures to that young lord if we find them?"

Only then did Chen Pingan lightly flick the talisman with two fingers, and it ignited, illuminating the path to the cave.

However, he did not lead the way but held onto the slowly burning barrier-breaking talisman and offered it to Di Yuanfeng, smiling ingratiatingly, "Why don’t you take the lead, Young Master Qin? My old bones can’t withstand even the slightest pain; if I accidentally trigger a dangerous mechanism and injure myself, I could still speak about it, but if it leads to a major disaster, it would be unfortunate."

Di Yuanfeng looked toward Huang Shi, who was studying the stone walls of the cave.

Huang Shi showed no hesitation, taking the barrier-breaking talisman and stepping toward the depths of the cave.

The four of them wound along the path for several miles, still not reaching the end.

A cool breeze blew, yet there was no sense of any malevolent aura.

This reassured Brother Sun somewhat.

The previous owner of this immortal cave must have been a benevolent lineage master. Although there were life-threatening mechanisms beyond the barriers, the first illusion was a kind reminder, and according to the wild cultivator who had escaped, the illusion caused no harm; two prior entries had resulted in merely going in circles, and when the time was up, one would be confusedly led out of the cave. Otherwise, in an ordinary abandoned residence, the first barrier was typically a perilous existence, not to mention that cultivators trespassing into someone else's dwelling were deserving of death.

Because the four of them walked slowly and cautiously, it took them a full half hour to arrive at a cold and eerie cave chamber.

Brother Sun had to say many times before the black-robed elder would take out another barrier-breaking talisman to illuminate the path while also guarding against lurking evils.

During this time, Brother Sun, considering the value of that talisman and his own life, carefully told the black-robed elder about the prohibitions of this journey.

These were lessons learned at the cost of two lives from the previous wild cultivators.

Brother Sun certainly didn’t want this fellow to act rashly and trigger mechanisms, dragging the three of them to their graves.

On the stone walls surrounding the chamber were vibrant, newly-painted murals depicting four heavenly kings, towering over three meters tall, exuding an imposing presence, their fierce eyes gazing down at the unexpected guests.

The four lifelike figures held weapons drawn, cradled pipa, entwined with serpents, and held up umbrellas.

Underfoot was a bagua formation, carved with the ancient design of two dragons fighting for a pearl. However, the spot where the pearl should have been was slightly sunken, empty of anything—likely taken by some previous visitor.

Brother Sun only glanced at the divine statues but felt a prickling unease.

Still, he forced himself to pull out a small compass from his sleeve carefully.

The compass was small but intricate, with over thirty-six layers both inside and outside. If an ordinary person were to hold it, they would likely be left dumbfounded by the complexity.

The tall, old Daoist began to walk around the bagua formation, "wandering" beneath the feet of the four heavenly kings.

Di Yuanfeng softly reminded, "Brother Sun, it’s best to hurry. Once that North Beiting young lord enters, we’ll be trapped like fish in a barrel. According to the lucky wild cultivator, as long as we don’t touch the four divine statues, we can mess around without any concerns. He wouldn’t dare make such claims if he didn’t have confidence, or he’d have no way to leave North Beiting."

Brother Sun's scalp began to sweat, and he replied seriously, "Care must be taken; we should be cautious."

Huang Shi glanced at the statue holding the sword and then shifted his gaze to the pipa strings.

Di Yuanfeng crouched down, carefully examining the two stone dragons that had lost their pearls.

Huang Shi suddenly halted his gaze, focusing on a spot that extended from the sword's tip, crouching next to one of the statues to peer closely. He squinted, spotting some minuscule writing that even a cultivator would find challenging to notice. However, much of it had been erased, leaving only a few trivial words. Judging by the traces, it seemed to have originally been two or three hundred characters, but the crucial parts had been completely wiped away. It was highly likely that someone had intentionally left behind these useless words to frustrate later visitors.

The writing on the wall near the statue remained, and now only the phrase "…of good nature, fond of visiting immortals, with a bamboo staff and straw sandals, having traversed numerous mountains, but this mountain is the most serene—yet this place has many prohibitions, which must not be overlooked. Should there be future peers who chance upon this place, they should…"

And the last interrupted phrase "focus on what lies beyond the sky… ancient dragon pool in the rain…" clearly resembled a poet's nonsensical verse.

Huang Shi was infuriated.

Undoubtedly, it was the previous visitors who had intentionally obscured this precious clue.

However, Huang Shi glanced at Di Yuanfeng, who was just as much a bamboo staff and straw sandals type. 

Could it be that this fellow was the one truly fated with this place?

Chen Pingan crouched down beside Huang Shi, who was also left confused. Di Yuanfeng was no exception.

But relative to the others, Chen Pingan was the most indifferent.

If he were to unlock the second layer of the cave’s barriers, he would only need to remain alert; why bother?

Yet Chen Pingan quickly sighed, silently reminding himself that this kind of thinking was not advisable.

Huang Shi suddenly spoke, "If I use a ground escape talisman, will it really trigger the mechanisms?"

Di Yuanfeng replied solemnly, "That’s confirmed! The previous wild cultivator attempted it and met his end. Unless it’s that legendary talisman that can shake the mountain without a tremor, there might be a chance, but I suspect it would require consuming many talismans, which are invaluable. Even if we could obtain them, it would likely not be worth the cost."

Chen Pingan had no idea what the mountain-opening talisman was, but he shifted his mindset and began to genuinely observe the characters, frowning. He spread his palm and gently stroked the letters and the extensive wear marks.

Then Chen Pingan said, "Could it be possible that the writings and the erased parts were done by the same person, and the opening clue has been hidden within these characters all along?"

Huang Shi scoffed audibly, showing no restraint. 

Looking back, the tall, old Daoist was still fumbling around like a headless fly.

Huang Shi figured that if all else failed, he would have to resort to force.

As for whether the other three would die under the mechanisms, that would be left to fate.
