But Di Yuanfeng found some merit in Chen Pingan’s words, focusing his gaze on the remaining text and pondering carefully.

Di Yuanfeng stood up, leaning back to inspect one of the statues, then slowly turned and glanced at the other three fierce-looking statues.

Then Di Yuanfeng walked to the center of the chamber, extended one hand, bent his knees slightly, and lowered his palm.

Finally, Di Yuanfeng crouched down, his open hand resting below a dragon’s claw.

Di Yuanfeng said to the tall, old Daoist, "Can you calculate the precise hexagram of this place, Brother Sun? Surely you can do this!"

Brother Sun, holding the mountain compass in one hand, wiped the sweat from his forehead with the other, then quickly tucked his hand back into his sleeve, swiftly forming hand signs while his eyes fixed on the point where Di Yuanfeng's palm rested, murmuring, "The death gate is not logical."

Di Yuanfeng kept his palm pressed against the ground, his expression brooding, urging, "Why would Daoists fear death?! Brother Sun, can’t you see through this?"

Moments later, Brother Sun exclaimed, "This is an auspicious place!"

Di Yuanfeng then turned his palm over, gently making a fist and striking the ground, yet there was still no response.

Di Yuanfeng frowned.

Huang Shi approached, pressing his ear to the ground, then looked up and said, "There’s an echo, like the sound of dripping water, but it’s unusual. This must be how to trigger the correct mechanism."

Di Yuanfeng took a deep breath and struck the ground once more.

In an instant, phenomena erupted.

The bagua formation beneath them began to spin, transforming quickly, leaving spectators transfixed. There was no longer an arrangement, and both Chen Pingan and the old Daoist found themselves jumping around, but each time they landed, they found themselves shifted out of position, looking quite out of sorts. However, it was still better than one of them stumbling and falling, as the ground shifted beneath them like a blade.

Di Yuanfeng and Huang Shi stood firm, their feet rooted, avoiding unnecessary movement. The ground occasionally offered resistance, causing them to lightly push off their toes, but they remained in place, showing more grace than the other two.

The two originally lifeless green dragons seemed to have lost their restraints, wanting to swim into the sea.

As for the entrance to the cave chamber, the heavy stone door had already crashed down, and even Huang Shi couldn’t intervene in time, let alone attempt to escape.

Di Yuanfeng surveyed the surroundings, ultimately fixing his gaze on the only unchanged spot—the indentation where the pearl had once been placed.

Di Yuanfeng called out to Huang Shi, "Pass me the wine flask!"

Huang Shi passed over a flask, and Di Yuanfeng removed the mud seal, pouring it into the indentation.

The ground shifted slightly.

Di Yuanfeng felt a sense of assurance and turned to shout, "Chen, hurry up and take out a water talisman; don’t bother with fancy techniques! Just transform it into water!"

Chen Pingan flicked out a water talisman, tossing it into the air, where it transformed into a column of water imbued with spiritual essence. Di Yuanfeng reached out, cupping the water in his hand and gently placing it in the indentation.

In the blink of an eye, a splendid light erupted in the cave chamber. Huang Shi was the last to close his eyes; the black-robed elder was the first, and only after that did Huang Shi feel at ease with him.

The four figures swayed.

It felt as though they had crossed into another world.

Brother Sun stumbled to the ground, feeling dizzy and beginning to vomit.

As for Chen Pingan, he was worse off, already sitting down and dry-heaving.

Di Yuanfeng straightened up, looking around, the smile on his face couldn’t be restrained as he burst out laughing, "What an extraordinary hidden paradise in the mountains!"

This immortal cave was teeming with spiritual energy, far surpassing the worldly kingdoms of North Beiting, invigorating the spirit.

In the distance stood a majestic green mountain, with tranquil waters winding at the foot, creating a small realm where the air was thick but refreshing. 

On the high mountain, pavilions and towers were built in layers along the slopes, continuing endlessly. At its peak sat an ancient Daoist temple with a roof covered in green glazed tiles, surrounded by flocks of cranes circling in the sky.

This was what one would call a paradise on earth.

Huang Shi slowly stood up, but he believed that Di Yuanfeng had already guessed he was not just some ordinary fifth realm martial artist.

But at this point, what did it matter?

This Di Yuanfeng, a mere fifth realm martial artist with a broken sword and a few techniques, wouldn’t dare challenge him.

If not for the many unforeseen events that might still occur, Huang Shi could easily eliminate the three of them, as if he were wringing the necks of three chicks.

Di Yuanfeng grinned, "Brother Sun, Brother Chen, Brother Huang, our collaboration this time was truly a testament to the power of sincerity! It’s evident that we should all occupy this land of fortune together!"

Brother Sun shook his sleeves, stroking his beard and smiling, returning to his former transcendental demeanor.

Yet, the lingering taste of wine mixed with meat in his mouth made him reluctant to speak.

Chen Pingan observed his surroundings, feeling a sense of nostalgia.

If he had been alone in that chamber, he might have pondered longer and discovered clues, but Di Yuanfeng’s hand had landed precisely on the death gate of the bagua formation, which might have caused him to feel anxious. However, this Brother Sun was able to rely on the compass to deduce that place was indeed an auspicious spot for life and death transitions. This encouraged Di Yuanfeng to strike without hesitation.

As for needing the water talisman, Chen Pingan had not tried to hide it; he had already drawn the talisman before Di Yuanfeng could remind him.

The other party had likely taken notice, and though they hadn’t paid attention at the time, they were beginning to appreciate it now.

Chen Pingan was merely indicating to Young Master Qin that while his cultivation might be lacking, his mind was still sharp, so if they managed to find themselves in an immortal cave, even if they engaged in treachery, it would be better to wait a little longer before taking action.

In the cave chamber, two young men and women stood alongside the two elders, one of whom smiled as he stored away a talisman that had appeared from thin air, gently turning it into ashes.

The earlier scene of the four successfully breaking the formation had been witnessed and heard by all.

If Chen Pingan had been present, he would have immediately recognized the three individuals: the old man from Cloud City from whom he had purchased talismans, and the two young men and women patrolling the market streets.

They were none other than the old master Huan Yang and the two direct disciples of Shen Zhenze from Cloud City.

The young woman expressed her surprise and shock, curiously asking, "Did Master Huan predict that this group of wild cultivators would lead us to the door?"

Huan Yang chuckled, not pretending to be a wise man, shaking his head. "They’ll be near the cave entrance soon. Along the way, several talismans have already stirred; this old man merely wished to avoid conflict. In a narrow encounter, with no retreat, would we engage in a fight? Moreover, although the North Beiting young lord has yet to leave the pavilion, his attitude suggests he considers this place his own. If we make a fuss, he’ll likely come rushing in, resulting in a chaotic three-way battle with more casualties. Your city lord’s master sent you down to experience the world, not to seek death.”

Huan Yang walked to where the ground had returned to its original state, lamenting, "So, in the path of the Great Way, sometimes retreating a step is akin to advancing several steps."

Huan Yang suddenly laughed, "Ah! No wonder you two seventh realm martial artists are here; with just one punch each, you’ve already smashed my two valuable roadside talismans. There must be a master among your group; an ordinary martial artist would never perceive the subtle ripples of the talismans. Or perhaps that young lady is actually a Golden Core Earth Immortal?"

The young woman, feeling anxious, asked, "Why doesn’t Master Huan quickly trigger the mechanism?"

The old elder from Cloud City slowly replied, "If those wild cultivators are lying in wait, consider this: if you two act rashly and move forward with a punch, will you live or die? Even if you survive, you’ll be injured; isn’t that still a loss?"

The young couple exchanged concerned glances, feeling a sense of dread.

The elder hesitated before asking, "Master Huan, can I collapse the cave's entrance?"

Huan Yang smiled, "If you aren’t afraid that the other party would lose their way and we would have no way back, then you can naturally act without hesitation."

The elder fell silent.

Huan Yang, catching a glimpse of the two youngsters, sighed inwardly, discerning the clear distinction in character between the two.

The young woman was anxious, while the young man remained calm.

If this continued, it would be uncertain whether they could become immortal companions.

Within that spiritual cave filled with energy, Chen Pingan felt like a fish back in water. 

He could easily imagine the little green-robed boys in his own Water Palace getting busy soon.

*(The chapter ends here.)*

 **Chapter 640: Treasure Obtained**

The four paused for a moment, exchanging a glance before Di Yuanfeng, with his hand resting on the hilt of his sword, nodded at Master Huang. Together, they sprinted toward the distant green mountain.

Earlier, where they had landed, there was a large round blue stone resembling a coffered ceiling pattern, which should have been positioned above the interior of a Daoist temple. To their surprise, in this fairy realm, it lay beneath their feet. 

At the center of this coffered ceiling design was a lotus blossom, encircled by two intertwined dragons, and further surrounded by sixteen flying celestial beings. The layers were numerous, intricately detailed, and exquisitely beautiful.

Di Yuanfeng struck the stone multiple times with his bamboo staff, producing a sound like metal striking stone, indicating its unyielding nature. 

However, even though he could potentially move it, Di Yuanfeng dared not act recklessly, as they needed to pass through this place to leave the fairy mansion's ruins. The reason he and Master Huang feigned a pause earlier was undoubtedly precautionary. If someone had secretly followed them into this place, they would have to face the consequences of their actions.

Lagging behind, Chen Ping'an discreetly withdrew a Yang Energy Lantern Talisman, still showing no signs of malice. Compared to the outside world, the talisman burned much more slowly here, likely due to the abundant spiritual energy (Qi) in this location. The other three merely glanced at it before dismissing it.

Between the green hills and clear waters lay a white jade arch bridge. It resembled a white rainbow resting upon the water.

The bridge's railings and pillars were intricately carved with a variety of mythical beasts, each unique, crafted with such skill that they appeared to be slumbering creatures.

Near the water's surface beneath the bridge were large stone piers, carved into the likeness of one of the legendary dragon species, sporting two horns and covered in dragon scales, sculpted in a crouching position, peering into the water.

Chen Ping'an fell into contemplation. 

The creature beneath the bridge was not an exceptionally rare beast statue; it was merely odd that its name was quite peculiar. 

In the realm of Haoran, it was generally referred to as "Baxia" or "Eight Summers," but in the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, Chen Ping'an had seen this creature while traversing the rivers and bridges of the southern garden country. Its appearance differed slightly from that in Haoran. According to the books that National Master Zhong Qiu had retrieved from the Ministry of Works, the one Chen Ping'an had read the most was "Yingzao Fashi," which recorded this creature as a "Gongwen," a water-avoiding beast that could swallow entire rivers. It was said to have been raised by an ancient master of the rivers and lakes and was rumored to have been boiled alive by the Fire God using methods of lake boiling and sea burning.

However, there were no such bizarre records in Haoran. Only vague mentions of the dragon's nine offspring were noted, and there was certainly no mention of any "master of the rivers and lakes."

Suppressing his thoughts, Chen Ping'an pulled out a Sword Qi Bridge Crossing Talisman. After a moment of hesitation, he chose not to hand it to Master Huang and the others, instead walking directly onto the arch bridge.

There was no wind, no waves, and no danger.

Chen Ping'an crossed the white jade arch bridge, turning back to wave, signaling that there were no traps, and it was safe to cross.

The other three had their own thoughts. Sun Daoren felt that this Chen Daoist likely thought they were about to enter a treasure mountain and wanted to show off a little. It was futile; this Daoist was destined to die regardless. Back at the rocky cliff by the stream, he shouldn't have agreed to accompany them, let alone enter this treasure-laden fairy mansion's ruins together. But just as he thought this, the tall, lean Daoist was suddenly alarmed, wondering if he might also encounter misfortune.

The young clerics of the ledger were on their way down the mountain for training, seeking treasures and cultivating their skills. As long as they didn't run into hostile sects, they usually got along amicably; even if they were strangers, revealing their identities would establish a bond of Daoist affinity and shared incense. The dynamics were generally not too ugly.

However, among the mountain dwellers and wild practitioners, most formed small groups of three or four. Fewer wouldn’t accomplish anything, while more often led to many disputes; the slightest disturbance could lead to internal strife before they even reached the point of sharing the spoils. Competing with ledger clerics for opportunities was like ascending to the heavens, so during the competition, they were usually more willing to risk their lives. Once trapped in a desperate situation, loose cultivators might even unite against a common enemy, unwilling to part with their capital. However, once the spoils were divided, what was so hard about backstabbing? As wild practitioners, if the overall situation was settled, yet none had thoughts of devouring the benefits alone, what sort of wild practitioners would they be?

Di Yuanfeng noticed Sun Daoren's wandering gaze and chuckled, "What's wrong? Are you worried that Huang and I will trick you? It's such a rare blessed land; how much can we three really carry away? Since we can't take everything, is there really a need for us to kill each other?"

Hearing this, Sun Daoren felt it made sense and couldn't help but stroke his beard, squinting with a smile.

The three crossed the white jade arch bridge. Sun Daoren, taking advantage of the moment when no one was watching, squatted down to touch the surface of the white jade bridge. It wasn't the ordinary sheep-fat jade of the secular world; wasn't this yet another pile of immortal wealth just lying there? 

Sun Daoren tapped it lightly with his fingers, the sound crisp and melodious. 

It was as enchanting as hearing the gentle clinking of two small summer coins for the first time, captivating and endlessly pleasurable.

As Di Yuanfeng approached the mountain gate, he looked up at the staircase leading straight to the mountain peak and said with a smile, "Let's take a detour, enjoy the scenery, and confirm there's no one around before we head straight to the top."

The other three had no objections. 

At the mountain gate stood a simple yet massive archway, boasting the bold characters "Cave Heaven Blessed Land." 

The couplets on either side were still carved from stone. 

"Silent and motionless, communication is divine." 
"The one who gains its elegance is the most spiritual."

Chen Ping'an stared at these couplets for a long time.

In truth, they were not even close to being parallel. 

But the tone was grand, and the meaning profound.

Master Huang was the first to look away from the plaque and couplets, his gaze shifting to the distance and the heights. 

Di Yuanfeng instead looked toward the back of the archway, where thirty-six stone monuments stood at varying heights, but for some reason, the inscriptions on them had all been worn smooth. 

It seemed this relic could only convey its origins through the four characters "Cave Heaven Blessed Land," which were nearly meaningless. As for the couplets, they were even more bewildering. 

Sun Daoren looked up at the ancient seal on the plaque and clicked his tongue. "What a hodgepodge of terms; it's only fitting it was destroyed."

Throughout history, cave heavens and blessed lands have undergone many changes; they were not immutable. They could be shattered by powerful cultivators or could mysteriously vanish. Alternatively, a cave heaven could fall to become a blessed land; yet Sun Daoren firmly believed that there was no such thing as "the world's cave heaven." Moreover, while the spiritual energy here was abundant, it should still be somewhat lacking compared to the legendary cave heavens, as records from various unofficial histories on the mountain often linked cave heavens to "spiritual energy as thick as water." This place, with its dense water flow, was still far from that assertion.

Compared to the other three, Chen Ping'an had a deeper understanding of cave heavens and blessed lands. However, he had never heard of "the world's cave heaven." As for inferring the era of the cave dwelling based on architectural style, that was futile, as Chen Ping'an's knowledge of the North Continent was still quite shallow. 

In times like this, he couldn't help but feel a deeper admiration for the ledger clerics who came from sect backgrounds. The depth of a mountain's foundation truly required generations of patriarchs to accumulate.

He could only take note of it, and if given the chance, he would return to sketch the main architectural structures and later show them to Cui Dongshan. 

Di Yuanfeng withdrew his gaze and nodded with a smile. "Quite peculiar indeed."

Afterward, the four set off again, moving briskly past grand halls, pavilions, and corridors, occasionally spotting withered bones littering the ground, suggesting that those corpses had suddenly perished. 

No one attempted to enter through the doors. 

They still wanted to investigate the Daoist temple at the mountain peak first. 

Generally speaking, the most valuable treasures were found at higher elevations. 

This unknown fairy mansion was rife with fine scratches, but none were particularly deep. 

It was as if a sudden downpour of Sword Qi had struck without warning, catching everyone off guard. 

This sword strike was undoubtedly the work of a sword immortal; it was just unclear whether they were from the Jade Purity realm or an immortal sword cultivator. 

As for why there had been such a peculiar sword strike, with Sword Qi flooding the area, it seemed to accurately target people as if it were waiting for them to be struck. 

Chen Ping'an looked up. 

It was truly anyone's guess. 

In any case, this vast fairy sect had collapsed and vanished in an instant. 

As they continued upward, the atmosphere grew increasingly silent. 

Sun Daoren walked anxiously, as if a bucket of cold water had been poured over him, instinctively reaching to rub the pagoda bell at his waist. 

What if there were demons or ghosts hiding here? 

Or perhaps among these corpses, someone had died and their soul condensed into a vengeful spirit, occupying this fairy mansion for who knows how many years, and they had been a fool in life, yet should have transformed into a ghostly being by now? 

Thus, Sun Daoren felt the need to rub the pagoda bell more to find some peace of mind. 

In fact, this bell had its own peculiar use; the closer a lowly existence approached, the more frantic and frequent the sound of the bell would become. The higher the realm, up to the Dragon Gate realm, the more it would annoy the bearer with its noise. However, if a Golden Core demon were nearby, the pagoda bell would not shake violently; to outsiders, it would appear entirely still, yet it would quietly ring once in the heart lake of its owner after being refined.

It was the pagoda bell's subtle warning that had allowed Sun Daoren to escape a calamity. 

Sun Daoren could only hope that this time, the bell would not sound in his heart lake. 

The three allies had discussed that dealing with a Dragon Gate realm cultivator, even if they had a magical artifact, wouldn't pose too much of a problem for a ledger cleric. 

Thus, Sun Daoren hoped that the more violently the pagoda bell shook, the better, as long as it didn’t disturb the heavens. 

As the four passed those corpses, Di Yuanfeng would wave his sleeve, and the clothes worn by the bones would disintegrate into dust from the shockwave. Moreover, many ornaments that should have contained spiritual energy still met the same fate, turning to ash. 

Only the bones remained, untouched by the force. 

Another strange occurrence. 

After ten or so attempts, with no results, the tall, lean elder began to take action, trying to imitate Di Yuanfeng, but regrettably, his luck was poor and he still failed to find a single robe. 

Di Yuanfeng turned to Master Huang, saying, "How about you give it a try, Brother Huang? Perhaps the winds of fortune have shifted."

Indeed, after that, Master Huang did find something on the mountain staircase, waving his arm, and the clothes on the corpse remained intact, prompting Sun Daoren to rush over to strip the garments. 

To hell with the divine demeanor of the Thunder God! 

I’m just a wild practitioner who has never touched even half a summer coin in my life! 

However, even after acquiring them, Sun Daoren painfully handed them over to Master Huang. 

This was the rule among wild practitioners. 

Of course, there were even greater rules awaiting the four, but for now, it seemed that it was all up to this Chen Daoist. 

Sun Daoren rarely felt a twinge of compassion. 

Could it be that he should show some Bodhisattva-like kindness and persuade Di Yuanfeng and Master Huang? 

If everyone were to return loaded with treasures and it was impossible to empty this place of its hoard, then there would be no need for killing and looting, right? 

But Sun Daoren hesitated, deciding to wait and see what they could find before discussing other matters. 

Otherwise, if in the end, they couldn't even fill one or two bags, his indecision and softness would only lead to resentment from those two, and who knew, they might even decide to eliminate him too.

Chen Ping'an kept trailing behind the three. 

After finishing the last step, he arrived at the white jade plaza in front of the Daoist temple, where he spotted two smaller corpses. After Di Yuanfeng waved his sleeve, their clothes vanished, but each left behind one relic. 

However, the two mountain treasures were heavily cracked and marred in appearance. 

Di Yuanfeng squatted down to collect them, carefully stowing them in his sleeve. 

Master Huang remarked, "It seems that the spiritual artifacts here aren't in very good condition." 

Di Yuanfeng nodded, laughing, "Then let’s win by quantity." 

Sun Daoren was overjoyed. 

Master Huang also revealed a rare smile. 

Chen Ping'an still did not join in; he was accustomed to considering an escape route before discussing treasure hunting.

Standing at the mountain's peak, he gazed out, taking in the scenery. Beyond the green hills and clear waters, he could see everything within a hundred miles—just varying distances and blurred vision. However, further still, there appeared to be a remarkably clear boundary, beyond which a sudden transformation made the world shrouded in mist, giving Chen Ping'an a sense of oppressive emptiness, as if he had reached the end of the road.

This was both a good and a bad thing. 

The good was that this fairy cave was a legendary land without roots, akin to the shattered ancient cave heavens, not truly built within the mountains and waters. 

It indicated that this fairy ruin had a long history and profound origins, perhaps holding treasures of immense value, or even a couple of secret texts pointing directly to the Earth Immortal realm.

The bad thing was that entry was easy, but exit would be difficult, unless someone could break the restrictions of this small world. 

With a sword immortal behind him, Chen Ping'an certainly could do so; he believed that even the firmest canopy couldn't compare to the ghostly valley of bones. 

Yet at that time, he would become the target of all the mountain heads, which contradicted his original intention of "sneaking around to pick up small treasures and quietly leaving."

Chen Ping'an did not wish to become the second Jiang Shangzhen, becoming a pariah among the cultivators of the North Continent, hunted by all.

The reason Master Huang and the others felt so at ease was likely that they had yet to notice the strange phenomena in the mountains and waters beyond. This indicated that Master Huang, a martial artist of the Golden Body realm, was not just a paper tiger, but neither was he particularly strong.

The existence of that line held little significance for Chen Ping'an at the moment. 

However, if the worst-case scenario occurred, he would be the only one who could see and escape from this small world. 

The other three remained oblivious, possibly planning how to backstab their Daoist friend. 

The Daoist temple before them was small, the plaque missing. Before entering, all four couldn't help but admire the green glazed tiles on the roof. 

In a place with so many buildings, only this spot had such tiles. 

Years rolled by, yet the tiles still shimmered; they were clearly not the kind of ordinary glazed tiles found in the palaces or noble houses of the secular world, but true treasures of the mountains, objects used by the immortal families. 

In short, every single tile was worth an immortal's coin. 

This scene made Sun Daoren tremble all over, estimating that each tile could be worth seven or eight small summer coins. If these were truly high-quality tiles crafted using immortal methods, perhaps he could even exchange summer coins for rainy season coins! 

Both Master Huang and Di Yuanfeng, coming from purely martial backgrounds, could not accurately assess the value of these glazed tiles, much like Sun Daoren. However, among the sects and fairy mansions they had encountered, none had ever covered their rooftops with such tiles; they were more common in the secular world below.

Chen Ping'an finally looked back at where the four had come from, noticing still no movement. 

There was one question he wanted to ask the person below if he had the opportunity. 

Roughly, at what hour had they entered this small world? 

In fact, Chen Ping'an had been keeping track of time all along. 

If the flow of time within this place significantly differed from that of the Haoran world, then he had better and worse plans. 

The young lord of North Pavilion, Zhan Qing, and his entourage arrived at the cave's entrance. 

The martial artist from the Huqi Kingdom, Gao Ling, spoke in a deep voice, “Young lord, there are many people hiding near the mountain.” 

Zhan Qing laughed, “They’re just eating our dust. If they have the courage to enter the cave, they should also have the courage to reincarnate.” 

He held no fondness for mountain dwellers or ledger clerics. 

Even though he himself was a genuine practitioner, perhaps deep down he was still a scion of nobility, accustomed to scheming with cunning while relying on his fists and a few treasures, rather than the brutality of killing. Therefore, Zhan Qing felt utterly annoyed with those high and mighty fellow cultivators. 

However, when it came to a situation where he needed to kill, Zhan Qing would not hesitate. 

Bai Bi joked, “Aren't you the least bit worried? What if those two groups get ahead of us?” 

Zhan Qing replied with a laugh, “If they can refine immortal treasures and consume secret texts in the blink of an eye, even if I have bad luck, I’d just have to accept it. Otherwise, where could they possibly escape to?” 

Gao Ling began to see Zhan Qing in a new light. 

Previously, he had thought of the young lord of North Pavilion as a waste who had simply been born into a good family. 

Now it seemed that anyone who underestimated this person during the so-called 'great way competition' would surely find themselves in hot water. 

The two Golden Body realm martial artists led the way, holding candles as they stepped into the dark cave. 

Bai Bi felt relaxed; as long as there were no major accidents, this treasure hunting trip would not require her to act personally. 

Even if the likes of Caique's Sun Qing and Yunshang City’s Shen Zhenze were to come in person, they would only be minor inconveniences. 

The two Golden Body realm martial artists in her party were enough to handle everything. 

They reached a cave chamber adorned with four painted murals of celestial kings. 

Zhan Qing frowned slightly; breaking formations was not his forte. His Yuan Ying master, a wild practitioner, had a mixed bag of skills and should be well-versed in this, yet he never taught Zhan Qing anything about seeking opportunities in secret realms, always saying that such tricks would hinder his cultivation, and he could discuss it once Zhan Qing reached the Dragon Gate realm.

Since the first group of wild practitioners and the Yunshang City cultivators had vanished, they must have entered the fairy mansion ruins one after another. 

Bai Bi smiled, "What should we do next? Just stand here staring at each other?" 

Zhan Qing replied helplessly, “If we knew the exit location, we could wait for a rabbit. What I fear is that we might be separated by a hundred miles and not discover anything.” 

Bai Bi placed her hands behind her back, surveying the surroundings. “Let’s look for clues. If that fails, you’ll owe me a huge favor.” 

Zhan Qing asked, “Is the price steep?” 

Bai Bi nodded, “Not small. It would cost me a decade of cultivation.” 

This direct disciple of the Water Dragon Sect cautiously summoned a rare talisman, an ancient blue talisman depicting flowing water, simple yet peculiar. The water drawn on the talisman appeared to flow gently, and one could even faintly hear the sound of water flowing. 

A Golden Core cultivator from a sect who was willing to refine a talisman into a life-bound artifact meant that this talisman was at least of magical artifact quality. 

Bai Bi explained, “This is an ancient talisman my master obtained by chance years ago, from the ruins of one of the three ancient shrines in Jidu, named the Inch Gold Talisman. It has many marvelous uses, especially for cultivating water techniques, yielding twice the result with half the effort. There was some unpleasantness in my sect regarding its ownership, but that’s not worth mentioning. One of its uses can help us enter the secret realm.” 

The Inch Gold Talisman was also known as the Talisman of Time. 

It was enigmatic and profound. 

Though Zhan Qing was uncertain about the talisman's origins, he still shook his head, “Let’s pass on it.” 

Bai Bi sighed, “I’m already a Golden Core Earth Immortal, equivalent to ten years of cultivation for a Dragon Gate realm qi practitioner. What’s the big deal? The greater the difference in realms, the more disparate the results. It's the same for qi practitioners and martial artists.” 

Zhan Qing smiled wryly, “Sister Bai.” 

Bai Bi smiled back, “Just calling me Sister Bai is enough.” 

Even Zhan Qing, with his cold demeanor, found it hard to resist wanting to reach out and hold her hand. 

But Bai Bi shook her head, maintaining her calm demeanor. “Many of those sheltered in your golden nest would willingly die for you. Why are you not moved? Just because I’m a Golden Core Earth Immortal and would lose a few years of my cultivation, you feel touched? Such sentimental attachments are better left aside. If in the future, a Yuan Ying female cultivator were to make such sacrifices for you, would you not then change your affections? True immortal companions on the mountain are far from such superficialities.” 

Zhan Qing felt as if he had been struck by lightning, left speechless. 

Bai Bi suddenly said, “Before using the Inch Gold Talisman, let’s first ponder for clues and avoid charging in recklessly. The fists of the two Golden Body realm martial artists shouldn’t be wasted. If neither works, then I’ll take action.” 

Zhan Qing felt somewhat relieved at this. 

Looking at the enchanting Bai Bi, he felt a bit estranged. 

Huan Yun appeared in this fairy cave and immediately placed a unique talisman on the three individuals beside him, concealing their presence and aura. 

As for the ripples in their auras while walking, Huan Yun, merely a Golden Core Earth Immortal from the talisman sect, couldn’t achieve perfection like a Daoist deity with celestial techniques. 

The old cultivator from Yunshang City sighed in relief; avoiding an ambush was a good thing. 

Huan Yun suddenly said, “You all can wander about now. Aside from life and death struggles, I won’t concern myself with you three. The gains and losses beyond life and death are all up to fate.” 

Then Huan Yun smiled, “Rest assured, I won’t compete with you. At most, I’ll just pick up what you leave behind or what you failed to discover.” 

Huan Yun’s form dissipated like mist, leaving no trace. 

The old cultivator and the two juniors laughed. “Huan Zhenren always keeps his word. Let’s go, and you two should focus on how to deal with the wild practitioners.” 

Hearing the underlying meaning in the protector’s words, the woman worriedly asked, “What about you, Master?” 

The old cultivator replied helplessly, “Should I really pick up things for you two and carry them? Did you come here just for a leisurely outing? Am I your porter?” 

The old cultivator soared into the wind, wanting to see just how high the canopy of this cave was and, from a height, to observe the greater mysteries hidden below. 

But being cautious, he summoned a spirit artifact that wasn't his life-bound object, rising into the air to avoid crashing into mountain formations. 

Entering this unowned fairy mansion ruin, there were certainly treasures to be found everywhere. 

But there would also be hidden dangers waiting for those picking up money. 

In fact, the old cultivator felt both happy and worried. The opportunities here were undoubtedly great, beyond imagination. This was not the dwelling of a Dragon Gate realm cultivator but an entire sect. Just judging by the scale of the buildings, it was not at all inferior to Yunshang City or Caique's mansion. 

Thus, when the city lord Shen Zhenze handed him that small object, it was the perfect decision. 

What worried him was that this fairy mansion could not be taken away. If it were truly the cultivation ground of a Yuan Ying Earth Immortal or even a top five realm cultivator, once they returned to Yunshang City, as long as there was a hint of news leaked out, when they came back for treasure hunting, it was likely that not a single Golden Core would be able to salvage even a bit of the leftovers. They would only be taken by the sect closest to them, using the legendary mountain-moving divine ability to relocate it. 

The sects nearest to Beiting country, one to the west and one to the north, were not far from here. That slight difference would be negligible for sect cultivators who had their own boats. 

This old cultivator could only hope that the former owners of this place were merely nameless Earth Immortals, and that their realms were not too high. 

The best would be Golden Core; having a Yuan Ying would be troublesome, making follow-up difficult. 

It was possible that a ledger cleric from a sect background would visit Yunshang City without needing to exchange words, and the city lord would have to surrender most of the juicy bits, complying with their demands and still worry about their dissatisfaction. 

If a top five realm cultivator were to take residence in the mountain's ruins, there would be no hope left; it would certainly be a case of fortune and calamity coexisting. 

Unless they could immediately shatter this small world and destroy all traces of it in one go. 

Unfortunately, Yunshang City could not do that. 

Unless Shen Zhenze acted decisively, after their return to Yunshang City with Huan Yun, actively reaching out to one of the sects to negotiate a fair division. 

As for this place, with its dense water energy and so many impressive buildings, it would naturally become a summer retreat for that sect in the future. 

The spirit artifact meant to scout ahead flew freely without obstruction. 

The old cultivator felt reassured and soared into the air. 

Just as the old cultivator reached several hundred zhang above the ground, the spirit artifact shattered with a loud bang. The old cultivator sensed something was amiss and was suddenly yanked downwards toward the ground. 

With a jolt, the old cultivator relaxed; it was merely the old Daoist Huan Yun who had pressed down on his shoulder, carrying him down to the ground. 

Then, the old cultivator noticed a thin thread of aura above his head flicker by in an instant, vanishing without a trace. 

Huan Yun said in a deep voice, "I advise you not to go further up. Even Golden Core Earth Immortal martial artists cannot withstand that thread of sword qi patrolling the area." 

Earlier, the old Daoist had sent several patrol talismans into the sky, only to find that whenever a talisman ascended, it would instantly disintegrate into powder. 

The old cultivator looked up; the earlier aura had already vanished without a trace. 

The Dragon Gate realm cultivator from Yunshang City was shocked. “Could it be that there's a sword immortal guarding this ruin?!” 

Huan Yun, who had quietly circled around the green mountain, shook his head. “All are dead; there are no living beings or ghostly entities left. Only this sword qi continues to exist in this small world.” 

Huan Yun’s expression turned grave. “Let me tell you a piece of good and bad news: this place is an ancient cave heaven that shattered, leaving behind a mysterious region, roughly a hundred miles in radius. The age of this small world is hard to say; it could be a thousand years or even older. However, I estimate that this mountain cave's existence quietly perished around seven to eight hundred years ago, which is strange because there has never been a sect like this in Beiting's history.” 

Huan Yun halted his descent, hovering a hundred zhang above the ground, maintaining a wind barrier with the old cultivator, and slowly said, “This leaves only one possibility: this small world was carried here after the sect perished, unknown to the world. For some reason, this immortal could neither occupy this secret realm nor cultivate smoothly. Perhaps they suffered misfortune, and the treasure capable of carrying this small world fell unnoticed into the deep mountains of Beiting. Or perhaps this person, upon reaching Beiting, no longer traveled far, hiding here to quietly cultivate, eventually fading into obscurity and reincarnating.” 

Huan Yun sighed, “Life and death are uncertain; the great path is unpredictable.” 

Each time he contemplated this matter, it inevitably left him somewhat disheartened. 

But after his moment of reflection, Huan Yun suddenly snapped back to reality, remembering the words he had said to Shen Zhenze in Yunshang City, and quickly returned to normal, with no shadow of gloom in his heart. 

Daoist cultivation, self-deception leads to others’ deception; thus, it has become the most difficult hurdle to overcome among the three teachings and a hundred schools. 

The old Daoist Huan Yun was indeed gifted, but all the Earth Immortals along the great river of the North Continent believed that Huan Yun had a bright future in the realm of talismans, aligning with his own great path, leading to his current success. 

Yet Huan Yun understood, this was akin to a mute eating bitter herbs, unable to express his sorrows. 

Once, a great figure had stated that had Huan Yun entered a sect early on, and not learned those intricate talisman tricks, he would have long since been a Yuan Ying cultivator with the potential to reach the top five realms.

Thus, regarding the matters of gains and losses, Huan Yun felt deeply affected. 

In times of helplessness, the only thing he could do was treat it as a practice of his Daoist heart to ease his worries. 

At the peak, the Daoist temple housed a statue of a middle-aged Daoist sitting in a meditative posture, gazing forward with his palms placed together in front of him. 

On the incense table was a small brass incense burner, still containing half a furnace of ash. 

Everyone knew that this shining little incense burner was undoubtedly a crucial artifact of the Daoist sect, yet no one dared to touch it. 

Di Yuanfeng quietly asked, “Sun Daoren, have you seen this person’s likeness in your sect's statue register?” 

Sun Daoren shook his head, “Never seen him.” 

There was something he didn’t dare to say aloud; this Daoist’s appearance was unremarkable, and the entire statue gave an impression of being plain and ordinary, not even as shocking as the four celestial king statues in the cave chamber. 

Chen Ping'an observed the statue, recalling the time he traveled with an old Daoist from the East Sea Temple in the flowing waters of the Lotus Flower Blessed Land for over three hundred years. Occasionally, he would see the old temple master appear in a similar sitting posture, though it was rare. Perhaps to ordinary people, this posture seemed unremarkable, but Chen Ping'an had a vague feeling that there was a resemblance between the old temple master's true Daoist essence and this middle-aged Daoist’s statue. 

Chen Ping'an remembered four characters from a Daoist classic. 

“Leaving the Realm, Sitting in Forgetfulness.” 

Time flows ever onward. 

The cultivators are unaware of the changes in seasons below the mountain; the departed leave only a statue, no matter how profound their Daoist skills were in life, what does it matter? Do they not know how the seasons change? 

In the end, how high can a Daoist ascend through their cultivation? 

Chen Ping'an sighed internally, taking out three incense sticks from his possessions. After igniting them, he placed them in the small incense burner. 

Sun Daoren thought this Daoist friend was being overly idealistic, did he really hope that the statue would still have a remnant of its essence just because he lit three incense sticks? 

Master Huang and Di Yuanfeng did not stop this person from lighting the incense. 

In fact, they were more curious to see if the black-robed elder's reckless act of burning incense would trigger any mechanisms or bring about opportunities, or perhaps cause a deadly mishap. 

After all, the little incense burner was something they would definitely take with them; having someone willing to take risks to explore was even better. 

When the three incense sticks had burned down with no response, Di Yuanfeng laughed, saying, “Brother Huang has already obtained a magical robe, and I’ve acquired two ornaments; so what does that leave for this incense burner? Sun Daoist or Brother Chen?” 

Chen Ping'an smiled, “I’ll pass. There are so many buildings in the mountain that I haven’t explored, and after we split up, I’ll have enough to keep me busy. If Sun Daoist wants the incense burner, feel free to take it.” 

Master Huang said, “I can exchange that magical robe for the incense burner with Sun Daoist.” 

Sun Daoren felt a pang of regret but still nodded in agreement. 

Master Huang tossed the magical robe, then went to pick up the incense burner and put it in his pack. 

He then cleared out the worthless clothes and jars from his large bag, tossing them casually on the ground. 

Then he tore the bag in half, giving one half to Di Yuanfeng as a makeshift carry-all, casting a glance at Sun Daoren, who looked awkward. “Sun Daoist, with such a large robe on, wouldn’t taking it off just turn it into a bag?” 

Sun Daoren suddenly realized, feeling delighted. 

The four of them busied themselves within the small Daoist temple. Di Yuanfeng found a pristine white mat, while Sun Daoren tore off several pieces of unknown golden silk fabric. 

Master Huang speculated that there might be secrets hidden within the statue, so he suddenly struck the entire statue with a punch, only to yield nothing. 

At that moment, Chen Ping'an was crouched on the ground, pressing his hand against the damp blue bricks, knocking and tapping. Just as he was formulating a plan, he heard the commotion and looked up at Master Huang, who smiled broadly at him.

Sun Daoren was startled, while Di Yuanfeng merely glanced at the shattered statue on the ground, which was merely the least valuable painted wood, before losing interest in it. 

The four stepped out of the Daoist temple, and just as Sun Daoren crossed the threshold, a series of explosive sounds erupted from his waist. 

It turned out that the pagoda bell had exploded. 

Sun Daoren wailed, “This is terrible! It must be our disrespect that has angered this Daoist immortal!” 

Master Huang and Di Yuanfeng exchanged glances, without any hesitation, descending the mountain to search for treasures in other buildings. 

Sun Daoren hesitated for a moment, choosing not to follow Di Yuanfeng but instead rushing after Master Huang while shouting for him to wait, dashing forward. 

Soon, the small Daoist temple behind them collapsed with a thunderous crash, sending dust flying and shrouding the sky. 

Chen Ping'an, however, did not hurry down the mountain like the others. 

Instead, he began to collect items that the other three were unwilling to take. 

For instance, the heavy, space-consuming green glazed tiles, as well as the blue bricks that contained rich water energy. 

Aside from the bag he slung over his shoulder, Chen Ping'an also had the small and inch-sized objects. 

He had cleared out a lot of space in his shop in Chunlu Garden on Old Huai Street. 

Yet what Chen Ping'an truly wanted to collect was the broken wood from the statue that Master Huang had smashed. 

In the ruins of the Daoist temple, Chen Ping'an moved at a steady pace. 

He carefully gathered the shimmering glazed tiles, while simultaneously tossing aside the odds and ends among the ruins of the temple, meticulously selecting the broken wood from the statue, searching for fragments while loading the glazed tiles. 

It was said that the Glazed Pavilion in Baidi City had specially crafted blue tiles, layered upon the rooftops, earning the reputation of “The glazed tiles on the Glazed Pavilion reflect the clouds like azure waves.” 

After collecting all the broken wood from the statue, Chen Ping'an also loaded one hundred and twenty glazed tiles, causing him to feel somewhat peculiar. 

One, looking up, it seemed as if he had moved the temple ruins to a different spot, from the original site to the white jade plaza. 

Moreover, those blue bricks, imbued with strands of water energy rather than ordinary spiritual energy, left Chen Ping'an in a dilemma. 

To completely collect the glazed tiles from the temple roof and the blue bricks on the ground, it would seem impossible even with more inch-sized objects. 

However, regarding this, Chen Ping'an felt no hesitation. 

Instead, among the inch-sized objects, he placed some old and worthless items. 

Compared to the blue bricks infused with strands of water energy, or the other opportunities and treasures awaiting him in the various halls and pavilions, they were worlds apart. 

Chen Ping'an squatted on the spot, hands tucked in his sleeves. 

He looked up, stroked his chin, and stood back up, trying to carry more blue bricks and glazed tiles. 

Not a single old object among the inch-sized items was discarded. 

Finally, Chen Ping'an lit three more incense sticks and inserted them into the crevices between the blue bricks of the temple ruins. 

Once they had burned down completely, he lightly blew a breath, scattering some ash. 

When digging up the blue bricks, Chen Ping'an worked methodically, ensuring no erratic digging left visible traces on the ground. 

Ultimately, he didn’t overlook even the inch-sized objects, collecting over thirty blue bricks alongside them. 

After some thought, Chen Ping'an stuffed another blue brick and two glazed tiles into his slung pack, feeling the weight was quite reassuring. 

Then he descended the mountain. 

To see his kind-hearted friend, Sun Daoren. 

If nothing unexpected occurred, once this Sun Daoist found something that would make even Master Huang drool with envy, it would likely be the moment of his demise. 

Before Sun Daoist had called out for Master Huang, he had actually sent a mental warning to Chen Ping'an: "Be very careful of Qin Juyuan; it’s best if he doesn’t show up again. Take this opportunity to grab the treasures and run as far as you can; life is worth more than money!" 

Chen Ping'an felt that just this piece of advice could spare Sun Daoist from an unforeseen calamity. 

This treasure hunting trip had already yielded far beyond Chen Ping'an's expectations, enough to make him smile awake from his dreams. 

So next, it would just be a journey through the mountains and rivers. 

If he happened to gain more, that would be splendid; if not, that was fine too. 

However, the sudden shattering of Sun Daoren's pagoda bell was quite strange. 

Yet compared to the oddities of this cave, it was no longer astonishing. 

Even though Chen Ping'an had just lit another Yang Energy Lantern Talisman, there remained signs of clarity and purity in the surroundings, devoid of any malevolent energy. 

Chen Ping'an was at a loss. 

Just like dealing with soldiers, he would face water and earth as they came. 

Many disasters and calamities were merely human misfortunes. 

Chen Ping'an circled around the mountain, passing the pile of ruined temple rubble in the white jade plaza. His prior actions of rummaging were meticulous, and his techniques were clever; he wouldn’t overlook anything. 

If he did miss something, there was no need for further worry. 

Standing at the top of the steps, he looked out. 

Finally, the second wave of people had arrived. 

Compared to the first wave’s stealthy approach, this group was much more swaggering. 

It was the young lord of Beiting, Zhan Qing, along with Bai Bi, the direct disciple of the Water Dragon Sect from the Huqi Kingdom. 

Chen Ping'an affixed a talisman to himself, gliding down like a bird. 

(End of chapter)

 ### Chapter 641: Winding Paths, Wild Practitioners

Sun Daoren followed Huang Shi as they searched for treasures, and they were quite successful in their endeavors.

The two of them had a decent rapport, parting ways to explore but not straying too far from one another. Sun Daoren was anxious about getting too far from Huang Shi, fearing that if he encountered danger, his meager skills would leave him helpless. Huang Shi, on the other hand, was wary of this slender, proactive Daoist; he didn’t want him to run off with a prized treasure.

In a two-story pavilion, Sun Daoren found many valuable books reduced to ashes, but he managed to uncover a Daoist manual that he couldn’t open or browse. It still exuded a radiant glow of multicolored light, and even when wrapped in a Daoist robe, its brilliance overflowed. The ancient golden characters inscribed in obscure scripts were entirely unfamiliar to him. Only those with a lineage and the qualifications as celestial masters could access such long-lost ancient texts.

After reuniting with Huang Shi, Sun Daoren felt a bit awkward; the treasure was too impressive, and that also brought trouble.

Huang Shi smiled, pretending not to notice.

Sun Daoren asked, "Did you find anything good, Brother Huang?"

Huang Shi nodded. "Not bad."

The two separated again, each seeking other rare materials and celestial artifacts.

Huang Shi took his time moving, glancing back at the slender Daoist’s silhouette, his smile deepening.

Earlier, in a small pavilion, Huang Shi had seen two skeletons seated at a stone table, their hands engaged in a game of chess. The table was engraved with a chessboard, featuring a mere seventeen lines, indicating that the game was in its concluding phase. Huang Shi had no interest in chess; he merely noted that the numerous pieces on the board indicated that both players were close to victory. Unfortunately, he couldn't be bothered to study the board any further.

Within the small pavilion, Huang Shi not only obtained two robes but also acquired those two jars of chess pieces. The pieces had a natural arc to them. Huang Shi couldn’t discern their material, but under the light, the translucent white pieces appeared with a faint golden hue, while the black pieces were opaque in the center, creating a rippling emerald halo in the light. Anyone not blind could see the value of these chess pieces.

The two robes were heavily worn, but the jars of chess pieces instead benefitted from time, much like ordinary stones that had soaked in mountain streams for centuries, becoming increasingly delicate and smooth, much to his delight.

As Huang Shi collected the black and white pieces from the stone chessboard, the white pieces felt scorching hot, as if burning his soul, while the black pieces were freezing cold. After swiftly tossing two pieces into the jar, he noticed that his fingers bore no injuries. His heart surged with joy; these jars were undoubtedly magical treasures. Ordinary spiritual weapons might injure a Gold Body realm warrior, but they wouldn’t disturb Huang Shi’s soul. Yet, merely picking up those pieces made him reluctant to hold them for long.

From this, Huang Shi deduced that the stone table, which had preserved the chess game for centuries, must be a celestial artifact; otherwise, the pieces wouldn’t have sat undisturbed for so long, with the board remaining intact.

However, Huang Shi had no intention of running around carrying a stone table.

He had considered destroying the table, thinking that if he couldn’t obtain it, neither would anyone else. But when he struck down with his palm, the table didn’t budge at all. It seemed like it could withstand force, only deepening Huang Shi’s regret at not being able to take it with him. If he could combine it with the two jars, it would fetch a sky-high price.

Meanwhile, Chen Ping’an quietly appeared near the pavilion. The chessboard’s spiritual energy still rippled with faint golden and emerald colors, possibly because the pieces had been embedded in the board for too long, seeping into the stone. Chen Ping’an swept his gaze over the residual spiritual aura of the chess pieces, closed his eyes, and silently memorized the game. After he opened his eyes, he thought that a good memory was not as reliable as a poor pen, so he took out some paper and a pen from his bag to record the ancient chess game.

The chessboard had only seventeen lines, unlike the widely popular nineteen lines, which itself was a clue. The various opening formations and life-and-death moves could reveal heavenly secrets.

Huang Shi, a martial artist, was utterly indifferent to these subtle clues. Chen Ping’an, however, was attentive and focused, yet he couldn’t hope to deduce the rough timeline of the game like Lu Tai or Cui Dongshan could with just a glance.

Chen Ping’an envied the mountain’s magic that allowed practitioners to observe the world from their sleeves.

Both techniques, “Observing Mountains in Hand” and “Sleeve Universe,” were the most desired skills for him to master.

Yet, these two superior techniques were only barely graspable by Golden Core earthly immortals, and to truly master them, one would need to reach the fifth realm.

Chen Ping’an considered the pavilion a prime location for cultivating Qi, as the two jars of chess pieces were rich in spiritual energy, having remained undisturbed over the years. It was much less conspicuous than the ruins of the Daoist temple paved with green bricks.

The spiritual energy here was thick, an opportunity not to be missed.

Chen Ping’an set down his bag on the table, removed his extravagant hundred-eyed robe, first putting on the highest quality golden robe, followed by the snowflake robe he had acquired from a female ghost in the greasy city. Finally, he donned the black robe again. With all three robes on, he could absorb and store more water spiritual energy.

Chen Ping’an took to the pavilion, crossed his legs, and, using the Toad Stone talisman, regulated his breathing, becoming as still as a mountain, trying to keep track of the movements of his companions Huang Shi and Sun Daoren.

From the pavilion, the chessboard’s spiritual energy, now infused with faint golden and emerald hues, slowly gathered towards the pavilion’s ceiling, gradually seeping into Chen Ping’an’s robes.

This illustrated just how precious the chessboard's spiritual energy was.

With Chen Ping’an’s deliberate guidance, the golden robe was the first to become saturated, absorbing about seventy to eighty percent of the water spiritual energy that had lingered in the pavilion due to the chess pieces. It had reached a level comparable to that of the abundant spiritual energy found in other halls. Chen Ping’an hesitated, opting not to drain this place completely dry to avoid revealing any signs. Taking everything would be tempting fate; after all, the real test lay ahead with all the celestial beings ascending the mountain, bringing with them layers of intrigue.

If there’s a chance to save some luck, then why not hold onto a bit? 

Ultimately, a momentary lack of profit was intended for long-term gain.

Once the situation was settled, they could discuss gains and losses.

Chen Ping’an then altered his strategy, no longer tailing Huang Shi but instead quietly following Sun Daoren.

If before obtaining that manual, Sun Daoren had been focused on tracking Huang Shi, now it seemed that even if Sun Daoren wanted to slip away, Huang Shi wouldn’t let him succeed.

This mountain, not being a true temple, had its central axis defined by the white jade steps leading from the mountain gate to the summit. 

It resembled a celestial sect without a clear inclination toward any of the three teachings. What puzzled Chen Ping’an most was that this mountain lacked a Hall of Patriarchs.

Especially on the mountainside, there were scattered huts and grand halls, all in a disordered jumble, lacking any apparent structure.

After entering and exiting various buildings, Sun Daoren intentionally distanced himself from Huang Shi, now no longer swaggering through the corridors but rather sneaking along, trying to conceal his presence.

Eventually, he hid in a small, exquisite secluded hall with a broken plaque that faintly read “Water Hall.”

The hall housed a statue of a female deity, adorned with fluttering ribbons, exuding an ethereal aura.

Sun Daoren used his robe to wrap various treasures he had collected as he moved through the corridors. He gathered everything that hadn’t turned to ashes—antique items and literary treasures—all stuffed into his bag, slung over his shoulder. He was laden with spoils, but the prerequisite was to leave this celestial mansion alive.

Sun Daoren closed the hall door, but after a moment’s thought, he remembered that the other buildings he had passed seemed to be left open. Hesitating, he quietly reopened the hall door to avoid raising any suspicions with Huang Shi.

From his vantage point on a roof ridge, Chen Ping’an watched anxiously, feeling for Sun Daoren. This was akin to stealing silver and placing a wooden plaque, indirectly telling Huang Shi, “Sun Daoren didn’t steal any money.” It would have been better for Sun Daoren to move about more, opening more doors to create the illusion of having crossed the central axis of the steps, fleeing towards Prince Qin of Jiayou Country. Otherwise, if he remained here, Huang Shi, if he had any sense at all, would surely begin his search from this small hall. If it were Chen Ping’an, he would have made sure to open or close those doors from the very start.

However, as he had been sneaking along, Sun Daoren often had to make choices, discarding items from his bags, unsure whether the new treasures or the old ones were more valuable. He finally relied solely on his instincts.

Chen Ping’an was left to pick through the discarded items.

In contrast, Huang Shi, if he found that his bag was becoming too full, would simply smash unwanted items with a punch. If he couldn’t break them, he would have other tricks, likely needing to replace them entirely.

Most of the treasures left behind by celestial beings were already on the verge of breaking. Repairing them would likely require a substantial amount of celestial money, but Huang Shi, with his solid foundation as a Gold Body realm warrior, could easily smash them. Items he had initially intended to discard, if they didn’t break with a single punch, would certainly be added to his collection.

This illustrated the immense opportunity of this treasure hunt on the mountain.

For ordinary celestial caves coming back to light, a group of wild practitioners battling against one another would typically yield three to four celestial artifacts per person, which would be enough to make anyone ecstatic.

Yet Huang Shi remained unsatisfied.

As expected, after suddenly losing track of Sun Daoren, he began to abandon his search, hastily making his way back following the route he had taken to find this small hall.

As Huang Shi approached, Chen Ping’an ceased his sitting position, lying flat on the ridge, holding his breath, completely still.

Huang Shi glanced at the plaque on the ground and smiled, “Sun Daoren, are there more treasures inside the Water Hall? How about I lend you a hand? Don’t worry, according to our earlier agreement, whoever opens the door first gets to keep all the treasures inside, no matter how valuable.”

Inside the Water Hall, Sun Daoren trembled, silently praying to the Three Pure Ones to have Huang Shi leave quickly.

Perhaps because Sun Daoren was not a disciple of the Daoist sect's three branches, his prayers were in vain, as Huang Shi directly stepped over the threshold, smiling, “Sun Daoren, what’s this? Have you gotten some treasures and turned your back on me, even fearing your ally? Shouldn’t we be worried about that Di Yuanfeng, who wields a deadly weapon? Does a fifth realm warrior like me truly frighten you so?”

With no way to escape, Sun Daoren had no choice but to step out from behind the statue, forcing a smile, “Brother Huang is joking.”

Huang Shi teased, “We’ve only covered a fraction of this celestial mansion; there’s still so much more to explore. Not to mention, we discovered a great view in the back mountain earlier. Why did you abandon that robe so early? You know it’s bad luck to walk back after burning incense in a temple.”

Sun Daoren had to retrace his steps, picking up the package he had carefully set on the ground behind the statue, slinging it over his shoulder, forehead glistening with sweat. “Brother Huang, how about we join forces and keep an eye on that Di Yuanfeng? Wouldn’t that be better? If we end up quarreling, we’d only be giving Di Yuanfeng the advantage.”

Huang Shi nodded, “How about you let me take a look at that radiant robe’s manual?”

Sun Daoren sighed, “Brother Huang, you’ve already got that incense burner. Shouldn’t you know when to stop? Besides, this manual is a Daoist classic; it wouldn’t mean much to you.”

Huang Shi smiled, “Whether it means anything or not is up to you, Sun Daoren.”

Sun Daoren’s expression darkened, “Huang Shi, allow me to give you some advice too. I’m quite adept at close combat as a sea-watching realm Daoist.”

Huang Shi said, “If not for that, it would be a problem. I know your trump card is that broken bell that you use for defense. Unfortunately, it’s gone now. Aside from that, you have just an offensive piece of your life’s essence. Do you know who I really am? I’m actually a sixth realm warrior; it wouldn’t take more than a couple of punches to take you down.”

Sun Daoren was shocked, “A sixth realm warrior?!”

He quickly scoffed, “Anyone can scare people! I could claim to be a Golden Core earthly immortal; would you be afraid?”

Just then, Huang Shi was about to deliver a punch to end this old Daoist’s life when a sudden sound of footsteps approached from outside the Water Hall. Huang Shi turned to look, only to find a black-robed elder, Chen Dao, who hadn’t gone to seek treasures with Di Yuanfeng.

Huang Shi cast a glance at the shabby bag slung across the elder’s shoulder, which seemed to contain some glazed tiles and… a few pieces of Daoist temple green bricks?

Was it a lack of courage, or just bad luck? 

After all this time, had he really just crashed into the gates of death without any other gains?

If that were the case, Huang Shi felt it would be a waste of effort to kill such a pitiful creature.

Sun Daoren saw the hurriedly arriving Daoist and felt both delighted and helpless.

This Chen Dao had not heeded his warnings. Nevertheless, now that it had come to this, he would see if there was an opportunity to team up against Huang Shi, to prevent him from monopolizing the treasures they had both worked hard to find.

Seeing that shabby bag on the elder’s shoulder, Sun Daoren thought that if things went south, the two of them could escape together, gifting Chen Dao a few seemingly worthless treasures.

Chen Ping’an wiped the sweat from his forehead, “I’ve been searching for you both. I was just flying around the rooftops and saw two groups of people heading up the mountain. I quickly landed. The first group was two young disciples, clearly celestial masters we can’t afford to provoke, all wearing robes. The second was that little Marquis from Beiting Country, accompanied by five others. One person guarded the bridge at the foot of the mountain, while another rushed directly to the mountaintop Daoist temple, clearly aiming to occupy the vital passage. The remaining three were slowly searching their way up the mountain, and it’s only a matter of time before we run into them. What should we do?”

Huang Shi’s mood darkened.

The dilapidated pavilion by the winding path was home to two pure martial artists, both of whom were true masters. Facing the two alone would require him to fight desperately.

With three others joining, Huang Shi felt he couldn’t confidently escape with treasures in hand.

Thus, the situation had changed; both companions inside and outside the Water Hall couldn’t be killed for the time being.

So Huang Shi smiled, “Just joking with Sun Daoren; don’t take offense.”

Sun Daoren huffed, “Brother Huang, such hurtful jokes are best avoided!”

Huang Shi felt an anger bubbling inside, nearly losing control and striking down this old Daoist. After all, this so-called close-combat wild practitioner was far less threatening than the black-robed elder adept in talismans. Should he kill Sun Daoren, all treasures could be left temporarily in the hands of the black-robed elder, and Huang Shi didn’t believe Chen Dao wouldn’t be tempted!

Suddenly, Sun Daoren raised his voice, “Chen Dao, can we negotiate? Could you spare me a few attack talismans?”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “Sure, let’s make a deal.”

Sun Daoren fell silent.

Huang Shi frowned, then relaxed, nearly forgetting that Sun Daoren was a half-hearted Daoist practitioner; drawing talismans wasn’t too difficult for him.

This wasn’t bad news. With both Sun Daoren and the black-robed elder wielding attack talismans, coupled with his own strength as a Gold Body realm warrior, and meeting Di Yuanfeng, the four of them would pose a formidable force.

Huang Shi stepped out of the Water Hall, making way for the black-robed elder, who had already halted, standing to the side while casting a sidelong glance at the two frail Qi practitioners. “Whether we can seize this opportunity depends on our willingness to cooperate in earnest. Let me be clear: I, Huang Shi, am a sixth realm warrior, not just boasting. If it comes to combat, I won’t hold back. However, once we leave this place, in return, you both need to grant me an opportunity.”

Chen Ping’an clapped his bag, revealing the outline of the green bricks. “Take what you want.”

Huang Shi felt his eyelids twitch.

Sun Daoren gritted his teeth, “Aside from the Daoist manual, feel free to take anything else from my bags!”

Huang Shi hesitated, then nodded. “It’s a deal!”

Chen Ping’an stepped over the threshold, meeting Sun Daoren’s gaze. Without needing to exchange words, they both approached the statue in the Water Hall.

They crouched down, and Sun Daoren asked, “How many types of attack talismans do you have, Chen Dao?”

Chen Ping’an replied, “Three types. Aside from the most valuable one, the Thunder Talisman, I have the River Severing Talisman and the Mountain Constraining Talisman. Just by their names, you can guess they’re all precious talismans. As for how many…”

Sun Daoren, sensing Chen Ping’an’s hesitation, grew impatient and firmly stated, “Aside from that Thunder Talisman, keep it for your own protection. I’ll take all the others!”

Chen Ping’an was still unsure. “Sun Daoren, do you have enough celestial money? These precious defense talismans are worth quite a bit, and I’ll be heartbroken to part with them.”

Sun Daoren asked, “Didn’t you say you drew these talismans yourself?”

Chen Ping’an answered, “Do you really believe that? If I could draw such deadly talismans myself, why would I be a wild practitioner struggling at the mountain’s base? I’d be serving in a top celestial sect like Caijue Mansion or Yuncheng, living a life of comfort instead.”

Sun Daoren grimaced, rubbing his cheek. “Chen Dao, just tell me how many talismans you have left. I’ll buy them all.”

Chen Ping’an shook his head. “Sun Daoren, you may be a senior, but business is business. First, you need to show me the celestial money.”

Sun Daoren grumbled, “Chen Dao, you should be fair in business!”

Chen Ping’an retorted, “Sun Daoren, fairness is essential in transactions!”

Sun Daoren felt disheartened. Damn, this Chen Dao was harder to deceive than he thought.

After some hesitation, he opened his robe package and laid it on the ground, saying seriously, “I’ll buy six talismans, three of each Water and Earth, and you can pick a priceless treasure from the mountain.”

Chen Ping’an rummaged through his sleeve and produced two ordinary yellow paper talismans, twisting the talismans with one hand while the other hand began to search around, stating, “For these two talismans, I’ll trade one for a broken celestial artifact.”

Sun Daoren’s face turned dark, and he was about to roll up his package.

Chen Ping’an then placed those two talismans at the edge of the package, saying, “Once I pick a treasure, I’ll hand over two talismans.”

Sun Daoren conceded, “Chen Dao, this deal is too much of a loss for me.”

Chen Ping’an eyed the twenty-odd celestial artifacts, his gaze wavering, thoroughly examining each one while grumbling, “Sun Daoren, since you hail from Yinger Mountain, the Thunder God’s abode, why didn’t you bring down a few Thunder talismans? Relying on your status as a celestial master, you’ve acted too presumptuously. Now you’re blaming me?”

Sun Daoren recalled his identity as a celestial master and chuckled, stroking his beard. “There are countless unexpected events when traveling down the mountain. How can one predict every detail? If I could foresee everything, I wouldn’t need to descend the mountain to strengthen my resolve.”

Chen Ping’an nodded and continued his selection.

Among the first two items he liked, one was ideal for gifting, while the rank of the other didn’t concern him too much. 

It could be given to Li Huai.

It was a wooden statue of a deity, palm-sized, depicting the Daoist Yuanjun, resembling the female statue in the Water Hall. The figure was graceful and elegant, with fine fingers performing magical gestures, a serene expression on her face, wearing a delicate crown, and dressed in exquisite robes that flowed down to the seat.

The base bore twelve characters in small, elegant script, promising clarity within and protection from external devilish distractions.

Chen Ping’an thought it had good symbolism.

There was also an ancient, round fan that looked quite valuable, likely to attract the attention of customers in his future shop on Old Huai Street or at the Bagua Zhai shop in Niujiao Mountain. After all, women in the world loved to shop, often more so than men, and as long as they liked it, reasoning and quality mattered little.

The last item was the most shocking one.

To be precise, it was overwhelming.

It was a pair of bamboo cages, drawn together by golden silk threads, with a greenish bamboo color, vibrant and glistening. However, like the other items, they had many fine cracks, greatly diminishing their appearance. Each cage was fist-sized, resembling common cricket cages, with inscriptions reading “Fight the Jiao” and “Submerge the Pans.”

Seeing these, Chen Ping’an broke out in a cold sweat.

He felt a bit nervous.

He was convinced that if there was a chance, he must team up with Sun Daoren to explore mountains and seek treasures.

Sun Daoren noticed something was off, sensing this was bound to be a lucrative deal. Why did Chen Dao seem so awkward? Was he suddenly realizing that despite the value of the items in his bag, they were still inferior to talismans? Having an extra talisman meant an extra chance at survival? This made Sun Daoren sweat as well, wanting to stealthily snatch the two talismans. He thought, “Brother Chen, we’ve built a bond; two talismans should suffice.” Sun Daoren rolled the talismans into his sleeve, letting out a sigh of relief. Just when he was about to say the remaining two could be forgotten…

Unexpectedly, Chen Dao took the fan, sticking to their agreement, and produced two Water and Earth talismans from his sleeve, handing them to Sun Daoren.

Then he removed the bag slung over his shoulder, pulled out a folded package from among the glazed tiles and green bricks, shook it lightly, and placed the fan inside.

Sun Daoren felt astonished and envious, realizing Chen Dao carried so many blue cloth packages, a true veteran of the trade.

Chen Ping’an then pulled out four talismans, laying them next to Sun Daoren’s robe on the ground, and stored the wooden statue inside his bag.

Sun Daoren was in high spirits, smiling broadly, “Chen Dao, you’ve even got four more talismans? Feel free to choose from the treasures on the ground, take your time.”

Chen Ping’an hesitated, dragging his feet, but ultimately pulled out a stack of over twenty talismans, among which were three golden talismans, likely the prized ones!

Sun Daoren looked at the stack tightly clutched in Chen Ping’an’s hand, glancing down to assess.

These were likely the last of Chen Dao’s talisman stash.

Sun Daoren swallowed hard, reminding himself to remain calm and composed, yet his smile remained stiff. He tentatively asked, “Chen Dao, do you have your eye on anything else? Good things come in pairs; I’d be willing to buy one more in exchange for four attack talismans.”

The black-robed elder laughed in disbelief, “Sun Daoren has good taste!”

Sun Daoren stroked his beard, chuckling, “Fair business is the way to go. If you let this opportunity pass, Chen Dao, you should think twice and cherish the rare bond we share.”

The other party was still indecisive.

Outside the Water Hall, Huang Shi urged impatiently, “Are you two planning to spend a few days inside this hall?”

Finally, the black-robed elder handed Sun Daoren two golden talismans, only one of which was the Thunder Talisman, while the other was a Mountain Breaking Talisman.

However, Sun Daoren was satisfied, merely teasing Chen Dao for being stingy.

Among the remaining stack of talismans, only one golden talisman remained, presumably the elder’s last prized attack talisman. Yet Sun Daoren didn’t press the issue, at least giving him a chance to keep one for self-defense.

This way, Sun Daoren felt more assured that this Chen Dao, who claimed to come from a small Daoist temple in Wuling Country, wasn’t a master of talisman drawing after all.

Chen Ping’an took the pair of bamboo cages that Sun Daoren couldn’t identify and was about to grab another item when Sun Daoren cheerfully folded his package, slinging it over his shoulder.

As the two crossed the threshold of the Water Hall, Huang Shi’s expression soured. “There’s been some commotion on the other side of the steps; I wonder who ran into whom.”

Now three groups of people were mixed together on the mountain.

The four of them should have been the first to enter the mansion’s secret realm.

Huang Shi was unaware of the two young disciples from the Yunshang City sect; he didn’t know who they were, but they likely belonged to Yunshang City, as Cai Que Mansion had only female cultivators.

The third group presented the biggest challenge.

So the best-case scenario would be for the two young disciples from the Yunshang City sect to clash with the little Marquis from Beiting Country.

If Di Yuanfeng were to engage someone first, it would not bode well.

Given Di Yuanfeng’s character, if he encountered danger, he would surely drag Huang Shi and the others into it, leading to their demise together on the road to the underworld.

Huang Shi suddenly leaped onto the roof, witnessing figures falling from the rafters like dumplings into boiling water, numbering over forty. It seemed more would soon follow.

The commotion was far greater than the sporadic sounds of fighting on the other side of the steps.

Huang Shi found himself puzzled; in such a chaotic situation, the odds seemed to favor him.

As long as he found an escape route and seized Sun Daoren’s manual, he could leave without a second thought.

He was a pure warrior, with no particular attachment to the spiritual energy of this place.

The ensuing chaos among everyone else was their own struggle, irrelevant to him.

Huang Shi said, “We won’t take the mountain steps but will take the longer route to the back mountain.”

Chen Ping’an asked, “Shouldn’t we wait for Prince Qin?”

Sun Daoren sighed, thinking that this young man was truly naive to the dangers of the world.

Having exchanged items inside the Water Hall, Sun Daoren had already sensed Chen Dao’s cautiousness, which was actually quite frivolous and unreliable.

Huang Shi smiled, “Brother Chen can go greet Prince Qin while Sun Daoren and I wait here.”

Sun Daoren noticed the awkward expression on Chen Dao’s face and ceased to speak.

Sun Daoren quietly conveyed through his thoughts, “Chen Dao, remember, too much talk can lead to mistakes. Once we’re in the treasure trove, take what you can and don’t overplay your hand. Who knows, Prince Qin might have already found a great fortune; he may not even wish to see you. If you go over, wouldn’t that put him in a difficult position?”
