Chen Ping’an replied with a smile, “As expected of Sun Daoren, wise and steady.”

At this moment, Chen Ping’an’s best plan was to find an outsider to confirm the flow of time in this small realm. If it wouldn’t delay his journey along the great river, he could linger here for a bit longer, hoping to avoid any conflicts with the various celestial beings and allowing him to cultivate safely, gathering spiritual energy from the Water Hall and the Mountain Shrine.

He aimed to absorb as much of the essence of the water energy contained in the Daoist temple’s green bricks as possible.

The Water Hall and the Mountain Shrine had limited spiritual energy reserves; as for other energy realms, due to the existence of pure true energy, they couldn’t hold much. Combined, they likely would not be as effective as the energy gathered in a hundred-eyed gluttonous robe. However, even if the spiritual energy at the Water Hall and Mountain Shrine overflowed, it wouldn't matter, as Chen Ping’an could draw talismans here.

Using the best celestial dan shan from Chunlu Garden to draw talismans on golden material, consuming as much spiritual energy as possible would enhance the rank of the talismans.

Cultivating Qi, studying talismans, and earning celestial money would be a win-win situation.

Chen Ping’an even planned to use this spiritual energy to attempt to open a third crucial energy point, making way for his future third life essence artifact of the wood element.

He had an intuition that the wood-based life essence artifact had already found its place.

From another perspective, being in this small world was not necessarily a bad thing for Chen Ping’an, who was located in Beiju Luzhou.

It severed his connection with He Xiaoliang of the Qingliang Sect.

She had followed him into the Bone Marsh Ghost Valley, closely tracking him in Jingguan City. After he had endured the heavenly tribulation, she had to proactively cut off the invisible connection, likely hiding in that small cave to avoid further complications, fearing she would be dragged down by him again.

Thus, whatever gains or losses within this small realm were entirely his own matters.

In fact, this was a good thing.

The worst-case scenario was that Chen Ping’an would break through the restrictions of this realm and escape.

Even without discussing the green glazed tiles and the Daoist temple’s green bricks, those two small bamboo cages had left him utterly astonished.

They could very well be the Dragon King’s nets!

Even if they were severely damaged with the lowest rank, those two small cages were still worth repairing to new condition; they could be used for capturing dragons.

So, was Sun Daoren’s surprise worth pursuing endlessly?

It was easy to deceive others, but self-deception was also simple. For those who cultivate the Dao, as long as they still have the heart to seek the Dao and the aspiration to reach the peak, self-deception itself becomes the greatest issue.

This is precisely because what appears simplest could lead to the largest obstacles in the future.

For instance, Liu Laocheng from Shujian Lake nearly perished because of this.

Would simply giving Sun Daoren two golden talismans allow him to feel at ease and guilt-free?

Or perhaps, to save trouble and effort, simply deal with the unexpected source of trouble that was Huang Shi?

Should he weigh the outcomes based on appearance or based on intention? Or perhaps both were necessary?

Gu Can didn’t have to go through all that.

Ma Kuxuan didn’t need to either.

All the wild practitioners of the mountains might need to consider such things.

And for Cui Dongshan, Lu Tai, Zhong Kui, and Qi Jinglong, they might have their own choices, whether to align with or differ from Chen Ping’an, but they wouldn’t have to endure the same struggles he faced.

Once Chen Ping’an embarked on the path of cultivation, becoming half a practitioner, he would discover all the principles that had supported him to this day.

Those principles would indeed become burdens.

Just like when he first ascended the mountain as a child, carrying that large backpack felt heavy even before it was filled with herbs.

But the difficulty lay precisely in those burdens from earlier, which had carried him to where he was today.

Putting oneself in a difficult position was the hardest challenge in the journey of cultivation.

At that moment, Sun Daoren conveyed to Chen Ping’an through thoughts, “Chen Dao, be careful. Huang Shi is deeply concealed; he’s actually a sixth realm warrior. You don’t have many attack talismans left. I’m quite adept at close combat; just retreat a bit when the time comes. But don’t forget to support me; don’t be stingy with the talismans—just hurl everything you have at Huang Shi, but be careful not to hit me.”

Chen Ping’an was taken aback, realizing the clarity of the situation. He smiled and replied, “Rest assured, Sun Daoren. To be honest, aside from talismans, I’m also quite skilled in combat.”

Sun Daoren sighed, “Chen Dao, don’t say that. Hearing you boast only makes me more anxious.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “Sun Daoren, you come from a prestigious celestial family with profound techniques; perhaps you won’t even need my help.”

Sun Daoren fell silent, thinking about how flattering this shallow-minded fellow made him feel. He had no sense of achievement.

Huang Shi’s keen instincts hinted that the two were communicating in secrecy.

He didn’t think two Daoists could come up with anything clever, especially in such dire circumstances. 

Chen Ping’an had come to understand certain things, feeling as if the world was vast, the mountains and waters were beautiful, and everything felt welcoming.

Yet, upon closer inspection, Chen Ping’an couldn’t help but frown.

He shook his head, sensing no anomalies.

Chen Ping’an couldn’t help but remind Sun Daoren, “Be careful, Sun Daoist.”

Sun Daoren laughed, “No need for such exaggeration, my friend.”

On the other side of the steps, Di Yuanfeng had indeed clashed with the two young celestial masters from Yunshang City.

The two young disciples from Yunshang City, having accidentally stumbled upon an ancient cultivation site of a celestial being, fortuitously opened a mechanism from a piece of writing and discovered the remains of a “Golden Branch and Jade Leaf, Radiant and Glorious” skeleton.

With such a sight, the brilliance that had lasted for hundreds or even thousands of years could only belong to a Gold Core earthly immortal or someone who had received an extraordinary fortune, a remnant of legendary Yu Pu realm practitioners.

As for the more extraordinary celestial remains, they should not have turned to dust and vanished.

The robe worn by the remains was almost flawless, with no sign of wear at all.

Originally, Di Yuanfeng had been secretly following the inexperienced young practitioners, not expecting much. However, upon seeing this, he realized that he had hit the jackpot. The value of the remains and the robe was evident just from their appearance, not to mention that one of the young male practitioners had already stored the remains and robe in a white misty brush tube, clearly a legendary celestial artifact.

Di Yuanfeng weighed the cultivation levels of the two and saw an opportunity. He concealed himself at the exit, waiting for a chance to strike, hoping to take the treasure and flee. A brush tube, along with the celestial skeleton and robe, would be three precious items.

Yet, unexpectedly, under a fierce strike, the young male practitioner’s robe was torn, and he sustained severe injuries, but he managed to protect the brush tube.

Di Yuanfeng was about to go for the kill against the panicked female practitioner.

Just then, an old practitioner suddenly appeared, not only repelling Di Yuanfeng but nearly leaving him trapped in that celestial’s meditative hut.

Relying on that ancestral weapon, Di Yuanfeng broke free from the magical prison and fled, cursing under his breath. The damned celestial masters were wearing two robes!

The young male practitioner turned pale and realized blood was pooling in his palm. Had he not taken precautions by wearing two robes, he would have been dead from that solid blow.

The female practitioner felt deep sympathy, her heart aching for him, and despite her own safety, she was ready to chase after Di Yuanfeng, who was seriously injured, hoping to deal a blow to his downfall.

The old Daoist who had been watching them calmly said, “Don’t pursue a desperate foe. Moreover, after such a great fortune, you should know when to quit. Now, you should consider how to leave this place. The little marquis from Beiting Country has stationed a martial arts master at both the foot and summit of the mountain to guard the way; you’ll have to discuss among yourselves.”

Then the old practitioner vanished.

The pair of young practitioners from Yunshang City, having survived, were filled with mixed emotions, not noticing the struggle in the old practitioner’s gaze.

If it weren’t for the extra protector, the ancient practitioner Huan Yun, who had been the chief protector of Yunshang City for nearly a century, they might have understood what it meant to face sudden misfortune.

And not far away, another old practitioner, adept in using talismans to conceal his presence and aura, silently observed the situation with a complex expression. He felt a mix of relief and an almost imperceptible disappointment.

Huan Yun murmured, “Cultivation is hard, but cultivating the heart is even harder.”

After a sigh of resignation, Huan Yun once again disappeared.

The previously untouched treasures that had caught his eye were now within reach.

For this pair of disciples from Shen Zhenze, they were no longer focused on treasure hunting but were concerned with figuring out how to escape.

As for the old protector at Longmen realm, he likely had similar thoughts.

Aside from the celestial artifacts in the various halls, Huan Yun was more interested in checking out the glazed tiles he had seen from afar atop the mountain; they seemed more precious than anything.

However, he wasn’t in a hurry for this; with the Gold Body realm warrior from Beiting Country stationed at the summit, Huan Yun wouldn’t dare to force a breach unless it was absolutely necessary.

Behind a rock, Di Yuanfeng, burdened with a pack, swallowed a pill and gasped for breath, blood trickling from the corner of his mouth as he cursed angrily.

As long as he still had the energy to curse, it meant he hadn’t suffered critical injuries.

Di Yuanfeng had no regrets about his attempt to seize the treasure. 

Having failed once, he didn’t want to continue entangling himself.

At the halfway point on the steps, little Marquis Zhan Qing held a folding fan, lightly fanning to create a breeze, standing beside Bai Bi, a female Gold Core earthly immortal. 

High Ling, a military general from Fuhua Country, stood at the other end of the white jade arch bridge at the foot of the mountain.

The family protector warrior from the marquis’s house had gone to the summit.

The remaining royal protector from Fuhua Country, after receiving Bai Bi’s nod, went to search for treasures.

Zhan Qing gazed into the distance, frowning. “So many people—how did they get in? Did someone break the cave’s restrictions directly?”

Bai Bi sighed, “This place itself is the biggest problem. I’ll go around the mountain to see if I can use my flying sword to contact the sect.”

Zhan Qing stood and said, “I’ll accompany you.”

Bai Bi shook her head. “You should stay at the foot of the mountain; Gao Ling knows best how to safeguard your safety. There’s no need to rush to the summit; it’s too risky, and I wouldn’t feel at ease exploring the boundaries here.”

Bai Bi soared into the air, transforming into a rainbow as she departed.

Zhan Qing’s heart yearned for her.

This was the demeanor of a Gold Core earthly immortal.

Zhan Qing slowly descended the mountain. A Gold Body realm Gao Ling might not be able to handle all treasure hunters.

However, as long as the influx of visitors to the summit didn’t manage to form a cohesive force, they would be scattered and easy for Zhan Qing to handle.

After entering the secret realm, she had discussed with Bai Bi and changed her mind.

Thus, Zhan Qing didn’t plan to massacre everyone; instead, she aimed to strike a deal with those passing practitioners and warriors.

They could ascend the mountain, but upon descending, they would need to privately meet with Zhan Qing and hand over one of the items she had her eye on.

Just one would suffice.

As for the other items carried by the lucky ones, Bai Bi would naturally keep a record and later report to the Water Dragon Sect’s Hall of Ancestors, allowing those earthly immortals to capture these ants and reclaim their treasures.

This way, Zhan Qing wouldn’t need to kill anyone herself, and they could profit through peace.

It would save much trouble and unexpected complications.

Wild practitioners, unless they felt they were in a dire situation, generally feared death and valued their lives, making them easy to negotiate with.

In contrast, those celestial masters, caught in the middle, often failed to grasp the situation.

Her master, an earthly immortal from a wild practitioner background, was now a nominal protector of the Water Dragon Sect, and Bai Bi was her future divine partner, making them practically family.

Thus, this celestial mansion relic was a treasure trove for the Water Dragon Sect.

Before this, Bai Bi had discussed with her to gather as many precious items as possible, ensuring they didn’t exceed five; greed would only lead to ruin. If they were to take too many treasures, it would be hard to explain to the sect, and Zhan Qing’s actions must remain discreet. During this period, they must avoid touching treasures that would make earthly immortals dream of riches. Otherwise, the elders of the sect would be vigilant, and if they heard of any disturbances, they would investigate every intruder, leaving no stone unturned. Should Zhan Qing reveal herself, Bai Bi would also be implicated, risking being branded a traitor to the sect, which would be a disaster.

However, if they successfully retrieved three or four valuable artifacts, even if the Hall of Ancestors learned of it, the respect for Bai Bi’s mentor and Zhan Qing’s master would grant them leniency.

Every celestial master on the mountain, bound by rules and heritage, was also restricted by their duties and doctrines.

As Zhan Qing approached the foot of the mountain, she instructed Gao Ling, the newly promoted Gold Body realm general from Fuhua Country, to ensure compliance.

Gao Ling had no objections.

On the day that Zhan Qing escorted the female practitioner Bai Bi back home to the capital, an imperial decree arrived at Gao Ling's general office.

Thus, Gao Ling understood one thing: in the Fuhua Country, where military merit was as hard to earn as climbing to the heavens, establishing a connection with the Water Dragon Sect was worth more than anything.

Zhan Qing stood at one end of the white jade arch bridge, lightly knocking on the bridge’s strange beast with her folding fan, appearing like a jade tree in the wind, graceful and elegant.

Gao Ling loudly reminded the nearby crowd of the rules they needed to abide by.

Of course, no one was inclined to obey.

Some, not daring to charge ahead, attempted to leap over from other locations across the emerald river, resembling a moat.

Yet Gao Ling dashed forward, intercepting one with a punch, killing him instantly and scattering the body into seven or eight pieces.

Gao Ling held back little with that punch.

Thus, the nearby practitioners gasped, recognizing Gao Ling’s identity as a Gold Body realm warrior, the first among the martial artists of Fuhua Country.

After that punch, the previously noisy crowd across the bridge fell silent, only whispers remaining.

Unbeknownst to them, someone had used a celestial secret technique. A raspy voice echoed, “We have the numbers; let’s team up to take these two down. Then we can each take our share and head up the mountain. Why should we wait for their approval? If luck is on our side, we might only get one treasure, but do we really want to hand it over to those spoiled nobles from Beiting Country? If we don’t unite now, it’ll be even harder to act as one when we descend the mountain.”

These words stirred many hearts.

The two female practitioners from Cai Que Mansion exchanged glances and smiled.

The one who had uttered these tempting words was a direct descendant of the Hall of Ancestors, a young girl. 

Though young, she was sharp-minded.

They were Cai Que Mansion’s leader, Sun Qing, and the lawmaster of the Hall of Ancestors, Wu Qian.

Originally, Wu Qian had been sufficient to protect them, but Sun Qing had come along for a change of pace and unexpectedly stumbled upon great fortune.

Wu Qian secretly communicated with the young mansion leader, “That young earthly immortal we encountered earlier must be Bai Bi from Fuhua Country, right?”

Sun Qing scoffed, “What if she’s a direct disciple of the Water Dragon Sect? In a chaotic battle, if she lacks the depth and skill, it doesn’t matter if she dies.”

Having said this, Sun Qing’s expression turned calm. “What’s done is done.”

Wu Qian felt anxious, glancing at the composed young mansion leader. No wonder she was the youngest Gold Core mansion leader in history while he was merely the lawmaster for a year.

On their side of the riverbank, the clamor grew, with people shouting to kill the Fuhua Country general and skin the little marquis from Beiting Country.

Yet Zhan Qing smiled brightly, snapping her fan open, fanning a gentle breeze. She simply said, “If you want to kill me, go ahead; it’s first come, first served.”

Sun Qing chuckled and lightly nudged Wu Qian with her elbow. “You should take the lead; otherwise, we’ll just waste time.”

Wu Qian understood her intentions.

Wearing a veil and using a concealment technique, Wu Qian boldly stepped out of the crowd, crossing onto the white jade arch bridge, initially walking slowly.

Those on the bridge hesitated, fearing this unknown woman might lead them into danger, making them the first to get struck down by Gao Ling’s fists.

But soon, as Wu Qian walked faster, she suddenly unleashed celestial offensive techniques, taking two of Gao Ling’s punches head-on. One punch broke her spell, while the other sent her flying backward across the bridge.

The female practitioner, however, was tough; after struggling to rise, she remained silent and headed back toward the bridge.

With someone leading the charge, the crowd felt relieved, erupting into cheers and rushing across the bridge.

Zhan Qing was furious, hating the reckless woman who had blazed the trail.

Without any hesitation, she turned and, with a flick of her fingers, blew a loud whistle that echoed throughout.

The family protector, a seventh realm warrior, dashed down the mountain, leaping high from the white jade square and landing heavily on the ascending steps.

Those at the foot of the mountain noticed this scene and felt their hearts race, weakening their resolve.

Yet another raspy female voice rang out, “Let’s take down those two at the bridge first; what can one more do? One strike each, and they’ll be nothing but mush!”

At the foot of the mountain, chaos erupted.

In the distance, Bai Bi hovered in the air, her figure suspended at the edge of a boundary, surrounded by a thick mist. No matter how she employed her techniques, she couldn’t see the landscape beyond that line.

Gradually, she descended, using a pebble to break through the mist, but it vanished without a trace.

Then, she tore apart a large section of the ground and entered the cloud of mist, still finding no response.

This was far more frightening than the mountain’s water restrictions.

What lay ahead was the unknown.

In the history of the Water Dragon Sect, a Jade Pu realm elder and a Gold Core great practitioner had both perished within this secret realm, and the sect had never recovered their remains.

Bai Bi felt anxious, realizing she needed to consider a way out.

What had once seemed like a shallow pond now appeared to be a significant treasure trove.

The river running through the middle of North Ju Luzhou was the foundation of the Water Dragon Sect, and its most vital Hall of Ancestors had originally been one of three ancient shrines along the river. The other two had either been seized by the Dayuan Dynasty, which honored it as the true shrine, or had been claimed by a now-defunct sect and subsequently destroyed in battles with sword cultivators.

The atmosphere here bore some resemblance to her own Hall of Ancestors, which gave Bai Bi the confidence to allow Zhan Qing to take four treasures.

If this truly were a relic of an ancient river shrine, the two of them would be credited with the merits of their discovery.

However, Bai Bi felt a lingering worry, fearing the worst outcome.

It wasn’t merely about being unable to escape or finding no way out.

If she and Zhan Qing were to disappear for too long, the Water Dragon Sect would surely follow the trail to find them.

Bai Bi was genuinely worried that this place could turn into a new grave for everyone.

What if those seemingly orderly bones were actually the remains of new victims rather than those of ancient celestial beings?

That would indicate that this place was essentially a massive trap, waiting for outsiders to walk in, believing they had stumbled upon a great fortune and could share in the spoils.

Of course, that was just a possibility.

But in Bai Bi’s heart, this possibility had transformed from a mere chance to a certainty, growing more probable with the passage of time.

In a moment of panic, Bai Bi decided not to linger at the boundary of this small world any longer. She swiftly rode the wind back to find Zhan Qing, seeking to devise a foolproof plan.

After Bai Bi vanished, a tall, ethereal elder emerged from the mist, smiling. “Three Gold Core practitioners, two Gold Body realm warriors… and a peculiar little one. This should make for a delightful feast.”

A strand of sword energy fell from the sky, piercing through the elder’s crown, yet his ethereal figure reappeared elsewhere, smiling, “Goodness, we’ve been neighbors for many years; you’re still behaving so poorly. With all these restrictive barriers, I can’t refine this mountain’s waters, but layers upon layers of mountains encircle this small world. You’ve only been able to protect this place from losing its essence; what else can you do?”

The elder’s head was pierced again by that persistent strand of sword energy but reassembled in another place, his expression unperturbed. “According to our old customs, I’ll leave just one last person behind, allowing him to die a moment later to chat with me about the world outside. He’ll come to understand how intricate this trap truly is. All those treasures—where can you take them? A meal on the table, a place to die, this small world is where the children’s luck seems fortunate. But it’s a pity for a Daoist temple; that little sword-bearing child has a keen eye, but you can’t take those things with you. After all, I’ll have to piece together my belongings again. How many times has it been? Each time, I have to move again; it’s truly exhausting.”

Once again, the elder’s figure was torn apart by the relentless sword energy, but he continued to retreat into the mist, his towering form slowly disappearing. He lightly patted his belly, chuckling, “Haha, what a vast world; what a unique little pocket I have. In any world, people kill one another the most. How utterly meaningless.”

Once the elder’s figure had vanished, that strand of sword energy lingered nearby for a long time, sweeping through the ground before finally shooting into the sky and returning to the heights.

Chen Ping’an suddenly turned his head, gazing into the distance, perhaps the only one who noticed that strand of sword energy descending and then ascending.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 642: A Thousand Young Men in One’s Eyes

The back mountain was filled with strange flowers and unusual grasses, yet there were no birds, insects, or ants to be found. 

Chen Ping'an noticed something peculiar: when he and his companions first entered this celestial household, they had seen a crane circling the mountain. However, after the four of them ascended, the crane had vanished without a trace. Whether Chen Ping'an looked up from the foot of the mountain or gazed down from the summit's Taoist temple, or later followed Huang Shi and Sun Daoren on their treasure hunt, right up to this point on the back mountain, he had not caught even a glimpse of that crane again.

If indeed there was a recluse residing here, and assuming the worst—if the host harbored sinister intentions towards all visitors—then this person would undoubtedly be a master at manipulating human hearts.

For ordinary folk, such as mountain dwellers or woodcutters, merely catching sight of the crane upon entering the mountain might suffice. Most would be stunned by the subsequent majestic white jade bridges and archways, perceiving this place as a realm of immortals. Coupled with the sight of scattered white bones, they would naturally consider this a land without a master.

Yet for practitioners of the Dao, the fleeting images seen unconsciously—especially the first sight—could greatly influence one's disposition, silently and imperceptibly. 

In the future, every thought and action of a Qi practitioner, no matter their level, would inevitably be scrutinized repeatedly. 

When Chen Ping'an first saw the verdant mountains, crystal-clear waters, and the snow-white crane, he felt a profound sense of admiration. His first thought was simply: what a splendid celestial abode, what a beautiful landscape. 

From then on, everything he encountered was merely an extension of the celestial household, along with some ruins. 

The celestial aspects remained celestial, and the blessings were still blessings. 

Everywhere there were clues, intricate and complex, as if hidden mechanisms lay in wait. Over time, the abundance of them could leave one feeling lost in a tangled mess, resulting in a reluctance to ponder further.

Chen Ping'an also had little clarity, yet the sudden drop of that sword energy felt like a flash of insight. If the crane had been some clever trick, and considering that the bell at Sun Daoren's waist had inexplicably exploded during their journey, a thread could be pulled from this, or rather, a potential worst-case scenario could be imagined.

This nuanced perception of the best and worst possibilities based on a fleeting moment was key to Chen Ping'an's survival when he had walked out of the Bone Marsh Ghost Valley beneath the watchful eyes of Gao Cheng.

The world is complex; seeing or not seeing, thinking or not thinking—these are all matters of learning and cultivation of one's heart.

Of course, there were also those who stumbled upon opportunities by sheer luck, merely muddling through life until they either perished or stumbled upon fortune.

The three continued to explore the back mountain, which appeared to be a much more leisurely affair compared to the desperate struggles of the front mountain.

As for the life or death of Di Yuanfeng, Chen Ping'an bore no burden. He wasn’t related to him by blood or any ancestral ties; had he been a man of good intentions, Chen Ping'an might have intervened to broker some kind of equitable trade.

At this moment, by the roadside stood a solitary green bamboo, catching the attention of the trio. It appeared lonely and forlorn, its shadows dancing in the breeze.

The bamboo was as thick as a bowl's mouth, and its leaves were a vivid green, not just in poetic terms, but truly vibrant and dripping with moisture. Many leaf tips had gathered droplets of water, which trembled precariously in the wind. As the three gazed at the bamboo, a droplet of emerald water fell to the muddy ground, dissipating instantly. Chen Ping'an focused intently, sensing something significant; though it wasn’t the essence of water produced by the emerald tiles or the blue bricks of a Taoist temple, it was still at an exaggerated level of spiritual energy coalescing into water.

As Sun Daoren passed by, he gently tapped the bamboo and leaned in to listen, letting out a soft “Hmm,” and remarked, “There’s something to this.”

While the two stared at the bamboo, Chen Ping'an turned to his satchel and took out his sword nurturing gourd, holding it in his hand before adjusting his pack. He then smiled and said, “Could you shake the bamboo for me, Daoist Sun? I’d like to collect some water from the tips of the leaves.”

Sun Daoren, being a genuine practitioner at the Ocean Observing Realm, could gauge the depth of the situation and shook his head with a smile, “Chen Daoist, I advise you not to bother. The droplets of bamboo leaf water nurtured by spiritual energy cannot be contained by ordinary vessels. Not to mention trying to collect them in a wine jug, even if you manage to gather a handful of leaves with water drops, once you’re away from this strange bamboo, they too will evaporate.”

Though the tall, thin Daoist mentioned this, it didn’t stop him from unwrapping his robe to take out a small blue porcelain bottle painted with a depiction of a pine hermit.

Huang Shi, annoyed by the two's dalliance, kicked the bamboo stalk. Instantly, droplets fell like a light rain. Sun Daoren burst into laughter, shifting his stance, and stepped forward with a blue porcelain bottle to collect the water.

Chen Ping'an, too, was reluctant to let a single droplet hit the ground and, without competing with Sun Daoren, used a water technique to gather many droplets that were about to fall into the mud, slowly collecting them into his sword nurturing gourd.

Huang Shi glanced at the black-robed elder’s technique, finding no flaws to question, and thus let it go.

Since Chen Ping'an had taken out his sword nurturing gourd, he did not put it away, instead hanging it at his waist. The water droplets, coalescing from the heavens' spiritual energy, gathered to form a weighty substance, amounting to the weight of ten or more pounds.

The three continued on their way.

Chen Ping'an glanced back at the green bamboo.

Could it be that, like the bamboo grove carefully cultivated by Wei Ban on Chess Stone Mountain, they all traced their roots back to the Qing Shen Mountain of the Bamboo Sea Cave? 

Otherwise, according to the celestial records he had previously acquired from the Upside-Down Mountain, many of the celestial bamboos in the vast world seemed to be less capable of gathering water than this bamboo.

It's a pity it couldn’t be transported like the chess table stone.

Sun Daoren, feeling a bit unsatisfied, reached out and said with a smile, “Bamboo is connected to the divine, lightens the body and replenishes energy. In my early years of cultivation, I came across an ancient text that noted bamboo leaves brewed into tea are most refreshing and invigorating. During the hot summer days, just a handful of bamboo leaves combined with a few lotus seeds from the mountain, and after drinking one or two cups, it would make one feel as if they were floating as if they were an immortal.”

Chen Ping'an glanced at Sun Daoren, then at the tall green bamboo that remained utterly unyielding.

Since it had come to this, he felt somewhat at a loss for flattery.

Sun Daoren, retracting his hand, calmly said, “Never mind, let this opportunity be reserved for future generations.”

Huang Shi, eager to take action, said, “These bamboo leaves, if collected by practitioners of the lower realms, could be refined into their life’s essence. They could indeed be treasures! The treasures are right before us; be cautious not to incur heaven’s wrath by refusing what is offered. Daoist Sun, would you truly not take a few handfuls? Even if not for brewing tea, gifting them to the descendants of the Thunder God’s abode would still be an exceptional token for our return to the sect.”

Sun Daoren, unperturbed, replied, “Cultivating the Dao involves fundamental matters; one cannot carelessly grant opportunities. I am not their teacher; gifts that are too extravagant may be unseemly. Enough of this.”

Chen Ping'an quietly praised, “Daoist Sun, your words are profound and thought-provoking.”

Sun Daoren carefully tucked the blue porcelain bottle into his sleeve, moving forward with a thoughtful smile—a man of great depth.

Huang Shi could hardly endure the unsophisticated demeanor of this wandering Daoist from the Wuling Kingdom. Ever since learning that Sun Daoren was a disciple of the Thunder God’s abode, he had been overly attentive towards him.

Suddenly, Huang Shi, using the method of the Golden Body Realm, applied the strength of the fifth realm in a punch, slightly holding back as he gauged the physique of the black-robed elder. Without warning, he threw a punch at the elder, resulting in a loud bang. The elder was knocked back, rolling and struggling to rise, seemingly dazed. Sitting on the ground, he suddenly coughed up a mouthful of dark blood, as if he had just regained his senses, standing with his hands hidden in his sleeves, clearly preparing a talisman at his fingertips, he yelled angrily, “Huang, are you looking to die?!”

Huang Shi felt relieved; indeed, he was a useless fellow.

Sun Daoren, startled, quickly leaped several feet away, also preparing a defensive talisman he had just purchased from Chen Ping'an.

The three formed a triangle.

Huang Shi didn’t even glance at the black-robed elder, merely turning to Sun Daoren with a smile, “Daoist Sun, one must be wary of treachery; we are allies with Young Master Qin, at least familiar with each other. But this person, we met by chance; if he is a crafty rogue, we would be the ones caught off guard. In the end, we might lose all our treasures and opportunities, sacrificing our lives to benefit others. I believe Daoist Sun would not wish for such an outcome?”

Sun Daoren conveyed through his heart, “Chen Daoist, what do you say? Should we have a contest? This Huang Shi is not to be trifled with. If we truly tear our masks apart, we brothers would be like grasshoppers on the same string; neither of us could hide our true intentions.”

In comparison, Sun Daoren naturally trusted the black-robed elder more. After their journey, he felt the connection with good and evil was tenuous; he regarded Chen Daoist as a lesser threat due to his apparent lack of ability. Nevertheless, if the black-robed elder’s actions were shrewd and cunning, and he were to shift sides, Sun Daoren would not be inclined to risk his life in confrontation with Huang Shi.

As he communicated this in his heart to Chen Ping'an, Sun Daoren verbally expressed, “Chen Daoist, Huang’s actions are somewhat excessive. However, the situation is unpredictable. If we engage in infighting, it would be the true act of dressing another’s wedding gown. How about you both give me some face, and Chen Daoist, please calm down. I will have Huang apologize; let’s consider this matter settled, shall we?”

Chen Ping'an, infuriated, responded, “No! After receiving such a punch and suffering this unwarranted disaster, a mere apology won’t suffice! How about Huang Shi face my thunder talisman instead? Consider it even!”

Huang Shi twitched his lips, opening a corner of his package to extract an object, lightly tossing it toward the black-robed elder, and said with a smile, “If an apology is not enough, let’s add a gift of thanks.”

The black-robed elder’s eyes lit up at the sight of the object, hesitating briefly, but still stealthily prepared his talisman while raising a hand to catch the antiquated copper mirror thrown toward him.

Sun Daoren’s expression changed drastically, and he quickly warned, “Don’t catch it!”

But it was too late.

Huang Shi stepped forward, using his peak strength from the sixth realm, arriving in front of the black-robed elder in an instant, and threw a punch.

The black-robed elder was stunned, standing there in shock, frozen in place, unable to catch the copper mirror, instead taking the punch head-on.

Huang Shi suddenly halted his punch, letting the force merely brush past the unfortunate elder’s face, causing his hair to blow back.

Huang Shi retracted his fist, adjusting his heavy bag, and turned to leave, glancing back after taking a few steps to say, “Chen, old brother, this copper mirror is yours now.”

Sun Daoren sighed inwardly. 

How had he ended up with such a dim-witted ally? 

What a hardship.

The road ahead would not be easy. 

There was no choice but to take on more responsibility himself.

Sun Daoren watched as Chen Daoist offered him an apologetic smile, squatting down to pick up the fallen copper mirror, placing it in a somewhat deflated blue cloth bag. 

Even though he tried his best to hide his fear and anxiety, his hands were still trembling slightly.

Seeing this, Sun Daoren shook his head in frustration, turning to follow Huang Shi, feeling somewhat sympathetic yet irritated at this fellow. He said in his heart, “Chen Daoist! Remember your place moving forward; don’t get too close to Huang Shi. It’s best to keep yourself a distance away from him. If Huang Shi gets too close, no amount of talismans will help you; don’t you understand this simple principle that a Qi practitioner should never allow a pure martial artist to get close?!”

“Daoist Sun, I understand the principle, but when it comes to actually fighting Huang Shi, my mind goes blank and my limbs don’t respond; I really can’t keep up with the theory in practice,” replied Chen Ping'an.

After securing the copper mirror, the man quickened his pace to catch up with Sun Daoren, then slowed down to walk behind him, keeping in step. 

Sun Daoren sighed and said no more; at least he was a person who would learn from mistakes, not entirely hopeless.

Chen Ping'an brought up the rear, gently wiping the blood from the corner of his mouth. 

Ordinary martial artists traversing the world often ended up with bloodied faces due to bad luck.

But for Chen Ping'an, it was different; he had to do it himself.

However, thinking about that ancient copper mirror, his resentment faded.

The inscription was tiny, with the front reading “Repel Soldiers, None Shall Stand” and the back stating “Ward Off Evil, Eliminate Misfortune.”

This was undoubtedly an anti-evil mirror, and it was an imitation, as upon careful inspection, Chen Ping'an discovered the minuscule inscription “crafted by the Gong family.” This detail was what made it truly valuable. 

For anyone to quietly inscribe the surname “Gong” on a copper mirror artifact was a testament to its quality.

The celestial records spoke of this matter, particularly regarding the ancient mirrors with sea beast grape patterns like “Li Pu Zao” and “Nalan Sanshan Zao,” which were immensely valuable. Imitations that came after were often traps for half-baked Qi practitioners; even if they were exquisite and flawless, they remained a big pitfall. Those who believed they had found a treasure would regret it if they attempted to refine them into their life’s essence.

Earlier, Chen Ping'an had almost given in to the temptation to let Sun Daoren have a look, under the pretense of helping him appraise it, before taking it seriously himself. 

This Daoist Sun’s hands had to have been blessed, right?

Aside from this acquisition, the string of pagoda bells hanging from the waist of the tall, thin Daoist was clearly not an ordinary object.

Otherwise, it wouldn’t have shattered spontaneously as a warning outside the mountain-top temple.

On the back mountain, the structures were far fewer than the densely packed front mountain, and only three grand buildings could be counted.

As the three descended the mountain, the view was sparse.

This also prevented a lot of trouble.

As per the usual arrangement, Huang Shi would search for treasure at a place nearby, while Sun Daoren headed off to another location with a tall building. Chen Ping'an was assigned to the closest hall at the foot of the mountain.

After parting from Sun Daoren, Chen Ping'an walked leisurely as if wandering through a garden, taking out his sword nurturing gourd to sip the bamboo leaf spirit water. It genuinely felt refreshing.

Though the flavor was a bit bland, lacking the richness of wine.

Just the thought of this spiritually rich bamboo leaf essence being precious and rare, far surpassing celestial brews, instantly made him feel the taste was exquisite, a lingering aftertaste.

With just this sip, he was drinking not mere tea but a fortune of celestial money—how could it not be delightful?

Turning back, he saw no trace of Huang Shi or Sun Daoren. Chen Ping'an then secured his sword nurturing gourd, bent low, and suddenly dashed forward, effortlessly leaping over a high wall and landing gracefully.

It was as though he had melded with the heavens and earth, making no sound and creating no ripples.

At the foot of the front mountain, near the white jade bridge, a chaotic battle raged.

In the words of the customs of North Julu Prefecture, they were fighting fiercely enough to drink the brain matter as wine; now that was true heroism.

This fierce battle for the bridge had become exceptionally brutal.

Even the royal offering from the Fuhua Kingdom searching for treasures on the mountain had heard the commotion, having to abandon readily obtainable opportunities and rush to the battlefield.

However, this Fuhua Kingdom offering had a clever plan, selecting a portion of the treasures he deemed valuable to hide in a loft's beam while casually wrapping the rest together and moving them to another corner of the house. When it came time to return with Bai Bi and the young marquis, he wouldn't raise any suspicion. As for how to ultimately smuggle out his hidden treasures, he'd take it step by step.

Gao Ling had taken out the military armor, donning a divine armor that revealed his presence while partnering with the family offering to safeguard Zhan Qing’s safety.

Zhan Qing, a practitioner of the cave realm trained under a Nascent Soul grandmaster, feigned panic. This act, combined with his previous haughty words, proved effective; few believed this North Ting noble youth was an actual mid-stage five realm practitioner, nor did he possess two powerful offensive treasures.

The originally one-sided battle shifted slightly in favor after the Fuhua Kingdom offering joined the fray.

Zhan Qing held a grudge against the woman in the cloud-castle robe with the cloud-like aura, as she was the one who first crossed the bridge and disrupted his scheme to gain wealth.

What’s more, this hidden female practitioner was exceptionally strategic during the ensuing chaos, avoiding direct confrontation with the golden body martial artists while not sitting idly by, allowing various practitioners and martial artists to die; every time Gao Ling was able to strike down an opponent, the female practitioner would counteract in time, saving the lives of seven or eight people in just a short while.

The two defensive life treasures she possessed were a jade bracelet that glimmered with a blue light, spinning erratically, and a golden embroidered rug adorned with five dragons. Gao Ling's punch merely made a dent in it, causing it to vibrate without shattering. After a punch, its golden dragon sheen would dim slightly. However, the bracelet and rug alternated in defense; once saturated with spiritual energy, the golden sheen would quickly restore.

With over forty people surrounding them, everyone unleashed their offensive treasures, creating a grand spectacle. If not for the practitioners' unfamiliar cooperation, some of the four and five realm pure martial artists would not dare to get too close, mostly resorting to long-range attacks with bows and crossbows or sending out pressure waves to trouble the opposing side, making it hard to connect seamlessly; otherwise, they would find it even harder to cope. But once the mountain-dwelling wild practitioners chose to fight for their lives, even someone like Zhan Qing, who had only seen minimal blood, or Gao Ling, who came from a military background, along with the family offering accustomed to luxury, would feel their hearts race.

The family offering was ambushed by someone with a secret treasure, penetrating their abdomen and causing a severe bleed. However, relying on their golden body physique, they held on for dear life. Gao Ling, skilled in battle formations, was not unfamiliar with the encirclement of spears and halberds, which still left him relatively unscathed. As for the Fuhua royal offering, they were in a miserable state, struck by a stream of offensive artifacts. Had Gao Ling not assisted with a punch to disperse most of the attack, the offering would have certainly perished on the spot.

Still, these two golden body martial artists were no pushovers; even with the assistance of the Cai Que Mansion, they still killed seven or eight people, leaving behind a gruesome scene reminiscent of a public execution.

Thus, the swift arrival of the Water Dragon Sect’s Golden Core immortal Bai Bi was not just a bonus, but a timely resource.

Yet as soon as Bai Bi summoned both an offensive and a defensive treasure, the young mansion lord of Cai Que Mansion, Sun Qing, took to the skies, choosing to engage this young sect disciple in battle.

Surrounding Bai Bi was a set of eighteen victory talismans gifted by the Water Dragon Sect, which was well-suited for Bai Bi, a naturally talented practitioner of water techniques. The talisman inscriptions held significant meaning, containing remnants of national fortune, once used to mint coins in an ancient dynasty, then scattered in various places, placed in old Taoist temple beams, or buried in ancient tombs, or even collected by the royal treasury over the years, making up two sets of eighteen, one of which was gifted to Bai Bi.

This set of victory talismans, regarded as valuable items within the Water Dragon Sect, was both offensive and defensive.

However, Bai Bi still summoned a heavy artifact from the mountain, an ancient zither from the hands of a renowned zither master in North Julu Prefecture, named “Falling Snow.”

Once the two Golden Core practitioners made their move, the battle intensified.

Then someone with a raspy voice shouted, “Let’s take down the young marquis first!”

Zhan Qing was furious; this person was truly difficult to deal with.

Every time he opened his mouth, it had the effect of using four ounces to counter a thousand pounds.

But the opponent clearly wielded some secret technique from the mountain; combined with the perilous chaos, it became a mess, making it difficult for Zhan Qing's group to identify their adversary.

Neither Gao Ling nor the family offering would dare to watch as they were killed by techniques and artifacts. However, if they took care of Zhan Qing too much, it would inevitably lead to neglect elsewhere. Once a flaw appeared, it would cause a chain reaction, easily endangering Bai Bi. Zhan Qing could assert that as long as they lost a Golden Body realm martial artist or someone was severely injured and had to withdraw from the battlefield, these desperate wild practitioners would fight even harder.

Zhan Qing had already warned Gao Ling and the two family offerings, suggesting they focus their efforts on taking down one or two of the enemy’s groups, cleaning them out entirely to deter vengeance from their friends, only to find that fate had conspired against them. The battles had become increasingly reckless, and due to a series of unfortunate events, Gao Ling and the two offerings could no longer act cautiously. They had to focus on killing, while the opponent had the advantage in numbers, attacking indiscriminately with a flurry of treasures and insidious techniques.

At this moment, Zhan Qing began to regret his earlier arrogance.

He should never have viewed seizing all the local opportunities as a simple task.

Instead, they should have taken a step-by-step, methodical approach rather than believing their group could easily slay a Nascent Soul practitioner, dismissing the wild practitioners as mere ants.

The situation had turned dire, and now he found himself regretting his earlier belief that he could block the path of anyone, like the narrative of a hero standing against a thousand.

Zhan Qing had initially calculated well, but on the path of cultivation, one misstep could lead to a complete failure.

Bai Bi suddenly realized that as a distinguished Golden Core disciple of the Water Dragon Sect, he could not compete with the young female practitioner before him who concealed her face. 

Bai Bi angrily stated, “Sun Qing from Cai Que Mansion! Do you dare to kill me? Are you not afraid of incurring the wrath of the Water Dragon Sect? A single slap from my family’s elder could flatten your Peach Blossom Crossing Cai Que Mansion!”

The reason Bai Bi refrained from shouting directly was that, being a disciple of the lineage, he was far more cautious in dealing with the wild practitioners, weighing his options carefully.

Sun Qing, wielding her offensive artifact, shattered the “Falling Snow” zither strings, scattering the “snowflakes” that were unleashed, and replied with a smile, “What are you saying? I can’t understand you.”

Bai Bi, infuriated, exclaimed, “Sun Qing! Are you truly seeking a fight to the death with me?!”

With eighteen victory talismans surrounding him, Bai Bi was still holding his ground against Sun Qing. Moreover, this talisman arrangement was both offensive and defensive, and he had yet to exert his full power. Furthermore, as a lineage disciple, he certainly had one or two ultimate escape techniques up his sleeve. Thus, Bai Bi’s anger stemmed more from the loss of an opportunity for solitary gain than from any immediate peril, and compared to Zhan Qing, who was already in the thick of battle, Bai Bi was in a much better position.

Sun Qing remained unyielding, smiling, “As free-spirited wild practitioners, we care nothing for ties; we live or die at our own whim.”

For a female practitioner to utter such words was truly overstepping.

Bai Bi took a deep breath, calming his mind to a tranquil state, devoid of any distractions, to the point where he could entirely ignore Zhan Qing’s situation.

Since the rules of the disciples of the lineage were unyielding, and both parties were of equal standing, the only way to resolve this was through a battle of cultivation.

Although Sun Qing appeared nonchalant, she was far more composed than Bai Bi, who had only recently entered the Golden Core stage. However, she remained vigilant, knowing she was facing a talented young genius of a well-established sect, and awaited the opportunity for a decisive strike. If that failed, then it would be time to sit down and negotiate as disciples.

Should the opponent be superior in skill, it would be no great loss to her.

She could kill, and others could kill her.

Thus, when that sword cultivator, who resembled a teacher, had traveled with her, he once said, “No one in this world is exempt from death.”

However, that same land dragon from North Julu had also added, “But everyone in this world can reason.”

Sun Qing had never fully accepted that latter statement, finding little truth in it.

But she liked him, so she wouldn’t argue.

Of course, should she truly engage Liu Jinglong in a debate, it would merely be self-inflicted suffering.

She would never win against him.

Back then, Liu Jinglong, as a Golden Core sword cultivator, had managed to persuade an old monster of the Jade Purity stage, who was intent on slaughtering, with merely his words. Not only that, he had even formed a somewhat adversarial yet friendly relationship with the old monster, who had subsequently guided their group safely out of the region.

Last time Sun Qing had “coincidentally encountered” Liu Jinglong, after some polite exchanges, they had run out of things to discuss. She casually inquired about that encounter, and Liu Jinglong had said he had met the old senior while traveling south, and they had enjoyed a pleasant conversation. However, the senior had insisted that Liu Jinglong return north to the Tai Hui Sword Sect to cultivate without making another trip back up the mountain.

As Chen Ping'an searched the area, he found few bones scattered on the ground. He silently apologized to them, then squatted down to examine a bone, which was still like any mundane skeletal remains, unlike the ones at the Bone Marsh that were tainted with dark energy and appeared a ghostly white. 

It was the same on the front mountain.

This indicated that the local practitioners had never truly produced a capable immortal in their lifetimes, at least not one who had reached the Earth Immortal stage. 

There was also something odd. In the pavilion with the stone table engraved with a chessboard, the two players were clearly adorned in well-crafted robes. However, after Huang Shi stripped them of their clothing, Chen Ping'an discovered that those two corpses still lacked the quality of Golden Core lineage.

Wherever Chen Ping'an went, the winding paths were still filled with rich spiritual energy, and he felt no discomfort.

Thus, he wasted another Yang Energy Lamp Talisman.

Chen Ping'an’s gains were meager, with only a few severely cracked mountain artifacts, confirming that he should have explored with Sun Daoren instead.

He arrived at a dried-up pond, with decaying leaves scattered about.

It seemed that if it were full of water, it would have been a place of springs.

Chen Ping'an pondered over the inscriptions at the entrance of the cave. The one who left them must have been someone who had entered this celestial ruin.

It could be either a hidden immortal leaving behind clues for future generations or merely someone fearing even the fish were too dull to bite the bait.

Chen Ping'an climbed over the railing and leaped into the pond, finding the dry leaves crumbling at his touch, showing no hidden secrets.

The spiritual energy related to water from the back mountain was indeed most concentrated near that green bamboo.

What the Fallen Mountain truly lacked was a good bamboo.

If it could be like the courageous bamboo ancestor that Wei Ban cherished so much on Chess Stone Mountain, year after year branching out, with roots spreading underground, producing children and grandchildren, it could easily give rise to a lush grove of bamboos.

Of course, in Chen Ping'an's eyes, Fallen Mountain lacked everything.

He gathered a handful of soil, which quickly crumbled into dust at his fingertips, scattering in all directions.

As for the great river in North Julu, Chen Ping'an knew a fair bit.

Yet he remained largely ignorant of the deeper undercurrents, the rise and fall of shrines, and the shifts in history. 

He had only ever heard Wei Ban mention that there had once been an east-west river in Liuxia Prefecture, winding thirty thousand miles, which would overflow with sages and earth immortals whenever mountains and waters met.

There was also a river in Fuyou Prefecture, where a massive floodwater had breached a dam, causing the great river to surge into the sea, which led to calamity affecting the entire waterway. In just three hundred years, the river completely vanished, meaning all the water deities and river gods along its banks would dissolve into their golden forms. The rituals and protocols for deifying deities along the river were exceedingly complex, far more so than those required by a monarch for local mountain and river deities, often requiring documents submitted to the Confucian academies of the Central Plains.

Chen Ping'an surveyed his surroundings, finding no signs of life, and took a deep swig from his sword nurturing gourd, draining it in one go, immersing his mind and spirit, his thoughts as small as a mustard seed, exploring the waters.

He noticed the gates of the water realm wide open, as if they hadn’t been closed at all.

At his feet flowed a stream of emerald water, gradually coalescing from various water lines, slowly winding its way into the pond of the water realm.

The little green-clad children scurrying about didn't even glance at the great benefactor who had arrived; they were all bustling about, filled with excitement.

This scene made Chen Ping'an feel a pang of sadness, realizing that the little ones were truly impoverished.

He also took a look at the mountain shrine, where a finer stream flowed, trickling toward the sacred site of the mountain shrine. This water, having had all its essence intercepted in the water realm, flowed clear and colorless, devoid of the rich emerald hues that had previously characterized it. The dense spiritual energy transformed into a gentle rain, saturating the earth once it reached the shrine’s location.

Chen Ping'an contemplated this for a moment, then withdrew his spirit, no longer lingering in this treasure-less residence. With the cultivation and steps befitting a Daoist friend, he took off running, stealthily returning to that green bamboo that was likely from the Qing Shen Mountain, placing his palm on the bamboo stalk and giving it a gentle shake, causing the bamboo to sway slightly. 

Then, with his sword nurturing gourd in hand, he waved his sleeve to gather the remaining droplets of water from the bamboo leaves, all of which he successfully collected into the gourd.

Chen Ping'an felt quite pleased with himself.

It seemed he truly was a master at picking up bargains.

After securing the gourd, he began to climb the bamboo, only to find that those seemingly fragile bamboo branches, which looked as if a child could easily snap them, were surprisingly resilient.

Chen Ping'an turned his gaze toward the distant temple, where Huang Shi stood atop a wall, having watched this scene for quite some time.

“Late to realize,” Chen Ping'an smiled and waved his hand.

Huang Shi stepped off the wall and returned to the ground.

What a pathetic creature, obsessed with wealth yet unable to find a way to obtain it.

With Huang Shi's gaze now diverted, Chen Ping'an tested the bending bamboo branches, managing to pluck some leaves. With his current cultivation level, he could barely accomplish this, gathering one handful after another and stuffing them into a side satchel, forcefully filling the once-deflated bag.

Switching positions, he continued observing the martial artist Huang Shi, feeling truly impressed. If this person were the rumored hidden immortal, Huang Shi would willingly offer his neck to the law of the sword.

Once Huang Shi truly departed, Chen Ping'an quickly aligned his fingers, striking swiftly to sever the varying thicknesses of bamboo branches, swiftly storing them in his pocket.

The items in his satchel were now truly packed.

After completing his task, Chen Ping'an remained by the green bamboo for a while, not yet eager to touch the ground.

He vaguely recalled the time in his youth, climbing trees to catch cicadas with two others; one was his closest friend who always protected him, and the other was a half-relative he had grown accustomed to safeguarding.

Back then, life seemed impoverished, yet each year, month after month, they were carefree and worry-free.

Chen Ping'an sighed.

Retrieving his thoughts, a teasing voice suddenly called out from the distance, “Old Chen? What are you doing?”

Turning to look, Chen Ping'an laughed heartily, “Just enjoying the cool breeze and the beautiful view!”

It was Di Yuanfeng, disguised as Qin Juyuan, whose complexion was slightly pale, likely due to suffering some injuries.

“Juyuan, great ape?” 

The largest species of monkey in the world, was it not the mountain-moving ape?

That name had a rather annoying ring to it.

Di Yuanfeng paid no heed to the black-robed elder, instead directing his gaze toward the nearest temple complex and inquired, “How did Daoist Sun and Brother Huang fare?”

Chen Ping'an replied with a smile, “We all did well.”

Di Yuanfeng couldn’t resist glancing at the old man clutching the bamboo, with two cross-body bags filled with either tiles or bricks, wondering, what's the hurry to go home and build a house or marry?

Unfortunately, Chen Ping'an could not guess his thoughts.

Otherwise, he would have genuinely given him a thumbs up, sincerely praising him as a true immortal.

The old immortal Huan Yun had returned with a full load, a talisman-sized item already packed to the brim.

The old offering from the Cloud City was also satisfied, carrying a large bag on his back, with two additional bundles in his hands, his face brimming with joy.

The two old men met atop a loft, overlooking the battlefield at the mountain gate.

The old offering chuckled, “What a dog-eat-dog situation.”

Huan Yun smiled in response, saying nothing.

On the path of cultivation, a single misstep can lead to multiple missteps.

If the two direct disciples of Shen Zhenze had not been guarded, and had entered this place first, they would have been forced to engage in deadly combat with the group led by the young marquis from North Ting.

However, Huan Yun was sharp-eyed and quickly discerned the telltale signs of the two major practitioners from Cai Que Mansion, most likely the immortal Sun Qing and the law master Wu Jun.

As for the young female practitioner floating in the air, holding the ancient zither, it was evident that she wielded the “Falling Snow” zither, carved long ago by a master.

Yet this zither had once belonged to a female Nascent Soul practitioner of the Water Dragon Sect, who had engaged in a legendary battle by the waters, using the zither and terrain to outmaneuver an old Nascent Soul rival.

Now, in the hands of the Water Dragon Sect's female practitioner, it was only displaying about fifty to sixty percent of its unique abilities.

The old offering quietly asked, “Should we take a detour to the algae well and leave quietly, or go take another look at the back mountain?”

Huan Yun smiled, “We are the protectors; let those two youngsters decide. We just need to remain hidden and not actively get involved. This journey should pose no worries.”

Huan Yun glanced at the sky above, his gaze drifting to the distant border of this small realm.

Bai Bi had already noticed something unusual, but the old immortal had certainly confirmed it far earlier.

However, there was a hidden talisman buried beneath the entrance of the algae well, and as long as it did not malfunction, it meant the escape route was still intact.

Although this place was filled with mysteries and intricacies, it appeared devoid of any filth or malevolence, a comforting thought for the old immortal.

The spiritual energy of the land and water was the hardest to fabricate or disguise.

Even if a major demon from the Nascent Soul realm were to create a dazzling illusion of a celestial secret realm, it would still be detectable by someone skilled in talismans like Huan Yun, who could uncover the clues and recognize the situation early on.

In the vast world of the righteous path, there were once many factions flourishing, a vibrant scene.

However, many once-prominent branches had since faded away, their incense extinguished and no longer impactful, while some had gradually been lost to time.

For instance, the once-thriving sword immortal lineage of the Central Plains was truly a grand sight; back then, even with innumerable sword cultivators and standing sword immortals, they dared not claim to occupy eight parts of the world’s sword energy. 

In the past, the four notorious ghostly figures of the mountain had shared a place with the sword cultivators and blade masters. At that time, the Daoist sword immortals did not regard themselves simply as sword cultivators.

Huan Yun lamented the changes in the righteous path, observing the bloody chaos unfolding at the foot of the mountain, feeling a deep sense of regret.

In the eyes of the old immortal, those fighting for opportunities at the mountain gate were merely children.

Unbidden, he recalled a poet’s words: “In the eyes of a child, the world is vast and rugged.”

Later generations would annotate this line, noting that “rugged” was the antonym of “magnanimous,” thus revealing the fickleness of human emotions and the treacherous paths of the heart—far more perilous than the steep roads of a thousand miles.

Huan Yun suddenly said, “You go protect them in seeking opportunities in the future; I will go down to the foot of the mountain and try to mediate, saving as many lives as possible.”

The old offering hesitated, caught in thought. After weighing the situation, he understood the old immortal’s good intentions and nodded in agreement.

Unless the group from Cloud City left quickly, if the chaos at the foot of the mountain escalated, especially if the Water Dragon Sect’s direct disciple fell, the wrath of their Golden Core elders would surely thunder down upon North Ting and Fuhua Kingdom, ensnaring Cai Que Mansion and Cloud City without a doubt. 

Whoever gained the most today would bear the heaviest burden.

Moreover, if the old immortal could help break the deadlock between both sides, allowing them to sit down and negotiate a viable solution, it would earn him the favor of the Water Dragon Sect, Cai Que Mansion, and North Ting Kingdom alike.

Huan Yun handed a talisman to the old offering from Cloud City, saying, “In case of trouble, activate this talisman and I will arrive immediately.”

The old offering accepted the talisman, vanishing in a flash.

Huan Yun’s mood was not light—“Going to mediate is easy, but doing it well is hard. It’s not just about the mediator's realm; understanding the timing of human hearts is key.”

After Huan Yun took action, he neither assisted one side nor the other. With talismans at the ready, he aimed to prevent the two groups from continuing their slaughter.

At the same time, he appealed to their emotions, explaining that there were many opportunities on the mountain. If they could still trust him, Huan Yun, they might as well join forces to search for treasures instead of fighting to their mutual destruction.

The once-chaotic battle situation suddenly transformed, like turbulent waters flowing into a large lake, quickly calming down.

Especially as Huan Yun called upon five individuals to hold a secret discussion.

Among them were Zhan Qing, the young marquis of North Ting Kingdom, Sun Qing from Cai Que Mansion, Bai Bi of the Water Dragon Sect, and two of the most formidable leaders among the mountain dwellers.

Thus, they devised a plan for both sides to take a step back from the bridge, of course, Zhan Qing and Bai Bi's side would concede more. The reasoning was simple: if the battle continued, the only survivor from their side might end up being Bai Bi, who would be forced to flee.

Meanwhile, the other side was bound to see very few survivors, at most ten, and with bad luck, perhaps only a handful.

Therefore, Huan Yun’s appearance was a tremendous boon for both parties.

Otherwise, they would find themselves in an awkward situation, unable to escape without shattering one another’s heads.

At the same time, under Huan Yun’s lead, they roughly agreed on compensation for those who had fallen in battle.

During a secret conversation between Huan Yun and Bai Bi, the latter even took out a sum of celestial money on the spot to hand to three others, allowing them to negotiate the distribution of this compensation.

On Zhan Qing and Bai Bi’s side, they had lost a family offering, while Gao Ling was also heavily injured, his precious rain armor on the verge of collapsing. The Fuhua royal offering wasn’t in much better shape either.

Zhan Qing himself had even lost the secret treasure folding fan that had not yet been refined into his life’s essence; he had no idea whether it had fallen into the river or had been secretly taken by some unscrupulous bastard.

The young marquis, with his hair disheveled and his robe tattered, no longer bore the demeanor of a noble family heir.

However, the family had lost a pillar of strength in the form of a seventh realm martial artist.

Zhan Qing neither complained nor sought to vindicate himself against Bai Bi; instead, he maintained a calm expression, leaving all decision-making power in Bai Bi’s hands.

This left Bai Bi feeling quite gratified.

During this time, Sun Qing took the initiative to communicate with Bai Bi, who was at a disadvantage, through their thoughts, “As for the ownership of this place, our Cai Que Mansion is willing to help you wait until the elders of the Water Dragon Sect arrive, doing our utmost to prevent Cloud City from alerting other sects. But if Shen Zhenze from Cloud City arrives with other major practitioners first, don’t blame our Cai Que practitioners for withdrawing.”

This single sentence greatly changed Bai Bi’s impression of this Cai Que Mansion master.

Previously, both sides had been holding back, and apart from the old immortal Huan Yun, it was likely no one else had noticed. Thus, after they established a verbal alliance, Bai Bi began to contemplate forming a private friendship with Cai Que Mansion in the future.

Seeing that both sides had roughly come to an agreement, Huan Yun felt a sense of relief.

Mediating is easy but doing it well is quite challenging. It requires not only the mediator's level of cultivation but also the skillful grasp of human emotions.

At the old temple site on the mountaintop, a towering old man appeared out of nowhere, glancing at the mounds of debris from the temple ruins, shaking his head with a smirk as he slowly walked toward the top steps. “Do you children think this is the end? Is there such easy treasure to be taken in this world? People kill one another at most, driven by their desires. Otherwise, what joy would there be in watching you children brawl?”

He lightly stamped his foot.

Upon reaching the steps, he peered down at the ceasefire between the two sides, casting a quick glance before his ethereal figure was instantly shattered by a wisp of sword energy.

Yet the emerald river at the foot of the mountain began to exhibit strange phenomena. Initially, it rippled gently, but soon it started to bubble violently.

Huan Yun was the first to notice the unusual signs, his sleeves fluttering as talismans flew out like water.

In the blink of an eye, the river beneath the bridge fell silent, and then two figures emerged, standing on either side of the white jade bridge—each was a towering figure of five meters tall. One was a deity clad in green, wielding a silver spear, while the other held a heavy iron club. 

Simultaneously, the white jade bridge shrouded in mist solidified into a white-clad goddess with golden eyes, her expression unreadable as she held a scroll that resembled a Taoist decree. 

She floated gracefully, unfurling the scroll, her voice heavenly as she began to speak slowly.

Even the well-read old immortal Huan Yun found the words of this white-clad goddess absurd, yet he couldn’t help but feel a sense of belief.

The gist was that this place was where an ancient immortal had attained enlightenment and ascended, once ranked as the thirty-sixth cave heaven and seventy-first blessed land. It was a pure and serene realm, and their reckless intrusion was both a chance and a crime. 

Before ascending, the immortal had left behind a decree for the three of them, promising future cultivators that based on the number of treasures they obtained, the size of their opportunities would be determined. Ultimately, five individuals would remain, allowing them to keep all the heavenly materials and earthly treasures they had gathered, while the leader among them could inherit the status of the ascendant immortal, with the rest temporarily registered as disciples, receiving a teaching that pointed directly to immortality.

Within a span of ten days, only five could survive; otherwise, all would be forfeit, and they would face heavenly retribution, struck down at the scene. As disciples, if they could not cleanse the impurities for their master, they were not worthy of such a fate.

Once the scroll unfurled, it expanded like a cascading waterfall, dropping from the heavens to the ground.

The scroll depicted portraits of five individuals.

These were the five currently holding the most treasures and fortunes.

Apart from this water screen, at various locations on the mountain and behind it, smaller screens hung in the air wherever people were present.

The white-clad goddess's voice, while soft, resonated throughout the realm, reaching every ear.

The young male practitioner carrying the white jade pen tube from Cloud City stared in disbelief; he was among those listed, and his rank was not low—he placed second.

Beside him, the female practitioner felt a mix of happiness and worry.

The one at the bottom was a young gentleman with a sword.

Di Yuanfeng.

This handsome young man, whose complexion was slightly pale, was left speechless.

In the fourth position was a disheveled man who stood before the stone tablet in the temple, arms crossed and eyes squinted.

The third was the tall, thin Daoist who had been using a robe as a bag.

It was none other than Sun Daoren, who claimed to be the disciple of the Thunder God’s abode.

At this moment, the tall Daoist was sweating profusely.

And the one in first place?

It was the black-robed elder, who was currently levitating with a bamboo in his arms.

Chen Ping'an.

As everyone gazed at the mural, he still refused to touch the ground, scratching his head with a sincere expression, addressing the floating landscape scroll beside him, “What’s going on here? You’ve got it all wrong, truly all wrong.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 643: Those Aboard the Vessel Face the Enemy Nation (Part One)

The White-Clad Goddess and the two Green-Clad Deities had already dissipated.

After half a shichen (a period of two hours), the water curtain would appear once more. If a full shichen passed and the number of remaining people here exceeded five, a heavenly calamity would descend, killing everyone present.

Huan Yun discovered that the talismans buried in the moss-covered beams had shattered, indicating that the mountain and river spirits of this place had closed off the exit to the immortal abode.

On the side of the White Jade Arch Bridge, a variety of cultivators and martial artists, mixed together like fish and dragons, exchanged glances. The fragile unity Huan Yun had painstakingly fostered moments ago was instantly shattered, returning to a state of disarray. Even with six people left, they all unconsciously stepped back, creating distance between each other.

Only Bai Bi and Zhan Qing stood side by side, silently communicating.

In an instant, the world fell into silence, the sound of a pin drop could be heard.

The young couple from Cloud City (Yunshang Cheng) grew increasingly heavy-hearted. The young woman asked, “Senior Brother, can Huan Laozhen (Old Man Huan) protect us?”

The young man forced a bitter smile. “Perhaps Old Man Huan is unwilling to kill us, and that would already be a great kindness.”

The young woman's face paled.

The young man sighed helplessly. “In the end, Huan Yun is not one of our own. The only one we can trust now is Xu Gongfu (Lord Xu).”

After a moment, the two pondered their predicament, trying to break the current deadlock, but unfortunately, they could not come up with a solution.

The dusty figure of the Dragon Gate's protector, who had hurried over, stood beside them, his expression grave as he slowly spoke, “Why not hand that white jade pen tube to me? I will draw everyone’s attention away.”

Without hesitation, the young man handed over the small item, expressing his gratitude, “Thank you, Xu Gongfu.”

The old protector carefully stowed the white jade pen tube into his sleeve and departed.

The young woman looked on in surprise.

The young man shook his head, signaling her to remain silent. Although the young woman was not as composed and meticulous as her senior brother and had often been scolded by the city lord Shen Zhenze, she understood that handing over the small item at this moment was definitely not a good thing.

The young man communicated through thought, “If we hadn’t handed it over, we would have already become two corpses by now. After half a shichen, if we and this Tao Gongfu can survive until then, just wait— the item will return to its rightful owner.”

The young woman said anxiously, “So, we just wait until the water curtain disappears and it gets taken away?”

The young man chuckled, “What else can we do?”

Tears welled in the young woman's eyes.

The young man gently wiped her tears, his movements tender, but he remained silent. It wasn't that he didn't want to say something; rather, there was nothing to say.

Under the green bamboo on the back mountain, Di Yuanfeng's expression was solemn. He glanced up, clearly having no intention of provoking the old man in black robes, planning to stay as far away as possible.

Without hesitation, Di Yuanfeng dashed down the mountain, bypassing the palace complex.

Chen Ping'an slid down a bamboo pole and, passing by the palace buildings, noticed that Huang Shi was completely silent, unsure of what to make of it.

Daoist Sun removed two bundles, placing them at his feet. He didn't dare to simply abandon his belongings and flee, worried that someone might beat the old master to death, leaving him with no way to explain himself. As a rogue cultivator at the Sea Viewing level, he simply wasn’t strong enough.

Daoist Sun could only gamble that a group of people would notice him, take what they saw as good fortune, and not take his life.

At this moment, even if he were truly the immortal teacher of the Infant Mountain Thunder God’s abode, what good would it do? None at all.

After witnessing this scene, Chen Ping'an thought to himself that the old man had finally shown some wisdom. He hadn't abandoned his treasures and made a run for it.

Daoist Sun looked up with tearful eyes, pitifully gazing at Chen Ping'an, who stood atop the wall, before waving his hand, “Let’s go, let’s get as far away as possible.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Take care.”

However, before leaving, he tossed over three talismans, all of which were concealment talismans. 

Gifting him offensive talismans wouldn't hold much meaning anymore.

After explaining the use of the talismans with his thoughts, Chen Ping'an also hastily fled down the mountain.

After catching the talismans, Daoist Sun looked up again, and the figure of Chen Ping'an atop the wall had already vanished. He sighed, “Adversity reveals true hearts.”

Chen Ping'an only hoped that Daoist Sun had given up his chance at treasure and could temporarily keep his life.

After that, there was indeed a glimmer of hope.

The Lotus Flower Blessed Land had also been in a similar predicament back in the day. After a chaotic battle that darkened the sky, the Arm Saint Cheng Yuanshan, without having to fight at all, not only survived until the end but if he hadn’t missed the chance to reach the city’s peak, he would have easily acquired the fortune of ascending to the Great Harmony Realm.

As for whether five people would ultimately survive—he found it hard to believe they could have such incredible luck, being accepted as direct disciples or named disciples by some high-level ascendant.

On the path of cultivation, opportunities often seemed most enticing when linked to treasures, making it appear that the more opportunities one had, the more they were cut out for cultivation.
