However, Chen Ping'an understood that for those at higher realms, evaluating disciples required considering their foundational skills, talents, temperament, and opportunities—all aspects were indispensable.

When an ancient ascendant took on disciples, especially those of direct lineage, they would not merely consider how many treasures the future disciple acquired in the mountains.

Everywhere was fraught with hidden dangers. If previously, seeking treasures and opportunities felt like the reasonable calculations of rogue cultivators, now the environment forced everyone to turn against each other, where anyone could die at the hands of their neighbors. The one in control here was obviously no kind-hearted soul, possibly even deliberately inciting discord to let the remaining forty or so people slaughter each other, allowing him to reap the benefits.

With the sudden shattering of Daoist Sun's pagoda bell, Chen Ping'an even speculated that the mastermind behind this place might be a great demon, only hampered by certain old rules, unable to act freely. The presence of that fierce sword energy could very well be a form of restraint.

Chen Ping'an suddenly recalled a conversation he’d had with Cui Qian on the steps of the Falling-Into-Poverty Mountain.

Cui Qian had expressed great certainty about the state of the world, and at that time, Chen Ping'an had wanted to ask the Grand Master of the Great Li why he didn’t inform certain people or directly proclaim the matter to the world.

However, he had held back the question, eventually finding his answer: it was because no one would listen, and even if they did, they wouldn’t believe it.

Chen Ping'an hadn’t strayed far from the area of Daoist Sun’s building. 

However, he had done some calculations.

Should he break the heavenly curtain with his sword immediately?

This was a choice that could very well determine life or death. 

Because after witnessing the supernatural events of this site, his understanding of the hidden “Heaven” behind the scenes had heightened. When he had successfully escaped from the Ghost Valley, it had been a sudden and unforeseen event, catching the higher powers of Jingguan City off guard. But the one here might have already started to keep a close watch on Chen Ping'an.

Thus, he had a more moderate idea.

Like that Arm Saint Cheng Yuanshan from the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, he should hide until half a shichen later; at that time, whether it was fortune or disaster, the intentions of the one behind this would become clear.

Deciding whether to draw his sword would then be much easier.

Huang Shi emerged from around the corner, puzzled. “You’re so concerned about Daoist Sun’s life? Worried I might kill this so-called Thunder God’s abode immortal with a punch?”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “What do you think?”

Huang Shi smirked, “Why don’t we join forces to fend off the enemy?”

Chen Ping'an asked, “Aren’t you afraid I’ll drag you down?”

Huang Shi’s suspicion deepened, and he could no longer restrain himself from asking, “What realm are you in, exactly? A Dragon Gate cultivator proficient in talismans or a Golden Core Earth Immortal?”

Chen Ping'an countered, “What about you?”

Huang Shi honestly replied, “I’m just an average Golden Body martial artist, with a major vendetta to settle, so I can’t die.”

Chen Ping'an said, “Then treat me as a Golden Core cultivator, well, an average one.”

After pondering for a moment, Huang Shi said, “Let’s retreat from this mountain first. We should strive not to be encircled and killed. This is undoubtedly the worst-case scenario, but considering our current situation, it’s not wrong to think negatively.”

Chen Ping'an inquired, “Why not learn from Daoist Sun and just hand over the treasure?”

Huang Shi scoffed, “What? Do you think those so-called immortal teachers are all compassionate? Or are you hoping the mountain and field cultivators suddenly become good and willing to sacrifice themselves to be righteous?”

Chen Ping'an rubbed his chin, seemingly considering whether to sincerely cooperate with Huang Shi to overcome the crisis.

Huang Shi urged, “Opportunities like this don’t come often. If we keep hesitating, it’ll just increase our danger.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “Let’s forget it. I’m afraid you’ll sneak in another punch. My old bones can’t take it.”

Huang Shi shook his head, “You’ll definitely die before I do.”

After saying that, Huang Shi took a few steps back and disappeared around the corner.

Chen Ping'an then affixed another concealment talisman to himself, searching for a secluded place. He donned a simple blue shirt; the three layers of robes combined with the ordinary shirt made him look somewhat bulky, but it was winter, and it made sense to dress warmly.

He changed the old man's face for that of a youth and adopted the posture of Zhu Lian's monkey fist style, slightly bending over to appear a bit shorter. He then removed the two slung bags he had and buried them underground, while the sword immortal and the sword nurturing gourd were also taken off and placed into the small item.

At this point, Chen Ping'an felt that, aside from his resentment towards the imitation swords from Sword Mountain, he would also need to acquire another small item in the future.

Next, Chen Ping'an planned to follow the river along the foot of the mountain, circling back to the front mountain, and then find an opportunity to check out the White Jade Arch Bridge without rushing.

The phrase “a tree stands out in the forest, only to be cut down” captures two meanings.

Since he had once explained this principle to Gu Can at the Book Lake, Chen Ping'an himself would naturally be even more adept at it.

Choosing to travel together with Daoist Sun or whatever he would do next, all would be efforts made based on this principle.

Cui Dongshan once said something very thought-provoking.

The principles at both ends of a line, once unraveled and understood, are like two sides after a fight, ultimately landing in the middle—that is the moment of “true knowledge.”

Otherwise, reasoning would not be reasoning; once taken from the world outside the belly, it’s all nonsense, woe upon woe.

During that journey through the Great Sui, Cui Dongshan had playfully said many such careless words and jokes, but perhaps he had been too cynical and flippant at the time, causing Chen Ping'an to not take them in.

Reflecting later, he realized it was the student teaching the teacher.

A tall old man slowly strolled along the borders of that small world.

Time and again, sword energy shredded his ethereal form, only for him to gather anew, one unperturbed, the other indifferent.

The old man, of course, knew the cleverness behind this setup.

Each possible outcome, even the hearts of those little fellows, was uncertain. At a critical moment of life and death, and with the hope of obtaining immortal inheritance looming, great misfortune and great fortune were intertwined; thus, everyone’s words and deeds would extend into various unexpected possibilities, interweaving strategies, calculating against each other, making it hard to distinguish friend from foe, and leading to hidden patience or reckless violence.

Simply determining who to find first, who to kill, and how to kill was an endless array of delightful appetizers.

If it weren't for the numerous remnants of rules in this little world, one of which resembled an insurmountable thunder pool, he might have already refined the entire mountain and river, instead of repeatedly approaching the verdant hills and clear waters, bound by constraints. Once he truly took hold of this little world, he would likely have cultivated a Dao fruit of a round heaven and square earth.

But after so many years of trials and tribulations, he could only select a few lowly ants to fill his belly; it was not entirely a bad thing. He used the thoughts of others to temper his own Dao heart, and through repeated experiences, he gained deep insights into the word “truth.”

After this hearty meal, he would have to move again to avoid being discovered by the nearby sects of North Julu Prefecture.

He couldn’t go to the Central Earth Divine Continent; there were too many high-level cultivators. The northern snowy continent was a decent choice.

As for the southern Baoping Continent, he had previously overheard those cultivators chatting on the mountain peaks; unless one took a detour, they would have to pass through the Northern Peaks' territory. Once that Northern Peaks' deity entered the Jade Purity realm, it would be akin to a cultivator at the Immortal realm.

That would be quite troublesome.

Especially since the other party was a mountain god, it would be even more challenging for him to completely hide his tracks. 

He couldn’t very well become a minor protector for the Song clan of the Great Li, could he? If he had known earlier, when the new mountain god of Baoping Continent had not been confirmed, it would have been a good choice to fish for a mountain deity.

The old man was probably truly weary of the persistent entanglement of that strand of sword energy, so he retreated into the mist and sat cross-legged, surrounded by origami cranes that circled around him.

The entrance to this ruin, painted with four murals of heavenly kings, was actually an artifact from another shattered mountain peak, which he had refined and piled together. In truth, he had refined more than just this mountain. Thus, next time, when new opportunities emerged elsewhere, it would present a different scene altogether.

Once suitable lowly cultivators entered the mountain and accidentally stumbled upon it, he would intentionally set up a low-level restriction to prevent Earth Immortal cultivators from taking too much interest, at most attracting someone like Bai Bi from the Water Dragon Sect or Huan Yun, who merely served as protectors. It wasn’t that the old man couldn’t consume one or two Nascent Souls rolling around in his belly; it was simply that caution was key.

Thus, the inscriptions on those walls were all written by the old man himself.

They were meant to deal with those who thought too highly of themselves.

Later, as the fifty or so people entered, they were simply too foolish, far less clever than the first three batches of cultivators. He simply removed all restrictions, employing a small trick, leading someone to rush ahead, and thus everyone followed suit.

Human nature had always surprised him.

The first batch entering the immortal’s cave, upon raising their heads, saw cranes circling; it was also a small clever trick.

Cultivators in the world, each one suspicious of others, if he didn’t create some spectacle, either they would be too foolish to take the bait or too frightened to dare nibble.

It was rather laughable.

If all those entering the mountain were filled with righteous spirit, refusing to kill one another and each taking their treasures, he would truly have no way to deal with them; at most, he could close the gates and let those cultivators age and die within.

The two corpses playing chess in the pavilion had long been in such a situation.

It wasn’t that killing couldn’t happen; rather, it would be too costly.

Once his true self was revealed, that strand of residual sword energy would not show any mercy, and could even trace back to kill him within the vast white mist.

The old man had suffered greatly twice during the long years of hiding.

Relying on his realm to kill, like a child smashing an anthill with a stick, the old man had done too much in a foreign land, ultimately running into that deity from a Daoist temple, which was why he had fallen to this state.

For the old man, the numerous palaces, heavens, treasures, and secret tomes on the mountain no longer held much meaning. His primary goal was still to prepare for the future, waiting for his own realm to reach a point where he could protect himself in any continent of the Great Harmony World, at which point he would establish a sect. By then, all treasures and opportunities would be the foundation of his sect. Those of too poor quality, he truly looked down upon; after being shattered, returning to heaven and earth to transform into spiritual energy was also acceptable.

This place was rich in spiritual energy, especially with the dense water element—not something that existed from the beginning.

The old man was genuinely concerned with people other than the three Golden Core Earth Immortals.

One had been too lucky, and thus luck had turned against him.

He had inexplicably gained three points of opportunity from the mountain peak’s Daoist temple: a shattered wooden deity statue, a green glazed tile refined by an immortal, and the blue bricks of the ground infused with water energy.

There were also two others; one was someone he had unprecedentedly considered taking as a disciple, who indeed had some connection to the mountain’s destiny. If they truly became master and disciple, with the disciple’s realm soaring, they would work together in the future, making it much easier for him.

Perhaps even the Nascent Soul could be casually consumed, leading to the master achieving Dao fruit, and the disciple gaining both Golden Core and Nascent Soul treasures, benefiting all, reaching the peak in the Great Harmony World. Perhaps one day, he could even return home in glory, shocking those arrogant old Daoists who looked down on him.

The other was the most intriguing and, thus, the one who had to die.

Moreover, it was likely he wouldn’t even have to lift a finger.

By then, when only five remained, killing a few more would happen naturally and without effort.

In truth, if those people could work together sincerely, abandoning biases to break the deadlock, coupled with the presence of that strand of sword energy, he would have much more trouble.

He could only “stomach” the journey, slowly waiting for those fellows to age and die in this belly-like cave, their entire cultivation transforming into spiritual energy, returning to the small world.

But was that even possible?

Absolutely not.

Even if they were so close-knit, one of them would eventually emerge as a likely candidate for the Jade Purity realm’s Nascent Soul.

If it truly came to that, all it would take was him paying a price to personally eliminate them.

As heaven and earth converged, calamity loomed.

This was no casual joke made by those three paper deities.

If anyone could gain the approval of that strand of sword energy, it would be the biggest trouble.

A colossal problem.

Fortunately, for now, there seemed to be no such destined person.

Since he was temporarily unoccupied,

The old man opened a book with pages as thin as cicada wings, the contents written in fine, nearly invisible script, interspersed with pages of cultivator portraits.

In addition, it was a chapter-based novel.

Each chapter detailed a cultivator’s experiences and life and death in this place, with meticulous descriptions of every action they took here, recorded word for word, though the lengths of the stories varied.

It seemed as if everyone was a protagonist, but everyone would die.

This had been the old man’s most important cultivation path for countless years, secretly refining famous mountains and rivers.

Within the vast white mist, under the mountain and water realm, every detail was vividly revealed.

This was the truly superior view of the mountains and rivers by a divine being.

The current sage controlling the small world was not a method learned from the three teachings; it was learned elsewhere.

What the tall old man most wanted to visit was not some sage of the three teachings, but the novelists among the various schools of thought who resided in the white paper blessed land.

Surely, they could mutually benefit each other’s paths, a fine example of sharpening each other’s skills.

The scholars of this world placed great importance on their words.

The tall old man raised his head, looking towards the direction of the Daoist temple atop the green mountain, filled with emotions.

He recalled the years he followed that person in cultivation; the mountain was sparsely populated, but books were plentiful, with an extensive library. He had read widely.

Once, that person had rarely spoken up, asking how his reading was going.

He replied, “Reading the Daoist classics, there’s life in death, which feels a bit cold. Reading Buddhist texts, there’s joy in suffering, which feels a bit warm. Reading Confucian teachings, everything is formal and proper, which feels a bit tedious.”

That person then laughed, saying, “You’ve taken some in, but you haven’t truly understood. In the deep mountains, one sees the mountain but not the people; that's not necessarily good.”

Before he could read more, a stunning event unfolded with a sword thrust, sword energy pouring like rain.

That one sword, even now, made one feel a chill down the spine and a splitting headache.

Before that person passed away, in order to break the heavenly curtain, he sent this small world, which had switched masters multiple times, along with himself, back to his homeland and the world. In truth, he could no longer restrain himself any further, and could only set three rules for himself.

Years passed; those so-called rules were no longer restrictions. Now, only that strand of sword energy remained, still desperately holding on.

As cultivators from this world entered, such as the martial artist Huang Shi, acting increasingly recklessly, breaking the wooden statues time and again, he would then patch them back together, and the last remnants of his awe for that person gradually diminished.

The old man casually glanced into the distance.

If anyone dared to spoil his heart-observing game, such as suppressing everyone with brute force, then they could die first.

It would serve as a warning to others, allowing those little brats to believe even more that this place was the domain of some ancient ascendant.

Paying a price would only mean consuming the superficial cultivation he had built up over decades; for someone like him, time was not valuable. Tempering his Dao heart and cultivating his methods was what truly mattered.

Those who had the opportunity to do so had not taken action.

Those incapable of doing so, were merely pretending to be brave; for instance, the young lord Zhan Qing was simply ridiculed, making one mistake after another—he was destined not to live long, and perhaps he would die a rather tragic death.

Perhaps at the hands of some lowly ant?

Or perhaps it could be arranged for this little fellow to perish at the hands of his beloved Sister Bai?

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 644: The People on the Boat are All Enemies (Part 2)

Near the White Jade Arch Bridge, the battle has ceased, transforming into a chaotic struggle of wills far more perilous than before.

The elder Huan Yun stood surrounded by a circle of talismanic formations. Bai Bi held the ancient guqin "Scattered Snow" in his arms, and the eighteen precious snowflakes he possessed were still unsheathed, showing no intention of retreat. The atmosphere around them was filled with rippling energy, chaotic to the extreme, which effectively cut off all other cultivators' prying eyes.

After the six of them steadied themselves, they began to exchange their thoughts. The elder Huan Yun, Sun Qing from the Colorful Sparrow Sect, and Bai Bi from the Water Dragon Sect were the only ones who seemed to have the opportunity and strength to survive until the end. Yet, each of the three harbored their own concerns. Sun Qing was worried about Wu Qian and her disciple. Bai Bi's thoughts were with Zhan Qing. Huan Yun had to protect the two direct disciples of Shen Zhenze.

The bonds of their sect traditions, the future partners on the path of enlightenment (Dao), and their own consciences weighed heavily on them. Thus, this situation was an extremely grueling moral dilemma for the three, no less so than for anyone else fighting desperately for survival.

Huan Yun had considered uniting everyone to resist the peculiar rules of this small world, but taking such risks could easily lead to an early demise. Sun Qing and Bai Bi likely felt the same. With no power to act, and perhaps not even the will to do so.

Bai Bi was the first to speak, "Let's find those five people first."

Sun Qing smiled, "And then what? What are we supposed to say to them once we find them?"

Bai Bi proposed, "We should at least locate that old man in the black robe, right?"

Sun Qing shook his head, "You think you can just kill someone like that once you find him? Will it be you, Bai Bi, leading the charge, or will our illustrious young lord take the lead himself?"

Soon, two others echoed Sun Qing’s sentiments.

Zhan Qing could only smile wryly. After being quickly eliminated in the first skirmish, everyone had aimed to kill him with all their might. Yet here was this comical old man, whom everyone seemed to regard with caution, making it clear that for now, they would not pursue him for a hunt.

Huan Yun hesitated before suggesting, "Let’s not kill anyone yet. We should just collect treasures, and for now, no one should take them; let’s leave them at the mountain top's Daoist temple."

A rough looking wild cultivator scoffed, "Isn’t that just like farting with your pants down? In the end, only five will survive. Let’s just do it swiftly; it’ll save them the torment."

Another elderly warrior nodded in agreement, "Dying early or late is still dying. Why not eliminate a group first? With the six of us, within half a day, each of us can protect four or five people. What do you say?"

These two were amongst those who supported Sun Qing.

Zhan Qing interjected, "Five is too many."

The wild cultivator clicked his tongue, "You and that woman beside you have no one to rely on, so of course you’d think it’s too many. According to the young lord's thinking, wouldn’t it be just right to spare two lives?"

Zhan Qing shook her sleeves dismissively, "You all can continue your discussion as if I’m not here."

Originally, Zhan Qing had wanted to suggest that everyone stop fighting and focus on those five before discussing further steps. Clearly, it was a wishful thought. She figured that whatever she said now would be futile.

Ignoring the five with the most treasures, there were still forty-two people alive.

Bai Bi said, "Then let’s each spare three, but let’s agree beforehand that I and Zhan Qing can rally two more people to protect them."

Huan Yun remained silent. After all, only three had come from Cloud City.

He, Huan Yun, was merely a temporary protector, not even a true disciple of those two young ones, nor was he a cultivator of Cloud City.

As for the lives of others, he truly could not afford to care about them.

Although Sun Qing was reluctant to get involved with these people, she did not voice her objections. Besides herself, Wu Qian and her disciple Liu Guibao, she had one more slot available.

The girl had already expressed her desire through their shared thoughts, pleading for Sun Qing to save one person—a stranger they had met on their journey.

It was nothing more than a fleeting infatuation.

Sun Qing did not feel anything was wrong with it. After all, she had once felt the same way upon meeting a young scholar.

If her master could feel that way, she had no right to scold her disciple about principles.

Suddenly, a wild warrior approached Sun Qing, using the technique of resonating thoughts: "I know you are Sun Qing, the head of the Colorful Sparrow Sect. My brother Chu and I don’t trust this young lord. Why don’t we join forces to persuade Elder Huan Yun to sit this one out? Let’s first eliminate Zhan Qing and her group. They don’t follow the rules, wilder than even the wild cultivators. After we kill them, Sun Qing, you will be our leader. Finally, my brother and I will deal with Huan Yun’s side. What do you think? In the end, we five will survive. Isn’t that stable?"

Sun Qing furrowed her brows. She neither agreed nor refused.

The warrior was not in a hurry. To him, Elder Huan Yun’s skills were high, and he should have been the best partner, but unfortunately, he was too much of a good-natured person, destined to not accomplish big things.

As for Zhan Qing and that Golden Core female cultivator, they were nothing but bad seeds, far less trustworthy than Sun Qing from the Colorful Sparrow Sect.

Moreover, recognizing Sun Qing’s identity, he was aware of her sufficient cultivation level, as well as the capabilities of her two followers.

As for Bai Bi from the Kingdom of Lotus, she had already made her identity clear before, but what did that matter? A direct descendant of the Water Dragon Sect? What of it? If she truly had the skills, how come she didn’t just kill them all in one go?

Zhan Qing had generally guessed the situation on her side.

Regret filled her heart as she realized what it meant to be a true noble cultivator, and what the innate shortcomings of the wild cultivators were.

At least one thing made Zhan Qing feel slightly better: eighteen people would soon die.

After all, neither she nor Bai Bi would lose anyone anymore, and they might even gain two temporary "sacrificial guests." In their group, every person who fell would increase their chances of survival.

On the waterside opposite the White Jade Arch Bridge, a young man, whose shoulder had grazed by an energy wave from Gao Ling’s punch, sat by the river looking pale and lost. 

Wearing a brocade robe, which had already become tattered from that overwhelming punch, he appeared quite disheveled.

A wild cultivator and his companion sat beside him. The burly man splashed water on his face and exhaled a mouthful of foul breath, then turned and comforted him with a smile, "Don’t worry, Young Master Huai. There’s always a way out. I believe you are destined for greatness. Just look at this journey; haven’t you turned danger into safety? I say, such great fortune should have a share for you. My wife and I will just follow along and share it with you."

The young man, speaking in a slightly unrefined dialect from North Julu, murmured, "Those earlier skirmishes were merely the mischief of four or five realms’ monsters. If I hadn’t met you, I probably would have taken another route and wouldn’t have dared to fight. I just wanted to go to the academy to study, but I never expected to end up in such a dire situation. We are all going to die."

The woman frowned. 

What a pretty face, but completely useless — all she could do was spout gloomy remarks. 

They had tolerated him earlier because this out-of-towner had hinted at a connection with a certain teacher from the academy, which allowed him to enter and borrow books. 

This was a fifth-realm cultivator, just at the bottleneck of the lower five realms. Earlier, when fighting, he had been so full of blood and excitement, even taking a blow from the young lord of North Ting, yet he still didn’t know the heights of heaven and the depths of earth. Later, he had recklessly charged ahead and almost crashed into Gao Ling’s punch if not for a girl who had pushed him away.

Truly, he was a scholar.

A slender girl wiped her face, having walked a long way, and spat out several mouthfuls of blood before boldly sitting down beside the young scholar, saying, "Huai Qian, from now on, just stick with me and don’t worry about anything else."

The young man looked confused and whispered, "There’s still going to be fighting?"

The girl laughed, "Are you going to save me again like you did earlier on the bridge?"

The young man felt a bit embarrassed; it was hard to say who was saving whom.

The girl took out a wine flask from her waist and handed it over, "Drink a little, to steady your nerves?"

The young man shook his head, his face slightly red, "Liu Guniang, I can’t drink."

The girl drank instead, wiped her mouth, and looked up at the mountain peak, smiling, "Huai Qian, if you want to say ‘that’s against propriety’, just say it."

The young man was left speechless.

The girl was Liu Guibao, the most cherished direct disciple of Sun Qing, the Golden Core cultivator from the Colorful Sparrow Sect.

Everyone in the Colorful Sparrow Sect, including Wu Qian, believed that she would undoubtedly become the next sect leader.

Though still young, Liu Guibao was already a recognized genius among the cultivators on the mountain, having reached the Cave Dwelling stage.

Moreover, before Wu Qian took the first shot at Gao Ling, she had spoken twice, directly influencing the entire battle’s direction. In fact, Zhan Qing and Bai Bi held a certain resentment towards this seemingly low-level girl.

The young scholar, Huai Qian, had inexplicably gotten caught in this disaster.

Liu Guibao was quite fond of him, especially when he pretended to be a seasoned veteran, that faux cleverness made him quite endearing.

Perhaps it was Liu Guibao’s own precociousness; she found herself attracted to Huai Qian, who was unpretentious at his realm.

As her master often said, if one had to justify their affections, then it wasn’t true affection at all.

Whenever her master, drunk, would share stories about Mr. Liu and inadvertently mention such words, Liu Guibao would find it quite amusing.

On her master’s side, discussions had already concluded.

Liu Guibao felt somewhat dispirited.

They had already decided who to kill, and now it was just a matter of how and who would do the killing.

A clever person should be able to sense the signs.

Liu Guibao glanced around and noticed there were still few clever people among them.

Meanwhile, the six on her master’s side were still deeply engrossed in their scheming.

A man sat alone by the riverside, his hands and feet cold.

He kept a distance from everyone else; after all, being a lone wanderer who survived the earlier chaos was already a stroke of luck.

The man wore a pair of severely worn boots.

Someone suddenly called out, stating that the six had agreed to Zhan Qing’s proposal to eliminate all wild cultivators.

No one was quite sure, but no one dared to doubt it either.

After a moment of paralysis, people began to scatter, either flying away or using wind techniques to retreat from the White Jade Arch Bridge.

The one who spoke clearly lacked Liu Guibao's unique resonance technique and underestimated the sharp senses of the six across the river.

He was immediately targeted.

To avoid revealing too much, he had not moved first, waiting until most had dispersed before attempting to turn around. However, he was directly struck by a sharp dagger thrown by Gao Ling, piercing his skull and killing him instantly.

Zhan Qing had just wanted to stop it, but it was already too late.

Such lowly schemes of framing and slandering, the truth no longer mattered.

He felt that his treasure-seeking adventure, which he had approached with confidence, had turned into one unexpected event after another, leaving him somewhat numb.

Wu Qian’s expression was desolate, but she concealed it well.

The one who died was a pivotal figure from a minor mountain sect. He was one of the few elderly cultivators who had hoped to extend his life a few more years by relying on this immortal mansion’s ruins.

Thus, Wu Qian and this old cultivator, both knowing the inevitable, made a transaction.

Of course, Wu Qian would keep his word, and the Colorful Sparrow Sect would secretly support his small mountain sect, promising to cultivate at least three fifth-realm cultivators within a century, including the old cultivator’s closed-door disciple.

This was a reward that the old cultivator had exchanged his life for.

Among the six across the river, many were still bewildered.

But who had given the secret orders? Or had the old cultivator lost his mind and wanted to drag the young lord down with him? It all no longer mattered.

However, the fleeing crowd left the six with no choice but to pursue and kill.

High Ling would undoubtedly be the most relentless of them all.

This Golden Body cultivator was filled with rage and killing intent, having pent up his frustrations for far too long.

Even if he was severely injured, a warrior's physical resilience meant that dealing with small groups of fleeing enemies was still a piece of cake.

However, Liu Guibao and the young scholar Huai Qian did not run away; Wu Qian had also approached them, beginning to tend to their injuries.

There were still two groups left, both of whom were trembling but had not moved.

These were the two wild cultivators and martial masters from the other side.

Among the fleeing crowd, a wild cultivator was desperately trying to distance himself from others. After all, he trusted no one and felt that anyone could kill him.

The expensive thunder talisman he had bought with eight precious snowflakes had indeed saved his life during the skirmish by the White Jade Arch Bridge, but now he had no hidden skills or treasures left.

Suddenly, he heard a half-familiar voice behind him, "Pork killer?"

The man turned around in shock, not stopping, and cautiously asked, "Two of them?"

The person nodded with a smile.

The man nearly burst into tears on the spot.

Finally, a kindred spirit had arrived.

He slowed his pace slightly, "You won’t kill me, right?"

The stranger, a young man in a green shirt who had suddenly appeared on the market streets of Cloud City, shook his head, "Can killing you earn me money? Even if it could, could I compete with those big shots?"

The man sighed with relief and remained silent.

The two of them continued to sprint.

Suddenly, someone ahead caught sight of a patch of white mist and exclaimed in horror, "Is this the end?!"

The white mist receded like a tide.

The undulating hills revealed the true form of the immortal estate, rapidly expanding.

Huan Yun showed no intention of killing anyone; he took the lead and flew up the mountain to search for the two direct disciples of Shen Zhenze.

Sun Qing did not take action either but instructed Wu Qian and the others to head south to investigate.

Bai Bi and Zhan Qing allowed Gao Ling to kill freely, while the royal offering from the Kingdom of Lotus was summoned to Bai Bi’s side.

Gao Ling directly removed his sweet dew armor, hiding it in his sleeve, and took up a long knife from a dead master, sprinting away.

In the white mist, an old man had already put away his book, standing still, yet his body slid back with the mist, always concealed like a dragon in the sea of clouds. With his hands behind his back, he smiled and said, "If the territory is too small, I fear you will die too quickly, and I will miss out on many splendid performances."

After half a day, he would announce several intriguing new rules to everyone. For instance, from now on, the one who kills the most could become the second direct disciple of the immortal estate.

Then what about you, Huan Yun and Sun Qing, two kind-hearted cultivators who were reluctant to start killing? Would you still refrain from killing, or would you unleash a bloodbath without restraint?

The old man turned to look at a young man who had early on hidden himself at the boundary, burying his own sword, and said, "Let’s see if you have the fortune and fate to become my first disciple."

That young man, clad in straw sandals and a flowing white robe, upon discovering the shift in the boundary, cursed under his breath and had no choice but to break ground, rushing into the deep mountains.

Afterward, Huang Shi suddenly stopped, changed direction, squatted down at the pit, grabbed some soil, and looked up at a distant figure the size of a mustard seed, smiling.

Killing that old man in the black robe, Chen Daoyou, might be risky, but killing you, the fifth-realm warrior Di Yuanfeng, would be no challenge at all.

At the foot of the mountain, the five of them gave their orders and began to ascend, agreeing to meet at the mountain peak before searching for the remaining four individuals aside from the male and female cultivators from Cloud City.

Find them first, then decide whether to kill them.

In the deep mountains and forests, Chen Ping’an led a man named Jin Shan, escaping for their lives.

On another route, Gao Ling wielded his knife with extreme precision; anyone he caught up with faced a fate of severed limbs.

Due to needing to care for the scholar Huai Qian's pace, Wu Qian and Liu Guibao were moving slowly.

Meanwhile, the wild cultivators and the martial masters had already come together, energetically pursuing those fleeing.

Huan Yun assured the two young men and women, who were at their wits' end, that they need not worry for their lives and could either stay put or continue seeking treasures.

Then, Huan Yun discovered a hidden offering from the Dragon Gate realm, but the old man pretended not to notice and continued ascending the mountain.

At the top of the mountain, in the ruins of the Daoist temple, the green glazed tiles and the ground’s blue bricks, rich with water essence, left Bai Bi in shock.

However, Bai Bi also couldn’t help but smile wryly; this treasure was right at her feet, but she dared not take much. She merely dug out a blue brick, holding it in her hand, silently absorbing the water essence to replenish her depleted spiritual energy after the battle.

Then, under Huan Yun’s lead, the six quickly found the very agreeable Sun Daoist.

Regarding whether to spare this person’s life or not, the three against three remained in a deadlock.

Sun Daoist sat slumped on the ground, resigned to his fate.

In the end, it was the old warrior who made a joke, asking the Daoist to casually toss a piece of divine coin to see which side it lands on—heads meant life, tails meant death.

At the same time, the old warrior secretly communicated with the other five that if this fellow dared to manipulate the divine coin with spiritual energy, he would take action to kill.

Sun Daoist was extraordinarily fortunate; not only did he not reveal any clever tricks, but he also tossed the divine coin that rolled down the stairs, landing on its head.

The six allowed him to take the initiative to send the two wrapped bundles to the mountain peak's Daoist temple, after which he could wander as he pleased.

Sun Daoist’s eyes were dazed, almost forgetting to feel happy.

Bai Bi communicated through thoughts, "The black-robed old man with the most treasures—if he remains at the top of the list after half a day, we will dig three feet into the ground to find him and kill him together!"

This time, even Huan Yun and Sun Qing had no objections.

After the six departed, Sun Daoist carried the two bundles, heading up the mountain while wiping tears from his eyes.

As he passed that green bamboo, he unexpectedly felt a longing for the Chen Daoyou.

Meanwhile, Chen Daoyou, having confirmed that no one was behind him for the time being, leaped onto a thick branch of a towering ancient tree, gazing out in all directions.

The man had not dared to go up there, fearing he would be attacked by someone for no reason.

Chen Ping’an looked down at the man and said, "I can only take you this far. Staying with me will only bring you harm. Remember to use those two concealment talismans well—stick them on yourself and find a quiet place where you feel safe, then don’t move around too much."

Before the man could plead for him to stay, Chen Ping’an had already darted away, disappearing in an instant.

The man appeared panicked, not expecting five talismans to fall from above—each one was an offensive talisman, along with two unknown talismans.

He clutched those five talismans tightly, suddenly bursting into tears, but quickly stifled his cries and continued to hurry along.

Chen Ping’an found a peak with a broad view, adhered to the monument talisman, and stood silently, surveying his surroundings.

This treasure-seeking journey had been full of twists and turns, with many familiar faces, besides the wild cultivator named Jin Shan, and the old gentleman who helped him open his market.

He had even shared tea with the Colorful Sparrow Sect’s Grand Master, Wu Qian.

In fact, he had a good impression of them both.

But what followed was hard to say.

For early on, regardless of their nature or cultivation levels, whether seen as good or bad by the world, their actions would not seem strange to others. Even those who were killed might only harbor resentment and hatred, without much surprise.

Chen Ping’an found himself lost in thought.

Why was human nature so fragile under scrutiny?

Yet what truly made Chen Ping’an uncomfortable was not others’ hearts, but his own.

Since he had such thoughts, it meant he harbored such sentiments.

Now that he was in North Julu, he had been cultivating, trying to become a cultivator of the mountains, especially focusing on calming his heart.

Chen Ping’an suddenly recalled a saying from a Daoist text.

Afterward, a sage from the military who authored scriptures had his own unique interpretations and extensions.

Two sentences had been etched into a bamboo slip by Chen Ping’an.

The latter was, "The people on the boat are all enemies."

This served as a reminder to the sovereigns of secular kingdoms that national affairs should focus on cultivating virtue; the mountains and rivers’ dangers are not true barriers.

The Daoist saying was meant to convey a broader meaning.

Chen Ping’an felt that at present, including himself, everyone’s situation perfectly matched this saying.

"Hiding a boat in a ravine, concealing a mountain in a marsh, is said to be solid. But at midnight, those with strength can carry it away, while the ignorant remain unaware."

Chen Ping’an couldn’t help but ponder that being in this perilous small world, or even residing in the seemingly well-ordered Haoran world, may appear vastly different on the surface, but fundamentally, they could be the same.

In the shifting boat and ravine, no one knows.

Chen Ping’an suddenly began to understand just how rare the tranquility pursued by the Daoists truly was.

It was akin to a phantom boat navigating through emptiness—there's no one in front or behind, no one to the left or right; there’s no restraint of rules, nor entanglement of cause and effect.

Chen Ping’an sighed softly.

Some knowledge, when deeply examined, once truly grasped, can make one feel utterly alone and lost.

He began to breathe deeply, quietly accumulating energy.

Once the killing begins, he would first locate the root of his troubles—the old man with the talismans.

Half an hour later.

Eighteen certain deaths were about to occur, except for a seemingly inconspicuous wild cultivator who had remained alive.

Then, when the white-clad goddess and the two green-robed deities appeared again, opening the curtain of mountains and waters, many more lives were lost.

Because the divine decree clearly stated that the one with the most kills would have a chance to become the second direct disciple.

So the wild cultivator from the six and that martial master each ruthlessly turned on their friends and family, acting without hesitation.

Since they were destined to die, it was better for them to take matters into their own hands rather than leave it to others.

This scene left Liu Guibao with a frosty expression.

The young scholar, hiding behind Wu Qian and the girl, sighed, "Why must they act so brutally?"

As anticipated by the young man from Cloud City, just before the time drew near, their offering appeared beside the two, knocking the girl unconscious, then using a binding technique to imprison her, rendering her unable to speak or move. He placed a small item in her palm before stepping back, hiding nearby. All previous treasures and opportunities were temporarily concealed.

But that wasn’t what upset the young man the most.

What truly stung was that Elder Huan Yun had not shown himself during this critical moment.

He might have appeared somewhere, but the elder chose to observe coldly from the sidelines.

Thus, the young man from Cloud City found himself still in second place on the leaderboard.

The one at the bottom was the old man Huan Yun, who was indifferent to being on the list.

The fourth place was a beaming young man in white, bloodstained, who seemed to be in a refined study adorned with a yellowing gourd hanging on the wall.

This man did not forget to greet the painting with a wave, smiling, "Safe travels, everyone—go die."

Then he added, "Huang Shi, my brother, are you out there acting as my doorman? Much appreciated, wishing you longevity."

The third place belonged to a scruffy man who was hiding in a deep pit, sitting cross-legged, with branches and grass covering his head, concealed beneath dirt. However, the scene depicted in the scroll showed bright as day.

Huang Shi glanced at the painting and raised a middle finger.

Not only that, he suddenly stood up, jumped out of the pit, seemingly standing at the entrance of a cave, now obscured by colorful clouds and mist that lingered for a long time.

It turned out that Huang Shi had chased Di Yuanfeng all the way here, and the seriously injured Di Yuanfeng had unexpectedly not died but instead escaped into this place. Once Di Yuanfeng entered the cave shrouded in colorful clouds, Huang Shi found himself unable to break the restrictions.

So, Huang Shi planned to trap this little scoundrel.

As for Di Yuanfeng anticipating this move, that was within Huang Shi’s expectations.

The leader remained the old man in the black robe, seemingly hiding in a cave, still depicted clearly on the mountain and water scroll. Compared to earlier, he still bore his sword and carried two bags, showing no signs of change. The black-robed elder stared at the painting, appearing somewhat furious, his voice hoarse as he spoke, "What’s going on, still not done? Whoever dares to find me, I will kill them. I, with my swordsmanship, can even cut myself if I get angry!"

On the other side, Sun Daoist, who was prepared for death, sighed upon witnessing this scene.

He had been cautiously staying at the mountaintop these past few days, having only ventured to the back mountain, but returned disappointed.

During this half hour, various people had been transporting celestial materials and treasures to the mountaintop, creating another small mountain outside the Daoist temple ruins.

Sun Daoist now felt too lazy to spare another glance at that genuine treasure mountain.

All were disasters.

Sun Daoist shook the green porcelain bottle filled with water beads condensed from bamboo leaves, sipping sparingly, still having some left.

He had previously braved the walk to that green bamboo, only to find not a single drop left.

Sun Daoist couldn’t help but admire Chen Daoyou; not a single blade of grass remained along the way.

This wild cultivator, truly becoming a noble cultivator, would be a loss.

Liu Guibao stood beside the fortunate young scholar Huai Qian, both at the edge of the mountaintop railing, and Huai Qian had already noticed the black-robed elder for the second time, muttering to himself, "This fellow has some skill."

Liu Guibao, ears perked, inquired, "What do you mean by that?"

Huai Qian thought for a moment and smiled, "Just the literal meaning."

Liu Guibao was taken aback, "Huai Qian, are you hiding something?"

Huai Qian cautiously replied, "Yes. Back home, there’s a betrothal arranged by my family’s elders; I actually came here to escape the marriage."

Liu Guibao laughed, "How about the girl?"

Huai Qian replied helplessly, "I’ve only met her once, my impression is vague. I just thought her temperament was decent, but she’s a martial artist, even fiercer than me. To escape the marriage, she ran off to the Golden Armored Continent early."

Liu Guibao responded with an "Oh."

Huai Qian felt a little flustered, his gaze wandering, "Liu Guniang, may I tell you something else?"

Liu Guibao laughed, "No need to say it; you like me, what’s there to be afraid of? I like you too."

Huai Qian was left speechless.

After discussing trivial matters that wouldn’t trouble Liu Guibao too much, she began to consider the unfolding situation ahead.

Sometimes, a clever mind is indeed more useful than brute strength.

That young lord of North Ting was simply lacking in intellect and strength.

While Huai Qian was admiring the girl’s profile, he chuckled, leaning against the railing, looking into the distance.

What he wanted to say was to explain the concept of having fate without a share.

Because the two of them were too different; their backgrounds and statuses were mismatched, and they couldn’t really connect. Today, they were chatting only because he was accommodating her.

There was too much disparity between them, whether in cultivation or scheming; as for family background, it went without saying.

Thus, he had always felt a bit sorry for this naive girl.

As for the opportunities here, he should be the most aware of their magnitude.

It was that thread of sword energy.

That was what he had come for.

He had just been playing around along the way, teasing those around him.

However, that thread of sword energy was indeed an unexpected delight.

He had originally planned to make another trip north to see the great sword immortal Bai Chang before returning home.

If all went well, this top sword immortal of the north would likely come out to greet him.

The thought of home made Huai Qian feel increasingly bored.

Watching these ants dance like marionettes, swaying left and right, after half an hour, it became tiresome.

As for that behind-the-scenes figure, since they were being suppressed by that thread of sword energy, how high could their realm be?

Even if they didn’t reveal their background, he could still negotiate well with that figure. If he acquired that thread of sword energy, they would lose the long-standing suppression, a win-win situation.

He turned to glance at the foolish girl still furrowing her brow in thought.

Huai Qian leaned over the railing, turning to smile and ask, "Liu Guniang, do you want to become the sect leader of the Colorful Sparrow Sect today?"

Liu Guibao immediately staggered back, "Who exactly are you?!"

Huai Qian raised a finger, placing it over his lips, "Shhh."

He communicated through thought, "Before coming to North Julu, my ancestors warned me that the sword immortals here don’t play fair and particularly enjoy killing talents from other continents. So I must tread carefully."

Liu Guibao’s expression turned cold, her thoughts racing, yet she found herself unable to communicate with her master Sun Qing through resonance.

Huai Qian sighed, "Liu Guniang, if you continue like this, we won’t be able to become friends."

This young man, appearing scholarly, shook his sleeves and looked up at the sky, "I’m not going to waste time with you. These little tricks of white paper talismans are making me nauseous. I must teach this rural deity a lesson, as well as that old man Huan Yun, what true talismans are."

Suddenly, he had an item in each hand; one was a golden military armor talisman, the highest-ranked incense spirit armor. 

This armor was among the very few ancient artifacts within the incense talismans.

Huai Qian donned it behind him.

In the other hand, he had two green talismans, casually tossing one as he smiled, "Bind with iron nails and send to the underworld, summon the thunder god, control the thunder and lightning, and command the forces of heaven."

A towering, two-zhang-tall golden-armored deity appeared out of thin air, its body interwoven with dazzling white lightning. When it landed, the mountain trembled, stirring the energetic essence of the entire mountain.

After tossing the second talisman, a white-clad swordsman hovered in mid-air.

Though his expression was dull, he was suffused with raging sword energy that swirled around him, turning the surrounding spiritual energy into powder.

Finally, Huai Qian held a golden, hollow small sphere in his palm.

Inside, strands of sword light flew about, racing like wind, crashing into the small net and sparking with bursts of fire.

This journey to the sword-cultivating haven of North Julu aimed to rely on his own abilities to gather a few of the Golden Core swordsmen's life swords for this potential puppet attendant, hoping to gain some of North Julu’s swordway fortune to break through the Nascent Soul bottleneck.

Huai Qian gently shook the golden sphere in his palm, then tossed it to the middle-aged swordsman, "Take your time."

The sphere sank into the swordsman’s point of contact.

That strand of sword energy, which had patrolled this realm for countless years, came to a halt, seemingly gazing down at Huai Qian.

Huai Qian smiled, "I knew you would choose me."

Then he looked toward the heavens, "Such a unique demonic aura that enjoys transforming mountains into food—there’s no such creature in our Haoran world?"

The world fell silent.

Everyone was left dumbfounded.

Huai Qian narrowed his eyes, "Let’s make a deal: after the killing, if I can’t kill you, you won’t have any means against me. You can follow me back to the Central Divine Continent, and I guarantee a bright future for you."

The clouds hung low.

A tall old man sat at the edge of the cloud sea, smiling, "You’ve got quite the audacity, little brat."

With a wave of his hand, a mountain-and-water painting unfolded, covering the skies. Anyone who looked up could see it.

Since the other party was so sincere, this elder also planned to show some sincerity of his own.

Huai Qian nodded, smiling, "I can’t help it; my ancestor is one of the ten in the Central Divine Continent."

In reality, a certain young master from Longhu Mountain and a certain Liu Youzhou from Aihai Continent were very good friends of his.

The elder above the cloud sea fell silent.

Huai Qian continued, "To put it bluntly, even if I stick out my neck and let you do it, would you dare to kill me?"

Huai Qian emphasized the words, scoffing, "Would you dare?!"

The elder remained silent.

Huai Qian scanned the area, "Are these wasteful people going to be killed by you or me? If you’re going to take action, I’ll be taking a few with me."

In the depths of the mountain, Chen Ping’an was equally astonished by this scene.

After the water curtain disappeared, Chen Ping’an immediately transformed into a youthful visage, donned in a green shirt.

At this moment, he felt enlightened.

Can it really be this chaotic?

Looking at the spirited young man, could this be considered excitement?

Chen Ping’an chuckled.

If such a person were to experience the same circumstances as himself, no matter how much higher their realm, how many times would they have died by now?

However, one couldn’t put it this way.

With such words and actions, and standing here saying such things, they undoubtedly had their strengths and some hidden merits.

Yet at this moment, Chen Ping’an only saw one aspect of the other party.

If Chen Ping’an were in that person’s shoes, he certainly wouldn’t have reached the point that person had today.

Yet Chen Ping’an felt that, given the temperament of such a person, should misfortune befall them, they might not necessarily survive leaving North Julu.

Ultimately, it was just that they had yet to encounter the likes of the Sword Immortal Ji Yue from the Yan Tui Mountain.

However, since this person had chosen to reveal themselves, no longer hiding, it must be a result of weighing the pros and cons.

At present, it seemed not only would they likely survive, but they could also bring that tall elder along back to the Central Divine Continent.

Undeniably, they were quite a formidable character.

No wonder they had come to North Julu specifically to hunt sword cultivators.

Chen Ping’an was not so bored as to curse that person for stumbling in North Julu.

All paths lead to the mountain.

Looking left and right, there are bound to be highs and lows.

Just like Cao Ci, who had walked the same path as Chen Ping’an in martial arts; Chen Ping’an could only bury his head and chase after them.

Should he really be wishing misfortune upon the other?

Chen Ping’an rubbed his chin, feeling that this moment of deep thought was perhaps inappropriate, yet it seemed rather interesting.

Regarding Cao Ci, on the city wall of the Sword Qi Great Wall, after three rounds of fighting, Chen Ping’an’s only regret was not having put on a fierce front in front of Chen Laojian and that female Martial Divinity.

But rather, it was that Cao Ci always seemed to have that infuriating aura of ease, looking effortlessly handsome, and always calm, the only focus of his sight being the legendary pinnacle of martial arts.

This was genuinely vexing, especially since he couldn’t even defeat him temporarily, making it even more infuriating.

Slow and steady wins the race.

However, the next scene made Chen Ping’an feel chills run down his spine.

He saw the Sun Daoist, who had initially been frightened to the ground, suddenly stand up.

Then this "Sun Daoist" fell back to the ground.

However, a second, ethereal Sun Daoist appeared as if the spirit had left its body to travel far.

The Sun Daoist reached out, capturing the remaining sword energy that attempted to struggle and flee, controlling it in his hand, squeezing it gently.

The tall old man above the cloud sea sensed something was wrong; even though he had no idea why the Sun Daoist had transformed like this, he rolled the clouds, concealing his form and preparing to escape.

With a blank expression, Sun Daoist murmured, "You little demon, how dare you attempt to refine this mountain and try to lay hands on the Daoist temple?"

Sun Daoist glanced at the ruins, seemingly feeling a hint of sadness, looking towards a place in the distant cloud sea, "Do you think that with this Haoran world, you can be at ease? Bullying my lineage that is withering, unable to raise my sword?"

Sun Daoist clenched his palm, directly crushing that strand of sword energy.

Then he brought his fingers together and gently swiped forward.

The cloud sea parted in half.

A figure the size of a mustard seed was split in two.

Huai Qian was about to speak.

But Sun Daoist turned to smile, "What are you? You’re still young, yet you speak such big words? If you have your life lamp’s wick left in the Ancestor Hall, just tell your family’s ancestor to come find me in the Qingming world for revenge."

Huai Qian wanted to respond, wanting to report his family’s elder’s life.

But Sun Daoist again swiped with his fingers, slaying the young scholar on the spot, along with the Nascent Soul sword cultivator puppet, transforming them into two pieces of severed talismans as they hit the ground.

Finally, Sun Daoist looked down at the Daoist temple ruins.

The offering at the mountaintop was his junior disciple.

Both were the backbone of the sword immortals’ lineage in the Qingming world.

Unfortunately, the junior disciple, having been exceptionally talented, ascended quickly but also fell early.

He could not blame the White Jade Capital; he could only blame himself for being indecisive, which resulted in this elder brother being unable to avenge him.

In this world, there are countless ways to die, but seeking death oneself is the most unnecessary to save.

In the distance at the mountain peak, Chen Ping’an had already retrieved all the fragments of the wooden statue.

Sun Daoist smiled, "Little one, you still remain so clever, not wasting my moment of distraction, which counts as self-rescue."

Sun Daoist extended his hand, pulling out the concealed Di Yuanfeng, along with the young lord Zhan Qing and Liu Guibao, and brought them before him.

Sun Daoist’s expression was calm as he asked, "You three, are you willing to follow me to the Qingming world?"

He had accumulated enough merit during his travels in this realm to take three people with him.

As he awaited their responses, time seemed to freeze.

Only Sun Daoist stroked his beard, smiling at the young man in the distance, "Chen Daoyou, for the sake of those three incense sticks, you can keep the shattered wooden statue."

Chen Ping’an blinked, "Sun Daolong, it’s actually six sticks."

Sun Daoist burst into laughter, waving his sleeve as if he didn’t care about gathering or scattering items. "Chen Daoyou, just pick up your scraps. It’s enough to feed your sword."

Meanwhile, hundreds of miles away on another mountaintop, a tattered sword energy emerged in front of Chen Ping’an. 

(End of Chapter)

 # Chapter 645: Why Dare to Be Angry but Unable to Speak

After the flow of time had come to a standstill, the mountains loomed high, the waters ran deep, and the world was silent and still.

In the depths of the mountains, Master Huang was hiding on a cliff covered by ancient pines. He had chiseled out a narrow cave that barely accommodated himself and his large backpack. At this moment, he was drenched in sweat, frozen in the river of time. A group of four had ventured into the mountains seeking treasure, and Master Huang had always believed he could easily dispose of the other three. Little did he expect that he was the one who could easily be killed—a mere insignificant character.

The scruffy man named Jin Shan was hiding among the reeds by a lake, a talisman stuck to his chest, looking dazed.

Not far from this man were the two direct disciples of Shen Zhenze from Cloud City, holding hands, their veins bulging, revealing the inner turmoil of the couple at this moment.

Nearby, a certain Elder Xu, a venerated figure from Longmen, had a grim expression, his eyes somewhat vacant.

At the summit of the mountain, the old master Huan Yun had his eyes closed, exuding fatigue, seemingly lost in thought, unaware of where his mind had wandered.

The martial general Gao Ling, clad in a dew-soaked armor, clenched his fists tightly, his face contorted in pain.

Wu Qun’s gaze was blank, one hand pressed against his heart, likely stunned into shock by one unexpected event after another.

A myriad of emotions swept across the crowd.

After Huai Qian’s death, the golden statue deity and the Nascent Soul puppet that had stood in for him transformed from two green talismans into four. A golden hollow sphere containing numerous sword cultivators' life swords, which had previously rolled onto the ground, now quietly leaned against the railing, stained with blood.

The sword qi had been so fierce that Huai Qian’s soul, along with his Golden Core and Nascent Soul, had been instantly shattered. Even the two priceless items on his person had been destroyed in that moment, and all his treasured possessions had naturally dissipated, merging into the rich spiritual energy that filled the mountains and waters of this realm.

The stasis of time occasionally gave rise to waves of seven-colored glass-like ripples, akin to a small stone tossed into the river—though the disturbance was minimal, it still created tiny splashes.

Only the fragments of green glass tiles from the ruins of the Taoist temple at the mountain peak seemed to resonate with the stilled river of time, radiating the unique halo of the immortal's refined glass tiles.

Chen Ping’an had become accustomed to such circumstances; it wasn’t necessarily a bad thing, as it could temper a martial artist's body.

He had once witnessed the old master of the East Sea Taoist Temple, over the span of three hundred years in the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, occasionally picking up tiny golden fragments the size of rice grains.

However, Chen Ping’an did not reach out to catch that swirling sword qi.

“Are you afraid?” the Daoist Sun asked with a smile.

Chen Ping’an nodded, “I am indeed a bit afraid.”

Sun Daoist continued, “This is an opportunity that belongs to you. It has little to do with the ‘Daoist Sun’ you know. Just accept it without worry. In this world, those who do not seek death will never die. At least, that’s how it is from my perspective. As for those who seek death, they should blame their lack of a strong backing or their ancestor’s name not being terrifying enough.”

At this point, Sun Daoist cast a glance at the corpse.

A top figure from the Central Continent.

Could he compare to the top figures of the entire Qingming realm?

If challenged to arm-wrestle, even Sun Daoist would fear the small limbs of your ancestor, and he wouldn’t dare to engage.

However, Sun Daoist’s sword and true self had remained within that Taoist temple in the Qingming realm, and under the constraints of Confucian rules in the Haoran realm, Sun Daoist currently was far from reaching his peak form.

Only then did Chen Ping’an retrieve the Sword Nourishing Gourd, carefully storing that extraordinarily pure shattered sword qi within, causing the gourd to become exceedingly heavy.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “I dare not refuse the gifts from the Elder.”

Sun Daoist smiled in response, withdrawing his gaze. In an instant, Di Yuanfeng, Zhan Qing, and Liu Guibao regained their senses, finding themselves amidst the stagnant river of time. They felt slightly dizzy, especially Zhan Qing, who felt as if her insides had shattered, teetering on the brink of collapse, forcing herself to hold on and not fall.

Moreover, Sun Daoist had also restored Sun Qing and Bai Bi, both Golden Core cultivators, to their normal state.

Sun Daoist said, “I intend to take the three of you as registered disciples. However, I won’t force anyone; you can choose whether to change your allegiance. Remember, this opportunity only comes once, so ask your true heart.”

The young lord Zhan Qing from Beiting Country knelt immediately, kowtowing in gratitude, tears brimming in her eyes.

She didn’t even glance at Bai Jie.

Bai Bi appeared lost in thought; she could speak but remained silent, unsure whether to congratulate him or feel sorrow herself.

Di Yuanfeng, who had traversed the world with straw shoes and a bamboo staff, imitated the manners of the Taoist and bowed to this old immortal, his heart churning with mixed emotions.

After a moment, feeling that his respect wasn’t enough, he knelt on the ground and knocked his head three times, not daring to rise for a long time.

Prostrated on the ground, Di Yuanfeng felt as if he were dreaming.

First, he had been approached by that seemingly powerful old man in the cave’s study, who had actively offered to take him as the first disciple of the sect. Then that fellow had died, replaced by the current “Sun Daoist,” who claimed he wanted to take him as a disciple.

How much virtue had he accrued in his past life?

However, Sun Daoist did not divulge the secrets of Di Yuanfeng’s lineage connection; the timing for such revelations was better delayed than rushed.

His senior brother had walked the world with straw shoes and a bamboo staff.

But the Dao was hard to fathom; he had met with death and annihilation, having suffered a full-force strike from Bai Yujing’s second-ranked Daoist.

Throughout the Qingming realm, it was said that his senior brother had died a glorious death, as it was a rare occurrence for someone to force the second-ranked Daoist to take full action in three thousand years.

Sun Daoist did not wish to dwell on these seemingly flattering yet nonsensical words.

As for the demon willing to bestow a favor upon Di Yuanfeng, it stemmed from this; it wasn’t genuine gratitude for the offering to that Taoist temple but rather a desire to seek good fortune.

As for the girl Liu Guibao, she was no different from Zhan Qing; she was merely a temporary distraction devised by Sun Daoist. Nonetheless, for them, this was still a fateful connection, and it was not insignificant. Their future fortunes were merely a matter of the master leading them through the door; the onus of cultivation lay with the individual, and even Di Yuanfeng was no exception. In fact, the Peach Blossom Crossing in Cai Que Prefecture, where Liu Guibao was from, had a faint connection to Sun Daoist’s lineage, and even the smallest connection in the world still counted as a connection.

The Dao hearts of these three could be slowly sculpted. How they fared today, or even their cultivation level in this life, might long-term be akin to stepping stones on the path up the mountain.

Liu Guibao hesitated.

Sun Qing tried to convey to this disciple through her thoughts that the opportunity for the Great Dao was just within reach, and if she did not seize it now, she might regret it in the next moment!

However, Sun Qing suddenly flew backward, blood gushing from her seven orifices, her spirit shaken, and her soul tormented, causing her great pain.

Sun Daoist looked at Liu Guibao and shook his head, “Her aptitude is better than Zhan Qing’s, but unfortunately, her temperament is lacking, and the Dao does not align. Forget it.”

In an instant, the girl felt a void in her heart.

Unable to control herself, tears streamed down her face.

Yet she still gritted her teeth and remained silent, standing there without a word.

Sun Qing struggled to rise, wanting to persuade her disciple a few more times, wishing to tell that little fool that it was she, the lord of Cai Que Prefecture, who had expelled her from the ancestral hall, not her rebellion against the master.

Even if it was treason against the master, so what? In the realm of the Dao, such fortune, even if you reincarnated a hundred times, how could you encounter it again?

On the path of cultivation, many profound opportunities truly are unique in this life; once missed, they would be impossible to find again in countless lifetimes.

Sun Daoist glanced at the young Golden Core cultivator, slightly surprised, and smiled, “Your temperament is not bad, but your aptitude is too poor. With some luck, you might reach the Nascent Soul at best.”

Perhaps the words were harsh.

But they were the truth.

Sun Daoist said, “Then I will only take two of you. Di Yuanfeng and Zhan Qing, stand up; you won’t need to observe the formalities of master-disciple etiquette here.”

Sun Daoist contemplated for a moment and took the demon that had been severed in two into his hands at the mountain peak, “Like to pretend to be dead? I’ll send you on your way?”

The corpse combined back into one, kneeling on the ground, saying nothing, merely silent.

Sun Daoist sneered, “My junior brother, who once brought you along the cultivation path, while my lineage has always viewed grievances and enmities with indifference, you, as a beast, don’t even know to express a shred of gratitude; that’s a world apart.”

The great demon trembled uncontrollably.

Sun Daoist nodded, “I may not have been able to save my junior brother back then, but I can help him cut this fate.”

Manipulating human hearts? Is it amusing? Not even aware of one’s own heart, just kneading mud in a pile of muck, without fear of being laughed at.

Having been beside his junior brother for so many years, in the end, he had read so many texts from the Three Teachings and Hundred Schools in vain.

Only knowing the surface of “seeking the truth,” yet not understanding the essence of “be cautious.”

Sun Daoist placed his hand gently on the top of the great demon's head and gave it a light pat. The latter didn’t even have time to struggle before its primordial spirit was obliterated, without even a single cry of anguish. Instead, two items popped out and fell to the ground.

One was a broken book, and the other was a talisman-sized object.

Sun Daoist took a glance and then dismissed it, smiling, and waved a hand in a direction.

At the same time, the five people, including Di Yuanfeng, returned to the river of time, unaware.

In an instant, Chen Ping’an appeared as if he had performed the Mountains and Rivers Contracting Technique, standing at the mountain peak without any pretense or concealment; there was no need for it.

Sun Daoist was slightly surprised, “You’ve crossed the river of time quite a few times?”

Chen Ping’an honestly replied, “Not many times, but it hasn’t been short.”

Sun Daoist smiled, “Since you’ve seen the scenery from a higher place, you should cherish it. Don’t be like that Huai Qian, unaware of the heights of heaven and depths of the earth. Even ordinary commoners know to paste door gods for protection. This kid, however, wanted to paste ‘seeking death’ on his own forehead. The strand of sword qi left by someone had targeted Huai Qian, and I tolerated it, but seeing someone so determined to seek death, they will always get their wish.”

Chen Ping’an hesitated for a moment.

Sun Daoist said, “That Huang Master? He doesn’t seek death; he struggles to survive. In my eyes, your and Huang Master’s ways of living are similar, merely differing in paths. As for the differences in your paths, that is not for me to say; the path is not about height, but length.”

Chen Ping’an then had no small questions left to ask.

However, he had one big question he was eager to ask.

Sun Daoist continued, “You weigh the good and bad of human hearts and the karmic retribution of this world too heavily, yet still too shallowly, which is why your heart is so burdened. Many things, once done, are ultimately useless; heaven and earth are not lifeless—they will naturally correct human matters. However, when one reaches a sufficiently high realm, there may still be a slim chance to truly change some constants. Is it that thinking too much makes everything seem uninteresting? That’s right; life in this world, from the very first day, is not particularly interesting. But nowadays, very few people in the three realms are willing to remember this.”

Chen Ping’an’s expression darkened.

Sun Daoist jokingly said, “It seems your heart cultivation isn’t quite enough yet.”

Sun Daoist shook his sleeves, and many heavenly materials and earthly treasures, along with immortal artifacts, transformed into tiny particles that flew into his sleeves.

Even a portion of what Huan Yun and the old priest of Cloud City had stored in their talisman-sized items obediently left and headed into Sun Daoist’s sleeves.

Yet that “Sun Daoist” lying on the ground had turned to ashes.

This intentionally wasted outer body of the yang spirit was just a useless shell.

All the entanglements accumulated over the years in the Haoran realm had been attached to that shell.

He would not take it away.

The “treasure mountain” beside the ruined Taoist temple at the mountain peak was left with only a few scattered small bundles.

Then, in the next moment, everyone departed from the mountain peak, arriving at the open space beyond the White Jade Arch Bridge.

The green mountains and clear waters, along with the numerous mountain peaks that had been diligently refined by the great demon, were still entirely collected by Sun Daoist into his sleeves.

It was as if the heavens and earth had suddenly become vast and misty.

Sun Daoist slowly smiled, “Apart from the one opportunity you’ve already seized in the mountains, I will remain here, waiting for them to wake up. Whether they deserve to be punished or killed, whether it is sorrow or joy, everything will remain as it was.”

The corpse of Huai Qian, the green talisman, and the golden sphere were all nowhere to be found.

A volume of radiant Daoist scripture fluttered out, hovering in front of Liu Guibao, “Even if you cannot become master and disciple, I still want to gift you a tome.”

The Golden Core Sun Qing from Cai Que Prefecture also had a piece of fortune, that talisman-sized item.

Chen Ping’an hesitated to speak.

Sun Daoist glanced at the young man and smiled.

Sun Daoist seemed to see through human hearts, or perhaps he was prophetic, “Chen Daoist, with your dual identities of mountain dweller and package master, you ought to be thriving?”

Thus, the two bundles that Chen Ping’an had buried in the mountains fell at his feet.

Even someone like Chen Ping’an, who had a rather thick skin, felt a bit embarrassed, but that didn’t stop him from bending down to pick them up, slinging them over his shoulder.

After the belongings returned to their rightful owner, Chen Ping’an hurriedly said, “Thank you for your auspicious words, Daoist Sun!”

To hell with it; who knows if the old immortal from the Daoist sect has the ability to foretell? It’s best to agree first! There’s no loss; it’s a sure gain!

Sun Daoist found it amusing, laughing, “Cultivators, who in this world is more qualified to speak of the Dao than the Daoists? Young man, your Daoism is quite high; it’s worth taking a closer look.”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “I will.”

Sun Daoist stroked his beard and laughed, “Chen Daoist, do you wish to continue exploring the mountains and seeking opportunities?”

Chen Ping’an’s face turned somber, and he wiped his face vigorously, “For now, I have no such thoughts.”

This time it was Huai Qian who encountered Sun Daoist; who knows who Chen Ping’an might meet next time.

Sun Daoist said, “After I leave, there’s no need to overthink. Just do as you wish, whether as a wild cultivator or a package master; rely on your own abilities. Fortune and misfortune will come as they may.”

Chen Ping’an began to consider how to wrap things up.

Sun Daoist smiled at Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an felt a bit dazed.

Sun Daoist teased lightly, repeating a phrase he had mentioned before, “Chen Daoist, your resolve in cultivation isn’t firm enough.”

Chen Ping’an immediately understood, blurting out, “Daoist, Daoist!”

The same character “Dao” was pronounced differently.

Sun Daoist stroked his beard and smiled, nodding gently in satisfaction, reminding him, “After half a stick of incense, the river of time will begin to flow again.”

Sun Daoist then drew Di Yuanfeng and Zhan Qing into his sleeves, transforming into a rainbow as he soared away.

Perhaps this was what they called the rise of chickens and dogs.

With a crash from the dazzling rainbow light, the entire celestial mansion’s canopy shattered, creating a large door. As the hole slowly expanded, the restrictions of mountains and waters gradually dissipated. However, after the white rainbow left the small realm, it vanished instantly, silent and unremarkable.

Chen Ping’an froze for a moment, retracting his gaze and beginning to sprint away.

Temporarily distancing himself from the land of turmoil.

As for the few packages containing treasures on the ground, Chen Ping’an didn’t spare them a glance, but once the dust settled, he could carefully consider them again.

Half a stick of incense later, Chen Ping’an had long since vanished without a trace.

The mountains returned to normal.

He just didn’t know where Huang Master and Jin Shan were.

However, Chen Ping’an on his way “coincidentally” ran to the Zaojing area, discovering that the spiritual energy remained abundant, but it was once again items that could be moved but not taken away.

Wait a moment.

It wasn’t the previous stone table or green bamboo.

Now that the restrictions of the small realm were gone, how could he not take it away? It just required a bit of effort.

Chen Ping’an then began to dig the earth, ultimately shouldering a gigantic zhao jing that resembled a huge grinding disk, dashing away while not forgetting to stick a talisman on his forehead.

Sticking it straight on his forehead inevitably obscured his vision; it would have been better to stick it horizontally.

He had learned this from his first disciple.

At the canopy of the Haoran realm, Sun Daoist looked back at the mountains and rivers of the mortal realm beneath him, clicking his tongue, “Not a blade of grass grows, not a blade of grass grows.”

An old Confucian scholar, with a golden jade badge hanging at his waist, said calmly, “The observer may leave now.”

Sun Daoist smiled, “Then please open the door and send me off.”
