After Shen Zhenze took a seat, he said, "If the Colorful Sparrow Manor has no such eye for talent, why not let Chen Xiansheng take a name with us? Aside from the annual offering of divine money, this residence, along with all thirty-two residences and shops on Xu Yu Street in Cloud City, would belong entirely to you."

Chen Ping'an replied, "It's not that I don't want to agree, Lord of the City, but I truly cannot."

His journey to North Julu Prefecture had been fraught with dangers.

The events in the Bone Marsh and Jingguan City, hiring assassins from the Deer-cutting Mountain behind the scenes, and the death of Huai Qian, weighed heavily on him. 

Chen Ping'an did not wish to involve more people or entangle them in danger; he preferred to travel alone, accompanied only by his fists, sword, and wine, for a more refreshing experience.

Thus, Shen Zhenze refrained from further persuasion. 

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Lord of the City, though I cannot accept your generous offer to become a tenant quietly collecting rent in Cloud City, I appreciate your good intentions. Whenever I feel it's the right time, I will surely come to Cloud City to ask for a Xu Yu Street."

Shen Zhenze nodded, "Then it's settled." 

Even if he, Shen Zhenze, could not wait for that day, it was fine; Cloud City still had Xu Xinger wine.

Shen Zhenze was a forthright man.

He didn't linger unnecessarily, stating his business before leaving. 

Chen Ping'an took the opportunity to ask for some mountain and water reports from Cloud City, both old and new. 

Shen Zhenze agreed, saying he would have Xu Xinger send them over. 

Chen Ping'an then walked around the stone table in the pavilion, practicing his stance, in a trance, with his fist intent flowing throughout his body. 

After two hours of practicing, he returned home for a short rest before sitting back on the mat to start refining the spiritual energy. 

As noon approached, Chen Ping'an took out the spiritual artifact he had received from the Pi Ma Sect's ferry, placing it on the stone table in the pavilion. It was a blue porcelain pen wash, which, once the restrictions of the Tili Mountain were lifted, would reveal the wondrous scenery of the mountains above, visible only to those not leaving North Julu Prefecture. If viewed from a distant continent, it would appear fuzzy.

Though Chen Ping'an had constructed a water mansion, he actually possessed no water techniques, so he had to create a large river flow talisman from yellow paper, gently tearing it apart, causing the wash to fill with water, shrouded in mist. 

Instantly, a vast, flat blue stone platform appeared above the pen wash; this was Tili Mountain, the most renowned mountain in North Julu Prefecture, more familiar to practitioners than any imperial mountain.

On the flat stone platform, neither party had yet appeared.

The scenery beyond the platform was obscured, like the fog of the immortal ruins, with a clear boundary existing.

This made Chen Ping'an regretful, as he had originally wanted to see the viewing mountain purchased by the Qionglin Sect. 

This sect, known for its "Two Sleeves of Clear Wind Qionglin Sect, Unmatched Power in the Yupu Realm," was one of the main parties with whom Chen Ping'an sought to interact during his travels in North Julu Prefecture. Naturally, he did not admire the Yupu Realm sect leader who boasted of being "defeated by the sword immortal at the fifth realm," but rather this wealth-rolling Qionglin Sect, the largest buyer from another continent of the Life Pearl Cave's life essence porcelain back then.

Chen Ping'an certainly did not intend to seek out the Qionglin Sect.

His Bagua Zhai was not to be wasted; he needed the other party to come to him. 

How to negotiate reasonably, at what time, and where to meet all required Chen Ping'an to tread carefully, step by step, laying the groundwork and timing perfectly. 

A sect with a mountain gate that could be mocked by practitioners across the continent indicated that the other side was extremely restrained. While being restrained, they might act without any bottom line, and that was the truly frightening opponent.

Xu Xinger arrived with a large pile of mountain and water reports, smiling, "Chen Xiansheng, are you also looking at Tili Mountain?"

Chen Ping'an accepted the reports and smiled, inviting, "If you're not busy, sit down and look together."

Chen Ping'an took out two jars of immortal wine, handing one to Xu Xinger, and they sat facing each other, slowly drinking.

In the battle of Tili Mountain, among the ten young practitioners of North Julu Prefecture, the wild cultivator Huang Xi and the martial artist Xiu Niang ranked closely, one fourth and the other fifth.

In a recent mountain and water report, there were many new speculations about the two's life-and-death battle, some suggesting it was a matter of love turned to hate, while others indicated that Huang Xi, though still young, had been too ruthless, inadvertently killing Xiu Niang's loved ones.

Xu Xinger tossed a snowflake coin onto the pen wash, which instantly vanished, transforming into a strand of spiritual energy, merging into the mountain and water energy of Tili Mountain miles away. All spiritual artifacts capable of carrying the mirror flower water moon had this "money-eating" ability.

Previously, it had been the Taihui Sword Sect's Qi Jinglong and the Taiping Mountain's female immortal Huang Ting, caught in a fight. Both were bottlenecked Yuan Ying sword cultivators, and their battle had significantly impacted the aura of Tili Mountain. After that fight, the spiritual energy of Tili Mountain had been severely depleted. If the battle reached the fifth realm, it would surely consume even more of the spiritual energy of heaven and earth. Yet, Tili Mountain remained abundant in spiritual energy, thanks to the countless watching practitioners continuously throwing divine money into the mix. 

Xu Xinger hesitated for a moment and tentatively asked, "Chen Xiansheng, if I have the opportunity to leave the mountain and travel in the future, may I visit Mr. Liu at the Taihui Sword Sect?"

Xu Xinger blushed slightly, "I've always admired Mr. Liu."

Chen Ping'an smiled, "I can give you a heads-up, but I can't guarantee that Liu Jinglong will definitely meet you."

Xu Xinger's eyes lit up, quickly getting up to bow in thanks. 

Chen Ping'an reminded, "Remember one thing: when you go to visit Liu Jinglong at the Taihui Sword Sect, make sure to bring a few jars of good wine. When you meet, just drink to your heart's content first; Mr. Liu loves wine but usually doesn't let his guard down. Someone must take the lead. If he says he doesn't drink, don't believe him; it means you haven't poured enough."

Xu Xinger exclaimed, "I see! So, Liu Xiansheng is just like the land-bound dragon I imagined, exactly! A sword immortal who prefers reason must be a person of great character!"

Chen Ping'an nodded vigorously, "Absolutely."

Looking at Tili Mountain on the table, Chen Ping'an waved his sleeves, and the blue stone platform of Tili Mountain suddenly expanded in all directions.

He and Xu Xinger stood like "two towering deities" on Tili Mountain, amidst the stone platform.

However, the more important the mountain and water, the greater the restrictions, and the rank of the spiritual artifacts carrying the mirror flower water moon would also affect the viewing experience.

Chen Ping'an discovered that his blue porcelain pen wash could only see the minuscule figures of Huang Xi and Xiu Niang.

He had once asked Qi Jinglong whether the sword energy of the great sword immortal could be used to kill someone across the distance at Tili Mountain.

At that time, Qi Jinglong shook his head, laughing, saying that while it might be possible for an immortal, it was unrealistic for a Yupu Realm practitioner because sword cultivators' sword energy emphasized sword intent and was fundamentally different from the pure spiritual energy of divine money. Any hint of intention could cause fragile spiritual artifacts carrying the mirror flower water moon to shatter on the spot. However, Qi Jinglong also mentioned that some ancient divine techniques and side methods existed on the mountain, historically exploiting the mirror flower water moon to harm certain mountains profiting from it. But practitioners using such means must carefully hide their identities; otherwise, they could easily become enemies across the continent, as it might pique the curiosity of immortals and even ascended masters.

As noon approached, approximately another incense stick's worth of time remained.

Suddenly, Chen Ping'an noticed a fine ripple appear in the sky over Tili Mountain.

Then a voice echoed, "Where is the invincible Yupu Realm from the Qionglin Sect?"

Soon the landscape of Tili Mountain rippled again, and someone responded, "I do not know what guidance you seek, senior."

The first speaker evidently dropped a divine coin with a laugh, saying, "I regret giving birth to you back then."

The dignified Yupu Realm practitioner of the Qionglin Sect, surprisingly good-tempered, not only did not retort but also tossed a grain rain coin back, respectfully replying, "Senior is jesting."

The two ceased their conversation.

However, someone suddenly smiled and said, "Congratulations, Sect Leader, have you made a decision? If you do not speak, I will take it as your agreement."

Xu Xinger whispered, "That must be Xu Xuan."

Chen Ping'an nodded.

Xu Xuan, the top disciple of the North's greatest sword immortal Bai Chang, ranked second among the young practitioners, surpassing Qi Jinglong.

A weathered voice sounded, "Aiyo, am I to drink to your wedding with Xu Xuan and He Xiaoliang? Such a match made in heaven, I must have this cup of wedding wine."

A cold female voice replied, "I already have a dao companion."

An uproar ensued.

"Congratulations, Sect Leader He."

"May I ask, Sect Leader, who is the person you are joining with?"

"Sect Leader He, my heart has shattered; henceforth, the world will lose one more infatuated person."

Finally, Xu Xuan's words caused the commotion to cease, "No worries, if he dies, you will lose your divine partner."

He Xiaoliang coldly smiled, "Why don't you and I set a time to visit Tili Mountain? If you dare to kill him, I will ensure Bai Chang's incense is severed."

Xu Xuan fell silent.

Xu Xinger lamented, "I never expected that Sect Leader He, such a divine person, would have a dao companion. I truly wonder which man has such fortune."

Xu Xinger suddenly noticed the sword immortal's expression across the table was not too pleasant.

Chen Ping'an lowered his head and took a sip of wine, his expression returning to normal.

As noon approached.

A white rainbow soared through the sky, descending in the central area of Tili Mountain's stone platform.

At the edge of Tili Mountain, a woman wearing a veil stepped onto the blue stone platform, with a long knife and short sword hanging at her waist.

Chen Ping'an manipulated the mist rising from the Tili Mountain painting, attempting to ensure both combatants appeared within the painting, though the clarity of their faces was not essential.

In fact, many Qi practitioners observing Tili Mountain through the mirror flower water moon might not have seen the specifics of either side’s actions, merely enjoying the spectacle. It was destined that many fifth realm practitioners would hardly see the figures on the painting, at most catching glimpses of the brilliance emitted from offensive treasures and divine techniques.

Thus, there had long been rumors on the mountains of North Julu Province that unless one was a Golden Core Earth Immortal, there was no hope of discerning any nuances in the battles at Tili Mountain.

As for the martial artist Xiu Niang's background, especially regarding her martial arts lineage, no mountain and water reports from North Julu Province could clarify.

Xu Xinger soon began to feel fortunate that she was here instead of watching the Tili Mountain battle beside her master. Usually, when watching the Tili Mountain battles with her master, Shen Zhenze would adjust the angle of the painting, constantly shrinking its size, but they would still miss many critical scenes. However, in Xu Xinger's view, it couldn't compare to the precision with which the sword immortal before her grasped the battle situation, observing the elusive Xiu Niang, her punches, and Huang Xi's overwhelming techniques and the dispatch of offensive treasures. Though there were still some omissions, Xu Xinger found that this was her first time witnessing the Tili Mountain battle so "clearly," where everything was interconnected, allowing her to roughly see the flow of the two sides' conflict.

Chen Ping'an focused intently on the battle, continuously adjusting the painting.

The martial artist, for the moment, revealed her true strength as a genuine distant traveler, with exceptionally fast punches and a solid physique.

This was still before she had drawn her blade.

As for whether she was a mountain top martial artist, they would wait and see.

Though the appearance and age of martial arts masters were not as difficult to discern as those of mountain cultivators, the higher the realm of pure martial artists, the faster they ascended, making it less likely for the two to directly intertwine. 

Especially for female martial artists, this applied even more; they could similarly delay the signs of aging.

Huang Xi was an extremely young Yuan Ying practitioner, younger than Qi Jinglong by a few years, ranking third and fourth among the list, all under one hundred years old.

The existence of such talented practitioners itself was a pressure, making those who were often two or three hundred years old, Golden Core Earth Immortals, question if they had lost so much time to the dogs.

Suddenly, the painting of the mountains and waters became blurred, swaying unsteadily.

Chen Ping'an was momentarily stunned.

Xu Xinger quickly tossed a few snowflake coins, and the painting regained clarity.

Chen Ping'an felt that the mirror flower water moon of this immortal mountain was indeed a highly profitable business, but if Ruin Mountain were to enter this line of work in the future, how would they make money? Would they rely on Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafu to tell stories? Chen Ping'an worried that Ruin Mountain’s reputation might become notorious; when his disciples ventured down the mountain, perhaps women would be fine, but wouldn't men be treated like thieves? 

Other avenues were hard for Chen Ping'an to conceive; should he invite Qi Jinglong to Ruin Mountain as a scholar and have a philosophical discussion once or twice? Or was it best for Zhu Lian, the old chef, to prepare a grand feast? Or perhaps Pei Qian could perform a set of mad sword techniques? Have Wei Bo engage in chess matches with others?

Chen Ping'an pushed aside these distractions and continued to focus on the battle.

For some reason, both sides seemed in no hurry to determine life or death.

Xu Xinger was already feeling a bit dizzy from watching and took a sip of wine to steady herself.

Chen Ping'an remained as steady as a mountain, continuing to manipulate the mirror flower water moon painting.

Xu Xinger found herself increasingly impressed by him.

Chen Ping'an asked, "In the long history of Tili Mountain battles, what was the longest one?"

Xu Xinger replied, "The longest recorded battle involved a Yupu Realm sword immortal and an immortal realm practitioner. One attacked with full force, while the other defended with all their might. The two were evenly matched and apparently fought for over a month."

Chen Ping'an rubbed his forehead; if he watched to the end, how many snowflake coins would it take?

Xu Xinger added, "There was also a battle between two sword immortals that lasted only half an hour, completely exhausting Tili Mountain's spiritual energy. No matter how hard the watchers threw divine money, it would be a drop in the bucket. Thus, in that astonishing battle, only the residences near Tili Mountain could see some semblance of what happened; however, they said the sword energy had overflowed from Tili Mountain. To protect their mountain from being affected, the Qionglin Sect had to activate their mountain and water formation, consuming over a hundred grain rain coins all at once and borrowing two hundred from the mountain's practitioners, repaying them double afterward. Since then, the Qionglin Sect has always kept three hundred grain rain coins stored on the mountain, steadily preserved."

Xu Xinger, full of spiritual energy, suddenly stood up, intending to take her leave. 

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Good news, once the cave opens, you can ascend to view the vast sea."

Xu Xinger soared off, and Cloud City had prepared her breakthrough location.

She had been on the brink of a breakthrough for days, just waiting for a subtle opportunity. 

After Xu Xinger left, her master Shen Zhenze would naturally help guard her.

Whether in three to five days or two to three years, no one could say for certain; it wasn’t necessarily the case that breaking through faster was better, nor that breaking through slower was more stable; it all depended on seizing opportunities.

A hundred bones and orifices, breezes of clarity. In the depths of the water, the true face could be seen.

Unfortunately, Chen Ping'an had yet to experience this phenomenon.

His path as a Qi practitioner in the third realm had been circuitous, with some minor bumps.

Chen Ping'an continued to observe the battle.

At Tili Mountain, both sides were filled with murderous intent.

Yet they remained in mutual testing, evidently searching for a chance to strike a decisive blow.

Chen Ping'an had already tossed down several snowflake coins.

Having taken a few sips of wine, he had only ever picked up snacks from the bowl, never tossing them into the dish. 

The two combatants were behaving a bit unfairly.

An hour later, Chen Ping'an sat cross-legged on a stone bench, one hand propping up his chin, with a small mountain of snowflake coins piled beside him.

From the looks of those two, it seemed they could fight for quite a while.

After another hour or so, the peak of Chen Ping'an's snowflake coin mound had flattened out.

A distinguished figure tossed down a grain rain coin, laughing and scolding, "You two lovebirds! If you really want to love and kill each other, why must you waste others' divine money! Huang Xi, since you are a sword cultivator, if you manage to survive Tili Mountain, you'll eventually have to receive a sword from me!"

It turned out that the wild cultivator Huang Xi was actually a concealed sword cultivator.

And that martial artist Xiu Niang also surprised everyone, as she was well-versed in many immortal techniques.

While it appeared they were mutually refining their skills, as they clashed, the murderous intent was heavy, and Chen Ping'an was quite curious about what enmity existed between them that they had to fight to the death in front of countless spectators at Tili Mountain.

At a certain moment during the incense stick, Chen Ping'an stood up, suddenly crushing a handful of snowflake coins into spiritual energy, striving to maintain the mountain and water painting he had created with the blue porcelain pen wash.

That female martial artist seemed to have unleashed a high-ranking mountain artifact, bathing Tili Mountain in brilliant sunlight, making it somewhat blinding even through the painting.

This caused the mountain and water energy of Tili Mountain to become chaotic, making it hard for the spectators to see clearly. 

Chen Ping'an could only faintly make out a thin black line slicing through the radiant light enveloping the world.

Moments later…

On the stone platform of Tili Mountain.

Half of Huang Xi's flesh had nearly dissolved, leaving behind only a half skeleton, yet he remained alive, while the astonishingly skilled female martial artist Xiu Niang had vanished without a trace, leaving uncertain whether her body and soul had perished or if she had successfully escaped at the brink of life and death.

Huang Xi shook himself, taking a few steps before soaring into the air, leaving Tili Mountain.

Chen Ping'an sighed, realizing that as long as the realms of combatants weren't too disparate, countless techniques ultimately didn't measure up to a single sword.

A sword could break through myriad techniques.

Chen Ping'an collected the blue porcelain pen wash and the pile of snowflake coins.

This observation had yielded some insights.

The way the female martial artist Xiu Niang executed her punches and the essence of her fist style was quite intriguing, resembling another extreme compared to Gu You's Mountain Shaking Fist and the fist techniques of Cui Cheng from the bamboo house.

In the pavilion, Chen Ping'an mimicked a rough imitation of her fist style, slowly executing the stance.

After a moment, he stopped, realizing he couldn't learn it, lacking any inkling of her fist intent.

However, the real gain was not in the stance but in expanding Chen Ping'an's understanding of the world's fist techniques, enabling him to be more aware when facing opponents in the future.

Chen Ping'an began to close his eyes and cultivate, striving to remember her fist intent, even if he could only imitate a few aspects; at least it would serve as a form of deception.

After opening his eyes, Chen Ping'an started to walk around, practicing and rehearsing. Once he had a rough understanding, he suddenly remembered a sorrowful matter.

The golden talismans were running low.

There were only ten left.

He had to be frugal.

The ancient talismans recorded in the **"Dan Shu Zhen Ji"** were now beyond his ability to draw as a mere third realm Qi practitioner; aside from the basic talismans like the **Yang Qi Talisman**, he couldn't create more.

In fact, drawing talismans as a pure martial artist was easier than doing so as a Qi practitioner, with a higher rank.

Unfortunately, talismans drawn by martial artists could not close mountain gates, and the spiritual light of the talisman dissipated too quickly.

Chen Ping'an took out those ten golden talismans from his Bagua Zhai, counting and checking them carefully, knowing none could magically appear.

Leaving the pavilion, he sat on the mat in his room, took down the sword immortal from the wall, placing it horizontally across his knees, then retrieved the sword nurturing gourd, carefully guiding the shattered sword energy away from it.

For the next full ten days, the young talisman seller was nowhere to be seen in the markets outside Cloud City.

In the capital of Dali, the young emperor convened a small court meeting in his study, as was customary. 

More than twenty officials gathered, and the small room felt slightly cramped with so many people.

The oldest among them was the Minister of Personnel, Old Master Guan, who seemed to have spent too much energy on the grand court meeting, now dozing in his chair, holding a small charcoal basket wrapped in cotton cloth—a gift from the late emperor, managed by the palace eunuchs, always brought to the small court meeting in winter without needing a reminder from Old Master Guan. 

At present, the old man had begun to snore lightly, but from the emperor to the other Dali ministers, no one indicated they would remind him; whenever it came to a serious topic, he would wake up and say a few words.

At that moment, a robust middle-aged deputy minister of the Ministry of Justice was reporting an important matter to everyone.

The female cultivator known as Shi Qiu had been rescued and was now missing. 

Previously, two groups of servants and assassins from the Zhu Ying Dynasty, varying in skill but uniformly cautious and steady, had traveled across continents to North Julu Prefecture, to the Tili Mountain, investigating the records of the ferry's owner from years ago, hoping to uncover key clues linking the Dali Dynasty with the Tili Mountain to frame Zhu Ying's sword practitioners.

In fact, one group had already succeeded but did not take the intercontinental ferry back to Baopingzhou, instead taking a detour across the sea, only to be intercepted and killed by Dali's cultivators at sea.

The most troublesome was the woman from the Tili Mountain named Qiu Shi. 

In the process of observing the mirror flower water moon, she had revealed a critical piece of information: that the sword-wielding gentleman from North Julu was the one who had framed Zhu Ying's Dynasty. This woman hoped that someone could relay this matter to the Heavenly Lord Xie Shi, as she, Qiu Shi, was willing to sacrifice her life to prove the truth of this matter.

Now, the mountain where Qiu Shi had been sheltered had been sealed off by Dali's Qi practitioners.

Yuan's family, the pillar of the state, was a thin-faced old man, rubbing his palms with a smile, "What a butterfly effect, I wonder what our National Master is busy with in the Green Wave Pavilion."

The burly head of the Cao family leaned against his chair, sneering, "Even if the Green Wave Pavilion makes a mistake, at least they do more actual work than you, Yuan Yunshui, who only knows how to spit venom in the court, nitpicking as the best at it."

The head of the Yuan family smiled, "Cao Qiao, I am still a pillar of the state, as for whether you think you are a great pillar of the state, I am unsure."

The Minister of Rites was lost in thought.

As a key figure in charge of many mountain gods, if it were not for the conspicuousness of his official robe, he would be an inconspicuous middle-aged man. He actively spoke up, interrupting the two state pillars' petty squabbles, with a stern face, saying, "Lord Cao, Lord Yuan, every word spoken here in this small court meeting can determine the fortune and misfortune of the Dali people. Can we set aside personal grudges for now?"

An elderly member of the Song family, now managing the royal genealogy of the Dali Song family, chuckled, "My goodness, I almost thought the Dali dynasty was surnamed Yuan or Cao, scaring this old fellow with the surname Song."

A short yet sturdy martial general, not like Cao Ping or Su Gaoshan, who led iron cavalry south, sat in his chair looking somewhat comical, yet his words held weight, speaking solemnly, "Instead of wasting time here, it would be better to deal with that troublesome Tili Mountain woman. If the Green Wave Pavilion enjoys living off others, then let my subordinates handle it and guarantee no trace of the rescuer will remain."

The young emperor did not sit behind the desk but moved a chair closer to the ministers and remained silent, sitting by the fireplace, bending down to warm himself.

Beside him was an ordinary yellow wood chair that had been placed in this room for over a hundred years.

Several emperors of the Dali dynasty had "grown up" under the watchful eye of this chair.

The late emperor had touched it but never sat on it, and the new emperor had also only touched it without sitting down.

That dragon throne had changed hands many times, yet this chair, which seldom saw anyone sit upon it, had never been replaced.

In the corridor outside the study, an old eunuch quietly announced, "The National Master has arrived."

All the high-ranking Dali officials qualified to attend this small court meeting stood to greet him, even Old Master Guan shifted in his seat, propping his hands on the armrest of his chair as if he had awakened, then stood to welcome the embroidered tiger.

Though the young emperor did not rise to greet him, he did straighten his back.

An old Confucian scholar stepped through the threshold, bowing to the young emperor with no trace of arrogance in his demeanor.

Emperor Song He nodded with a smile.

Cui Zhen sat in his chair, turning to the old Minister of Personnel, who was still leaning on the armrest, and asked, "Old Minister Guan, are you planning to stand or sit?"

Old Master Guan smiled, "Forgive me, National Master, at this age, aside from squatting down to relieve myself, I can only take advantage of little things, everything else is difficult."

Cui Zhen waved his hand, "Let's discuss serious matters."

Once the National Master arrived, the atmosphere in the entire study turned solemn.

Everyone involuntarily sharpened their focus. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 649: A Different Kind of Training (Part Two)

Cui Zhan spoke, "Today, I plan to discuss the current state and trends of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, Shujian Lake, and the Qingluan Kingdom with you all. If we can establish our respective regulations, then in the future, both the mountains and valleys of Baoping Continent will have laws to follow and principles to adhere to. Thus, the discussions today will effectively decide the future national strength of our Great Li for the next century. Everything said today will be recorded verbatim; anyone who coughs even once, dozes off, drinks tea, or speaks nonsensically, as well as those who offer valuable insights that benefit the Great Li dynasty, will be clearly noted. In the future, all emperors and ministers still qualified to sit in this room will see it clearly."

Cui Zhan concluded, "Whether His Majesty can become the first monarch in the history of Baoping Continent, and whether our Great Li cavalry can force everyone in this vast world to keep their eyes wide open and remember the name of the Great Li Emperor, depends entirely on your actions and words today."

Cui Zhan stood, his expression solemn.

In the small court meeting, the young emperor slowly rose, his heart stirred with emotion.

The civil officials stood and bowed. The military generals rose and clasped their fists.

In Jin Jia Continent, an ancient battlefield lay strewn with the ruins of collapsed statues. Here, the fierce winds could make any Qi practitioner below the Golden Core stage feel as if they were suffering in hell after just a short while. Many pure martial artists came to this place to hone their bodies, but most never left alive. The sudden bursts of wind, unpredictable and sharp as sword energy, could envelop a radius of ten miles, crushing even those at the Golden Body stage to dust.

A young woman, who once broke through her limits with unparalleled strength, had the unique talent to wander and reside here for many years. Currently, she was throwing punches like thunder at a slowly advancing man in white.

The man was merely at the Golden Body stage. For an ordinary martial artist at this level, she might have been able to kill him with a single punch. Yet, despite throwing thousands of punches at this younger Golden Body warrior, every single one was nullified by his own intent.

In simple terms, he wasn't even retaliating. This pure martial artist, who hoped to reach the strongest level, had not even managed to touch the hem of his garment.

This young man in white was indeed just at the Golden Body stage.

Unfortunately, he was Cao Ci, who had traveled from the Central Divine Continent to here.

Every stage Cao Ci possessed marked a level of martial arts never seen before. The girl, who had been honing her skills here for a long time, had once found this hard to believe. But she had gone through a complex emotional journey: eager to try, testing him with punches, giving it her all, gradually becoming desperate, and then numb.

Just when she was about to stop, Cao Ci finally spoke for the second time, "Since your fist intent has been rising, why stop now?"

After that, the young woman gritted her teeth and continued to throw punches in anger.

Earlier, Cao Ci's first remark came after Liu Youzhou had spoken. At that time, Liu Youzhou from Aiai Continent, bolstered by Cao Ci's presence, had made a harsh remark, "Hua Qian is right; in Cao Ci's eyes, your six realms are nothing but paper and clay, easily shattered."

Cao Ci, not wanting her to misunderstand, had to clarify with his first words upon meeting her, "I never said such a thing."

Now, Liu Youzhou was squatting on the palm of a fallen statue, where a dense cluster of flowers and grass had grown. They had not been swept away by the fierce winds of the ancient battlefield, which was indeed strange.

Liu Youzhou couldn't understand how someone from a top sect, one that had produced many who ranked among the top ten in the Central Continent, would cause such a big misunderstanding over a mere marriage contract with Hua Qian. They weren't even being asked to become immortal partners; it was just a piece of paper. A name on that paper wouldn't impose any substantial restrictions on them. If it were him, as long as the price was fair, he could sell himself without hesitation.

Cao Ci had been visiting and admiring the ruins, examining each statue closely, hoping to discern some martial intent from them. In fact, he had indeed gleaned quite a bit. Thus, the girl’s efforts would inevitably result in futility because her growth in fist intent would always lag behind Cao Ci.

Standing before a half-destroyed statue, Cao Ci paused, gazing upward as if struck by a sword, a gash appearing from his shoulder down to his waist.

The girl in white paused her punches, bent over with hands on her knees, and coughed up blood.

Seeing this, Liu Youzhou felt his scalp tingle, realizing that every talented pure martial artist in the world was a bit mad. It was still better to cultivate. As long as one had enough treasures, one could comfortably hide in their shell. 

For instance, during this journey, he had accompanied Cao Ci far and wide, having traveled to Liuxia Continent, and now to Jin Jia Continent. Besides several treasured robes, he had two pieces of incense spirit armor on him. However, he had given one of them to his friend Hua Qian years ago.

Though he called them friends, they were merely acquaintances, bonded by family ties rather than true camaraderie. Unlike the usual fair-weather friends who sought to borrow from him, the young master of Aiai Continent, Liu Youzhou, found more of a connection with Hua Qian, who never sought to take advantage of him.

Often, Liu Youzhou wished he could tell those who borrowed treasures and seldom returned them that it wasn't about their intelligence; rather, he had a persistent bad habit of feeling uncomfortable unless he gave things away. Fortunately, his parents were never strict about it. One time, when he genuinely gifted a treasure to a close friend, he later found out that the friend had not regarded him as a true friend. This left the young Liu heartbroken.

His father then took him to the Liu family's treasure mountain, an actual mountain. The wealthy man asked his only son how many years he thought he would live if he gave away one item every day.

Liu Youzhou calculated and provided an accurate number. His father then opened a secret prohibition, revealing an even more magnificent treasure mountain behind the first, so splendid that the colorful light nearly blinded the child.

Liu Youzhou immediately burst into tears, overwhelmed by the wealth of his family. That day, he left the family’s forbidden area, laden with treasures, beaming with joy, though he didn't forget to wipe his snot and tears on his father's sleeve.

That day, the Aiai Continent's god of wealth, who never usually disciplined his son, imparted a family lesson: "Making money is easy, but keeping it without inviting disaster is hard. How to spend it without attracting trouble is a challenge."

He shared painful lessons from their family history with the young boy. Liu Youzhou learned that for a family with a rich legacy, if they didn't exercise caution, merely following old paths to make money could turn that wealth into a source of disaster.

Liu Youzhou had only been slapped by his father once. After a family friend who was known for dubious dealings fell into trouble, he lent the friend some money to weather the storm, comforting him and even scolding those responsible. Of course, he received his due share of the profits. However, right after his friend left, his father appeared, slapped Liu so hard that he bled, and demanded to know where he went wrong. When Liu replied that he shouldn't have lent money, he got slapped again and fell to the ground.

Liu Youzhou struggled to rise, sitting on the ground without saying a word. His father sneered, saying there was nothing wrong with business dealings; the purest thing in the world was money.

To this day, Liu Youzhou had never received a complete answer from his father. Perhaps it was a paper left by the merchant's ancestor to the Liu family. The eight characters written on that paper were: "Wealth with a Conscience, or It Will All Be Scattered."

Now, Liu Youzhou squatted among the flowers and grass in the palm of the broken statue, sighed, and thought, every family has its burdens to bear, hoping he could delay becoming the head of the Liu family and avoid dealing with conscience for a while longer.

He inquired from afar to Cao Ci, "When do you think Hua Qian will return from the North Julu Continent?"

Cao Ci replied with an "mm." 

Liu Youzhou rolled his eyes. This was Cao Ci's way of saying he hadn't thought about it and wouldn’t.

Liu frequently asked him all sorts of random questions. Cao Ci probably thought that without a clear response, it would be impolite, so he would often just acknowledge Liu's question.

The young woman saw an opportunity and threw a powerful punch. However, there was a crack in her wrist, and as she fell to the ground, her shoulder swayed, and after steadying herself, one arm hung limply by her side.

Liu Youzhou extended his hands, gently massaging his temples, feeling that encouraging Cao Ci to explore these ruins to see what kind of woman would overlook Hua Qian was not such a good idea.

Liu Youzhou wondered if this potentially strongest young woman of the six realms needed any treasures. He had plenty to spare, and even if she didn't need them for herself, having been away from home for so long, surely there were younger family members to whom he could give gifts as New Year’s money.

---

As they moved toward Longquan County, a new governor from the vassal Huang Ting Kingdom had arrived near the dilapidated mountain. The state city god had also been appointed, and the residence hanging the "Show Water and High Wind" plaque had seen a remarkable rise in the Gu family's influence, as they became the mountain lord of the old Northern Yue of the Great Li. Meanwhile, the bride in ghostly attire returned to her home, rarely seen except for the occasional visit from the Water God of Xiuhua River.

Among the five mountain gods of the old Northern Yue of the Great Li, four had been reassigned to other peaks in Baoping Continent, leaving only the relatively unknown Gu family ghost god and three native mountain gods who had worked hard and were rewarded with promotions. Although they weren't the primary mountain deities, they had already become top-tier mountain gods in Baoping Continent, just beneath the new Five Peaks.

The Northern Yue’s Wei Bo had begun to enter seclusion.

The area around Piyun Mountain was heavily guarded. The Great Li court placed great importance on this matter, and besides the sage Ruan Qiong, they even sent Xu Ruo to protect Wei Bo as he broke through.

On the dilapidated mountain, Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafeng were playing chess.

The young attendant in green had watched the game for a while, growing increasingly drowsy, and eventually fell asleep with his head resting on the stone table, drooling all over it. Zheng Dafeng pressed down on the boy's head, twisting his wrist to wipe the drool off Chen Lingjun's face before pushing his head away from the chessboard.

Zhu Lian rubbed his chin and said slowly, "Even considering Wei Bo's breakthrough, if we hold another night tour banquet, there will still be a significant deficit."

Zheng Dafeng replied, "If it comes down to it, we could just write to our wandering mountain lord and ask him to dig into his treasures to make up for the expenses. I refuse to believe that after wandering around North Julu Continent for so long, he wouldn't have a little surplus left, especially after charming pretty women into coming to Baoping Continent."

Zhu Lian chuckled, "Brother Dafeng, your handwriting is beautiful, truly a sight for sore eyes. You should write this letter. My young master would surely feel much better seeing it."

Sitting across from them were two young girls, Zhou Mi Li in black and Chen Ru Chu in pink.

Zhou Mi Li coughed lightly.

Zheng Dafeng turned to look, feigning shock, "This big water monster, where did you come from?!"

Zhou Mi Li crossed her arms, "Coincidentally, I'm also from North Julu Continent, from a place called Dumb Lake!"

There was a loud bang from the bamboo building.

Zheng Dafeng's eyelids twitched, and he declared grandly, "Playing chess is one thing; wealth is left to fate, we shall see how it goes."

Zhou Mi Li hung her head low.

Chen Ru Chu gently offered a handful of sunflower seeds.

Zhou Mi Li shook her head, lacking an appetite.

After saying goodbye, Chen Ru Chu put away the seeds and took Zhou Mi Li with her to the bamboo building.

Estimating that in another half an hour, the noise from the second floor would cease.

It was the same every day.

They needed to boil water together first before going upstairs to carry people.

That night, Pei Qian was in the room, grinning ear to ear as she bounced around, stretching her muscles. Only after pretending to be refreshed did she walk out of the first floor, where Chen Ru Chu and Zhou Mi Li sat on two small bamboo chairs at the door.

Pei Qian reached out and snatched the walking stick from Zhou Mi Li’s hand.

Zhou Mi Li gasped and began to clap, her eyes sparkling, "Mastery achieved!"

Pei Qian nodded, "The old man on the second floor thinks so too. He said if he doesn't teach me more boxing tomorrow or the day after at the latest, he might not be able to anymore. He was quite emotional when he said it; I could see the tears in his murky old eyes filled with fear of the younger generation..."

On the second floor, Cui Cheng chuckled, "Practicing boxing late at night isn't too bad, is it?"

Pei Qian snapped, "Zhou Mi Li, what are you talking about? Training boxing isn't something to be taken lightly!"

Zhou Mi Li frowned, feeling wronged, "I was wrong."

Pei Qian secretly gave her a thumbs up. 

She was responsible. No wonder she was the right protector of the family’s fortune shop, loyal and steadfast. That left protector, always jumping around, was truly infuriating.

Cui Cheng said, "Why don't you go and help Cen Yanji with some punches?"

Pei Qian replied, "Oh, how much effort should I put in?"

Cui Cheng said, "Go with your mood."

Pei Qian thought for a moment, furrowing her brows, seriously considering this question. This old man was truly cunning; feeding punches was just a ploy to get Cen Yanji to hit her.

Cui Cheng added, "No matter your mood, if you don't move far away, I guarantee my mood won't be too good."

Pei Qian sighed, made a face at the second floor, and after a silent display of gestures, she tossed the walking stick back to Zhou Mi Li. 

Zhou Mi Li held one hand behind her back and gently clenched her fist, twisting her ankle. With a loud bang, dust flew up from the ground, and her figure vanished like smoke.

Cen Yanji was practicing her punches on the steps of the dilapidated mountain. Suddenly, she felt a tightness in her heart and turned to look.

Someone lightly tapped her forehead with a punch before swiftly passing by her, disappearing in an instant.

Cen Yanji, drenched in sweat, gazed at the spot where the figure had vanished, recognizing a familiar slender silhouette. 

She stood on a slender branch high in a pine tree, one foot on her own instep. 

Cen Yanji knew Pei Qian had been practicing on the second floor recently. But this little girl, how long had she been training?

Pei Qian, with a serious expression, said, "Sister Cen, I was just greeting you. Next, I'll help you practice your punches, but you must not hit me too hard. You're older, have practiced longer, and are taller; you should go easy on me."

Cen Yanji took a deep breath, assuming a boxing stance, and said solemnly, "Please!"

She felt as if she was facing a formidable enemy.

Pei Qian felt a little flustered; what was this? Just a sparring session, mimicking the big white goose, doing a little acting would suffice, right?

Pei Qian hesitated for a moment, quickly taking out a talisman and sticking it to her forehead. 

She needed to bolster her courage. It seemed she had to be serious, or else how would she handle being knocked half to death by Cen Yanji?

Pei Qian knew very well that this sister practiced diligently every day, tirelessly going back and forth on the mountain, and the old chef always said that this was the resilience a practitioner should have.

Pei Qian pointed her toes.

The branch beneath her bent into a massive arc but did not break. As soon as Pei Qian's momentum ran out, the branch suddenly recoiled, and she vanished into thin air.

Cen Yanji, momentarily stunned, was suddenly struck in the back with a punch, sending her tumbling down the mountain.

In the air, an elbow struck her back, and Cen Yanji crashed onto the steps, her body bouncing heavily before her eyes rolled back, and she fainted.

Pei Qian landed softly, squatting to one side, drenched in sweat, wiping her face hard. What just happened?

Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafeng stood on the steps, exchanging glances.

Pei Qian quickly adjusted the talisman on her forehead and discreetly nudged Cen Yanji while turning to shout, "By the heavens! It’s really not my fault; Cen Yanji just fainted on her own! I couldn't hold her up!"

On a ferry passing through Cloud City, soon to arrive at Dragon Palace Cave, Chen Ping'an, dressed in a blue shirt, with the sword fairy on his back and a crossbody bag slung over his shoulder, leaned against the railing.

In no time, he would reach two hundred thousand punches.

He just wondered how Pei Qian was doing at the academy, if she was helping with the business, whether it would delay her copying, and how she was getting along with the water monster from Dumb Lake.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 650: What to Do When There Are Matters

As the ferry glided along, it encountered all sorts of peculiar sights.

A group of women in colorful garments swung joyfully beneath the clouds, their laughter attracting loud shouts from many male cultivators aboard the ferry. Given that this fleeting encounter meant they would never meet again in this lifetime, their words became increasingly bold and unrestrained.

Suddenly, a massive dragon head slowly emerged from the misty clouds, causing many cultivators on the ferry to freeze in shock. It wasn’t a genuine dragon but rather a mystical entity, which gently bumped its head against the stern of the ferry, sending it speeding away like an arrow.

Chen Ping'an noted this scene in his mind. Upon returning to his cabin, he continued with a common task.

After arriving at Tongyezhou from the Upside-down Mountain, Chen Ping'an parted ways with Lu Tai. Accidentally entering the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, he left that Daoist temple with Pei Qian and the others. Chen Ping'an began to write about his experiences in the mountains and rivers. Using his memory—from leaving the Upside-down Mountain, meeting Lu Tai, reaching Tongyezhou, walking through the Fuqi Sect's Heaven-shouting Street—he wrote all the way to the present, where he witnessed the cloud dragon pushing the ferry in North Julu Province.

On the table lay two stacks of paper.

Chen Ping'an had divided them into a draft and a fair copy. The draft was messy and revised multiple times, akin to a letter that was never sent; it became quite lengthy as he wrote. 

The fair copy, on the other hand, was neat and orderly, resembling an assignment submitted by a student to their teacher.

Sometimes, when there was truly nothing of interest to write about for an extended period, he would either refrain from writing or occasionally jot down, "Nothing happened today, all is well."

In the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, birds competed to fly, embroiled in a siege, throwing punches and swords at the local top cultivator. At an inn on the border of the Great Spring Dynasty, he met a gentleman who could compose humorous poetry. During his travels, he encountered the temperamental Water Goddess of the River, visited the Biyou Palace, and exchanged pleasantries with the Water Goddess who admired the old gentleman's learning. He stayed at a dusty shop in Old Dragon City, accompanied by the increasingly sensible black charcoal girl, and headed southeast to the Qingluan Kingdom on the fifth day of the fifth month, receiving his first-ever birthday gift…

The only time he didn’t write anything was during his years as a steward at Shujian Lake.

In the end, returning to his hometown of Mud Bottle Alley, while keeping vigil alone in his ancestral home, Chen Ping'an reflected deeply and simply wrote down one sentence:

"These years have been somewhat difficult, but they’ve passed, and it seems it’s not so bad after all."

Chen Ping'an finished one piece and copied another. The two stacked piles of paper on the table were both neatly written in small, regular script. In the eyes of an expert, his writing was likely still quite rough; regardless of the content, it was over three hundred thousand words, verbose and rigorous, orderly in presentation.

He put away his brush and ink, extended both hands to gently press down on the two books that seemed yet to be bound, smoothing and flattening them.

With no worries for the time being, he allowed his thoughts to wander far and wide. Once he returned to his senses, Chen Ping'an stored the two stacks of paper in a small space and began practicing his punches, still focusing on the three unifications.

Now, the martial artist's practice of punches and the cultivation of Qi were roughly split in half, during which drawing talismans became his greatest pastime.

After purchasing two editions of the mountain and water reports, he continued his journey without incident until he reached the ferry terminal of Longgong Cave Heaven.

Longgong Cave Heaven, like his hometown of Lizhu Cave Heaven, was one of the Thirty-six Small Caves. It was the ancestral property of the Water Dragon Sect, first discovered and occupied by its founding ancestor. However, after two significant upheavals, resulting from both external threats and internal strife, the Water Dragon Sect allied with the Da Yuan Dynasty's Chong Xuan Division and the Floating Water Sword Lake, finally managing to secure a stable income.

The Water Dragon Sect is an ancient sect in North Julu Province, boasting a long history and numerous tales. Compared to the Water Dragon Sect, the Chong Xuan Division and the Floating Water Sword Lake are relatively new forces, yet their current influence far surpasses that of the Water Dragon Sect.

Due to its proximity to water, the Water Dragon Sect had established mountain and water prohibitions. Passengers on the ferry could not see the outline of the Water Dragon Sect's celestial palace; they only beheld the fog-covered area for a hundred miles. It wasn't until the ferry passed through the dense misty formation, rich in humidity throughout the year, and slowly descended to dock at the terminal that they finally caught sight of the Water Dragon Sect's sprawling, majestic buildings.

Chen Ping'an noticed it was his first time taking a ferry in North Julu Province. Upon docking, all the passengers obediently disembarked.

Thinking of the tyrannical behavior of the Lu family emperors in the Da Yuan Dynasty, the stories surrounding the Yang family of the Chong Xuan Division's Yunxiao Palace, and his firsthand experience with the female sword cultivator Li Cai from Floating Water Sword Lake, he felt little surprise.

At Muni Ferry, there were over a thousand celestial orange trees, all personally planted by the founding ancestor of the Water Dragon Sect, who, upon his death, left behind a saying: "A life of mediocrity, only the orange trees remain as a gift to my disciples."

Dressed in a green robe and carrying the sword of a celestial swordsman, Chen Ping'an, with a sword-raising gourd hanging at his waist and a green bamboo walking staff in hand, walked slowly through the bustling ferry terminal adorned with a grand archway. The archway bore the calligraphy of a certain sage from the Central Plains, inscribed with "Underwater Cave Heaven." The great river flowed through this place, with a width reaching three hundred miles. Longgong Cave Heaven lay beneath the surface, similar to the Dragon Palace in Cangjun Lake, but without the need for cultivators to avoid the water; the Water Dragon Sect had invested considerable manpower and resources to construct an underwater bridge for tourists to explore Longgong Cave Heaven. Of course, a toll was required—ten Snowflake Coins to cross, and if they wished to enter the legendary ancient cave where a thousand dragons once coiled, sent forth by decree to control the clouds and rain, an additional Small Heat Coin was needed.

It was clearly a rip-off.

As Chen Ping'an thought of the hundred-eyed gluttonous legal robe he had picked up from Yang Ningxing of Yunxiao Palace, he felt that this celestial money was not unbearable.

At the Bone Marsh Ghostly Valley, Yang Ningxing of Yunxiao Palace, the "Little Heavenly Lord."

At the border of Wuling Kingdom, Sui Jingcheng, the direct disciple of Li Cai from Floating Water Sword Lake.

The ruins of the celestial palace, Bai Bi, the direct disciple of the ancestral hall of the Water Dragon Sect beside Young Marquis Zhan Qing.

It seemed that on the path of cultivation, those relational threads resembled a tangled mess, where every knot represented an encounter, giving one the illusion that the world was rather small.

Muni Ferry was bustling, so noisy that it didn’t seem like a celestial ferry terminal, but rather like a busy street in a worldly city.

This was especially true as the upcoming dates of the tenth and fifteenth of the tenth month were two crucial days, both below the mountain and above it.

One was one of the three great ghost festivals, and the other was the Water Officer's Day of Relief.

The Water Dragon Sect would hold two sacrificial ceremonies at the publicly accessible Longgong Cave Heaven, traditional rituals highly regarded. Depending on the year, the Water Dragon Sect’s cultivators either built Gold, Jade, or Yellow Altar venues to help beings pray for blessings and dispel disasters. Particularly for the second ceremony, which celebrated the Water Officer's birthday, it was a date the Water Dragon Sect valued most due to the ancient deity's dominion over many water-related deities.

Aside from the imposing archway, Chen Ping'an noticed that the style of this place was somewhat similar to the ruins of the celestial palace. Behind the archway stood dozens of stone tablets. Was this a common practice for hydrophilic areas near the great river? Chen Ping'an looked over one by one, and there were not a few who made similar choices. Many scholars in Confucian robes, presumably from academies, were engrossed in copying the inscriptions beside the stone tablets. Chen Ping'an carefully read the "Record of the Construction of the Stone Bridge by the Worthies" from the Great Peace Period and the "Stele of Water Gate's Offering" written by the local sage of North Julu Province, as these two inscriptions detailed the construction of the underwater stone bridge and the origins and excavation of Longgong Cave Heaven.

The line was as long as a dragon, and after nearly half an hour, Chen Ping'an finally saw a Water Dragon Sect cultivator responsible for collecting the toll.

After paying ten Snowflake Coins, he received a seal carved from celestial orange ancient wood, which was quite antique, with excellent seal script. The Water Dragon Sect cultivator informed him that upon reaching the other end of the bridge, he would return it to the Water Dragon Sect cultivator stationed there.

This was Chen Ping'an's first encounter with a wooden seal from a celestial sect in the mountains; the inscription read "Rest," and the edge noted "Fame and fortune are burdens, life and death are decisive."

Chen Ping'an inquired if these wooden seals could be bought or sold.

The Water Dragon Sect female cultivator smiled and explained that the bridge's orange wood seal belonged to their sect and was not for sale. Each seal had to be recorded. However, within Longgong Cave Heaven, there was a shop specifically selling various seals, not just the Water Dragon Sect's celestial orange wood seals, but all kinds of notable stone seals. Once guests entered Longgong Cave Heaven, they could certainly find something to their liking.

Just as Chen Ping'an was about to ask about the prices of wooden seals within Longgong Cave Heaven, he was met with complaints from the crowd behind him, urging him to hurry along and stop bothering the celestial maidens.

Having no choice, Chen Ping'an turned and apologized before quickly stepping aside to allow the other guests to pass. He felt a bit regretful; in celestial shops, even the smallest items were expensive, and the larger sects made it even harder to find bargains. Conversely, at smaller ferry terminals like Qingluan Square and Fengwei Ferry, there were still opportunities.

The long bridge itself had water-dispersing properties; although it was an arch bridge, this bridge into the water was inverted. It was said that the bridge's central arch was already close to the riverbed, which was undoubtedly another marvel.

Crossing the bridge felt like stepping into the great river.

The bridge was wide, bustling with traffic, even more so than the royal streets of worldly kingdoms.

It was clear that the Water Dragon Sect made a fortune just from tolls every day.

Chen Ping'an looked up and saw the water of the great river shimmering, unlike the murky water of ordinary rivers.

The bridge stretched over three hundred miles, allowing carriages and horses to be hired at both ends.

At the other end of the great river and the stone bridge, the Water Dragon Sect had a continuous expanse of residential buildings, with a master of Yu Pu at each end, habitually divided into the Southern and Northern Sects. The ancestral hall of the Water Dragon Sect was located to the north of the river, and the original site of the Water Dragon Sect's ancestral hall was one of the three ancient temples dedicated to the River God, which is why the Northern Sect disciples often held themselves in high regard, creating a vague invisible boundary between them and the Southern Sect.

Chen Ping'an could understand this; as long as it didn’t involve major moral issues, such human sentiments were inevitable. In the future, if Lu Baixiang were to branch out beyond the Fallen Mountain, he might also behave similarly. If Lu Baixiang's direct disciples were to visit the ancestral hall of the Fallen Mountain, they might feel uncomfortable as well.

How to prepare for unforeseen events truly tests the conduct of a sect.

Reading about the stories of ancient people and observing others along the way—this is probably the essence of the saying "To read thousands of books and travel thousands of miles."

Many things cannot be truly understood through mere reflection; even if one deduces some truths, they may still seem vague. As Cui Dongshan said, if one were to present good reasoning on the chaotic streets of this materialistic world, it would be easily dismissed; how could that not be regrettable?

However, some people have experienced numerous events yet failed to make sense of them, drifting along with the tide, finding solace in the chaos of life, which, while an act of resignation, remains a pity.

Chen Ping'an continued to ponder these gains and losses slowly.

No matter how extraordinary the scenery of the long bridge over the great river, after walking several dozen miles, it became ordinary.

Even the strange fish that glimmered like fireflies and the many ethereal beings under the command of the River God moved erratically around him; after seeing them too often, one would lose interest.

Chen Ping'an noticed that for the first few miles, everyone was in high spirits, looking around and calling out loudly, but gradually they quieted down, leaving only the sounds of carriages passing by.

His greatest interest lay in observing the inscriptions and texts on the wooden seals hanging at the waists of the tourists, committing them to memory.

If the celestial orange wood seals within Longgong Cave Heaven turn out to be too expensive, he could always select good wood for carving.

After walking over a hundred miles, there were actually more than ten tea houses and taverns on the bridge, somewhat resembling roadside pavilions along the mountain paths.

Chen Ping'an chose a five-story tavern, ordered a jar of the Water Dragon Sect's specialty celestial wine, some late-night snacks, and after paying extra, he secured a table by the window on the first floor, which was packed with people. As soon as he settled in, the tavern attendant quickly brought a group of guests over, smilingly asking if they could share the table. If Chen Ping'an agreed, the tavern would offer a complimentary bowl of late-night wine. 

Looking at the group—two men and one woman—who seemed not too intimidating, with the young men neither pure martial artists nor cultivators, but rather scions of wealthy families, and an old retainer with the strength of a sixth realm martial artist, Chen Ping'an accepted. The young master smiled and nodded in thanks, and Chen Ping'an raised his wine cup in return.

If he wanted a better view, it was simple—just pay more.

However, after walking over a hundred miles and seeing all the scenery beneath the great river, spending extra now would be a waste of money.

Of course, many treated celestial money as if it were nothing.

Chen Ping'an sipped his wine and quietly listened to the chatter of the other patrons.

It was hard to keep things under wraps; even though the emperor of the Da Zhan Dynasty strictly ordered not to leak the outcome of that confrontation, with so many eyes and ears around, various bits of gossip began to surface. Eventually, it appeared in the mountain and water reports. The battle between the sword cultivator Ji Yue of the Monkey Crying Mountain and the tenth realm martial artist Gu You became a hot topic at tavern tables among cultivators, escalating in intensity. Compared to the earlier news of the northern sword cultivator who fell at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the news that spread back to North Julu Province only called for sword offerings, and Ji Yue’s death and dissolution of his Dao, especially at the hands of a pure martial artist, drew no words of respect or mourning in the mountain and water reports; everyone discussed it with increasing abandon.

The tavern's reputation leaned heavily towards condemnation.

Even among sword cultivators, they praised the grandmaster Gu You, while mentioning Ji Yue only with ridicule and anger.

Gu You’s boxing skills were divine, and he had no disciples. Ji Yue, on the other hand, still had a formidable Monkey Crying Mountain, with many disciples under his wing. However, Monkey Crying Mountain was somewhat in decline, lacking a fifth realm sword cultivator to hold down the fort.

During Ji Yue's lifetime, a sword cultivator of the celestial realm sufficed.

After Ji Yue's death, his name as a sword cultivator seemed to turn into an unforgivable sin.

Someone angrily declared, "What a load of rubbish! This so-called great sword cultivator wouldn’t dare to kill demons at the Sword Qi Great Wall and ended up switching lives with a martial artist? He’s simply embarrassed us sword cultivators!"

Another person nodded in agreement, mocking, "They say Ji Yue has been in the celestial realm for only a short time, but in my opinion, he was never truly in the celestial realm; he was just a stubborn Yu Pu realm sword cultivator, likely self-proclaimed as a great sword cultivator."

Someone lamented in frustration, "Even though his opponent was one of our province's four greatest martial artists, Ji Yue still died too disgracefully—he actually let Gu You lock onto his life sword, shattering his body with one punch, his golden core and nascent soul with two, and he died after three punches. How could a dignified sword cultivator from Monkey Crying Mountain be so careless? It was a good thing he didn’t go to the Sword Qi Great Wall, or else it would have been even more humiliating, leading local sword cultivators to mistakenly think all sword cultivators from North Julu Province are just like Ji Yue—a flower pillow."

Moments later, a cultivator with ties to Monkey Crying Mountain angrily spoke up, "Everyone knows how formidable Ji the Sword Cultivator was; why wait until after his death to speak ill of him? Where were these voices before?!"

Someone exclaimed, "Well, at last, a friend from Monkey Crying Mountain has stepped forward to speak justly!"

Another person intentionally lowered their voice, smilingly remarked, "Let’s be careful; the great sword cultivator Ji Yue has many connections. If we say anything unpleasant, we might end up silenced—Monkey Crying Mountain’s rules are strict, and they strike fast, scaring one out of their wits."

Soon, others chimed in, sneering, "What? Are we only allowed to sing Ji the Great Sword Cultivator's praises? Are we not allowed to speak a word of truth?"

Chen Ping'an sipped his wine, gazing out at the flowing waters of the great river, resembling a silent, ancient elder.

Then someone stood up abruptly, "How can there be such a disgraceful sword cultivator? Do you all not think? Do you believe you could win against Gu You in a fight?"

Immediately, someone countered, slamming their wine cup down on the table, laughing, "Ha! Just because I'm not a sword cultivator, I can't have an opinion? So, in North Julu Province, aside from that small group, are we all supposed to keep our mouths shut? Is there such a thing as fairness in the world? Is there a rule that only Monkey Crying Mountain is allowed to have an opinion?"

Chen Ping'an chuckled softly.

It did seem quite reasonable.

The few cultivators defending Ji Yue and Monkey Crying Mountain felt utterly constrained.

Meanwhile, many others were thoroughly pleased, with numerous patrons loudly ordering more late-night wine, and some, after drinking good wine, tossed their unopened jars out of the tavern, lamenting that they had never met the esteemed Gu You, nor witnessed that fateful battle of the Royal Seal on the Jiang River. Even if they looked down on worldly martial artists, they ought to toast Gu You with a jar of wine.

The three at Chen Ping'an's table exchanged whispers.

The young woman quietly asked, "Wei Qi, are the cultivators from Monkey Crying Mountain truly that overbearing? Why do they provoke so much anger?"

The young man named Wei Qi shook his head, smiling, "Actually, it's not so bad. Every sword cultivator has their temper; it's just that Monkey Crying Mountain has a worse reputation compared to the Taihui Sword Sect up north."

The elder said calmly, "What’s the point of cursing Gu You? As a cultivator, to insult a great sword cultivator while revering a martial artist shows a lack of elegance."

The young woman curiously asked, "The ones cursing the loudest, do they hold grudges against Monkey Crying Mountain?"

Wei Qi shook his head and smiled, "If they truly held a grudge, they wouldn’t be so open about it upon hearing Ji Yue's death. Those who harbor resentment and voice it are rarely those with true enmity; they’re often those with half-formed relationships. These people’s words tend to sway onlookers. This is the same in the marketplaces, in official circles, and amongst wandering cultivators."

Chen Ping'an glanced at Wei Qi and the young woman, who seemed hesitant to speak, and reminded him silently, "Cultivators have keen ears, be cautious with your words."

Wei Qi smiled and nodded, raising his wine cup toward Chen Ping'an, replying with a ripple of thought, "That’s how it should be; let’s just drink and avoid discussing rights and wrongs."

Chen Ping'an was slightly surprised.

It turned out to be a Qi practitioner of no small caliber?

Previously, he hadn’t noticed.

However, Wei Qi himself was also quite taken aback, realizing that the seemingly ordinary martial artist with a sword on his back was, in fact, a Qi practitioner.

Inside the tavern hall, several like-minded strangers were delightfully cursing Monkey Crying Mountain and Ji Yue, lifting their wine cups to propose toasts to each other.

Chen Ping'an could even see the sincerity in their eyes; their faces shone with excitement while drinking, and it was not feigned—this was the most interesting part.

He held no objections towards them; in life, when things do not go as one wishes, speaking out loudly brings little true harm. After that, it's gone, and when the next lively discussion arises, it’s another round of grand declarations worthy of toasting.

Chen Ping'an was more attentive to others, who spoke with more discretion, expressing opinions without extremity, exuding a sense of understanding, more like reason.

The words of the world seemed to harbor both divine wisdom and the chaos of ghosts.

In the wilds, when great monsters were mentioned, travelers would retreat; that was fine.

Among the river's many spirits, there were numerous alluring creatures, swaying and enticing, quietly dragging people into the depths.

On the second floor, they were also casually discussing matters on the mountain. However, compared to the competitive atmosphere on the first floor, the second floor was more relaxed, with everyone engaged in their own conversations, and Chen Ping'an overheard discussions about Qi Jinglong's retreat and speculations about which three sword cultivators would inquire with the Taihui Sword Sect. They also talked about the battle at Dili Mountain involving Huang Xi and Xiu Niang, the rapidly rising Qingliang Sect, and a young female sect leader who claimed to have found a Dao partner.

On the third floor, he caught snippets of conversations about trade, with voices low but discussing profits and losses in the thousands of Snowflake Coins.

On the fourth floor, the discussions were indistinct, filled with magical prohibitions, and Chen Ping'an naturally would not pry; he could only hear as much as he could.

He vaguely heard discussions about the trends in Baopingzhou, mentioning Beiyue and Wei Ban. More discussions revolved around Aiai State and the Central Divine State, such as speculations about whether the young martial artist Cao Ci of the Da Duan Dynasty had reached the Golden Body realm by now, and at what age he might achieve the limits of martial arts.

As for the top floor, only the faint clinking of cups occasionally broke the silence.

After leisurely finishing a jar of late-night wine, Chen Ping'an stood and made his way to the counter to settle the bill before leaving the tavern alone.

During this time, he remembered to nod to the three at his table, and Wei Qi smiled back in acknowledgment, raising his wine cup slightly.

As he walked on the long bridge over the great river, a luxurious carriage suddenly caught his eye, moving grandly along the waterway, resembling a noble family's outing. An elder in purple robes with a jade belt held a jade tablet, accompanied by silver-armored divine beings wielding iron spears, and a white-clad goddess whose eyes sparkled like two radiant stars, lingering long after.

These figures were perhaps the water immortals and water spirits described in the unofficial histories, residing in the Dragon Palace, responsible for ensuring the region's weather was favorable.

The entrance to Longgong Cave Heaven lay fifty miles ahead along the bridge.

Longgong Cave Heaven is a genuine dragon palace relic.

According to the inscriptions, it was indeed once inhabited by ancient water immortals, with dragons coiling about.

Compared to the mixed descendants of dragons in Dragon Gulley from years past, this Dragon Palace resembled a mountain residence, while Dragon Gulley resembled a martial arts sect.

Chen Ping'an spotted the outline of a city gate and, as he approached, saw a gold plaque hanging that read "Jidu Summer Resort."

Beneath this largest plaque, there were layers of smaller plaques, each crafted by notable figures—some from talismanic immortals whose inscriptions had remained bright for centuries, others imbued with abundant sword intent.

Perhaps due to the need to pay a Small Heat Coin, the city gate was not as crowded as the bridgehead.

Such small cave heavens managed by sects for hundreds of years were not meant to be left for future generations, especially outsiders; even if a rare treasure were to appear, it would be swiftly claimed by the Water Dragon Sect, making it off-limits to others. Even with the Water Dragon Sect's local dominance, there were some who coveted offerings from great cultivators crossing the river, especially with the backing of Yang's thunderous magic and the flying swords from Floating Water Sword Lake, which helped keep their rivals in check.

Historically, Longgong Cave Heaven had experienced a significant theft incident, ultimately recovered through the combined efforts of three sects. The identity of the thief was unexpected yet fitting—a renowned sword cultivator who had concealed his identity among the Water Dragon Sect's miscellaneous workers for decades but still failed to succeed, having to return the stolen water treasure in the face of pursuit by three sects' ancestors; he narrowly escaped death and fled to Aiai State, becoming a servant to the God of Wealth, Liu, and has yet to dare return to North Julu Province.

Just as Chen Ping'an was about to hand over a Small Heat Coin, someone softly advised, "If you can save, then save; there's no need to pay."

Chen Ping'an turned around, pleasantly surprised, though he didn’t call out the person’s name.

Yet his eyes could not hide his joy.

It was none other than Li Liu, who should have been cultivating at Lion Peak.

During their reunion at the Daisui Academy years ago, according to Li Huai, this sister of his had become a practitioner at Lion Peak, serving the ancient immortal on the mountain by bringing him tea and water every day. As for her parents, they had opened a shop at the foot of the mountain, earning a great deal of money, and her marriage prospects had also been settled.

Chen Ping'an smiled, "What a coincidence! I was planning to walk through Jidu and then visit Lion Peak to find you all."

Li Liu gently shook her head, smiling, "Not really; I came specifically to find you."

Chen Ping'an hesitated, all his words ultimately swallowed back.

Li Liu was evidently a well-accomplished Qi practitioner, and her realm was certainly high.

However, this feeling of his flickered and vanished.

Li Liu took out an ancient-looking dragon-shaped jade plaque. The Water Dragon Sect's guard at the city gate glanced at it and immediately bowed respectfully to this unidentified young woman. Li Liu then led Chen Ping'an directly through the city gate and up a seemingly endless staircase of white jade.

For some reason, when Chen Ping'an turned back, it appeared that the city gate had been sealed off, preventing anyone from entering Longgong Cave Heaven.

Ahead, the figures were small as mustard seeds, gradually ascending.

Li Liu gently spoke, "Mr. Chen."

Chen Ping'an quickly replied, "Just call me by my name; temporarily, you can call me Chen Good Person."

Li Liu's eyes sparkled like water, smiling widely.

Chen Ping'an felt slightly shameless and thought about whether to take another alias, finally saying, "Then just call me Mr. Chen."

Li Liu nodded, and her first statement carried weight, "Mr. Chen should strive to reach the Golden Body realm soon; otherwise, there will be changes over in the Golden Armor Province."

Chen Ping'an hesitated for a moment and replied, "I’ll try my best."

Li Liu's next statement left Chen Ping'an's heart unsettled, "Not long ago, Zheng Dafu sent a letter to Lion Peak, and I made a trip to Fallen Mountain. The Lotus Flower Blessed Land has now been divided into four. Fallen Mountain occupies one part, and that Tongye Umbrella is the entrance. Zhu Lian and the others urgently need to upgrade the area temporarily named Lotus Flower Blessed Land into a medium blessed land; otherwise, it will fall into desolation, which requires two to three thousand Grain Rain Coins."

Chen Ping'an's expression stiffened as he carefully asked, "Grain Rain Coins?"

Li Liu nodded, "Grain Rain Coins."

Chen Ping'an sighed, "Even if I smashed my pots and sold my iron, it wouldn’t be enough."

Only then did Li Liu describe the recent developments on Zhu Lian's side.

After listening, Chen Ping'an could finally breathe a little easier.

If he could borrow money, that would at least be a skill.

Who to borrow from, how much, and how to repay; Zhu Lian already had a plan laid out. After listening carefully, Chen Ping'an had no objections. With Zhu Lian spearheading, along with Wei Ban and Zheng Dafu strategizing, there shouldn’t be any issues.

The key point was that this burden of owing two to three thousand Grain Rain Coins ultimately rested on the shoulders of this young mountain lord, and there was no escaping it.

Of course, Chen Ping'an wouldn’t run away; he had already begun acting as a steward, recalculating the wealth he had accumulated during his time in North Julu Province, starting from the scraps he had gathered to all the items he could sell, figuring out how many Grain Rain Coins he could cough up. After setting aside the portions he had already borrowed, he wondered if he could fill in the gap for Fallen Mountain. The answer was simple: he couldn’t.

When Chen Ping'an regained his focus, Li Liu had just shifted the conversation, "Actually, the earliest entrance to Lizhu Cave Heaven was quite similar to this Longgong Cave Heaven."

Chen Ping'an responded with regret, "I’ve never been there; by the time I left my hometown, Lizhu Cave Heaven had already settled down."

Li Liu laughed, "Care to sit for a while? After all, there’s no one behind us."

Without hesitation, Chen Ping'an sat down on the steps, took out his sword-raising gourd, and had a sip of wine. From now on, he could only drink glutinous rice wine.

Li Liu said, "With this jade plaque, no one from the Water Dragon Sect will use their powers to pry into our movements."

Chen Ping'an still didn’t ask much.

His impression of Li Liu was rather shallow; she was merely Li Huai’s sister and the object of admiration for Lin Shouyi and Dong Shuijing.

Until today, they hadn’t interacted at all.

Li Liu hesitated for a moment, "Mr. Chen, I have a mountain copy of 'Mirroring Flowers and Water Moon' that pertains to you, though it's not very significant. I didn’t intend to hand it over, fearing it might complicate your travels."

Chen Ping'an was puzzled, pondering for a moment before saying, "It’s fine; since it’s something that you’ll eventually find out, it’s better to plan ahead."

Li Liu then took out what looked like a copybook of sorts, suspending it in the air. She lightly pointed with her finger, causing ripples to spread, enveloping them in mist.

On the copybook, an image of a solemnly seated woman appeared.

Disguised as Shi Jiao, she was a female cultivator from a small sect in Baopingzhou.

She came from the Dao Offering Mountain in North Julu Province and was serving as a maid on the ferry that had already crashed in the territory of the Zhu Ying Dynasty.

Li Liu gazed into the distance, as if detached from the scene.

Having witnessed the joys and sorrows of the world, she felt hardly any emotion.

The last scene of 'Mirroring Flowers and Water Moon' was that of a woman who sought death, carefully retrieving a treasured silk pouch she had kept for many years. She frowned, as if trying not to cry, forcing a smile as she held the silk pouch high, gently shaking it, and softly said, "Hey, whoever you are, Qiu Shi likes you. Did you hear? Did you see? If you didn’t know, that’s fine. If you did, just knowing is enough."

Chen Ping'an sat quietly, listening to the story without missing a word.

She was Qiu Shi's sister, named Chun Shui.

Chen Ping'an recognized this at first glance.

Finally, he murmured, "Okay, I understand."

After a long silence.

Li Liu put away the copybook and tucked it into her sleeve.

Chen Ping'an set aside his sword-raising gourd, his face revealing no signs of sorrow or anger.

Li Liu didn’t find this strange.

She simply stated something that sounded rather cold, "Given the circumstances, her actions were pointless, nothing but a quest for death."

Chen Ping'an nodded, "Generally speaking, that’s the case."

Li Liu asked, "Is there an 'uncommon' perspective?"

Chen Ping'an did not provide an answer and instead said, "I plan to continue my journey and won’t visit Longgong Cave Heaven; I can’t afford anything there anyway. But will this cause you any trouble?"

Li Liu laughed, "Mr. Chen is overthinking it. In North Julu Province, I have no troubles. At least, I am safe."

Though Chen Ping'an said he would continue on, he did not rise immediately.

He recalled the couplet he intended to hang in the bamboo building at Fallen Mountain; the first line read, "In the stormy winds and rain beyond the mountain, I will draw my sword and descend."

Chen Ping'an then hung the sword he had been carrying on his back at his waist.

This would be the first time he truly wielded a sword.

Previously, he was used to just carrying it.

Li Liu asked, "Mr. Chen, are you planning to directly confront the Dao Offering Mountain, then question the Da Li Dynasty, and finally inquire of the Celestial Lord Xie Shi?"

Li Liu herself wasn’t fond of using swords; be it ancient deities or contemporary practitioners, she found them all unsatisfactory.

Chen Ping'an stood up, shaking his sword-raising gourd, and laughed, "Not at all, my skills aren’t sufficient; I’ll just rely on wine to bolster my courage."

Li Liu nodded with a smile, remaining seated as she watched the young man in the green robe, armed with a sword, slowly descend the steps.

What to do when there are matters?

Draw the sword and descend the mountain.

And if the world’s issues surpass one’s abilities, what then?

One can only keep the answers in their heart and sheathed.

*(End of Chapter)*
